## Agent 5 result — S1/T1 singular and transition routing

I followed the Agent 5 instruction: isolate the singular/transition branch and avoid forcing the ordinary Wronskian into scales where its normalization degenerates. The instruction specifically asks for a routing theorem and determinant-loss bookkeeping, with S1/T1 left as named analytic estimates if not proved. 

### Bottom line

The current draft has the right branch names, but **T1 is under-specified**. It should be strengthened from a vague “transition control” statement into a **weighted chart-overlap finite-jet observability theorem**.

The key repair is:

\[
\mu:=\lambda Q.
\]

Use three regimes:

\[
\mu\gtrsim 1
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{ordinary branch: O1+O2+O3},
\]

\[
(\log Q)^{-C}\lesssim \mu\lesssim 1
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{transition branch: weighted T1},
\]

\[
\mu\ll(\log Q)^{-C}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{deep singular branch: S1}.
\]

The transition theorem must be stated in a **weighted finite-jet norm** so the overlap loss is

\[
\mu^{-O(R)}
\]

rather than the determinant/Vandermonde loss

\[
\mu^{-O(R^2)}.
\]

The latter is too large for the fixed-polynomial bookkeeping when

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

# Proposed LaTeX insertion / replacement

I would replace the current short S1/T1 subsection with the following stronger formulation.

```latex
\subsection{Singular and transition Gate--1 branches}
\label{subsec:singular-transition-gate-one-branches}

Set
\[
\mu:=\lambda Q.
\]
The ordinary packet-frequency Wronskian construction is used only in the
ordinary range \(\mu\gtrsim1\).  It is not transported into the deep singular
range.  Instead Gate~1 is routed through three disjoint branches:
\[
\mu\gtrsim1,
\qquad
(\log Q)^{-C_\tr}\lesssim \mu\lesssim1,
\qquad
\mu\ll(\log Q)^{-C_\tr}.
\]

For an interval
\[
I_\lambda=m_0+\lambda X,
\qquad |X|\asymp1,
\]
write the normalized source-curvature profile as
\[
F_\lambda(x):=\lambda^3 q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x).
\]
Gate~1 is equivalent, up to the fixed finite-jet-to-energy loss, to proving a
polynomial lower bound for a finite jet of \(F_\lambda\).

\begin{definition}[Weighted transition jet norm]
\label{def:weighted-transition-jet-norm}
For \(0<\mu\le1\), define
\[
\|J_R(F_\lambda)\|_{\mu}
:=
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\mu^{-r}\,
\left|\partial_x^r F_\lambda(0)\right|.
\]
Equivalently one may use the Euclidean norm
\[
\|J_R(F_\lambda)\|_{\mu,2}^2
:=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\mu^{-2r}
\left|\partial_x^r F_\lambda(0)\right|^2.
\]
The weighted norm records the natural suppression
\[
\partial_x^r e^{i\lambda(\log n)x}
=
(i\lambda\log n)^r e^{i\lambda(\log n)x}
\asymp
\mu^r
\]
on the packet-frequency range \(\log n\asymp Q\).
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[S1: singular explicit-formula anti-design exclusion]
\label{def:S1-singular-explicit-formula-anti-design}
In the deep singular regime
\[
\mu=\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C_\tr},
\]
after singular rescaling
\[
m=\gamma+\lambda x,
\]
let
\[
\mathbf M_R^{\sing}
:=
\mathbf P_R-\mathbf G_R-\mathbf T_R
\]
denote the finite vector of normalized singular sine moments, with components
\[
M_k^{\sing}
=
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]
The S1 input is the pointwise lower bound
\[
\boxed{
\|\mathbf M_R^{\sing}\|_2\ge Q^{-A_\sing}.
}
\]
Equivalently, the actual singular packet cannot realize the full finite
sine-moment anti-design
\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3,
\]
once the prime, gamma/background, dual, and tail terms belonging to
\(q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\) are included.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[T1: weighted transition finite-jet observability]
\label{def:T1-weighted-transition-finite-jet-observability}
In the transition regime
\[
(\log Q)^{-C_\tr}\lesssim\mu\lesssim1,
\]
the T1 input is the weighted finite-jet lower bound
\[
\boxed{
\|J_R(F_\lambda)\|_{\mu}\ge Q^{-A_\tr}.
}
\]
Equivalently, the exact transition explicit-formula vector
\[
\mathcal A_R^\tr(m_0,\lambda)
:=
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^r
\left[
\lambda^3q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x)
\right]_{x=0}
\right)_{0\le r\le R}
\]
satisfies
\[
\boxed{
\|\mathcal A_R^\tr(m_0,\lambda)\|_2\ge Q^{-A_\tr}
}
\]
uniformly for admissible centers in the transition range.

This is a named actual-zeta input.  It must be proved for the full canonical
object
\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]
not for a zero-side proxy, \(B_2\)-only diagnostic, or flexible Dirichlet
polynomial model.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Routed Gate--1 theorem]
\label{thm:routed-gate-one-singular-transition-ordinary}
Assume the following three inputs.

\begin{enumerate}
\item In the ordinary range \(\mu\gtrsim1\), O1--O3 hold, hence the ordinary
Wronskian theorem gives Gate~1.

\item In the transition range
\[
(\log Q)^{-C_\tr}\lesssim\mu\lesssim1,
\]
T1 holds in the weighted form of
Definition~\ref{def:T1-weighted-transition-finite-jet-observability}.

\item In the deep singular range
\[
\mu\ll(\log Q)^{-C_\tr},
\]
S1 holds in the form of
Definition~\ref{def:S1-singular-explicit-formula-anti-design}, and the
singular finite-moment vector transfers to the normalized source jet with only
finite-dimensional loss:
\[
\|J_R(F_\lambda)\|_{\sing}
\ge
e^{-C R\log R}\|\mathbf M_R^{\sing}\|_2
-
\operatorname{Err}_{R,\sing},
\]
where
\[
\operatorname{Err}_{R,\sing}
\le
\frac12 e^{-C R\log R}Q^{-A_\sing}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Take
\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]
Then every admissible packet interval satisfies Gate~1:
\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\lambda}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\lambda|.
}
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The ordinary range is exactly
Theorem~\ref{thm:ordinary-gate-one-from-O1-O2-O3}.

In the transition range, T1 gives
\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\mu^{-r}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)|
\ge Q^{-A_\tr}.
\]
Hence for some \(r\le R\),
\[
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)|
\ge
\mu^r Q^{-A_\tr}
\ge
\mu^R Q^{-A_\tr}.
\]
Since
\[
\mu\ge(\log Q)^{-C_\tr}
\]
and
\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]
we have
\[
\mu^R
\ge
(\log Q)^{-C_\tr R}
=
Q^{-O(1)}.
\]
Thus
\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)|
\ge
Q^{-A'_\tr}.
\]
The existing finite-jet-to-energy lemma then gives
\[
\int_{I_\lambda}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B_\tr}|I_\lambda|.
\]

In the deep singular range, S1 and the singular transfer estimate give
\[
\|J_R(F_\lambda)\|_{\sing}
\ge
\frac12 e^{-C R\log R}Q^{-A_\sing}.
\]
For
\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]
the finite-dimensional conditioning loss satisfies
\[
e^{-C R\log R}=Q^{-O(1)}.
\]
Therefore
\[
\|J_R(F_\lambda)\|_{\sing}\ge Q^{-A'_\sing}.
\]
Applying the same finite-jet-to-energy lemma gives Gate~1 in the deep singular
range.

The three regimes cover all admissible \(\mu=\lambda Q\), so Gate~1 follows
uniformly.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Why determinant transition transfer is not acceptable]
\label{rem:determinant-transition-transfer-loss}
The transition theorem must not be proved by an unweighted determinant
comparison between ordinary and singular jet charts.  In the overlap range,
the \(r\)-th ordinary packet derivative carries the factor
\[
(\lambda\log n)^r\asymp \mu^r.
\]
A determinant comparison across \(R\) jet levels therefore loses
\[
\prod_{r=0}^{R}\mu^r
=
\mu^{R(R+1)/2}.
\]
When
\[
\mu\ge(\log Q)^{-C_\tr}
\quad\text{and}\quad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]
this becomes
\[
\mu^{O(R^2)}
=
\exp\!\left(-O(R^2\log\log Q)\right),
\]
which is super-polynomial in \(Q^{-1}\) and breaks the fixed-polynomial
bookkeeping.

The weighted jet norm of
Definition~\ref{def:weighted-transition-jet-norm} avoids this loss.  It
requires only
\[
\mu^R
\]
when passing from weighted jets back to ordinary unweighted derivatives, and
\[
\mu^R\ge Q^{-O(1)}
\]
throughout the transition range.
\end{remark}
```

## Exact unresolved analytic estimate

The unresolved estimate should be stated as one master observability theorem.

```latex
\begin{conjecture}[Master singular/transition source observability]
\label{conj:master-singular-transition-source-observability}
Let
\[
F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x),
\qquad
\mu=\lambda Q,
\]
where
\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]
For every admissible off-line packet center outside the ordinary range, one has
\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\mu^{-r}
\left|
\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]
whenever
\[
(\log Q)^{-C_\tr}\lesssim\mu\lesssim1,
\]
and in the deep singular range
\[
\mu\ll(\log Q)^{-C_\tr}
\]
one has
\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]
Both estimates must include the exact prime, gamma/background, dual, and
regularized tail contributions in the same normalization as the local row
package.
\end{conjecture}
```

This is the precise unresolved analytic content. It is not supplied by local packet geometry, positive finite quadrature, ordinary Wronskians, or determinant nonvanishing.

## Agent 5 audit conclusion

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{S1/T1 are still open, but their correct formulation is now clean.}
}
\]

The critical repair is to make T1 a **weighted finite-jet transition theorem**. Without weighted norms, the transition route pays a determinant loss

\[
\mu^{-O(R^2)},
\]

which is likely fatal. With weighted norms, the loss is only

\[
\mu^{-O(R)},
\]

and since

\[
\mu\ge(\log Q)^{-C},
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this remains polynomial in \(Q\).

## Agent 5 continuation — deeper S1/T1 attack

I pushed the singular/transition branch further. The result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{S1 cannot be proved from local singular geometry alone.}
}
\]

There is a phase-relaxed anti-design countermodel. Therefore S1 must remain an **actual-zeta arithmetic nonrecurrence input** unless one proves a genuinely arithmetic exclusion theorem for the realized singular angles, weights, background, dual, and tail terms.

This matches the coordinator’s instruction: Agent 5’s job is to prevent the ordinary branch from silently ignoring singular/transition packets, prove or isolate S1/T1, and track whether transition losses are \(\mu^{-O(R)}\) or the fatal \(\mu^{-O(R^2)}\).

# 1. New structural finding: S1 has a phase-relaxed no-go

In the deep singular regime,

\[
\mu:=\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

S1 asks for

\[
\left|\mathbf P_R-\mathbf G_R-\mathbf T_R\right|_2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Equivalently, the actual packet must not realize

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

But local singular geometry alone cannot exclude this. If the background term vanishes, or is ignored, then a symmetric phase configuration

\[
(\theta_j,w_j),\quad (-\theta_j,w_j)
\]

gives

\[
w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+w_j\sin(-k\theta_j)=0
\]

for every \(k\). Thus

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)=0
\qquad
\text{for all }k.
\]

So finite sine-moment anti-designs are not forbidden by the singular coordinate system itself. They are forbidden only if the **actual zeta arithmetic** prevents the realized packet from approaching that anti-design variety.

This is the key reduction.

---

# 2. Exact LaTeX insertion: S1 no-go / reduction

Insert immediately after the current definition:

```latex
\begin{definition}[S1: Singular explicit-formula anti-design exclusion]
...
\end{definition}
```

add:

```latex
\begin{remark}[S1 is not a local singular-geometry theorem]
\label{rem:S1-not-local-singular-geometry}
The S1 lower bound
\[
\left|\mathbf P_R-\mathbf G_R-\mathbf T_R\right|_2\ge Q^{-A}
\]
cannot be proved from the finite singular coordinate geometry alone.

Indeed, ignoring for the moment the actual arithmetic restrictions on the
angles and weights, a phase-relaxed singular packet with symmetric pairs
\[
(\theta_j,w_j),\qquad (-\theta_j,w_j)
\]
has
\[
w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+w_j\sin(-k\theta_j)=0
\]
for every \(k\).  Hence, when the normalized background vector vanishes, the
finite sine moments satisfy
\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)=0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3,
\]
exactly.

Thus S1 is not a consequence of positivity, finite quadrature, or the local
singular parametrization.  It is a genuine actual-zeta arithmetic
nonrecurrence assertion: the realized tuple
\[
\left((\theta_j,w_j)_j,\mathcal B_3,\ldots,\mathcal B_{R+3}\right)
\]
must avoid the anti-design tube
\[
\mathcal V_R(\varepsilon)
:=
\left\{
\left|
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}
\right|_2
\le \varepsilon
\right\}
\]
with \(\varepsilon=Q^{-A}\).

Consequently, any proof of S1 must use actual arithmetic information about the
zero/prime explicit-formula packet, the gamma/background term, the dual term,
and the regularized tail.  A phase-relaxed or purely local singular model can
only test the formulation; it cannot prove the lower bound.
\end{remark}
```

---

# 3. T1 refinement: use weighted transition jets, not determinant overlap

The transition region is

\[
(\log Q)^{-C}\lesssim \mu=\lambda Q\lesssim1.
\]

The correct transition object is not an unweighted determinant comparison between ordinary and singular charts. That loses

\[
\prod_{r=0}^{R}\mu^r=\mu^{R(R+1)/2},
\]

hence

\[
\mu^{-O(R^2)}.
\]

With

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\qquad
\mu\ge(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

this is super-polynomial and breaks the intended bookkeeping.

The correct object is the weighted transition jet

\[
\mathcal J_R^\tr(F_\lambda)
=
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)
\right)_{0\le r\le R},
\]

where

\[
F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x).
\]

For a packet frequency \(\log n\asymp Q\),

\[
\partial_x^r e^{i\lambda(\log n)x}
=
(i\lambda\log n)^r e^{i\lambda(\log n)x}
\asymp
\mu^r.
\]

So the factor \(\mu^{-r}\) exactly normalizes the transition derivative scale.

---

# 4. Exact LaTeX replacement for T1

Replace the current definition:

```latex
\begin{definition}[T1: Mild singular transition control]
...
\end{definition}
```

with:

```latex
\begin{definition}[T1: Weighted transition source observability]
\label{def:T1-weighted-transition-source-observability}
Set
\[
\mu:=\lambda Q,
\qquad
F_\lambda(x):=\lambda^3q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x).
\]
In the transition regime
\[
(\log Q)^{-C_\tr}\lesssim \mu\lesssim1,
\]
the T1 input is the weighted finite-jet lower bound
\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)
\right)_{0\le r\le R}
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A_\tr}.
}
\]
Equivalently, if
\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]
is expanded using the exact canonical explicit-formula decomposition, then the
transition packet cannot make all normalized packet moments
\[
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^r
\left[
\lambda^3q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x)
\right]_{x=0},
\qquad
0\le r\le R,
\]
simultaneously \(Q^{-A_\tr}\)-small.

This is a named actual-zeta input.  It is not supplied by the ordinary
Wronskian theorem, because that theorem is normalized for \(\mu\gtrsim1\).  It
is also not supplied by the deep singular anti-design theorem, because the
singular sine-moment chart is normalized for \(\mu\ll(\log Q)^{-C_\tr}\).
\end{definition}
```

# 5. Deterministic transition chart lemma

Insert after the new T1 definition:

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Weighted transition chart loss]
\label{lem:weighted-transition-chart-loss}
Let
\[
F_\lambda(x)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}a_n e^{i\lambda(\log n)x}
+
F_{\rm bg}(x)+F_{\rm tail}(x),
\]
where the active packet satisfies
\[
c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q.
\]
Set
\[
\tau_n:=\lambda\log n,
\qquad
\mu:=\lambda Q.
\]
Then
\[
\tau_n/\mu\in[c_-,c_+].
\]
For each \(0\le r\le R\),
\[
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^r e^{i\tau_nx}\big|_{x=0}
=
i^r(\tau_n/\mu)^r.
\]
Hence the weighted transition jet is a fixed-window moment vector in the
bounded frequency variable \(\tau_n/\mu\), rather than a degenerating moment
vector in \(\tau_n\).

Consequently, passage from the weighted transition jet to an unweighted
ordinary jet costs at most
\[
\mu^R
\]
at jet depth \(R\), not the determinant factor
\[
\mu^{R(R+1)/2}.
\]
In the transition range
\[
\mu\ge(\log Q)^{-C_\tr},
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]
one has
\[
\mu^R
\ge
(\log Q)^{-C_\tr R}
=
Q^{-O(1)}.
\]
Thus weighted transition transfer is compatible with fixed-polynomial Gate--1
bookkeeping.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The displayed identity
\[
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^r e^{i\tau_nx}\big|_{x=0}
=
i^r(\tau_n/\mu)^r
\]
is immediate.  Since \(\tau_n/\mu=(\log n)/Q\) stays in the fixed compact
interval \([c_-,c_+]\), the weighted jet uses a nondegenerating moment basis.

Recovering one unweighted derivative from the weighted jet costs only the
factor \(\mu^r\) for that derivative.  Taking the worst \(r\le R\) gives
\(\mu^R\).  By contrast, comparing full unweighted determinant charts across
all derivative levels \(0,\ldots,R\) multiplies the losses and gives
\[
\prod_{r=0}^R\mu^r=\mu^{R(R+1)/2}.
\]
The final estimate follows from
\[
\mu\ge(\log Q)^{-C_\tr},
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]
\end{proof}
```

---

# 6. Stronger routed theorem

Replace or strengthen the current routing theorem with:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Ordinary--transition--singular routed Gate--1 theorem]
\label{thm:ordinary-transition-singular-routed-gate-one}
Set
\[
\mu:=\lambda Q.
\]
Assume the following three branch inputs.

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Ordinary branch.}  If \(\mu\gtrsim1\), the ordinary inputs
O1--O3 hold for the full canonical source
\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

\item \textbf{Transition branch.}  If
\[
(\log Q)^{-C_\tr}\lesssim\mu\lesssim1,
\]
then T1 holds:
\[
\left\|
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^r
\left[
\lambda^3q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x)
\right]_{x=0}
\right)_{0\le r\le R}
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A_\tr}.
\]

\item \textbf{Deep singular branch.}  If
\[
\mu\ll(\log Q)^{-C_\tr},
\]
then S1 holds:
\[
\left|
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}
\right|_2
\ge Q^{-A_\sing},
\]
and the singular moment vector transfers to the normalized source jet with
finite-dimensional loss
\[
\|J_R^{\sing}(F_\lambda)\|
\ge
e^{-CR\log R}
\left|
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}
\right|_2
-
\operatorname{Err}_{R,\sing},
\]
where
\[
\operatorname{Err}_{R,\sing}
\le
\frac12e^{-CR\log R}Q^{-A_\sing}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Take
\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]
Then every admissible off-line packet interval satisfies Gate~1:
\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The ordinary branch is Theorem~\ref{thm:ordinary-gate-one-from-O1-O2-O3}.

In the transition branch, T1 gives
\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\mu^{-r}
\left|
\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)
\right|
\ge Q^{-A_\tr}.
\]
Therefore, for some \(r\le R\),
\[
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)|
\ge
\mu^rQ^{-A_\tr}
\ge
\mu^RQ^{-A_\tr}.
\]
Since
\[
\mu\ge(\log Q)^{-C_\tr},
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]
we have
\[
\mu^R\ge Q^{-O(1)}.
\]
Thus a usual unweighted finite source jet is \(Q^{-O(1)}\)-nonflat.  The
finite-jet-to-energy transfer gives
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B_\tr}|I_\rho|.
\]

In the deep singular branch, S1 and the singular transfer estimate give
\[
\|J_R^{\sing}(F_\lambda)\|
\ge
\frac12e^{-CR\log R}Q^{-A_\sing}.
\]
For
\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]
the loss satisfies
\[
e^{-CR\log R}=Q^{-O(1)}.
\]
So the singular source jet is also \(Q^{-O(1)}\)-nonflat.  Applying the
finite-jet-to-energy transfer gives Gate~1 in the deep singular branch.

The three alternatives cover all values of \(\mu=\lambda Q\).
\end{proof}
```

## Assistant (2026-04-27 18:35:48)

I’ll now test the weighted-moment route itself, not just the routing theorem. The question is whether compact-window moment theory can force T1, or whether T1 has the same anti-design pathology as S1.

The weighted moment test has a sharp failure mode: compact-window moments do not prevent finite anti-designs with complex weights. The actual issue is whether the zeta-generated coefficients can enter that anti-design tube at a routed packet center.

_Thought for 1m 25s_

## Agent 5 result — S1/T1 weighted observability

I executed the Agent 5 instruction: test whether T1 can be proved by weighted bounded-window moments, and determine whether S1/T1 are still independent actual-orbit anti-design exclusions. The coordinator’s target was explicitly the weighted transition jet

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(F_\lambda)
=
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)
\right)_{0\le r\le R},
\qquad
\mu=\lambda Q,
\]

with \(F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x)\), using the bounded variable \(\tau_n/\mu=(\log n)/Q\). 

## Conclusion

\[
\boxed{
\text{T1 cannot be proved from bounded-window moment theory alone.}
}
\]

The correct status is option **C**:

\[
\boxed{
\text{S1 and T1 remain independent actual-orbit anti-design exclusions.}
}
\]

Weighted moments repair the **conditioning problem**—they avoid the fatal \(\mu^{-O(R^2)}\) determinant loss—but they do **not** supply a lower bound. The missing ingredient is still an arithmetic nonrecurrence theorem for the actual zeta-generated coefficient orbit.

---

# 1. Exact weighted transition expansion

Let

\[
F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x),
\qquad
\mu=\lambda Q.
\]

Then

\[
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)
=
\lambda^3Q^{-r}\partial_m^rq''_{\can}(m_0).
\]

For a prime-side packet term

\[
a_n(m_0,\alpha)e^{i\lambda(\log n)x},
\qquad
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q,
\]

the weighted derivative gives

\[
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^r
\left[
a_n e^{i\lambda(\log n)x}
\right]_{x=0}
=
a_n i^r\left(\frac{\log n}{Q}\right)^r.
\]

Thus the transition jet is a bounded-window moment vector:

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
a_n(m_0,\alpha)
\left(
1,\,
i\xi_n,\,
(i\xi_n)^2,\,
\ldots,\,
(i\xi_n)^R
\right)
+
\mathcal B_R^{\mathrm{tr}},
\]

where

\[
\xi_n:=\frac{\log n}{Q}\in[c_-,c_+],
\]

and

\[
\mathcal B_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
\]

collects the weighted contributions from

\[
B_2+D_2+E_2
\]

and any nonlocal regularized tail terms.

This is the right normalization. It is stable. But it is not coercive.

---

# 2. Moment noncollapse fails in the phase-relaxed model

Here is the deterministic obstruction.

Let

\[
v_R(\xi):=(1,\xi,\xi^2,\ldots,\xi^R)\in\mathbb C^{R+1}.
\]

Choose \(R+2\) distinct points

\[
\xi_0,\ldots,\xi_{R+1}\in[c_-,c_+].
\]

Then the \(R+1\) by \(R+2\) matrix

\[
\left(\xi_j^r\right)_{0\le r\le R,\ 0\le j\le R+1}
\]

has a nontrivial kernel. Hence there exist coefficients \(c_j\), not all zero, such that

\[
\sum_{j=0}^{R+1}c_j\xi_j^r=0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\sum_{j=0}^{R+1}c_jv_R(\xi_j)=0.
\]

After inserting the harmless factors \(i^r\), this gives

\[
\sum_{j=0}^{R+1}c_j
\left(
1,\,
i\xi_j,\,
(i\xi_j)^2,\,
\ldots,\,
(i\xi_j)^R
\right)
=0.
\]

So a nonzero transition packet can have all weighted moments through order \(R\) equal to zero.

Therefore bounded-window moment theory alone cannot prove

\[
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}\|_2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

It only says the moments are well-conditioned **if the coefficient vector is known not to lie near the finite moment nullspace**. That non-nullspace assertion is exactly the missing actual-orbit arithmetic input.

---

# 3. Background/gamma/tail terms do not remove the obstruction

Including the full canonical object

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

changes the target vector but not the structure of the obstruction.

The weighted transition jet has the schematic form

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal M_R^{P}
+
\mathcal M_R^{D}
+
\mathcal M_R^{B}
+
\mathcal M_R^{E}.
\]

Here:

\[
\mathcal M_R^{P}
\]

is a bounded-window prime-log moment vector;

\[
\mathcal M_R^{D}
\]

is the folded/dual bounded-window moment vector, with its own phase relation;

\[
\mathcal M_R^{B}
\]

is a deterministic smooth gamma/background vector;

\[
\mathcal M_R^{E}
\]

is the regularized tail vector.

The transition anti-design condition is therefore

\[
\mathcal M_R^{P}
+
\mathcal M_R^{D}
+
\mathcal M_R^{B}
+
\mathcal M_R^{E}
\approx 0.
\]

The background and tail shift the anti-design target; they do not eliminate the finite moment nullspace. A proof of T1 must show that the **actual zeta orbit** does not realize this shifted cancellation.

So the exact missing theorem is not “moment noncollapse.” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual canonical transition anti-design exclusion.}
}
\]

---

# 4. S1 does not automatically imply T1 near the lower transition edge

The lower transition edge is

\[
\mu\sim(\log Q)^{-C}.
\]

At this edge, a chart-overlap theorem would be acceptable if it had loss

\[
\mu^{-O(R)}.
\]

Indeed, for

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

one has

\[
\mu^{-O(R)}
=
(\log Q)^{O(CR)}
=
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

But S1 and T1 live in different finite charts:

S1 uses singular sine moments

\[
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3},
\]

whereas T1 uses weighted prime-log moments

\[
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^r
\left[
\lambda^3q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x)
\right]_{x=0}
\right)_{0\le r\le R}.
\]

To derive T1 from S1, one would need a concrete overlap estimate of the form

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
A_{\mu,R}\mathcal S_R
+
\operatorname{Err}_{\mu,R},
\]

where

\[
\mathcal S_R
=
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3},
\]

with

\[
\sigma_{\min}(A_{\mu,R})\ge \mu^{O(R)}
\]

and

\[
\|\operatorname{Err}_{\mu,R}\|
\le
\frac12\mu^{O(R)}Q^{-A_{\mathrm{sing}}}.
\]

Then S1 would imply

\[
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}\|_2
\ge
Q^{-A_{\mathrm{sing}}-O(1)}.
\]

But the draft does not currently supply this overlap operator \(A_{\mu,R}\), its rank, or its error bound. Without that chart-compatibility theorem, S1 does not imply T1.

---

# 5. Exact missing theorem

The clean missing theorem should be named as follows.

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[T1: actual transition anti-design exclusion]
\label{hyp:T1-actual-transition-anti-design-exclusion}
Let
\[
\mu=\lambda Q,
\qquad
F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x),
\]
where
\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]
In the transition range
\[
(\log Q)^{-C_\tr}\le \mu\le 1,
\]
the actual canonical transition jet satisfies
\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)
\right)_{0\le r\le R}
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A_\tr}.
}
\]
Equivalently, the actual coefficient orbit generated by the prime,
dual, gamma/background, and regularized-tail terms avoids the shifted
finite moment anti-design tube
\[
\mathcal V_R^{\tr}(Q^{-A_\tr})
:=
\left\{
\left\|
\mathcal M_R^{P}
+
\mathcal M_R^{D}
+
\mathcal M_R^{B}
+
\mathcal M_R^{E}
\right\|_2
\le Q^{-A_\tr}
\right\}.
\]
\end{hypothesis}
```

And the S1 hypothesis should remain separate:

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[S1: actual singular anti-design exclusion]
\label{hyp:S1-actual-singular-anti-design-exclusion}
In the deep singular range
\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C_\tr},
\]
the actual singular packet satisfies
\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A_\sing}.
}
\]
This is an actual-zeta arithmetic input.  It is not implied by finite
singular geometry, because phase-relaxed symmetric configurations can cancel
all sine moments.
\end{hypothesis}
```

---

# 6. Conditional overlap theorem, if the paper wants an S1-to-T1 bridge

This is the strongest honest bridge statement:

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Conditional lower-edge transition from singular overlap]
\label{lem:conditional-lower-edge-transition-from-singular-overlap}
Assume that in the lower transition range
\[
\mu\asymp(\log Q)^{-C_\tr}
\]
there is a finite overlap operator \(A_{\mu,R}\) such that
\[
\mathcal J_R^{\tr}
=
A_{\mu,R}\mathcal S_R
+
\operatorname{Err}_{\mu,R},
\]
where
\[
\mathcal J_R^{\tr}
=
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)
\right)_{0\le r\le R}
\]
and
\[
\mathcal S_R
=
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}.
\]
Assume
\[
\sigma_{\min}(A_{\mu,R})\ge \mu^{C_1R}
\]
and
\[
\|\operatorname{Err}_{\mu,R}\|_2
\le
\frac12\mu^{C_1R}\|\mathcal S_R\|_2.
\]
Then S1 implies T1 at the lower transition edge, with polynomial loss:
\[
\|\mathcal J_R^{\tr}\|_2
\ge
Q^{-A_\sing-O(1)}.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
By the overlap formula,
\[
\|\mathcal J_R^{\tr}\|_2
\ge
\sigma_{\min}(A_{\mu,R})\|\mathcal S_R\|_2
-
\|\operatorname{Err}_{\mu,R}\|_2.
\]
The error assumption gives
\[
\|\mathcal J_R^{\tr}\|_2
\ge
\frac12\mu^{C_1R}\|\mathcal S_R\|_2.
\]
Using S1,
\[
\|\mathcal S_R\|_2\ge Q^{-A_\sing}.
\]
Since
\[
\mu\asymp(\log Q)^{-C_\tr},
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]
we have
\[
\mu^{C_1R}=Q^{-O(1)}.
\]
Therefore
\[
\|\mathcal J_R^{\tr}\|_2
\ge
Q^{-A_\sing-O(1)}.
\]
\end{proof}
```

This lemma is useful because it identifies exactly what is missing: the overlap operator \(A_{\mu,R}\), its singular-value bound, and the canonical error estimate.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 18:38:47)

_Thought for 1m 45s_

Continuing Agent 5. The instruction is to test whether T1 can actually be proved from weighted moments, and to treat S1 as actual singular anti-design exclusion rather than local geometry. 

## 1. T1 reduces to a finite moment anti-design problem

In transition,

\[
\mu=\lambda Q,\qquad (\log Q)^{-C}\le \mu\le 1,
\]

and

\[
F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x).
\]

For a packet term with

\[
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
\xi_n:=\frac{\log n}{Q}\in[c_-,c_+],
\]

the weighted jet gives

\[
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^r
\left(a_ne^{i\lambda(\log n)x}\right)_{x=0}
=
a_n i^r\xi_n^r.
\]

So the transition vector is

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
V_R a+b,
\]

where

\[
(V_Ra)_r=\sum_n a_n(i\xi_n)^r,\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

and \(b\) is the deterministic/regularized contribution from the other canonical pieces:

\[
b=b_{B_2}+b_{D_2}+b_{E_2}.
\]

Thus T1 is exactly

\[
\|V_Ra+b\|_2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Weighted normalization makes \(V_R\) stable as a **moment map**, but \(V_R\) has a huge kernel. So the question is not conditioning. The question is:

\[
a(m_0,\alpha)\notin -V_R^{-1}b+\ker V_R
\quad
\text{up to } Q^{-A}.
\]

That is an actual-orbit nonrecurrence statement.

---

## 2. Stronger no-go: polynomial-complexity transition anti-designs exist

The earlier no-go was just dimension-counting. We can strengthen it: exact transition anti-designs exist with only sub-polynomial coefficient complexity at the relevant depth

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Take \(R+2\) equally spaced points in the fixed interval \([c_-,c_+]\):

\[
\xi_j=c+jh,\qquad 0\le j\le R+1.
\]

Set

\[
c_j=(-1)^j\binom{R+1}{j}.
\]

Then the finite-difference identity gives

\[
\sum_{j=0}^{R+1}c_j \xi_j^r=0
\qquad
\text{for every }0\le r\le R.
\]

Therefore

\[
\sum_{j=0}^{R+1}c_j(1,i\xi_j,\ldots,(i\xi_j)^R)=0.
\]

The coefficient size is only

\[
\max_j |c_j|\le 2^{R+1}.
\]

Since

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we get

\[
2^R=\exp(O(R))=Q^{o(1)}.
\]

So this is not a pathological anti-design requiring enormous coefficients. It is a polynomial-bookkeeping-compatible obstruction.

Conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{bounded-window moment theory alone cannot prove T1.}
}
\]

It cannot even prove T1 after excluding huge coefficient ratios, because the kernel contains sub-polynomial-complexity vectors.

---

## 3. Background terms do not rescue T1

One might hope \(B_2+D_2+E_2\) shifts the target enough to destroy the anti-design. It does not, at the deterministic level.

For any vector \(b\in\mathbb C^{R+1}\) with polynomial size, one can choose \(R+1\) stable nodes \(\xi_j\in[c_-,c_+]\) and solve

\[
\sum_{j=0}^R c_j(i\xi_j)^r=-b_r,
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

The relevant Vandermonde inverse on a fixed compact interval has at worst

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))
\]

coefficient growth in the monomial basis. At the chosen depth,

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))
=
\exp\!\left(O\!\left(\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}\log\log Q\right)\right)
=
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Thus any polynomial-sized canonical background vector can be canceled in a phase-relaxed transition model by polynomial-sized coefficients.

So the canonical decomposition gives

\[
V_Ra+b
=
\mathcal M_R^P+\mathcal M_R^D+\mathcal M_R^B+\mathcal M_R^E,
\]

but local moment theory cannot prevent

\[
\mathcal M_R^P+\mathcal M_R^D+\mathcal M_R^B+\mathcal M_R^E\approx0.
\]

The missing content is specifically that the **actual** \(a_n(m_0,\alpha)\), generated by the prime/dual/gamma/tail orbit and constrained by the routed packet center, avoids this shifted affine anti-design tube.

---

## 4. Exact T1 reduction

Let

\[
\mathcal A_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(Q^{-A})
=
\left\{
a:
\|V_Ra+b\|_2\le Q^{-A}
\right\}.
\]

Then T1 is equivalent to

\[
a_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0,\alpha)\notin \mathcal A_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(Q^{-A})
\]

for every admissible transition packet.

More invariantly, let \(P_{\mathrm{row}}\) be the projection onto the row-space of \(V_R\). Choose any \(a_b\) with

\[
V_Ra_b=-b.
\]

Then

\[
V_Ra+b=V_R(a-a_b),
\]

so T1 follows from

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
a_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0,\alpha),
a_b+\ker V_R
\right)
\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

combined with the lower singular bound of \(V_R\) on its row-space. The latter is a stable finite-dimensional moment fact. The former is the arithmetic input.

So the clean formulation is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{T1 is actual transition anti-design avoidance for }
a_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0,\alpha).
}
\]

---

## 5. S1 is even more rigidly an anti-design exclusion

For S1, the target vector is

\[
\mathcal S_R
=
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}.
\]

Local sine geometry gives no lower bound.

If \(\mathcal B_k=0\), symmetric pairs

\[
(\theta,w),\qquad (-\theta,w)
\]

cancel exactly:

\[
w\sin(k\theta)+w\sin(-k\theta)=0
\]

for every \(k\).

Even if \(\mathcal B\neq0\), shifted anti-designs are still available in a phase-relaxed model. Choose \(R+1\) angles \(\theta_j\) where the sine-Vandermonde matrix

\[
\left(\sin(k\theta_j)\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}
\]

is invertible. Then solve

\[
\sum_j c_j\sin(k\theta_j)=-\mathcal B_k.
\]

If signs are an issue and positive weights are required, use the symmetry

\[
-c_j\sin(k\theta_j)=|c_j|\sin(k(-\theta_j))
\]

for negative \(c_j\). Thus signed coefficients can be represented by positive weights at reflected angles, provided the singular angular chart allows both signs.

Again the coefficient growth is finite-dimensional Vandermonde growth, at worst

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

So S1 is also not a finite geometry theorem. It is exactly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual singular packet avoids the shifted sine anti-design tube.}
}
\]

---

## 6. Lower-edge S1 \(\Rightarrow\) T1 remains conditional

Near

\[
\mu\sim(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

an S1-to-T1 bridge would be viable if one had a chart-overlap map

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
A_{\mu,R}\mathcal S_R+\mathrm{Err}_{\mu,R}
\]

with

\[
\sigma_{\min}(A_{\mu,R})\ge \mu^{O(R)}
\]

and

\[
\|\mathrm{Err}_{\mu,R}\|_2
\le
\frac12\mu^{O(R)}\|\mathcal S_R\|_2.
\]

Then

\[
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}\|_2
\ge
\frac12\mu^{O(R)}Q^{-A_{\mathrm{sing}}}.
\]

Since

\[
\mu\ge(\log Q)^{-C},
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we get

\[
\mu^{O(R)}=Q^{-O(1)}.
\]

So the loss is acceptable.

But the actual overlap map \(A_{\mu,R}\), its rank, and its canonical error bound are not currently proved. Without that map, S1 does not imply T1.

---

## 7. Final Agent 5 status

\[
\boxed{
\text{T1 weighted scaling is Green; T1 observability is Yellow/Red.}
}
\]

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
\text{T1 is not a bounded-moment theorem.}
}
\]

It is an actual-orbit avoidance theorem:

\[
\|V_Ra_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0,\alpha)+b_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0,\alpha)\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

And S1 is the singular analogue:

\[
\left\|
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The new useful fact is stronger than the prior no-go:

\[
\boxed{
\text{transition anti-designs exist with only }Q^{o(1)}
\text{ homogeneous coefficient complexity,}
}
\]

and shifted background cancellation costs only

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Therefore neither \(B_2\), nor the weighted normalization, nor finite moment conditioning can close T1. The missing theorem must use the actual prime-log/zeta orbit at the routed packet center.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 18:49:16)

I’ll treat this as a dimensional audit of Agent 5’s S1/T1 inputs, then test whether a high-dimensional repair remains compatible with the weighted transition scaling.

_Thought for 30s_

Agent 5 response to the new instruction: test S1/T1 under high-dimensional or family-valued observability. The coordinator’s key update is that low-dimensional pointwise Gate–1 inputs are statistically underpowered unless replaced by a higher-dimensional observable or by a new counter-random arithmetic theorem. 

## 1. T1 has the same dimension problem

Current weighted T1 observes

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(F_\lambda)
=
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)
\right)_{0\le r\le R},
\]

so its complex dimension is

\[
d_{\mathrm{T1}}=R+1
\asymp
\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

For a pointwise exclusion over roughly

\[
N(T)\asymp e^Q Q
\]

candidate zeros or packet centers, a random-vector union-bound heuristic says a \(d\)-complex-dimensional observable avoids a \(Q^{-A}\)-tube at all candidates only if

\[
N(T)\cdot Q^{-2Ad}\ll1.
\]

Taking logs gives

\[
Q+O(\log Q)-2Ad\log Q\ll -1,
\]

so one needs

\[
d\gtrsim \frac{Q}{\log Q}.
\]

But current T1 has only

\[
d_{\mathrm{T1}}\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\ll
\frac{Q}{\log Q}.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{T1 is dimensionally underpowered as a universal pointwise input.}
}
\]

The weighted normalization fixes conditioning, not dimension. It makes the moments stable in

\[
\xi_n=\frac{\log n}{Q},
\]

but it does not give enough independent coordinates to make pointwise anti-design exclusion plausible without a counter-random arithmetic theorem.

---

## 2. A dimension-sufficient T1 repair exists formally, but it stresses downstream transfer

The natural high-dimensional transition observable is

\[
\mathcal J_K^{\mathrm{tr}}(F_\lambda)
=
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)
\right)_{0\le r<K},
\]

with

\[
K\asymp \frac{Q}{\log Q}.
\]

For a packet term,

\[
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^r
\left(a_ne^{i\lambda(\log n)x}\right)_{x=0}
=
a_ni^r\left(\frac{\log n}{Q}\right)^r.
\]

So the high-dimensional transition vector remains a bounded-window moment system. In that sense, it is compatible with weighted scaling.

A more stable basis would use bounded orthogonal polynomials on \([c_-,c_+]\):

\[
G_\nu^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\sum_n a_n \Psi_\nu(\xi_n)+b_\nu,
\qquad
0\le \nu<K,
\]

where

\[
\xi_n=\frac{\log n}{Q}.
\]

Then the dimension-sufficient T1 replacement would be

\[
\sum_{\nu<K}|G_\nu^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0,\alpha)|^2
\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
K\asymp \frac{Q}{\log Q}.
\]

This fixes the dimension count.

However, if downstream requires converting this high-dimensional weighted object back into unweighted local derivatives, the lower transition edge becomes fatal. The conversion from weighted derivative \(r\) to unweighted derivative costs

\[
\mu^r.
\]

At depth

\[
K\asymp \frac{Q}{\log Q}
\]

and lower edge

\[
\mu\asymp(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

the loss is

\[
\mu^K
=
\exp\left(-C\frac{Q}{\log Q}\log\log Q\right).
\]

This is far smaller than any fixed power \(Q^{-A}\). Equivalently, the inverse loss

\[
\mu^{-K}
=
\exp\left(C\frac{Q\log\log Q}{\log Q}\right)
\]

is super-polynomial in \(Q\).

So high-dimensional weighted T1 is viable only if the downstream architecture accepts the family-valued observables directly as Gate–1 seeds. It cannot be naively compressed back into the old finite-\(R\) unweighted jet without losing the polynomial bookkeeping.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{high-dimensional T1 repair requires family-valued downstream compatibility.}
}
\]

---

## 3. S1 is also dimensionally underpowered as stated

Current S1 observes the sine-moment vector

\[
\mathcal S_R
=
\left(
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}.
\]

Its dimension is again

\[
d_{\mathrm{S1}}\asymp R
\asymp
\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

The same pointwise anti-design threshold applies. To exclude a \(Q^{-A}\)-tube at all relevant singular packets without a special arithmetic theorem, one needs roughly

\[
d_{\mathrm{S1}}\gtrsim \frac{Q}{\log Q}.
\]

So the current S1 vector is also dimensionally underpowered.

The dimension-sufficient singular replacement would be

\[
\mathcal S_K
=
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right)_{3\le k\le K+2},
\qquad
K\asymp\frac{Q}{\log Q}.
\]

But this again changes the nature of the input. The old finite singular anti-design exclusion was a low-dimensional moment condition. The repaired version is a high-dimensional sine-frame exclusion.

Hence:

\[
\boxed{
\text{S1 as stated is not dimensionally plausible as a universal pointwise exclusion.}
}
\]

It needs either:

\[
K\asymp\frac{Q}{\log Q}
\]

moments, or a counter-random arithmetic theorem saying the actual singular packet avoids low-dimensional anti-design tubes much better than random dimension counting predicts.

---

## 4. High-dimensional S1 \(\to\) T1 overlap is conditionally possible but not with the old finite-depth loss

Suppose one upgrades S1 to \(K\) sine moments and T1 to \(K\) weighted transition observables:

\[
K\asymp \frac{Q}{\log Q}.
\]

A lower-edge bridge would need

\[
\mathcal J_K^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
A_{\mu,K}\mathcal S_K+\mathrm{Err}_{\mu,K}
\]

with

\[
\sigma_{\min}(A_{\mu,K})\ge \mu^{O(K)}
\]

and

\[
\|\mathrm{Err}_{\mu,K}\|
\le
\frac12\mu^{O(K)}\|\mathcal S_K\|.
\]

But at

\[
\mu\asymp(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

the lower bound

\[
\mu^{O(K)}
=
\exp\left(-O\left(\frac{Q\log\log Q}{\log Q}\right)\right)
\]

is super-polynomially small in \(Q\). Therefore, if the final theorem needs a \(Q^{-A}\)-scale lower bound after transfer, this overlap is too lossy.

So the lower-edge S1-to-T1 bridge remains acceptable only for

\[
K=O(R)\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

At dimension-sufficient depth

\[
K\asymp\frac{Q}{\log Q},
\]

the bridge loses too much unless one proves a much better overlap bound, for example

\[
\sigma_{\min}(A_{\mu,K})\ge Q^{-O(1)}
\]

independent of the naive \(\mu^K\) scaling. That would be a serious new analytic theorem, not a bookkeeping detail.

---

## 5. Classification

### T1

\[
\boxed{
\text{T1 as currently stated is B/C.}
}
\]

More explicitly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{dimensionally underpowered; requires family-valued observability or a counter-random theorem.}
}
\]

A high-dimensional weighted T1 vector with

\[
K\asymp\frac{Q}{\log Q}
\]

is the natural repair, but it does not feed the old finite-\(R\) downstream machinery by ordinary derivative conversion.

### S1

\[
\boxed{
\text{S1 as currently stated is also B/C.}
}
\]

The sine vector has only \(R\) coordinates. A dimension-sufficient singular anti-design observable needs

\[
K\asymp\frac{Q}{\log Q}
\]

sine moments, or else S1 must be treated as a special actual-orbit counter-random theorem.

### S1 \(\Rightarrow\) T1 overlap

\[
\boxed{
\text{viable at low finite depth; not viable at dimension-sufficient depth by naive overlap.}
}
\]

The old loss

\[
\mu^{-O(R)}
\]

is acceptable for

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

but the dimension-sufficient replacement would incur

\[
\mu^{-O(K)}
=
\exp\left(O\left(\frac{Q\log\log Q}{\log Q}\right)\right),
\]

which is not polynomial in \(Q\).

---

## 6. Final Agent 5 verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{S1/T1 share Agent 1's dimension defect.}
}
\]

Weighted T1 solved the scaling defect, but not the dimensional defect.

The honest options are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Option 1: add a counter-random actual-orbit theorem for low-dimensional S1/T1;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Option 2: replace S1/T1 by high-dimensional family-valued observability;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Option 3: abandon pointwise S1/T1 and prove aggregate energy instead.}
}
\]

The cleanest mathematical classification is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{B: dimensionally underpowered and requiring family-valued observability,}
}
\]

with the caveat that, without downstream compatibility for the high-dimensional family, the current low-dimensional statements remain

\[
\boxed{
\text{C: independent counter-random arithmetic inputs.}
}
\]

_Thought for 45s_

Agent 5 — dimension-corrected S1/T1 route. I am following the latest coordinator prompt: finalize whether S1/T1 should remain low-dimensional counter-random hypotheses, be replaced by high-dimensional family observability, or be demoted as requiring a new architecture. 

## 1. T1 dimension threshold

Current T1 observes

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(F_\lambda)
=
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)
\right)_{0\le r\le R},
\qquad
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

So its complex dimension is

\[
d_{\mathrm{T1}}=R+1\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Assume the phase-relaxed model in which the actual transition vector behaves like a generic point in \(\mathbb C^d\). For a fixed polynomial lower threshold \(Q^{-A}\), the small-ball probability is approximately

\[
\Pr\{\|\mathcal J\|\le Q^{-A}\}\asymp Q^{-2Ad}
=
\exp(-2Ad\log Q).
\]

The number of candidate packet centers/zeros is on the order

\[
N(Q)\asymp e^Q Q.
\]

A union-bound scale requires

\[
e^Q Q\cdot Q^{-2Ad}\ll1,
\]

hence

\[
2Ad\log Q\gtrsim Q.
\]

Therefore the first plausible dimension scale is

\[
\boxed{
d\gtrsim \frac{Q}{\log Q}.
}
\]

Current T1 has

\[
d_{\mathrm{T1}}\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\ll
\frac{Q}{\log Q}.
\]

Thus the current T1 is dimensionally underpowered by a factor roughly

\[
\frac{Q/\log Q}{\log Q/\log\log Q}
=
\frac{Q\log\log Q}{(\log Q)^2}.
\]

So current finite-\(R\) T1 can only be retained as a **counter-random actual-orbit hypothesis**:

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(F_\lambda)\|_2\ge Q^{-A}
\quad
\text{at all admissible transition centers, despite } d\ll Q/\log Q.
}
\]

That is not a consequence of bounded-window moment theory.

---

## 2. High-dimensional weighted T1

The dimension-sufficient repair is to replace \(R\) by

\[
K\asymp \frac{Q}{\log Q}.
\]

The stable basis should not be raw monomials, since monomial conditioning becomes poor at degree \(K\). Use an orthonormal polynomial basis on the fixed window

\[
\xi=\frac{\log n}{Q}\in[c_-,c_+].
\]

Let \(\{\Psi_\nu\}_{0\le \nu<K}\) be orthonormal with respect to a fixed reference measure on \([c_-,c_+]\). Define

\[
G_\nu^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0,\alpha)
=
\sum_{n\in \mathcal B}
a_n(m_0,\alpha)\Psi_\nu(\xi_n)
+
b_\nu(m_0,\alpha),
\qquad
0\le \nu<K,
\]

where \(b_\nu\) collects the \(B_2,D_2,E_2\) canonical background/dual/tail contributions in the same basis.

The dimension-sufficient T1 replacement is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\nu<K}|G_\nu^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0,\alpha)|^2
\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
K\asymp \frac{Q}{\log Q}.
}
\]

This is the correct high-dimensional transition anti-design exclusion.

But it does **not** automatically imply the old scalar Gate–1 for \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\). The reason is scale loss. A weighted derivative coordinate of order \(r\) corresponds to an actual derivative multiplied by

\[
\mu^{-r}.
\]

Recovering the physical local source jet costs

\[
\mu^r.
\]

At the lower transition edge,

\[
\mu\asymp (\log Q)^{-C},
\]

and for dimension-sufficient depth

\[
K\asymp \frac{Q}{\log Q},
\]

the worst conversion loss is

\[
\mu^K
=
\exp\!\left(
-C\frac{Q}{\log Q}\log\log Q
\right),
\]

which is super-polynomially small in \(Q\).

Therefore high-dimensional weighted T1 certifies only:

\[
\boxed{
\text{high-dimensional transition packet non-anti-design energy,}
}
\]

not the current downstream scalar Gate–1 input, unless the downstream engine is redesigned to accept the whole family \(\{G_\nu^{\mathrm{tr}}\}_{\nu<K}\) directly.

This is the key point: high-dimensional T1 fixes the dimension count but breaks compatibility with the old finite-\(R\) scalar source route.

---

## 3. S1 dimension threshold

Current S1 observes

\[
\mathcal S_R
=
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}.
\]

Again,

\[
d_{\mathrm{S1}}\asymp R
\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

The same small-ball count applies. To exclude a \(Q^{-A}\)-anti-design tube pointwise over \(\asymp e^Q Q\) candidates without special arithmetic, one needs

\[
d_{\mathrm{S1}}\gtrsim \frac{Q}{\log Q}.
\]

So current S1 is also dimensionally underpowered.

The dimension-sufficient replacement is

\[
\mathcal S_K
=
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right)_{3\le k\le K+2},
\qquad
K\asymp\frac{Q}{\log Q}.
\]

But transferring \(K\)-many singular sine moments into transition or ordinary scalar Gate–1 has the same problem. Any chart-overlap estimate of the form

\[
\mathcal J_K^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
A_{\mu,K}\mathcal S_K+\mathrm{Err}_{\mu,K}
\]

with the natural lower singular scale

\[
\sigma_{\min}(A_{\mu,K})\gtrsim \mu^{O(K)}
\]

loses

\[
\mu^{O(K)}
=
\exp\!\left(
-O\!\left(\frac{Q\log\log Q}{\log Q}\right)
\right)
\]

near the lower transition edge. That loss is not polynomial in \(Q\). Hence high-dimensional S1 cannot feed the old finite-depth T1/Gate–1 route unless one proves a much stronger overlap theorem with polynomial singular-value control independent of the naive \(\mu^K\) scaling.

So current S1 has the same classification as T1:

\[
\boxed{
\text{low-dimensional S1 is a counter-random arithmetic input;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{dimension-sufficient S1 requires new downstream/family machinery.}
}
\]

---

## 4. Aggregate-energy alternative

There is one logical escape: abandon pointwise S1/T1 and prove aggregate energy over all routed centers.

A plausible aggregate target would be something like

\[
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
w(m_0)\,
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0)\|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}w(m_0),
\]

and similarly for singular packets. Such a statement might be accessible from mean-square or large-sieve methods because it no longer needs every individual center to avoid the anti-design tube.

But the current downstream contradiction is pointwise/local: each bad packet must route through Gate–1, then Gate–2, then row energy. An aggregate S1/T1 would require a new aggregate downstream theorem, roughly:

\[
\text{aggregate Gate–1 energy}
\Longrightarrow
\text{aggregate row-energy contradiction}.
\]

That theorem is not part of the current architecture. So aggregate energy is not a patch; it is a new proof architecture.

---

## 5. Final classification

### Low-dimensional S1/T1

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Counter-random hypotheses only.}
}
\]

They are mathematically clean but dimensionally implausible as consequences of generic moment theory:

\[
d\asymp R\ll Q/\log Q.
\]

Keeping them means explicitly assuming actual zeta packets avoid low-dimensional anti-design tubes much better than random dimension counting predicts.

### High-dimensional S1/T1

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Dimensionally plausible but downstream-incompatible with the current scalar route.}
}
\]

They require

\[
K\asymp Q/\log Q.
\]

They should be formulated in stable bases:

\[
\Psi_\nu(\log n/Q)
\]

for transition, and high sine harmonics for singular packets. But they certify family-valued packet observability, not directly the current scalar \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\) Gate–1 seed.

### Aggregate S1/T1

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Potentially plausible but requires a new aggregate downstream engine.}
}
\]

It avoids pointwise dimension pressure but no longer feeds the present local obstruction chain.

---

## 6. Agent 5 final recommendation

For the current paper architecture, the honest choice is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{keep low-dimensional S1/T1 only as explicit counter-random actual-orbit hypotheses.}
}
\]

Do **not** present them as consequences of weighted moments, bounded-window moment theory, sine geometry, or finite chart overlap.

For a future architecture, the correct replacement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{dimension-sufficient family-valued S1/T1 with }K\asymp Q/\log Q.
}
\]

But that replacement must come with a new downstream theorem showing how high-dimensional family observability certifies the same canonical scalar source

\[
u=q''_{\mathrm{can}},
\]

or else with a redesigned row-energy engine. Current D4 does not automatically process arbitrary high-dimensional observables.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 18:58:54)

_Thought for 14s_

Agent 5 response — pointwise vs aggregate S1/T1, per the latest coordinator instruction. The current premise is that low-dimensional S1/T1 are counter-random pointwise hypotheses, while high-dimensional S1/T1 are dimensionally plausible but do not feed the present scalar downstream route without new machinery. 

## 1. Aggregate transition input

Let \(\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}\) be the routed transition centers and

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0)
=
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^r
\left[
\lambda^3 q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
\right]_{x=0}
\right)_{0\le r\le R}.
\]

The aggregate replacement for pointwise T1 is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_0\in \mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
w(m_0)\,
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0)\|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in \mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}w(m_0).
}
\]

This is much more plausible than pointwise T1. Expanding the left side gives

\[
\sum_{r\le R}
\sum_{m_0}
w(m_0)
\left|
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
a_n(m_0)
i^r\left(\frac{\log n}{Q}\right)^r
+
b_r(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

Ignoring \(b_r\) for the moment, the main quadratic form is

\[
\sum_{n,n'}
\sum_{r\le R}
i^r(-i)^r
\left(\frac{\log n}{Q}\right)^r
\left(\frac{\log n'}{Q}\right)^r
\sum_{m_0}
w(m_0)a_n(m_0)\overline{a_{n'}(m_0)}.
\]

If the centers are sufficiently separated and the phases \(m_0\log(n/n')\) decorrelate, the off-diagonal terms should be smaller than the diagonal. That is exactly the kind of statement large-sieve technology can plausibly approach.

So aggregate T1 is not dimensionally absurd. It asks for average anti-design exclusion, not universal pointwise anti-design exclusion.

However, there are two necessary caveats.

First, lower bounds are harder than upper large-sieve bounds. A standard large sieve gives

\[
\sum_{m_0}
\left|
\sum_n c_ne^{im_0\log n}
\right|^2
\le
\text{controlled upper bound},
\]

whereas we need a **nontrivial lower bound** after adding dual, background, and tail terms. This requires diagonal mass plus off-diagonal control plus no aggregate cancellation against \(B_2+D_2+E_2\).

Second, the centers are not arbitrary sample points; they are routed transition centers tied to zeros or near-singular packets. Thus the needed large-sieve statement is zero-restricted:

\[
m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}},
\]

not a free interval average. That is still a serious arithmetic input, but it is less counter-random than pointwise T1.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{aggregate T1 is plausibly accessible, but not from a plain large-sieve upper bound alone.}
}
\]

It needs a zero-restricted lower large-sieve / second-moment theorem for the full canonical transition vector.

---

## 2. Aggregate singular input

For singular packets, let

\[
\mathcal S_R(m_0)
=
\left(
\sum_jw_j(m_0)\sin(k\theta_j(m_0))
+
\mathcal B_k(m_0)
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}.
\]

The aggregate S1 replacement is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
w(m_0)
\|\mathcal S_R(m_0)\|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}w(m_0).
}
\]

Expanding gives

\[
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
\sum_{m_0}
w(m_0)
\left|
\sum_jw_j(m_0)\sin(k\theta_j(m_0))
+
\mathcal B_k(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

This is also more plausible than pointwise S1. Phase-relaxed symmetric configurations can annihilate every sine moment at a single packet, but forcing that across many singular packets is much stronger. Orthogonality in \(k\), variation of \(\theta_j(m_0)\), and explicit-formula averaging may give aggregate energy.

But again, the issue is not pure sine orthogonality. The singular angles and weights are generated by actual zeta/prime data. The aggregate theorem must show that the routed singular packets do not, on average, land near the shifted sine anti-design variety.

A plausible analytic target is:

\[
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
w(m_0)
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
\left|
\sum_jw_j(m_0)\sin(k\theta_j(m_0))
\right|^2
\gg
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0}w(m_0)
\]

with the background vector handled by either orthogonality or an explicit cross-term estimate:

\[
2\Re
\sum_{m_0,k}
w(m_0)
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)
\right)
\overline{\mathcal B_k(m_0)}.
\]

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{aggregate S1 is also more plausible than pointwise S1, but it is still a zero-restricted anti-design average.}
}
\]

It is not a consequence of local sine geometry alone.

---

## 3. What downstream theorem would be needed?

The present downstream engine is pointwise:

\[
\text{Gate 1 at packet }m_0
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2 at }m_0
\Rightarrow
\text{row energy at }m_0.
\]

An aggregate S1/T1 statement gives instead

\[
\sum_{m_0}
w(m_0)\,\text{Gate1Energy}(m_0)
\ge
Q^{-A}\sum_{m_0}w(m_0).
\]

To use this, one needs an aggregate downstream theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_0}
w(m_0)\,\text{Gate1Energy}(m_0)
\gg Q^{-A}\sum w
\Longrightarrow
\sum_{m_0}
w'(m_0)\,\text{RowEnergy}(m_0)
\gg Q^{-B}\sum w'.
}
\]

Can the current Gate 2/D4/row mobility machinery be summed? Partially, but not automatically.

The linear pieces probably sum:

\[
L^2\text{-input real rigidity}
\]

is naturally compatible with aggregate energy if the hypotheses are stated in \(L^2\) form.

Carrier-quotient D4 is also local algebraic conversion, so if each packet lies in the same canonical scalar source regime and the Gram-good conditions hold uniformly, the conversion constants can be applied pointwise and summed.

The dangerous pieces are routing and thresholding. Current downstream likely uses implications of the form:

\[
\text{if packet is Gate1-good, then row-energy-good}.
\]

Aggregate Gate1 energy may be concentrated on a small subset of packets. That is acceptable only if the final contradiction needs aggregate row energy, not row energy at every packet.

So there are two possible aggregate downstream formulations.

### Version A: good-subset extraction

From aggregate Gate1,

\[
\sum w\mathcal E_1(m_0)\ge Q^{-A}\sum w,
\]

extract a subset

\[
\mathcal G
=
\{m_0:\mathcal E_1(m_0)\ge Q^{-A-C}\}.
\]

Then

\[
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal G}w(m_0)
\ge Q^{-C}\sum w(m_0),
\]

assuming a uniform upper bound

\[
\mathcal E_1(m_0)\le Q^C.
\]

Apply pointwise downstream only on \(\mathcal G\). This is the least disruptive aggregate repair.

But it only gives row energy on a positive polynomial-weight subset, not all routed packets.

### Version B: fully summed downstream

Prove directly:

\[
\sum w\mathcal E_1
\Rightarrow
\sum w\mathcal E_2
\Rightarrow
\sum w\mathcal E_{\mathrm{row}}.
\]

This is cleaner but requires rewriting Gate 2, wall escape, row mobility, and the final contradiction in aggregate form.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the current downstream can probably support good-subset extraction, but not a full aggregate proof without new statements.}
}
\]

---

## 4. Comparison of options

### Option A — retain low-dimensional S1/T1 as counter-random pointwise hypotheses

This is most compatible with the current architecture.

It preserves:

\[
\text{pointwise Gate 1}
\Rightarrow
\text{pointwise Gate 2}
\Rightarrow
\text{pointwise row energy}.
\]

But mathematically it is the least satisfying because it assumes exactly what the dimension count says should be rare only under a new actual-orbit theorem:

\[
d\asymp R\ll Q/\log Q.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{architecture-compatible but arithmetically strong/counter-random.}
}
\]

### Option B — high-dimensional family-valued S1/T1

This fixes the dimension count:

\[
K\asymp \frac{Q}{\log Q}.
\]

But it does not feed the present scalar \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\) downstream engine. The conversion loss near transition is

\[
\mu^K
=
\exp\left(
-O\left(\frac{Q\log\log Q}{\log Q}\right)
\right),
\]

which is super-polynomial.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{dimensionally plausible but downstream-incompatible unless the engine is redesigned.}
}
\]

### Option C — aggregate S1/T1

This is the best compromise.

It avoids pointwise dimension pressure and may be compatible with large-sieve/orthogonality technology. It also may feed the current downstream through good-subset extraction, provided the final contradiction only requires row energy on a polynomial-weight subset of routed packets.

The required new theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{aggregate Gate 1 energy on singular/transition packets}
\Rightarrow
\text{enough aggregate or subset row energy downstream}.
}
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{least incompatible with the current architecture, but still requires a new aggregate-routing theorem.}
}
\]

---

## 5. Recommendation

For S1/T1 specifically, the least incompatible formulation is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Option C: aggregate energy, with good-subset extraction.}
}
\]

I would not replace S1/T1 by high-dimensional family-valued observability unless the whole downstream engine is redesigned.

I would also avoid presenting low-dimensional S1/T1 as plausible consequences of moment theory. They should either be explicitly marked as counter-random actual-orbit hypotheses, or replaced by aggregate versions.

The clean final classification is:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{array}{ccl}
\text{low-dimensional pointwise S1/T1} &:& \text{architecture-compatible but counter-random},\\[2mm]
\text{high-dimensional S1/T1} &:& \text{dimensionally plausible but downstream-incompatible},\\[2mm]
\text{aggregate S1/T1} &:& \text{best next attack; needs aggregate downstream theorem}.
\end{array}
}
\]

For the current RH architecture, I recommend:

\[
\boxed{
\text{replace pointwise S1/T1 by aggregate S1/T1 plus good-subset downstream extraction.}
}
\]

That is the least damaging way to relieve the dimension defect without discarding the repaired canonical downstream route.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 19:02:06)

I’ll sharpen the aggregate route rather than restate the prior classification: write the exact aggregate inequalities, reduce them to Gram/large-sieve lower bounds, then identify which downstream implications can be summed without changing the engine.

_Thought for 32s_

Agent 5 response — aggregate S1/T1 and aggregate downstream compatibility. The prompt asks whether aggregate singular/transition energy can replace pointwise S1/T1, and whether that can still feed the repaired canonical downstream route. 

## 1. Aggregate transition theorem

The pointwise T1 statement is

\[
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0)\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

where

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0)
=
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^r
\left[
\lambda^3 q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
\right]_{x=0}
\right)_{0\le r\le R}.
\]

The aggregate replacement should be:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_0\in \mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m_0)\,
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0)\|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in \mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}\rho(m_0).
}
\]

Here \(\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}\) is the set of routed transition centers and \(\rho\) is a nonnegative localization weight.

For the prime-side contribution,

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0)
\sim
\left(
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
a_n(m_0)e^{im_0\log n}
i^r\left(\frac{\log n}{Q}\right)^r
\right)_{0\le r\le R}
+
\text{dual/background/tail}.
\]

Expanding the aggregate square gives a Gram form:

\[
\sum_{n,n'\in\mathcal B}
\left\langle v_R(\xi_n),v_R(\xi_{n'})\right\rangle
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m_0)
a_n(m_0)\overline{a_{n'}(m_0)}
e^{im_0\log(n/n')}
+
\text{canonical cross terms},
\]

where

\[
\xi_n=\frac{\log n}{Q},
\qquad
v_R(\xi)=(1,i\xi,\ldots,(i\xi)^R).
\]

So aggregate T1 reduces to a **zero-restricted lower large-sieve theorem**: the sample set \(\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}\) must make the exponential frame

\[
n\mapsto e^{im_0\log n}
\]

nondegenerate on average, after inserting the bounded-window moment features \(v_R(\xi_n)\) and the canonical dual/background/tail terms.

This is much more plausible than pointwise T1. Pointwise T1 asks every center to avoid a low-dimensional anti-design tube. Aggregate T1 only asks that the centers do not all lie in the anti-design tube on average.

But it is still not a standard large-sieve estimate. Standard large sieve gives upper bounds. We need a lower frame bound:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}\rho(m_0)
\left|
\sum_n c_n e^{im_0\log n}
\right|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\sum_n |c_n|^2
}
\]

for the relevant canonical coefficient class, plus control of the dual/background/tail cross terms.

That is the exact transition aggregate input.

---

## 2. Aggregate singular theorem

Pointwise S1 is

\[
\|\mathcal S_R(m_0)\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

where

\[
\mathcal S_R(m_0)
=
\left(
\sum_j w_j(m_0)\sin(k\theta_j(m_0))
+\mathcal B_k(m_0)
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}.
\]

The aggregate version is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m_0)
\|\mathcal S_R(m_0)\|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho(m_0).
}
\]

Expanding the main sine part gives

\[
\sum_{m_0}\rho(m_0)
\sum_{j,\ell}
w_j(m_0)\overline{w_\ell(m_0)}
K_R(\theta_j(m_0),\theta_\ell(m_0)),
\]

with finite sine kernel

\[
K_R(\theta,\phi)
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}\sin(k\theta)\sin(k\phi).
\]

This kernel is positive semidefinite as a Gram kernel of the sine-feature map

\[
\theta\mapsto(\sin(3\theta),\ldots,\sin((R+3)\theta)).
\]

So aggregate S1 asks that the actual singular packets are not, on average, arranged as shifted sine anti-designs.

This is again more plausible than pointwise S1. A single singular packet can be phase-relaxed into perfect cancellation by symmetric angle pairs. But requiring a positive fraction of routed singular packets to realize that anti-design is a much stronger condition.

Still, aggregate S1 is not local sine geometry. It needs an actual arithmetic averaging theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_0}
\rho(m_0)
\left\|
\left(
\sum_j w_j(m_0)\sin(k\theta_j(m_0))
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}
\right\|_2^2
}
\]

must dominate the background/cross terms involving \(\mathcal B_k(m_0)\).

The background terms are not harmless. The full square contains

\[
2\Re
\sum_{m_0,k}
\rho(m_0)
\left(
\sum_j w_j(m_0)\sin(k\theta_j(m_0))
\right)
\overline{\mathcal B_k(m_0)}
+
\sum_{m_0,k}\rho(m_0)|\mathcal B_k(m_0)|^2.
\]

So aggregate S1 must either show main sine energy dominates those cross terms, or include them inside the canonical aggregate vector from the start.

---

## 3. Good-subset extraction

The least disruptive way to feed aggregate S1/T1 into the existing downstream engine is not to rewrite all downstream lemmas in summed form. It is to extract a polynomial-weight good subset.

Let

\[
E_1(m_0)=\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0)\|_2^2
\]

or

\[
E_1(m_0)=\|\mathcal S_R(m_0)\|_2^2.
\]

Assume aggregate Gate–1:

\[
\sum_{m_0}\rho(m_0)E_1(m_0)
\ge
Q^{-A}\sum_{m_0}\rho(m_0),
\]

and a uniform upper bound

\[
E_1(m_0)\le Q^C.
\]

Define the good set

\[
\mathcal G
=
\{m_0:E_1(m_0)\ge \tfrac12 Q^{-A}\}.
\]

Then

\[
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal G}\rho(m_0)
\ge
Q^{-A-C-O(1)}
\sum_{m_0}\rho(m_0).
\]

So aggregate Gate–1 gives a polynomial-weight subset on which pointwise Gate–1 holds.

This is the cleanest bridge:

\[
\boxed{
\text{aggregate S1/T1}
\Rightarrow
\text{polynomial-weight good subset}
\Rightarrow
\text{pointwise downstream on that subset}.
}
\]

The price is that downstream row energy is obtained only on a polynomial-weight subset, not on every singular/transition packet.

So the final contradiction must tolerate losing a polynomial fraction of packet weight.

---

## 4. Which downstream pieces can be summed?

### Gate 2

Gate 2 is likely summable if its proof is genuinely \(L^2\)-input real rigidity:

\[
E_2(m_0)\ge Q^{-B}E_1(m_0)
\]

or an equivalent local inequality with uniform constants. Then summing gives

\[
\sum \rho E_2
\ge
Q^{-B}
\sum \rho E_1.
\]

If Gate 2 uses thresholded alternatives, then good-subset extraction is safer.

### Wall escape

Wall escape is usually pointwise and geometric. It can be applied on the extracted good subset if the Gram-good / wall-good hypotheses hold uniformly there.

A fully summed wall escape theorem would need to control packets near bad walls in aggregate. That is additional work. Good-subset extraction avoids most of it.

### Carrier-quotient D4

D4 is algebraic and local for the canonical scalar source

\[
u=q''_{\mathrm{can}}.
\]

If a center is good and lies in the canonical scalar regime, then D4 conversion applies pointwise. Therefore it also sums over the good subset:

\[
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal G}\rho(m_0)E_{\mathrm{row}}(m_0)
\ge
Q^{-B}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal G}\rho(m_0)E_2(m_0).
\]

The caveat is important: this works only if aggregate S1/T1 certifies the same canonical scalar source. It does not apply to arbitrary high-dimensional observables.

### Row mobility

Row mobility is the main downstream risk. If row mobility maps each good packet to a controlled neighboring row with bounded overlap, then it sums.

The needed condition is a bounded multiplicity estimate:

\[
\#\{m_0\in\mathcal G:\operatorname{Mob}(m_0)=r\}
\le Q^C
\]

or its weighted analogue. Then row energy on good packets transfers to aggregate row energy with only polynomial loss.

If row mobility requires every packet in a chain to be good, aggregate extraction may fail. Then a new summed mobility theorem is needed.

---

## 5. Where pointwise routing is essential

Pointwise routing is essential in three places:

1. **Branch classification:** each packet is ordinary, transition, or singular. Aggregate statements must be branch-specific.

2. **Local geometric hypotheses:** Gram-good, wall-good, and canonical-gauge hypotheses are local. Aggregate energy cannot be applied to packets outside those local hypotheses unless bad packets are separately shown negligible.

3. **Final contradiction:** if the final contradiction requires row energy at every routed packet, aggregate good-subset extraction is insufficient. If it requires total row energy above a threshold, extraction is enough.

Thus aggregate S1/T1 is compatible with the existing engine only if the final contradiction is aggregate or if a polynomial-weight good subset is enough.

---

## 6. Comparison of the three options

### A. Low-dimensional pointwise S1/T1

This preserves the current proof chain:

\[
\text{pointwise Gate 1}
\Rightarrow
\text{pointwise Gate 2}
\Rightarrow
\text{pointwise row energy}.
\]

But it is counter-random. Dimension is

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

where pointwise exclusion wants roughly

\[
Q/\log Q.
\]

So this option is architecture-compatible but arithmetically very strong.

### B. High-dimensional S1/T1

This repairs the dimension count with

\[
K\asymp Q/\log Q.
\]

But it does not feed the scalar \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\) downstream route. Near the lower transition edge the conversion loss is

\[
\mu^K
=
\exp\left(
-O\left(\frac{Q\log\log Q}{\log Q}\right)
\right),
\]

which is not polynomial.

So this option is dimensionally plausible but downstream-incompatible unless the downstream engine is rebuilt for source families.

### C. Aggregate S1/T1 plus good-subset extraction

This is the least incompatible option.

It avoids universal pointwise anti-design exclusion while preserving most of the repaired scalar downstream route. The needed new theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero-restricted aggregate lower large-sieve / anti-design energy}
}
\]

plus

\[
\boxed{
\text{good-subset downstream extraction with bounded row-mobility multiplicity}.
}
\]

This is still nontrivial, but it is less counter-random than pointwise low-dimensional S1/T1 and less disruptive than high-dimensional source-family redesign.

---

## Final Agent 5 recommendation

For singular/transition coverage, the best formulation is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{aggregate S1/T1 plus good-subset extraction}.
}
\]

The exact replacement inputs should be:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m_0)
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0)\|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}\rho(m_0)
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m_0)
\|\mathcal S_R(m_0)\|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho(m_0).
}
\]

Then prove:

\[
\boxed{
\text{aggregate Gate 1}
\Rightarrow
\text{polynomial-weight good subset}
\Rightarrow
\text{summed row energy through Gate 2/D4/mobility}.
}
\]

This is the least damaging modification to the current architecture. It avoids pretending that low-dimensional pointwise S1/T1 are moment-theoretic consequences, while still keeping the canonical scalar downstream engine mostly intact.
