## Assistant (2026-04-27 19:07:18)

I’ll treat the aggregate path as the fork candidate, not just as an S1/T1 patch. The key test is whether averaging turns the dimension defect from fatal into a polynomial loss.

_Thought for 14s_

Agent 5 — aggregate architecture as middle path. The assigned task is to test whether we can keep the canonical scalar downstream engine while replacing pointwise upstream Gate–1/S1/T1 with aggregate energy plus good-subset extraction. 

## 1. Aggregate ordinary Gate–1 is much more plausible than pointwise projection

The pointwise scalar projection theorem is

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Longrightarrow
\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X(m_0,\alpha)\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\|X(m_0,\alpha)\|^2.
\]

This is counter-random because

\[
\dim T_{\mathrm{can}}(E_Q)\asymp R
\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\qquad
\dim E_Q\asymp \frac{Q}{\log Q}.
\]

But aggregate projection has a different scale. For a random refined vector \(X\in E_Q\), the expected projection ratio is

\[
\mathbb E\frac{\|\Pi_{S_Q}X\|^2}{\|X\|^2}
=
\frac{\dim S_Q}{\dim E_Q}
\asymp
\frac{\log Q/\log\log Q}{Q/\log Q}
=
\frac{(\log Q)^2}{Q\log\log Q}
=
Q^{-1+o(1)}.
\]

That is polynomially small, not catastrophically small. Therefore an aggregate ordinary Gate–1 theorem of the form

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho(m_0)
\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X(m_0,\alpha)\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho(m_0)\|X(m_0,\alpha)\|^2
}
\]

is dimensionally plausible.

This is the key distinction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{pointwise low-dimensional projection is counter-random;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{aggregate low-dimensional projection has the correct polynomial scale.}
}
\]

So the aggregate path is not merely a patch for S1/T1. It may be the least disruptive repair for the ordinary branch too.

---

## 2. What analytic theorem would prove aggregate ordinary Gate–1?

Expand the aggregate ordinary energy. Schematically,

\[
T_{\mathrm{can}}X(m_0)
=
\left(
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
a_n \psi_\ell(\log n/Q)e^{im_0\log n}
\right)_{\ell\le R}
+
\text{dual/background/tail}.
\]

Then

\[
\sum_{m_0}
\rho(m_0)\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X(m_0)\|^2
\]

expands into

\[
\sum_{\ell\le R}
\sum_{n,n'}
a_n\overline{a_{n'}}
\psi_\ell(\xi_n)\overline{\psi_\ell(\xi_{n'})}
\sum_{m_0}
\rho(m_0)e^{im_0\log(n/n')}
+
\text{canonical cross terms},
\]

where

\[
\xi_n=\frac{\log n}{Q}.
\]

Thus the needed theorem is a **zero-restricted lower large-sieve/frame inequality**:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho(m_0)
\left|
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
c_n e^{im_0\log n}
\right|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}|c_n|^2
}
\]

for the canonical coefficient classes generated by \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\), including plus/dual coupling and background/tail shifts.

This is still a serious arithmetic estimate. But it is not the same as the impossible-looking pointwise projection theorem. It asks for average noncollapse over many zeros/centers, which is the natural setting for large-sieve or explicit-formula second-moment methods.

The hard part is that standard large sieve is usually an upper bound. Here we need a lower frame bound on a zero-restricted sampling set. That requires showing the Gram matrix

\[
G_{n,n'}
=
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho(m_0)e^{im_0\log(n/n')}
\]

is not too degenerate on the relevant canonical coefficient space.

So the aggregate ordinary input should be named:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero-restricted lower frame theorem for canonical prime-log packets.}
}
\]

---

## 3. Good-subset extraction

Assume aggregate ordinary Gate–1:

\[
\sum_{m_0}\rho(m_0)E_1(m_0)
\ge
\eta \sum_{m_0}\rho(m_0),
\qquad
\eta=Q^{-A},
\]

where

\[
E_1(m_0)=\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X(m_0)\|^2
\]

or the normalized ratio

\[
E_1(m_0)=
\frac{\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X(m_0)\|^2}{\|X(m_0)\|^2}.
\]

Assume a uniform upper bound

\[
0\le E_1(m_0)\le Q^C.
\]

Define

\[
\mathcal G
=
\{m_0:E_1(m_0)\ge \tfrac12 Q^{-A}\}.
\]

Then

\[
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal G}\rho(m_0)
\ge
\frac{\eta}{2Q^C}
\sum_{m_0}\rho(m_0)
=
Q^{-A-C-O(1)}
\sum_{m_0}\rho(m_0).
\]

So aggregate Gate–1 gives a polynomial-weight subset where pointwise Gate–1 holds.

This is enough if the downstream contradiction only needs polynomially many / polynomial-weight good packets.

It is not enough if the downstream proof requires every routed packet to be good.

---

## 4. Downstream on the good subset

### Gate 2

If Gate 2 is a local implication

\[
E_1(m_0)\ge Q^{-A}
\Longrightarrow
E_2(m_0)\ge Q^{-B},
\]

then it applies directly on \(\mathcal G\).

If Gate 2 is truly \(L^2\)-input rigidity, it may even be summable:

\[
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal G}\rho(m_0)E_2(m_0)
\ge
Q^{-B}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal G}\rho(m_0)E_1(m_0).
\]

Either way, good-subset extraction is compatible with Gate 2.

### Wall escape

Wall escape is local and geometric. It can be applied on \(\mathcal G\) provided the Gram-good / wall-good hypotheses hold there.

If some extracted good packets lie in wall-bad regions, one needs a branch-local bad-wall measure bound:

\[
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal G\cap \mathrm{WallBad}}\rho(m_0)
\le
\frac12
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal G}\rho(m_0).
\]

Without such a bound, aggregate routing can lose the good subset to bad walls.

### D4

Carrier-quotient D4 is local algebra for the canonical scalar source

\[
u=q''_{\mathrm{can}}.
\]

So D4 is compatible with good-subset extraction as long as aggregate Gate–1 certifies the same scalar source \(u\), not arbitrary high-dimensional observables.

On each good packet,

\[
E_2(m_0)\ge Q^{-B}
\Longrightarrow
E_{\mathrm{row}}(m_0)\ge Q^{-B'}
\]

in the carrier quotient. Summing over \(\mathcal G\) gives aggregate row energy with only polynomial loss.

### Row mobility

Row mobility is the main risk.

If row mobility maps each good packet to a row/target with bounded overlap,

\[
\#\{m_0\in\mathcal G:\operatorname{Mob}(m_0)=r\}
\le Q^C
\]

or weighted analogue, then summed row energy survives.

If row mobility requires contiguous chains of good packets, aggregate extraction is insufficient. A sparse polynomial-weight good subset may not contain chains.

Thus the necessary downstream add-on is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{bounded-overlap row mobility for good subsets.}
}
\]

or, if chains are essential,

\[
\boxed{
\text{density/spacing theorem for the extracted good subset.}
}
\]

---

## 5. Final contradiction

The aggregate path works only if the final contradiction is aggregate:

\[
\sum_{\text{rows}} \mathrm{RowEnergy}
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

conflicts with a global upper bound.

If the final contradiction is pointwise/topological and requires row energy at every routed packet, then aggregate Gate–1 cannot replace pointwise Gate–1.

So the proof needs a final-row contradiction of the form:

\[
\boxed{
\text{polynomial-weight many good packets}
\Longrightarrow
\text{too much total row energy}.
}
\]

This is plausible for an energy method. It is not plausible for a proof step that depends on every packet in a deterministic chain being active.

---

## 6. Comparison with Path A

Path A requires

\[
\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X(m_0)\|
\ge
Q^{-A}\|X(m_0)\|
\]

for every admissible zero or packet center. Random projection heuristics say this should fail often because

\[
\dim T_{\mathrm{can}}(E_Q)\ll \dim E_Q.
\]

The aggregate version only requires average projection energy:

\[
\sum \rho\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\sum \rho\|X\|^2.
\]

Random projection heuristics predict exactly such a lower bound at scale

\[
Q^{-1+o(1)}.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{aggregate ordinary Gate–1 is far more plausible than pointwise Path A.}
}
\]

It still requires a zero-restricted lower frame theorem, but that theorem is aligned with average zeta technology. The pointwise projection theorem is a new counter-random assertion.

---

## 7. Concrete aggregate theorem stack

The least incompatible middle path is:

### Theorem A: aggregate ordinary canonical Gate–1

\[
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho(m_0)
\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X(m_0)\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho(m_0)\|X(m_0)\|^2.
\]

### Theorem B: aggregate transition canonical Gate–1

\[
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m_0)
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0)\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m_0).
\]

### Theorem C: aggregate singular canonical Gate–1

\[
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m_0)
\|\mathcal S_R(m_0)\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m_0).
\]

### Theorem D: good-subset extraction

Aggregate Gate–1 plus uniform upper bounds gives a polynomial-weight subset \(\mathcal G\) where pointwise Gate–1 holds.

### Theorem E: good-subset downstream

On \(\mathcal G\),

\[
\text{Gate 1}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}
\Rightarrow
\text{D4 row energy}
\Rightarrow
\text{summed row-energy contradiction},
\]

with bounded row-mobility multiplicity.

This stack keeps the canonical scalar source and avoids high-dimensional source-family D4.

---

## Final recommendation

The aggregate path is the best middle path:

\[
\boxed{
\text{replace pointwise Gate–1/S1/T1 by aggregate canonical Gate–1 energy}
}
\]

plus

\[
\boxed{
\text{good-subset extraction and summed downstream row energy}.
}
\]

It is mathematically less incompatible with the dimension count than Path A, and less disruptive than full Path B source-family redesign.

The exact remaining hard theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero-restricted lower frame / lower large-sieve theorem}
}
\]

for the canonical prime-log packets sampled at the routed ordinary, transition, and singular centers.

This is still a major arithmetic input, but unlike the pointwise projection theorem, it has the correct dimensional scale.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 19:11:19)

I’ll give the branch-complete aggregate Gate–1 framework for Agent 5: precise ordinary-compatible transition/singular inputs, the lower-frame reductions, extraction, and whether the good subsets can be unified downstream.

_Thought for 15s_

Agent 5 — aggregate S1/T1 integration with ordinary aggregate Path C. The coordinator asks for branch-complete aggregate Gate–1 inputs covering ordinary, transition, and singular packets, with exact missing lower-frame theorems. 

## 1. Aggregate transition Gate–1

For a transition packet, set

\[
\mu=\lambda Q,\qquad
(\log Q)^{-C}\lesssim \mu\lesssim 1,
\]

and

\[
F_\lambda(x)
=
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x),
\qquad
q''_{\mathrm{can}}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

The weighted transition vector is

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0)
=
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)
\right)_{0\le r\le R}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal J_R^{P}
+
\mathcal J_R^{D}
+
\mathcal J_R^{B}
+
\mathcal J_R^{E}.
\]

For the prime packet,

\[
\mathcal J_R^{P}(m_0)
=
\left(
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
a_n(m_0)
i^r
\left(\frac{\log n}{Q}\right)^r
e^{im_0\log n}
\right)_{0\le r\le R}.
\]

The dual term \(D_2\) contributes a second folded packet with its AFE phase and weight. \(B_2\) is the gamma/background curvature vector. \(E_2\) is the regularized tail. None should be dropped or treated as merely diagnostic; the aggregate input must be stated for the full canonical vector.

The aggregate transition theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m_0)\,
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0)\|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m_0).
}
\]

This replaces pointwise T1. It avoids the low-dimensional pointwise anti-design problem by asking for average energy over routed transition centers.

---

## 2. Aggregate singular Gate–1

For a deep singular packet, retain the singular sine-moment vector

\[
\mathcal S_R(m_0)
=
\left(
\sum_j w_j(m_0)\sin(k\theta_j(m_0))
+
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}(m_0)
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}.
\]

Here

\[
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}
\]

is not just the gamma term. It should include the full canonical shifted target induced by the prime/zero-side singular expansion, gamma/background contribution, folded dual contribution, and regularized tail in the singular normalization.

The aggregate singular theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m_0)\,
\|\mathcal S_R(m_0)\|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m_0).
}
\]

The correct proof target is the full square

\[
\|\mathcal S_R\|^2
=
\left\|
\mathcal S_R^{\mathrm{main}}
+
\mathcal B_R^{\mathrm{can}}
\right\|^2,
\]

not merely the main sine energy. If one proves it by separating terms, the required estimate is

\[
\sum\rho\|\mathcal S_R^{\mathrm{main}}\|^2
+
2\Re\sum\rho
\langle
\mathcal S_R^{\mathrm{main}},
\mathcal B_R^{\mathrm{can}}
\rangle
+
\sum\rho\|\mathcal B_R^{\mathrm{can}}\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\sum\rho.
\]

So the cross term must be controlled. It is not harmless by default.

---

## 3. Lower-frame theorem for transition packets

The transition aggregate theorem reduces to a zero-restricted lower-frame estimate.

For a canonical coefficient family \(c_n(m_0)\), the model lower-frame statement is:

\[
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m_0)
\left|
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
c_n(m_0)e^{im_0\log n}
\right|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m_0)
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}|c_n(m_0)|^2.
\]

For the weighted transition vector, the coefficient family is enlarged by the bounded moment features

\[
\psi_r(n)=i^r\left(\frac{\log n}{Q}\right)^r,
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

Thus the needed theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m_0)
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
c_n(m_0)
\psi_r(n)
e^{im_0\log n}
+
\mathrm{dual/background/tail}_r(m_0)
\right|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0}\rho(m_0).
}
\]

This is a lower large-sieve theorem at zero-restricted routed centers. Standard large-sieve upper bounds do not imply it. The required analytic content is lower-frame nondegeneracy of the Gram matrix

\[
G_{n,n'}
=
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m_0)e^{im_0\log(n/n')},
\]

after insertion of the transition features \(\psi_r\) and canonical AFE weights.

---

## 4. Lower-frame theorem for singular packets

The singular aggregate theorem reduces to lower-frame nondegeneracy of the sine-feature map

\[
\theta
\mapsto
(\sin(3\theta),\ldots,\sin((R+3)\theta)).
\]

The kernel is

\[
K_R(\theta,\phi)
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
\sin(k\theta)\sin(k\phi).
\]

The main singular energy is

\[
\sum_{m_0}
\rho(m_0)
\sum_{j,\ell}
w_j(m_0)\overline{w_\ell(m_0)}
K_R(\theta_j(m_0),\theta_\ell(m_0)).
\]

The missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m_0)
\left\|
\left(
\sum_jw_j(m_0)\sin(k\theta_j(m_0))
+
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}(m_0)
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}
\right\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0}\rho(m_0).
}
\]

Again, this is not local sine geometry. A single packet can be an anti-design. The aggregate theorem must assert that routed singular packets do not land near the shifted anti-design variety on average.

---

## 5. Good-subset extraction for transition/singular branches

For either branch, let

\[
E_1(m_0)
=
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0)\|^2
\]

or

\[
E_1(m_0)
=
\|\mathcal S_R(m_0)\|^2.
\]

Assume

\[
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C}
\rho(m_0)E_1(m_0)
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C}\rho(m_0),
\]

and a uniform upper bound

\[
E_1(m_0)\le Q^C.
\]

For a threshold

\[
\theta=\frac12Q^{-A},
\]

define

\[
\mathcal G
=
\{m_0\in\mathcal C:E_1(m_0)\ge\theta\}.
\]

Then

\[
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal G}\rho(m_0)
\ge
Q^{-A-C-O(1)}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C}\rho(m_0).
\]

So aggregate transition or singular Gate–1 yields a polynomial-weight subset on which pointwise Gate–1 holds.

The upper bound \(E_1\le Q^C\) is necessary. Without it, aggregate energy could be concentrated on too few packets.

---

## 6. Can ordinary, transition, and singular good subsets be unified?

Yes, but only after branch routing.

Let

\[
\mathcal C
=
\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}
\sqcup
\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}
\sqcup
\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}.
\]

Each branch has its own energy:

\[
E_{\mathrm{ord}}(m_0)
=
\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X(m_0)\|^2,
\]

\[
E_{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0)
=
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m_0)\|^2,
\]

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m_0)
=
\|\mathcal S_R(m_0)\|^2.
\]

The branch-complete aggregate Gate–1 theorem is:

\[
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho E_{\mathrm{ord}}
+
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho E_{\mathrm{tr}}
+
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho E_{\mathrm{sing}}
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_0\in\mathcal C}\rho.
\]

Or, stronger and cleaner, require each branch separately:

\[
\sum_{\mathcal C_b}\rho E_b
\ge
Q^{-A}\sum_{\mathcal C_b}\rho
\qquad
b\in\{\mathrm{ord},\mathrm{tr},\mathrm{sing}\}.
\]

Then extract branch-specific good subsets

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{ord}},
\qquad
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{tr}},
\qquad
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{sing}}.
\]

Set

\[
\mathcal G
=
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{ord}}
\cup
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{tr}}
\cup
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{sing}}.
\]

This gives a routed good subset of polynomial total weight.

However, the downstream proof remains branch-aware at the first step:

- ordinary packets use ordinary Gate–1;
- transition packets use weighted transition Gate–1;
- singular packets use singular anti-design Gate–1.

After each branch has produced the canonical scalar Gate–1 seed for

\[
u=q''_{\mathrm{can}},
\]

the downstream chain can be unified:

\[
\text{Gate 1}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}
\Rightarrow
\text{wall escape}
\Rightarrow
\text{D4}
\Rightarrow
\text{row mobility}.
\]

The condition “canonical scalar Gate–1 seed” is essential. If transition/singular aggregate observables certify only branch-specific family energy and do not transfer to \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\), they cannot be merged into the scalar downstream engine.

---

## 7. Branch-complete aggregate framework

The least incompatible branch-complete Path C is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Ordinary aggregate lower frame}
}
\]

\[
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho\|X\|^2.
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Transition aggregate lower frame}
}
\]

\[
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}\rho.
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Singular aggregate lower frame}
}
\]

\[
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho\|\mathcal S_R\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho.
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Uniform upper bounds}
}
\]

\[
E_b(m_0)\le Q^C
\qquad
b\in\{\mathrm{ord},\mathrm{tr},\mathrm{sing}\}.
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Good-subset extraction}
}
\]

Each branch yields a polynomial-weight good subset.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Branch-to-canonical transfer}
}
\]

Transition and singular good packets must certify the same canonical scalar source \(u=q''_{\mathrm{can}}\), not merely branch-local family observables.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Good-subset downstream}
}
\]

On the union good subset, Gate 2, wall escape, D4, and row mobility are applied with polynomial bounded-overlap losses.

---

## Final Agent 5 verdict

Aggregate S1/T1 can be integrated with the ordinary aggregate path, but only in the following form:

\[
\boxed{
\text{branch-specific aggregate lower-frame theorems}
}
\]

plus

\[
\boxed{
\text{good-subset extraction}
}
\]

plus

\[
\boxed{
\text{branch-to-canonical scalar Gate–1 transfer}.
}
\]

The exact missing inputs are:

1. zero-restricted aggregate lower-frame theorem for ordinary canonical packets;
2. zero-restricted aggregate lower-frame theorem for transition weighted jets;
3. zero-restricted aggregate lower-frame theorem for singular sine moments with canonical background;
4. uniform polynomial upper bounds for branch energies;
5. good-subset downstream with bounded bad-wall loss and bounded row-mobility overlap.

This is substantially more plausible than pointwise low-dimensional S1/T1, and it preserves the repaired scalar downstream engine better than high-dimensional source-family Path B.

Agent 5 — branch-complete aggregate Gate–1 framework for Stack C2. I’m following the latest instruction: ordinary, transition, and singular branches must all feed the same scalar canonical downstream source \(u=q''_{\mathrm{can}}\), or else they do not preserve the repaired D4/Gate–2 engine. 

## 1. Ordinary branch

The ordinary aggregate Gate–1 input should be stated as

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho(m)\,
\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X(m)\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho(m)\,
\|X(m)\|^2.
}
\]

Here:

\[
X(m)
\]

is the dimension-sufficient refined canonical cell vector, and

\[
T_{\mathrm{can}}X(m)
\]

is the current finite-row canonical projection that produces the ordinary scalar Gate–1 seed for

\[
u=q''_{\mathrm{can}}.
\]

The missing theorem is a zero-restricted lower-frame theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho(m)
\left|
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
b_n n^{-im}
\right|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}\rho(m)
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}|b_n|^2
}
\]

for the canonical coefficient class seen by \(T_{\mathrm{can}}\), including the plus/folded-dual packet weights and finite-row symbols.

This is not the old pointwise projection theorem. It is an average lower sampling theorem. Its expected scale is polynomial because the visible projection ratio is roughly

\[
\frac{R}{Q/\log Q}
=
Q^{-1+o(1)}.
\]

So the ordinary aggregate theorem is dimensionally plausible.

---

## 2. Transition branch

In the transition range,

\[
(\log Q)^{-C}\lesssim \mu=\lambda Q\lesssim1,
\]

define

\[
F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x),
\]

and the weighted transition vector

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m)
=
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)
\right)_{0\le r\le R}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal J_R^{B_2}
+
\mathcal J_R^{P_2}
+
\mathcal J_R^{D_2}
+
\mathcal J_R^{E_2}.
\]

For a prime-side packet term,

\[
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^r
\left[
a_ne^{i\lambda(\log n)x}
\right]_{x=0}
=
a_ni^r
\left(\frac{\log n}{Q}\right)^r.
\]

Thus the transition vector is a bounded-window moment vector in

\[
\xi_n=\frac{\log n}{Q}.
\]

The aggregate transition Gate–1 theorem should be

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m)
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m)\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m).
}
\]

The missing theorem is again a zero-restricted lower-frame theorem, now for vector-valued bounded-window moments:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m)
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
a_n(m)i^r\left(\frac{\log n}{Q}\right)^r n^{-im}
+
\mathrm{dual}_r(m)
+
\mathrm{bg}_r(m)
+
\mathrm{tail}_r(m)
\right|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}\rho.
}
\]

The full canonical vector must be used. Treating \(B_2\), \(D_2\), or \(E_2\) as optional diagnostics would reintroduce the old proxy problem.

The important point is that this aggregate theorem does certify the scalar source \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\), because \(\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}\) is built directly from local derivatives of

\[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x).
\]

So transition aggregate Gate–1 is downstream-compatible.

---

## 3. Singular branch

For deep singular packets, the canonical singular vector should be

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_R(m)
=
\left(
\sum_j w_j(m)\sin(k\theta_j(m))
+
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}(m)
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}.
}
\]

The background term

\[
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}
\]

must include every canonical contribution in the singular normalization: gamma/background, prime-side singular correction, folded dual contribution, and regularized tail.

The aggregate singular Gate–1 theorem should be

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
\|\mathcal S_R(m)\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m).
}
\]

Expanding,

\[
\|\mathcal S_R\|^2
=
\left\|
\mathcal S_R^{\mathrm{main}}
+
\mathcal B_R^{\mathrm{can}}
\right\|^2.
\]

So a proof must control

\[
\sum\rho\|\mathcal S_R^{\mathrm{main}}\|^2,
\]

the cross term

\[
2\Re
\sum\rho
\left\langle
\mathcal S_R^{\mathrm{main}},
\mathcal B_R^{\mathrm{can}}
\right\rangle,
\]

and

\[
\sum\rho\|\mathcal B_R^{\mathrm{can}}\|^2.
\]

The missing theorem is an aggregate anti-design exclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{routed singular packets do not, on average, lie near the shifted sine anti-design variety.}
}
\]

A single singular packet can be a phase-relaxed anti-design. The aggregate theorem asserts that this cannot happen on average over the routed singular set.

The singular branch is downstream-compatible only if the singular vector transfers to the canonical scalar Gate–1 seed for \(u=q''_{\mathrm{can}}\). Thus one still needs a branch-to-canonical transfer estimate:

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathcal S_R(m)\|^2\ge Q^{-A}
\Longrightarrow
\text{canonical scalar Gate--1 for }q''_{\mathrm{can}}\text{ at }m.
}
\]

If \(\mathcal S_R\) merely certifies a singular model observable unrelated to \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\), it cannot feed D4.

---

## 4. Branchwise good-subset extraction

For each branch \(b\in\{\mathrm{ord},\mathrm{tr},\mathrm{sing}\}\), write its energy as

\[
E_b(m).
\]

So

\[
E_{\mathrm{ord}}(m)
=
\frac{\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X(m)\|^2}{\|X(m)\|^2},
\]

\[
E_{\mathrm{tr}}(m)
=
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m)\|^2,
\]

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
=
\|\mathcal S_R(m)\|^2.
\]

Assume

\[
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_b}
\rho(m)E_b(m)
\ge
Q^{-A_b}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_b}\rho(m),
\]

and

\[
0\le E_b(m)\le Q^{C_b}.
\]

Then the good set

\[
\mathcal G_b
=
\{m\in\mathcal C_b:E_b(m)\ge \tfrac12Q^{-A_b}\}
\]

satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal G_b}\rho(m)
\ge
Q^{-A_b-C_b-O(1)}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_b}\rho(m).
}
\]

Thus each branch produces a polynomial-weight pointwise-good subset.

Set

\[
\mathcal G
=
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{ord}}
\cup
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{tr}}
\cup
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{sing}}.
\]

This is the routed good subset for downstream.

---

## 5. Can the three branches use one downstream theorem?

Yes, after branch-to-canonical transfer.

The downstream theorem should not care how Gate–1 was obtained. It should require only:

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical scalar Gate--1 for }u=q''_{\mathrm{can}}
}
\]

plus pointwise O2/O3 or extracted aggregate O2/O3 on the same subset.

Thus the branch-specific stage is:

\[
\mathcal G_b
\Longrightarrow
\text{canonical scalar Gate--1 at }m.
\]

After that, all branches feed the same downstream chain:

\[
\text{Gate--1}
\Longrightarrow
\text{Gate--2}
\Longrightarrow
\text{wall escape}
\Longrightarrow
\text{carrier-quotient D4}
\Longrightarrow
\text{row mobility}.
\]

The transition branch is naturally compatible because \(\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}\) is literally a weighted jet of \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\).

The ordinary branch is compatible by definition.

The singular branch is the one that needs the most explicit transfer lemma from singular sine moments to canonical scalar Gate–1.

---

## 6. Exact missing theorem package for Agent 5 branch coverage

The branch-complete aggregate package is:

### Ordinary lower-frame theorem

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho
\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho
\|X\|^2.
}
\]

### Transition lower-frame theorem

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho.
}
\]

### Singular lower-frame theorem

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho
\|\mathcal S_R\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho.
}
\]

### Uniform upper bounds

\[
\boxed{
E_b(m)\le Q^C
\quad
\text{for }
b\in\{\mathrm{ord},\mathrm{tr},\mathrm{sing}\}.
}
\]

### Branch-to-canonical transfer

\[
\boxed{
m\in\mathcal G_b
\Longrightarrow
\text{canonical scalar Gate--1 for }q''_{\mathrm{can}}.
}
\]

### Good-subset downstream

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal G
\Longrightarrow
\sum_{\mathrm{row\ targets}}
\mathrm{RowEnergy}
\ge
Q^{-C}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal G}\rho(m),
}
\]

assuming bad-wall/bad-Gram loss and row-mobility overlap are polynomially controlled.

## Final Agent 5 conclusion

Path C is branch-complete if and only if the following three aggregate lower-frame theorems are proved:

\[
\mathrm{AggG1}_{\mathrm{ord}},
\qquad
\mathrm{AggG1}_{\mathrm{tr}},
\qquad
\mathrm{AggG1}_{\mathrm{sing}}.
\]

The ordinary and transition branches already certify the scalar canonical source \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\). The singular branch still needs an explicit transfer from the sine-moment vector to canonical scalar Gate–1.

The least-compatible missing theorem is therefore not pointwise S1/T1. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero-restricted aggregate lower-frame theory for all routed branches}
}
\]

plus

\[
\boxed{
\text{branch-to-canonical transfer for singular packets}.
}
\]

Once those hold, the three branch-good subsets can be unified and sent through the same repaired scalar downstream engine.

_Thought for 14s_

Continuing Agent 5. I am attacking the remaining weak point in the branch-complete aggregate framework: **singular branch-to-canonical transfer**. The previous Stack C2 direction requires aggregate ordinary/transition/singular Gate–1 plus good-subset extraction, but singular packets still need a deterministic transfer from sine moments to scalar canonical Gate–1 for \(u=q''_{\mathrm{can}}\). 

## 1. Target transfer

The singular aggregate input is

\[
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)\|\mathcal S_R(m)\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho(m),
\]

where

\[
\mathcal S_R(m)
=
\left(
\sum_j w_j(m)\sin(k\theta_j(m))
+
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}(m)
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}.
\]

Good-subset extraction gives a polynomial-weight set where

\[
\|\mathcal S_R(m)\|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

To feed downstream, we need

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathcal S_R(m)\|\ge Q^{-A}
\Longrightarrow
\text{canonical scalar Gate--1 for }u=q''_{\mathrm{can}}.
}
\]

Equivalently, for the singular local scale

\[
m=m_0+\lambda x,
\]

we need a lower bound like

\[
\int_{|x|\le c}
\left|
\lambda^3 q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
\right|^2dx
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

This would produce scalar Gate–1 after rescaling.

---

## 2. Deterministic transfer is plausible if \(\mathcal S_R\) is truly a coefficient vector

Assume the singular normal form has the structure

\[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
S_k(m_0)\Phi_k(x)
+
\operatorname{Rem}_R(x;m_0),
\]

where

\[
S_k(m_0)
=
\sum_jw_j(m_0)\sin(k\theta_j(m_0))
+
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}(m_0).
\]

Let

\[
S=(S_3,\ldots,S_{R+3}).
\]

If the finite system

\[
\{\Phi_3,\ldots,\Phi_{R+3}\}
\]

has a quantitative lower frame on the fixed singular window \([-c,c]\),

\[
\int_{-c}^{c}
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\Phi_k(x)
\right|^2dx
\ge
e^{-C R\log R}\|S\|^2,
\]

and the remainder satisfies

\[
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R\|_{L^2[-c,c]}
\le
\frac12 e^{-C R\log R/2}\|S\|,
\]

then

\[
\int_{-c}^{c}
\left|
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
\right|^2dx
\ge
\frac14 e^{-C R\log R}\|S\|^2.
\]

Since

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we have

\[
e^{-C R\log R}=Q^{-O(1)}.
\]

Thus

\[
\|S\|\ge Q^{-A}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\int_{-c}^{c}
\left|
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
\right|^2dx
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

So the singular transfer is **deterministic Green** if these two facts hold:

\[
\boxed{
\text{coefficient normal form with }S_k\text{ as actual coefficients;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite basis lower frame }e^{-O(R\log R)}.
}
\]

This is good: no new zeta arithmetic is needed for this part once the singular expansion is exact.

---

## 3. Where transfer can fail

There are three possible failure modes.

### Failure 1: \(\mathcal S_R\) is not the actual coefficient vector

If the singular vector is only a diagnostic moment vector and not the coefficient vector of the local expansion of

\[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}},
\]

then

\[
\|\mathcal S_R\|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

does not imply scalar source energy.

This would be fatal for Stack C2, because D4 consumes the scalar source

\[
u=q''_{\mathrm{can}},
\]

not an abstract singular sine vector.

So the singular branch must define \(\mathcal S_R\) by the actual canonical local expansion, not by a proxy zero-side moment model.

### Failure 2: basis conditioning worse than \(e^{-O(R\log R)}\)

If the lower frame constant for \(\Phi_k\) is

\[
e^{-O(R^2)}
\]

or worse, then at

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

the loss is

\[
\exp\left(-O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{(\log\log Q)^2}\right)\right),
\]

which is super-polynomial in \(Q^{-1}\). That breaks the fixed-polynomial bookkeeping.

So the transfer requires a Chebyshev/Markov/Riesz-type finite-frame estimate with only

\[
e^{-O(R\log R)}
\]

loss.

This is plausible for classical finite analytic bases on a fixed interval, but must be checked for the actual singular basis \(\Phi_k\).

### Failure 3: remainder is not half-leading

The expansion must have a remainder satisfying

\[
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R\|_{L^2}
\le
\frac12
\left\|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\Phi_k
\right\|_{L^2}.
\]

A mere absolute bound

\[
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R\|_{L^2}\le Q^{-A}
\]

is not enough unless it is smaller than the extracted singular good-set threshold after frame loss.

Thus the singular route needs a **relative half-leading remainder bound**, not only formal asymptotics.

---

## 4. Finite-frame lemma for the singular basis

If

\[
\Phi_k(x)=\sin(k\Theta(x))
\]

with \(\Theta\) real-analytic and monotone on the singular window, then the lower frame is straightforward.

Let

\[
y=\Theta(x),
\]

with

\[
0<c_0\le \Theta'(x)\le C_0.
\]

Then

\[
\int_{-c}^{c}
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\sin(k\Theta(x))
\right|^2dx
\asymp
\int_{\Theta(-c)}^{\Theta(c)}
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\sin(ky)
\right|^2dy.
\]

If the image interval has fixed positive length, the finite trigonometric system has a lower Riesz bound

\[
\int_I
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\sin(ky)
\right|^2dy
\ge
e^{-C R}\|S\|^2
\]

for a nondegenerate interval \(I\). Even a cruder polynomial-exponential estimate

\[
e^{-C R\log R}
\]

is acceptable.

So if the singular basis is genuinely trigonometric after analytic coordinate change, conditioning is not the blocker.

If instead \(\Phi_k\) are nearly collinear in the deep singular limit, then conditioning may deteriorate like \(e^{-O(R^2)}\). That would require renormalizing the singular vector or choosing a different basis.

---

## 5. Aggregate singular theorem becomes clean after transfer

With deterministic transfer, the aggregate singular route is:

\[
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho\|\mathcal S_R\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho
\]

plus upper bound

\[
\|\mathcal S_R(m)\|^2\le Q^C
\]

implies a good set

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{sing}}
=
\{m:\|\mathcal S_R(m)\|^2\ge Q^{-A'}\}
\]

of polynomial weight.

On \(\mathcal G_{\mathrm{sing}}\), deterministic transfer gives

\[
\int_{I_m}|q''_{\mathrm{can}}(t)|^2dt
\ge Q^{-B}|I_m|.
\]

Then the same downstream engine applies.

Thus singular Stack C2 does not require pointwise S1. It requires:

\[
\boxed{
\text{aggregate singular lower-frame}
}
\]

plus

\[
\boxed{
\text{deterministic singular coefficient-to-energy transfer}.
}
\]

That is the correct separation of arithmetic and deterministic work.

---

## 6. Interaction with transition lower edge

The singular-to-transition overlap is no longer strategically necessary if both branches have their own aggregate lower-frame theorems.

Previously we needed S1 \(\Rightarrow\) T1 near

\[
\mu\asymp(\log Q)^{-C}
\]

to avoid gaps. Under Stack C2, we can avoid that by using branch-specific aggregate inputs:

\[
\mathrm{AggG1}_{\mathrm{sing}}
\quad\text{for deep singular},
\]

\[
\mathrm{AggG1}_{\mathrm{tr}}
\quad\text{for transition}.
\]

The only requirement is that the branch partition has bounded overlap or clean coverage:

\[
\mathcal C
=
\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}
\sqcup
\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}
\sqcup
\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}
\]

up to polynomially negligible boundary packets.

So the old lower-edge overlap map is no longer a main blocker. It becomes a boundary convenience theorem.

---

## 7. Updated Agent 5 status

The singular branch has a clearer route than before:

\[
\boxed{
\text{arithmetic part: aggregate singular anti-design lower-frame;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{deterministic part: singular coefficient vector transfers to scalar }q''_{\mathrm{can}}\text{ energy.}
}
\]

The deterministic transfer is plausible and should be attacked directly through:

1. exact singular normal form for \(\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}\);
2. proof that \(\mathcal S_R\) is the actual coefficient vector;
3. lower Riesz bound for the singular basis with loss \(\le e^{-O(R\log R)}\);
4. relative half-leading remainder bound.

The most important new conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Stack C2 does not need S1}\Rightarrow\text{T1 overlap if singular and transition aggregates are proved separately.}
}
\]

So Agent 5’s next mathematical target would be the deterministic singular transfer lemma, not more anti-design heuristics.

Agent 5 — branch-complete Stack C2 with singular transfer. The assigned focus is aggregate ordinary/transition/singular Gate–1, and especially whether the singular vector gives deterministic scalar-source energy for \(u=q''_{\mathrm{can}}\). 

## 1. Ordinary branch

The ordinary aggregate input is:

\[
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho(m)|T_{\mathrm{can}}X_{\mathrm{can}}(m)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho(m)|X_{\mathrm{can}}(m)|^2.
\]

This is an **actual-coefficient** theorem, not a universal lower sampling theorem. The ordinary branch should not claim a lower frame for every Dirichlet packet in the band, because adversarial packets can concentrate in sampling gaps. The correct target is lower sampling for the actual canonical packet produced by

\[
q''_{\mathrm{can}}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

If \(\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}\) has large gaps, those gaps must either be negligible under \(\rho\), or covered by \(\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}\cup\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}\). Thus the branch-complete coverage condition is:

\[
\mathcal C
=
\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}
\cup
\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}
\cup
\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}},
\]

up to \(Q^{-A}\)-negligible weight, with no large unsampled region left outside all three branches.

---

## 2. Transition branch

Define

\[
\mu=\lambda Q,
\qquad
F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x),
\]

and

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m)
=
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)
\right)_{0\le r\le R}.
\]

The transition aggregate input is:

\[
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m)\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m)\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m).
\]

This branch is automatically scalar-source compatible because \(\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}\) is a weighted jet of the actual scalar function

\[
q''_{\mathrm{can}}.
\]

The only deterministic transfer needed is the finite-jet-to-local-energy lemma:

if

\[
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m)\|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

then

\[
\int_{|x|\le c}
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)|^2\,dx
\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

provided the weighted transition jet basis has polynomial conditioning on the transition window. That conditioning is precisely why we use

\[
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^r
\]

rather than raw derivatives.

So transition is structurally Green after its aggregate lower-frame theorem.

---

## 3. Singular branch: deterministic transfer lemma

Assume a singular local expansion of the form

\[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k(m_0)\Phi_k(x)
+
\operatorname{Rem}_R(x;m_0),
\]

where

\[
S_k(m_0)
=
\sum_jw_j(m_0)\sin(k\theta_j(m_0))
+
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}(m_0).
\]

Let

\[
S(m_0)=(S_3,\ldots,S_{R+3}).
\]

The deterministic transfer theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\|S(m_0)\|\ge Q^{-A}
\Longrightarrow
\int_{|x|\le c}
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)|^2dx
\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This follows from two finite analytic facts.

First, a lower Riesz bound:

\[
\int_{|x|\le c}
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\Phi_k(x)
\right|^2dx
\ge
\kappa_R\|S\|^2,
\]

with

\[
\kappa_R\ge e^{-C R\log R}.
\]

Second, a relative remainder bound:

\[
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R(\cdot;m_0)\|_{L^2[-c,c]}
\le
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}\|S(m_0)\|.
\]

Then

\[
\begin{aligned}
\|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}\|_{L^2[-c,c]}
&\ge
\left\|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\Phi_k
\right\|_{L^2}
-
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R\|_{L^2} \\
&\ge
\kappa_R^{1/2}\|S\|
-
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}\|S\| \\
&=
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}\|S\|.
\end{aligned}
\]

Squaring gives

\[
\int_{|x|\le c}
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)|^2dx
\ge
\frac14\kappa_R\|S\|^2.
\]

Since

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we have

\[
e^{-C R\log R}=Q^{-O(1)}.
\]

Thus

\[
\|S\|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

implies scalar source energy at polynomial scale.

So the singular transfer is deterministic, not arithmetic, **if** \(S_k\) are genuinely the coefficients of the canonical local expansion and not merely diagnostic sine moments.

---

## 4. Conditioning of the singular basis

If

\[
\Phi_k(x)=\sin(k\Theta(x))
\]

with \(\Theta\) real analytic and monotone on \([-c,c]\), and

\[
0<c_0\le |\Theta'(x)|\le C_0,
\]

then the Riesz bound is plausible.

Changing variables

\[
y=\Theta(x)
\]

gives

\[
\int_{-c}^{c}
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\sin(k\Theta(x))
\right|^2dx
\asymp
\int_{\Theta(-c)}^{\Theta(c)}
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\sin(ky)
\right|^2dy.
\]

For a fixed interval \(I=\Theta([-c,c])\) of positive length, finite trigonometric systems satisfy a lower bound of the type

\[
\int_I
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\sin(ky)
\right|^2dy
\ge
e^{-CR}\|S\|^2,
\]

or at worst

\[
e^{-CR\log R}\|S\|^2
\]

under rougher analytic-basis estimates.

That is acceptable.

The dangerous case is when the singular coordinate degenerates so that

\[
|\Theta([-c,c])|\to0
\]

or the functions \(\Phi_k\) become nearly collinear. Then the lower frame constant may fall like

\[
e^{-CR^2}
\]

or worse. That would be fatal because

\[
e^{-CR^2}
=
\exp\!\left(
-O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{(\log\log Q)^2}\right)
\right)
\]

is super-polynomial in \(Q^{-1}\).

Thus the exact conditioning requirement is:

\[
\boxed{
\kappa_R(\Phi_3,\ldots,\Phi_{R+3};[-c,c])
\ge e^{-O(R\log R)}.
}
\]

---

## 5. Half-leading remainder is the real deterministic audit

The transfer does not require a new arithmetic theorem, but it does require a strong remainder estimate.

An absolute asymptotic statement like

\[
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R\|_{L^2}\le Q^{-A}
\]

is insufficient unless the extracted singular threshold is known to be much larger than this after frame loss.

The needed estimate is relative:

\[
\boxed{
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R\|_{L^2}
\le
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}\|S\|.
}
\]

Equivalently, after good-subset extraction gives

\[
\|S\|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

it is enough to prove

\[
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R\|_{L^2}
\le Q^{-A-C}
\]

with \(C\) large enough to dominate the frame loss. But the relative version is cleaner and more robust.

This is the exact singular deterministic audit:

\[
\boxed{
\text{coefficient identity}
+
\text{Riesz lower bound}
+
\text{half-leading remainder}.
}
\]

---

## 6. Branch union and downstream compatibility

After branchwise extraction, we get

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{ord}},
\qquad
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{tr}},
\qquad
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{sing}}.
\]

For ordinary packets, Gate–1 is already scalar canonical.

For transition packets, \(\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}\) is a weighted jet of \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\), so finite-jet-to-energy transfer gives scalar canonical Gate–1.

For singular packets, the transfer lemma above gives scalar canonical Gate–1.

Thus on

\[
\mathcal G
=
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{ord}}
\cup
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{tr}}
\cup
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{sing}},
\]

all branches feed the same downstream theorem:

\[
\text{scalar canonical Gate--1 for }q''_{\mathrm{can}}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate--2}
\Rightarrow
\text{wall escape}
\Rightarrow
\text{carrier-quotient D4}
\Rightarrow
\text{row mobility}.
\]

The downstream no longer needs to know which branch produced Gate–1.

_Thought for 15s_

Agent 5 — branch-to-canonical transfer layer.

The instruction is to finish the deterministic transfer layer: ordinary, transition, and singular good packets must all become **scalar canonical Gate–1** packets for

\[
u=q''_{\mathrm{can}},
\]

otherwise they cannot feed the repaired Gate–2/D4 downstream engine. 

## 1. Ordinary branch

This branch is already scalar-canonical.

The ordinary good packet is defined by

\[
\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X_{\mathrm{can}}(m)\|\ge Q^{-A}\|X_{\mathrm{can}}(m)\|,
\]

where \(T_{\mathrm{can}}\) is the finite-row map built from the actual canonical source

\[
q''_{\mathrm{can}}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

So no additional branch-to-source transfer is needed. The only ordinary-side issues remain aggregate lower sampling and O2/O3/wall eligibility.

---

## 2. Transition branch: weighted jet-to-energy transfer

In transition,

\[
\mu=\lambda Q,
\qquad
(\log Q)^{-C}\lesssim \mu\lesssim1,
\]

and

\[
F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x).
\]

The transition observable is

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m)
=
\left(
\mu^{-r}F_\lambda^{(r)}(0)
\right)_{0\le r\le R}.
\]

Assume

\[
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m)\|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Then for some \(r\le R\),

\[
|F_\lambda^{(r)}(0)|
\ge
\mu^r Q^{-A}
\ge
\mu^R Q^{-A}.
\]

Since

\[
\mu\ge(\log Q)^{-C},
\qquad
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we have

\[
\mu^R
\ge
Q^{-O(1)}.
\]

Thus

\[
|F_\lambda^{(r)}(0)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

Now use a finite analytic jet-to-energy inequality. If \(F_\lambda\) is generated by canonical transition packets whose local \(x\)-frequencies are bounded by \(O(1)\), and the smooth background/tail terms satisfy the same derivative bounds, then for every \(r\le R\),

\[
|F_\lambda^{(r)}(0)|^2
\le
\exp(O(R\log R))
\int_{|x|\le c}|F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\int_{|x|\le c}|F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
\ge
\exp(-O(R\log R))
|F_\lambda^{(r)}(0)|^2.
\]

Since

\[
\exp(-O(R\log R))=Q^{-O(1)},
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m)\|\ge Q^{-A}
\Longrightarrow
\int_{|x|\le c}
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)|^2\,dx
\ge Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

So the transition branch is deterministic Green once the weighted jet is defined for the full canonical object. The weighted normalization is essential; without it, the lower-edge factor \(\mu^R\) is lost incorrectly.

---

## 3. Singular branch: coefficient-to-energy transfer

Assume the singular canonical local expansion

\[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k(m_0)\Phi_k(x)
+
\operatorname{Rem}_R(x;m_0),
\]

where

\[
S(m_0)=(S_3,\ldots,S_{R+3})
\]

is the singular vector extracted by the branch theorem.

The desired transfer is

\[
\|S(m_0)\|\ge Q^{-A}
\Longrightarrow
\int_{|x|\le c}
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)|^2\,dx
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

This follows from two deterministic estimates.

First, a lower Riesz bound for the singular basis:

\[
\int_{|x|\le c}
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\Phi_k(x)
\right|^2dx
\ge
\kappa_R\|S\|^2,
\]

with

\[
\kappa_R\ge \exp(-O(R\log R)).
\]

Second, a half-leading remainder bound:

\[
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R(\cdot;m_0)\|_{L^2[-c,c]}
\le
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}\|S(m_0)\|.
\]

Then

\[
\begin{aligned}
\|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}\|_{L^2[-c,c]}
&\ge
\left\|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\Phi_k
\right\|_{L^2}
-
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R\|_{L^2} \\
&\ge
\kappa_R^{1/2}\|S\|
-
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}\|S\|\\
&=
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}\|S\|.
\end{aligned}
\]

Squaring,

\[
\int_{|x|\le c}
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)|^2dx
\ge
\frac14\kappa_R\|S\|^2.
\]

Since

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\qquad
\kappa_R\ge e^{-O(R\log R)}=Q^{-O(1)},
\]

we get the required polynomial lower bound.

Thus singular transfer is deterministic if, and only if, the singular vector is the actual coefficient vector of the canonical expansion and the remainder is half-leading.

---

## 4. Basis audit: when the Riesz bound is available

If

\[
\Phi_k(x)=\sin(k\Theta(x))
\]

with \(\Theta\) real analytic and monotone on \([-c,c]\), and

\[
0<c_0\le |\Theta'(x)|\le C_0,
\]

then change variables

\[
y=\Theta(x).
\]

The Riesz problem becomes

\[
\int_I
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\sin(ky)
\right|^2dy
\ge
\kappa_R\|S\|^2,
\]

where \(I=\Theta([-c,c])\) has fixed positive length.

For a fixed nondegenerate interval \(I\), finite trigonometric polynomials have a lower restriction bound of the form

\[
\kappa_R\ge e^{-CR}
\]

or, with rougher analytic distortion and nonorthogonal normalization,

\[
\kappa_R\ge e^{-CR\log R}.
\]

Both are acceptable.

The transfer fails if the singular coordinate degenerates so that

\[
|I|\to0
\]

or the functions \(\Phi_k\) become nearly collinear. Then one may get

\[
\kappa_R\le e^{-cR^2},
\]

which is too small, because

\[
e^{-cR^2}
=
\exp\!\left(
-c\frac{(\log Q)^2}{(\log\log Q)^2}
\right)
\]

is super-polynomially small.

So the exact basis condition is:

\[
\boxed{
\kappa_R(\Phi_3,\ldots,\Phi_{R+3};[-c,c])
\ge e^{-O(R\log R)}.
}
\]

---

## 5. Coefficient identity audit

The major remaining singular issue is not the Riesz bound. It is the identity

\[
S_k(m_0)
=
\text{actual coefficient of }\Phi_k
\text{ in the local expansion of }
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}.
\]

If instead

\[
S_k
=
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}
\]

is only a diagnostic sine moment, then

\[
\|S\|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

does not imply anything about the scalar source. It could certify energy in a proxy model while the actual canonical source cancels.

Therefore the exact missing identity is:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
\left(
\sum_jw_j(m_0)\sin(k\theta_j(m_0))
+
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}(m_0)
\right)
\Phi_k(x)
+
\operatorname{Rem}_R(x;m_0).
}
\]

This must include all canonical pieces:

\[
B_2,\quad P_2,\quad D_2,\quad E_2.
\]

No zero-side-only or \(B_2\)-only version is sufficient.

---

## 6. BranchToCanonical theorem

The deterministic transfer layer can now be summarized as:

\[
\boxed{
m\in
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{ord}}
\cup
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{tr}}
\cup
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{sing}}
\Longrightarrow
\text{scalar canonical Gate--1 for }q''_{\mathrm{can}}.
}
\]

With branch hypotheses:

### Ordinary

\[
\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X_{\mathrm{can}}(m)\|\ge Q^{-A}\|X_{\mathrm{can}}(m)\|.
\]

Already scalar-canonical.

### Transition

\[
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m)\|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Transfer by weighted jet-to-energy.

### Singular

\[
\|S(m)\|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Transfer by coefficient identity, Riesz lower bound, and half-leading remainder.

Then all branches feed the same downstream chain:

\[
\text{canonical scalar Gate--1}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate--2}
\Rightarrow
\text{wall/D4}
\Rightarrow
\text{row mobility}.
\]

---

The branch-to-canonical layer is mathematically viable, with one unresolved singular audit:

\[
\boxed{
\text{verify the exact canonical singular expansion and half-leading remainder.}
}
\]

More explicitly, the unresolved deterministic singular tasks are:

\[
\boxed{

}

\kappa_R\ge e^{-O(R\log R)}
\text{ for the actual singular basis };
}

\boxed{
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R\|_{L^2}
\le
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}\|S\|.
}
\]

If those hold, aggregate singular good packets certify scalar \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\) energy and are compatible with corrected Stack C2.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 19:39:02)

I’ll now try to close the deterministic part as far as possible: prove a usable Riesz lower bound for the singular trigonometric basis, then isolate only the coefficient-identity/remainder audit.

_Thought for 25s_

Continuing Agent 5: deterministic singular transfer.

The useful progress is that the **basis-conditioning part is basically closable** under a mild nondegenerate trigonometric-coordinate hypothesis. The remaining hard deterministic audit is the **coefficient identity** and the **relative remainder bound**. This is exactly the branch-to-canonical issue in the latest Stack C2 setup. 

## 1. Riesz lower bound for the singular sine basis

Assume the singular basis has the form

\[
\Phi_k(x)=\sin(k\Theta(x)),
\qquad 3\le k\le R+3,
\]

on a fixed window

\[
x\in[-c,c],
\]

where \(\Theta\) is real \(C^1\), monotone, and satisfies

\[
0<a\le |\Theta'(x)|\le A<\infty.
\]

Let

\[
I=\Theta([-c,c]).
\]

Then \(|I|\asymp 1\). For

\[
P(y)=\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\sin(ky),
\]

we have

\[
\int_{-c}^{c}
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\sin(k\Theta(x))
\right|^2dx
\asymp
\int_I |P(y)|^2dy.
\]

So the task reduces to proving

\[
\int_I |P(y)|^2dy
\ge
e^{-C R}\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}|S_k|^2.
\]

This is true by a standard finite trigonometric Remez argument.

Let

\[
N=R+3.
\]

On the full circle,

\[
\int_0^{2\pi}|P(y)|^2dy
=
\pi\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}|S_k|^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\|P\|_{L^\infty(\mathbb T)}
\ge
c\|S\|_2.
\]

A trigonometric Remez inequality gives

\[
\|P\|_{L^\infty(\mathbb T)}
\le
C_I^N
\|P\|_{L^\infty(I)},
\]

where \(C_I\) depends only on the fixed interval length \(|I|\). Hence

\[
\|P\|_{L^\infty(I)}
\ge
C_I^{-N}c\|S\|_2.
\]

Let \(M=\|P\|_{L^\infty(I)}\), attained at some \(y_0\in I\). Bernstein’s inequality gives

\[
\|P'\|_{L^\infty(\mathbb T)}
\le
N\|P\|_{L^\infty(\mathbb T)}
\le
N C_I^N M.
\]

Therefore on an interval of length

\[
\delta\asymp (N C_I^N)^{-1}
\]

around \(y_0\), intersected with \(I\),

\[
|P(y)|\ge \frac12M.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_I |P(y)|^2dy
\ge
c\,\frac{M^2}{N C_I^N}
\ge
c\,\frac{C_I^{-3N}}{N}\|S\|_2^2.
\]

Since

\[
\frac{C_I^{-3N}}{N}\ge e^{-C R},
\]

we obtain

\[
\boxed{
\int_I
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\sin(ky)
\right|^2dy
\ge
e^{-C R}\|S\|_2^2.
}
\]

After the \(y=\Theta(x)\) change of variables,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{-c}^{c}
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\Phi_k(x)
\right|^2dx
\ge
e^{-C R}\|S\|_2^2.
}
\]

This is stronger than the required

\[
e^{-O(R\log R)}.
\]

Since

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

the loss is

\[
e^{-CR}=Q^{-o(1)},
\]

well within polynomial bookkeeping.

---

## 2. Perturbed singular bases

If the actual singular basis is not exactly

\[
\Phi_k(x)=\sin(k\Theta(x)),
\]

but instead

\[
\Phi_k(x)=\sin(k\Theta(x))+\Delta_k(x),
\]

then the same transfer works provided the perturbation operator

\[
\Delta:S\mapsto \sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\Delta_k
\]

satisfies

\[
\|\Delta S\|_{L^2[-c,c]}
\le
\frac12 e^{-CR/2}\|S\|_2.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\|\Delta\|_{\ell^2\to L^2}
\le
\frac12 e^{-CR/2}.
\]

This is the clean stability condition. More generally, if the unperturbed lower frame constant is \(\kappa_R\), then we need

\[
\|\Delta\|_{\ell^2\to L^2}
\le
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}.
\]

So the singular basis audit can be reduced to:

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_k=\sin(k\Theta)+\Delta_k,
\qquad
\|\Delta\|_{\ell^2\to L^2}
\le
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}.
}
\]

If this fails, then the basis itself may be too degenerate to transfer singular sine moments into scalar source energy.

---

## 3. Transfer theorem with constants

Assume the exact expansion

\[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k(m_0)\Phi_k(x)
+
\operatorname{Rem}_R(x;m_0)
\]

and the lower frame

\[
\int_{-c}^{c}
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\Phi_k(x)
\right|^2dx
\ge
\kappa_R\|S\|_2^2,
\]

with

\[
\kappa_R\ge e^{-C R}.
\]

If

\[
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R\|_{L^2[-c,c]}
\le
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}\|S\|_2,
\]

then

\[
\int_{-c}^{c}
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)|^2dx
\ge
\frac14\kappa_R\|S\|_2^2.
\]

Therefore

\[
\|S\|_2\ge Q^{-A}
\]

implies

\[
\int_{-c}^{c}
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)|^2dx
\ge
Q^{-A-o(1)}.
\]

In the paper’s polynomial bookkeeping, this is

\[
\boxed{
\int_{-c}^{c}
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)|^2dx
\ge
Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

So once the coefficient identity and half-leading remainder are in place, the singular branch is fully compatible with scalar Gate–1.

---

## 4. The coefficient identity is the real audit

The necessary identity is

\[
S_k(m_0)
=
\sum_j w_j(m_0)\sin(k\theta_j(m_0))
+
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}(m_0),
\]

with

\[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k(m_0)\Phi_k(x)
+
\operatorname{Rem}_R(x;m_0).
\]

The key phrase is: **coefficient of the actual expansion**.

It is not enough that

\[
S_k
\]

is a moment diagnostic extracted from a zero-side singular model. It must be the coefficient vector of the actual canonical source

\[
q''_{\mathrm{can}}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

in the local singular coordinate.

The coefficient audit should check:

\[
\boxed{
B_2\text{ contributes to } \mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
P_2\text{ contributes through the actual singular prime packet}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
D_2\text{ contributes through the folded-dual singular packet}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
E_2\text{ contributes through the regularized tail}
}
\]

and all four are in the same singular normalization.

If any piece is omitted, then the singular vector may certify the wrong object.

---

## 5. Half-leading remainder: what must be proved

Let

\[
\kappa_R\ge e^{-CR}.
\]

The clean remainder condition is

\[
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R\|_{L^2}
\le
\frac12e^{-CR/2}\|S\|.
\]

After good-subset extraction, one has

\[
\|S\|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

So a sufficient absolute estimate is

\[
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R\|_{L^2}
\le
Q^{-A-C_0}
\]

with \(C_0\) large enough to dominate the frame loss.

But the relative condition is better, because it does not tie the expansion accuracy to the extracted threshold.

The remainder must include all errors from:

\[
\boxed{
\text{truncating the singular expansion at }R;
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{regularizing near-zero or near-pole terms;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{folded-dual approximation;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{gamma/background Taylor tail;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{regularized far tail }E_2.
}
\]

The half-leading condition is the point where the deterministic singular transfer can still fail.

Specifically, show or refute that

admits a finite singular expansion whose coefficients are exactly

S_k=

up to a remainder satisfying the half-leading bound.

If that identity is true, singular transfer is deterministic and Stack C2’s branch-complete transfer layer is coherent.

I’ll now attack the singular coefficient identity itself: whether the sine-moment vector can genuinely be the coefficient vector of the local expansion of \(\lambda^3 q''_{\mathrm{can}}\), rather than only a diagnostic.

_Thought for 1m 13s_

Continuing Agent 5: singular coefficient identity.

The transfer layer is now clean enough to separate into two questions:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the singular sine vector }S_R\text{ actually appear as coefficients of }\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}?
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{Is the omitted remainder half-leading on the extracted singular-good subset?}
}
\]

This is the exact unresolved branch-to-canonical issue in Stack C2. The latest coordinator prompt explicitly requires singular good packets to feed the same scalar canonical downstream source \(u=q''_{\mathrm{can}}\), not a diagnostic source. 

## 1. The necessary kernel identity

The singular branch is valid only if the local singular kernel has a finite separable expansion of the following form:

\[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
D_k(\mu)\,
S_k(m_0)\,
\Phi_k(x)
+
\operatorname{Rem}_R(x;m_0),
\]

where

\[
S_k(m_0)
=
\sum_j w_j(m_0)\sin(k\theta_j(m_0))
+
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}(m_0),
\]

and \(D_k(\mu)\) is a known diagonal normalization factor.

The transfer theorem is stable if

\[
Q^{-C}\le |D_k(\mu)|\le Q^C
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3,
\]

after whatever normalization defines \(S_k\). Polynomially growing factors such as \(k\), \(k^2\), or \(k^3\) are harmless because

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

But if

\[
D_k(\mu)=\mu^k
\]

is left unnormalized in the singular vector, then at deep singular scale

\[
\mu\ll(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

one gets

\[
\mu^R
=
\exp(-C R\log\log Q)
=
Q^{-C+o(1)}.
\]

That is still polynomial if \(C\) is fixed, but it must be tracked. If the loss becomes \(\mu^{R^2}\), the route breaks.

So the coefficient identity must be stated with the diagonal normalization exposed.

---

## 2. Model identity: Poisson/Cauchy singular kernels

The sine moments

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)
\]

are exactly the Fourier-sine coefficients of a standard Cauchy/Poisson singular kernel. The model identity is

\[
\frac{\sin\theta}{\cosh \eta-\cos\theta}
=
2\sum_{k\ge1}e^{-k\eta}\sin(k\theta),
\qquad \eta>0.
\]

Thus a sum of singular atoms has

\[
\sum_jw_j\frac{\sin\theta_j}{\cosh\eta-\cos\theta_j}
=
2\sum_{k\ge1}
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)
\right)
e^{-k\eta}.
\]

This is the exact algebraic reason sine moments can be actual coefficients.

If the local singular form of \(\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}\) reduces to a differentiated or weighted version of this kernel, then the coefficients are still sine moments, possibly multiplied by harmless diagonal weights such as \(k\), \(k^2\), or \(k^3\).

So the singular coefficient identity is plausible if the local canonical source can be written as

\[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
=
\sum_jw_j K(x,\theta_j)
+
B_{\mathrm{can}}(x)
+
\text{tail},
\]

where

\[
K(x,\theta)
=
\sum_{k\ge3}
D_k\sin(k\theta)\Phi_k(x),
\]

and \(B_{\mathrm{can}}\) has the corresponding expansion

\[
B_{\mathrm{can}}(x)
=
\sum_{k\ge3}
D_k\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}\Phi_k(x).
\]

That is the exact identity to verify.

---

## 3. Riesz lower bound for the Poisson basis

If the basis is

\[
\Phi_k(x)=e^{-k\eta(x)}
\]

with \(\eta\) monotone and

\[
0<a\le \eta'(x)\le A,
\qquad
\eta(x)\in[\eta_0,\eta_1],
\]

then the lower frame is acceptable.

After changing variables,

\[
\int
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}c_ke^{-k\eta(x)}
\right|^2dx
\asymp
\int_{\eta_0}^{\eta_1}
\left|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}c_ke^{-k\eta}
\right|^2d\eta.
\]

The Gram matrix has entries

\[
G_{k\ell}
=
\int_{\eta_0}^{\eta_1}e^{-(k+\ell)\eta}\,d\eta
=
\frac{e^{-(k+\ell)\eta_0}-e^{-(k+\ell)\eta_1}}{k+\ell}.
\]

This is a diagonally rescaled Hilbert-type matrix. Its smallest eigenvalue on \(R\) consecutive frequencies is bounded below by

\[
e^{-CR}
\]

up to polynomial factors, provided \(\eta_0,\eta_1\) remain \(O(1)\) and the interval length is bounded below. Even with rougher conditioning, this is at worst

\[
e^{-O(R\log R)}.
\]

Hence the Poisson-basis transfer is deterministic Green.

The basis is dangerous only if the effective \(\eta\)-interval collapses:

\[
|\eta_1-\eta_0|\to0,
\]

or if the expansion uses an unnormalized basis with hidden factors like

\[
\mu^{kR}
\]

or determinant-type losses. Those would produce \(e^{-O(R^2)}\)-scale losses, which are not acceptable.

---

## 4. Small-\(\mu\) Taylor singular form

There is another possible singular normal form. In deep singular scale,

\[
\mu=\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

the local kernels may instead be expanded in powers of the small parameter \(\mu\):

\[
K(x,\theta;\mu)
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
\mu^k
p_k(x)\sin(k\theta)
+
\operatorname{Rem}_R.
\]

If the singular vector is normalized as

\[
S_k=\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}},
\]

then the actual coefficient is

\[
D_k(\mu)S_k
=
\mu^k S_k.
\]

The transfer remains polynomial because

\[
\mu^R
\ge
(\log Q)^{-CR}
=
Q^{-O(1)}
\]

as long as the singular window is the transition-lower-edge scale. In deeper singular range where \(\mu\) is much smaller than every power of \((\log Q)^{-1}\), this can fail unless the definition of \(S_k\) absorbs \(\mu^k\).

So the small-\(\mu\) version requires one of the following:

\[
\boxed{
\text{either }S_k\text{ includes the }\mu^k\text{ coefficient weight;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\mu^R\ge Q^{-C}\text{ on the branch being transferred;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{use a different normalized singular basis.}
}
\]

This is a real audit point: the singular vector must be normalized in a way compatible with polynomial transfer.

---

## 5. The half-leading remainder is not automatic

Even if the infinite kernel identity is exact, the finite vector \(S_3,\ldots,S_{R+3}\) only gives a leading block. The omitted part is

\[
\operatorname{Rem}_R
=
\sum_{k>R+3}D_kS_k\Phi_k
+
\text{other canonical tails}.
\]

The needed estimate is

\[
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R\|_{L^2}
\le
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}
\|(D_kS_k)_{3\le k\le R+3}\|_{\ell^2},
\]

where

\[
\kappa_R\ge e^{-O(R\log R)}.
\]

This cannot be replaced by “the expansion is asymptotic.” It must be relative to the leading extracted block. Otherwise a high-frequency tail could cancel the low-frequency block on the local interval.

In the Poisson model, the high-\(k\) tail is controlled if the radial coordinate satisfies a strong enough damping condition:

\[
e^{-R\eta_0}\ll \kappa_R^{1/2}\frac{\|S_{\le R}\|}{\|S_{>R}\|}.
\]

Without a bound on the high moments \(S_{>R}\), this is not automatic.

In the small-\(\mu\) Taylor model, the tail is controlled if

\[
(C\mu)^{R}
\|S_{>R}\|
\le
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}\|S_{\le R}\|.
\]

So the half-leading estimate is either:

1. an analytic consequence of strong damping/truncation, or  
2. a separate “no high-tail cancellation” condition.

This is the main remaining deterministic vulnerability.

---

## 6. A no-go if \(S_R\) is only diagnostic

Suppose \(S_R\) is not the coefficient vector of the actual local expansion. Then there is no deterministic implication

\[
\|S_R\|\ge Q^{-A}
\Longrightarrow
\|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}\|_{L^2}\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

Indeed, choose any nonzero vector \(S\) and any basis \(\Phi_k\). If the actual source is allowed to differ from

\[
\sum S_k\Phi_k
\]

by an unrestricted remainder, set

\[
\operatorname{Rem}_R(x)=-\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}S_k\Phi_k(x).
\]

Then the actual source is identically zero while

\[
\|S\|>0.
\]

Thus, without the coefficient identity plus a half-leading remainder bound, singular transfer is false even as finite-dimensional deterministic mathematics.

So the singular branch is not allowed to say:

\[
\text{large sine diagnostic}
\Rightarrow
\text{large scalar source}.
\]

It must say:

\[
\text{large actual coefficient block of the canonical source}
\Rightarrow
\text{large scalar source}.
\]

---

## 7. Current result

The singular transfer audit now reduces to the following exact checklist.

### Green

The basis-conditioning part is green under either of these standard forms:

\[
\Phi_k(x)=\sin(k\Theta(x))
\]

with nondegenerate monotone \(\Theta\), or

\[
\Phi_k(x)=e^{-k\eta(x)}
\]

with nondegenerate monotone \(\eta\). Both give

\[
\kappa_R\ge e^{-O(R\log R)}.
\]

### Yellow

The coefficient identity:

\[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
D_k(\mu)
\left[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)
+
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}
\right]
\Phi_k(x)
+
\operatorname{Rem}_R.
\]

This must be checked for the full canonical source

\[
B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

### Red/Yellow

The half-leading remainder:

\[
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R\|_{L^2}
\le
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}
\|(D_kS_k)_{3\le k\le R+3}\|_2.
\]

This is the most likely failure point if high singular moments or canonical tails can cancel the leading block.

## Final Agent 5 conclusion

The singular branch-to-canonical transfer is **not blocked by basis conditioning**. It is blocked only by the canonical expansion audit:

\[
\boxed{
\text{derive the exact singular kernel expansion for }q''_{\mathrm{can}}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove a half-leading bound for everything omitted beyond }S_3,\ldots,S_{R+3}.
}
\]

If those two are proved, singular-good packets genuinely become scalar \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\)-good packets and Stack C2 remains coherent.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 19:42:29)

I’ll push the half-leading remainder question. The key issue is whether omitted high singular modes are analytically damped or can cancel the extracted low block.

_Thought for 14s_

Continuing Agent 5: half-leading remainder and singular-mode truncation.

The previous state was: singular transfer is deterministic if

\[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}D_k(\mu)S_k(m_0)\Phi_k(x)
+
\operatorname{Rem}_R(x;m_0),
\]

with a Riesz lower bound for \(\Phi_k\) and a half-leading remainder estimate. The current attack is to determine whether that half-leading estimate is a reasonable deterministic consequence or a new hidden arithmetic assumption. This is the exact singular-transfer issue in Stack C2. 

## 1. What must be controlled

Let

\[
L_R(x)=\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}D_kS_k\Phi_k(x)
\]

and

\[
T_R(x)=\sum_{k>R+3}D_kS_k\Phi_k(x)+\text{canonical analytic tails}.
\]

The transfer needs

\[
\|T_R\|_{L^2[-c,c]}
\le
\frac12\|L_R\|_{L^2[-c,c]}.
\]

Using the Riesz lower bound

\[
\|L_R\|_{L^2}
\ge
\kappa_R^{1/2}
\|(D_kS_k)_{3\le k\le R+3}\|_2,
\]

it is enough to prove

\[
\boxed{
\|T_R\|_{L^2}
\le
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}
\|(D_kS_k)_{3\le k\le R+3}\|_2.
}
\]

So the issue is not the existence of an asymptotic expansion. The issue is **relative tail dominance**.

---

## 2. General deterministic bound

Assume the singular basis satisfies a Bessel upper bound

\[
\left\|
\sum_{k>K}a_k\Phi_k
\right\|_{L^2[-c,c]}^2
\le
C_\Phi
\sum_{k>K}|a_k|^2.
\]

Then a sufficient half-leading condition is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{k>R+3}|D_kS_k|^2
+
\|\text{canonical analytic tails}\|_{L^2}^2
\le
c\,\kappa_R
\sum_{3\le k\le R+3}|D_kS_k|^2.
}
\]

This is the cleanest deterministic criterion.

It says: after the same normalization \(D_k\), the omitted singular coefficient tail must be smaller than the retained coefficient block by a factor at least \(\kappa_R\).

Since

\[
\kappa_R\ge e^{-O(R\log R)}=Q^{-O(1)},
\]

this is not too severe. But it is not automatic.

---

## 3. Poisson kernel case

Suppose the singular kernel has Poisson-type coefficients

\[
D_k=e^{-k\eta_0}
\]

with

\[
\eta_0>0.
\]

Then

\[
\sum_{k>R}|D_kS_k|^2
=
\sum_{k>R}e^{-2k\eta_0}|S_k|^2.
\]

If the raw sine moments satisfy a polynomial growth bound

\[
|S_k|\le Q^C k^C
\]

for \(k\le K_{\max}\), then

\[
\sum_{k>R}e^{-2k\eta_0}|S_k|^2
\ll
Q^{2C}\sum_{k>R}k^{2C}e^{-2k\eta_0}.
\]

This is exponentially small in \(R\eta_0\) only if

\[
R\eta_0\gg \log Q.
\]

That condition is too strong if

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

and \(\eta_0\asymp1\) gives

\[
R\eta_0\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

which is only \(Q^{-o(1)}\) damping, not \(Q^{-C}\) damping.

But we do not necessarily need absolute \(Q^{-C}\) damping. We need tail small relative to the leading block. If the leading block has comparable Poisson damping, then the relevant ratio is

\[
\frac{\sum_{k>R}e^{-2k\eta_0}|S_k|^2}
{\sum_{k\le R}e^{-2k\eta_0}|S_k|^2}.
\]

This ratio can still be large unless there is a coefficient-tail regularity theorem.

Thus in the Poisson coefficient model:

\[
\boxed{
\text{damping alone does not prove half-leading unless }S_k\text{ has tail control.}
}
\]

A single large high mode \(S_{K}\) can dominate the omitted tail.

---

## 4. Small-\(\mu\) Taylor case

Suppose instead

\[
D_k=\mu^k
\]

with

\[
\mu\ll1.
\]

Then the omitted tail satisfies

\[
\sum_{k>R}|\mu^kS_k|^2.
\]

If

\[
|S_k|\le Q^C C^k
\]

and

\[
C\mu<1,
\]

then

\[
\sum_{k>R}|\mu^kS_k|^2
\ll
Q^{2C}(C\mu)^{2R}.
\]

This can be very small. In deep singular scale this is favorable.

But the retained block contains \(\mu^kS_k\) for \(k\le R\). If the singular vector used for good-subset extraction is the unweighted vector

\[
(S_3,\ldots,S_{R+3}),
\]

then

\[
\|S\|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

does not imply

\[
\|(\mu^kS_k)_{k\le R}\|\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

unless

\[
\mu^R\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

For very deep singular packets, \(\mu^R\) can be super-polynomially small.

Therefore in the small-\(\mu\) model, the correct singular vector is not necessarily

\[
(S_k),
\]

but the **weighted coefficient vector**

\[
\boxed{
\widetilde S_k=D_k(\mu)S_k.
}
\]

The aggregate singular input should then be expressed in terms of

\[
\|\widetilde S_{\le R}\|^2
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}|D_k(\mu)S_k|^2,
\]

not the raw sine moments, unless a polynomial lower bound for \(D_k\) is available.

This is a major normalization point.

---

## 5. Revised singular observable

The branch-compatible singular observable should be

\[
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_R(m)
=
\left(
D_k(\mu)
\left[
\sum_j w_j(m)\sin(k\theta_j(m))
+
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}(m)
\right]
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}.
}
\]

Then the local expansion is

\[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
\widetilde S_k(m)\Phi_k(x)
+
\operatorname{Rem}_R.
\]

The deterministic transfer becomes clean:

\[
\|\widetilde{\mathcal S}_R(m)\|\ge Q^{-A}
\Longrightarrow
\int_{|x|\le c}
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)|^2dx
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

This avoids hidden losses from \(D_k\).

Conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{singular aggregate Gate--1 must use the actual weighted coefficient vector, not raw sine moments.}
}
\]

Raw sine moments are safe only if

\[
\min_{k\le R}|D_k(\mu)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

---

## 6. Tail no-go without coefficient-tail control

There is a deterministic no-go for half-leading if high singular moments are unconstrained.

Take any nonzero leading vector \(\widetilde S_{\le R}\). Because the functions \(\{\Phi_k\}_{k>R}\) span a dense subspace in the relevant analytic model, one can often find high-mode coefficients \(a_k\) such that

\[
\left\|
\sum_{k>R}a_k\Phi_k
+
\sum_{k\le R}\widetilde S_k\Phi_k
\right\|_{L^2}
\]

is arbitrarily small, at least in a phase-relaxed model.

Thus

\[
\|\widetilde S_{\le R}\|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

alone does not imply scalar energy if the tail is arbitrary.

The canonical proof must use one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{analytic damping of high modes;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{a priori coefficient-tail bound;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{orthogonal projection definition of }\widetilde S_{\le R}\text{ with tail removed;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{include enough modes so omitted tail is automatically small.}
}
\]

The last option may require \(R\) much larger, which could break the polynomial bookkeeping.

---

## 7. Projection-based repair

A robust deterministic way to define the singular coefficient vector is by orthogonal projection.

Let

\[
V_R=\operatorname{span}\{\Phi_3,\ldots,\Phi_{R+3}\}\subset L^2[-c,c],
\]

and let

\[
P_R
\]

be the \(L^2\)-orthogonal projection onto \(V_R\). Define

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_R
\]

by

\[
P_R[\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)]
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}\widetilde S_k\Phi_k(x).
\]

Then

\[
\|P_R F\|_{L^2}
\]

is automatically controlled by \(\|\widetilde{\mathcal S}_R\|\) via the finite Gram matrix, and no tail cancellation can destroy it because the tail is orthogonal to \(V_R\).

In this formulation,

\[
\|\widetilde{\mathcal S}_R\|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

implies

\[
\|F\|_{L^2}
\ge
\|P_RF\|_{L^2}
\ge
Q^{-A'}.
\]

This avoids the half-leading remainder condition entirely.

The price is arithmetic: the projected coefficients

\[
\widetilde S_k
\]

may no longer equal the simple sine moments

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k.
\]

So the singular aggregate theorem becomes harder to prove, but the transfer becomes deterministic by definition.

This gives a fork inside the singular branch:

### Option S-A: explicit coefficient expansion

Use sine moments as actual coefficients. Then must prove half-leading tail.

### Option S-B: projected coefficient vector

Define coefficients by \(L^2\)-projection. Then transfer is automatic, but arithmetic lower-frame theorem must be proved for projected coefficients.

For Stack C2, S-B is cleaner logically; S-A is cleaner arithmetically if the kernel expansion has strong tail control.

---

## 8. Current recommendation for singular branch

Use the weighted actual coefficient vector

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_R=(D_kS_k)_{3\le k\le R+3}
\]

rather than raw sine moments.

Then choose between:

\[
\boxed{
\text{explicit expansion + half-leading tail}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{\(L^2\)-projection coefficients + automatic transfer}.
}
\]

If the current draft’s \(S_R\) is raw sine moments with no \(D_k\), it is not yet safe for branch-to-canonical transfer in deep singular scale.

## Final result of this attack

The singular branch-to-canonical transfer now has a sharper requirement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the singular good energy must be measured in the same weighted coefficient norm that appears in the actual local expansion of }q''_{\mathrm{can}}.
}
\]

The half-leading remainder is avoidable only if we define coefficients by orthogonal projection. Otherwise, it remains a real deterministic condition:

\[
\boxed{
\|\operatorname{Rem}_R\|_{L^2}
\le
\frac12\kappa_R^{1/2}
\|\widetilde{\mathcal S}_R\|.
}
\]

This is the main correction to the singular component of Stack C2.
