## Assistant (2026-04-27 19:45:43)

I’ll now make the singular branch robust by replacing “raw sine moments” with projection/biorthogonal coefficients, then quantify exactly what arithmetic theorem changes.

_Thought for 13s_

Continuing Agent 5: singular transfer via projected coefficients.

The last attack showed that raw sine moments are unsafe unless they are the actual weighted coefficients of the local expansion and the omitted tail is half-leading. I’ll now sharpen the robust alternative: **define the singular observable by projection onto the finite singular source space**. This makes branch-to-canonical transfer deterministic by construction, but changes the arithmetic aggregate theorem. This is directly within the current Stack C2 requirement that singular good packets certify scalar \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\), not a proxy. 

## 1. Set up the finite singular source space

Let

\[
F(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x)
\]

on the fixed singular window

\[
I=[-c,c].
\]

Let

\[
V_R=\operatorname{span}\{\Phi_3,\ldots,\Phi_{R+3}\}\subset L^2(I).
\]

Write the Gram matrix

\[
G_R=(\langle \Phi_k,\Phi_\ell\rangle_{L^2(I)})_{3\le k,\ell\le R+3}.
\]

Assume the finite Riesz bounds

\[
\kappa_R\|a\|_2^2
\le
\left\|
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}a_k\Phi_k
\right\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\le
K_R\|a\|_2^2,
\]

with

\[
\kappa_R\ge e^{-O(R\log R)},\qquad K_R\le e^{O(R\log R)}.
\]

For the trigonometric-coordinate case, we argued one can usually get \(\kappa_R\ge e^{-O(R)}\).

---

## 2. Projection coefficients

Define the projected singular coefficient vector by

\[
b_k=\langle F,\Phi_k\rangle_{L^2(I)},
\qquad 3\le k\le R+3,
\]

and

\[
\widehat S=G_R^{-1}b.
\]

Then

\[
P_RF=\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}\widehat S_k\Phi_k,
\]

where \(P_R\) is the \(L^2\)-orthogonal projection onto \(V_R\).

Now

\[
\|F\|_{L^2(I)}
\ge
\|P_RF\|_{L^2(I)}
=
\left(\widehat S^*G_R\widehat S\right)^{1/2}
\ge
\kappa_R^{1/2}\|\widehat S\|_2.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\|\widehat S\|_2\ge Q^{-A}
\Longrightarrow
\|F\|_{L^2(I)}^2\ge Q^{-A'}
}
\]

because

\[
\kappa_R\ge e^{-O(R\log R)}=Q^{-O(1)}.
\]

This completely removes the half-leading remainder condition from the deterministic transfer step.

So the robust singular branch observable is:

\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal S}_R(m_0)
=
G_R^{-1}
\left(
\langle
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m_0+\lambda x),
\Phi_k(x)
\rangle_{L^2(I)}
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}.
}
\]

This is automatically scalar-canonical.

---

## 3. Relation to raw sine moments

Suppose the actual expansion has the infinite form

\[
F(x)=
\sum_{k\ge3}a_k\Phi_k(x),
\]

where the expected raw/weighted sine coefficients are

\[
a_k=D_k(\mu)
\left[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)
+
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}
\right].
\]

Split

\[
a=(a_{\le R},a_{>R}).
\]

Let

\[
G_{RR}=(\langle\Phi_k,\Phi_\ell\rangle)_{k,\ell\le R},
\qquad
G_{R>}= (\langle\Phi_j,\Phi_k\rangle)_{j\le R,\ k>R}.
\]

Then the projection coefficients are

\[
\widehat S
=
G_{RR}^{-1}
\left(
G_{RR}a_{\le R}
+
G_{R>}a_{>R}
\right),
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\widehat S
=
a_{\le R}
+
G_{RR}^{-1}G_{R>}a_{>R}.
}
\]

This identity isolates the old half-leading condition.

Raw coefficients \(a_{\le R}\) are safe if

\[
\boxed{
\|G_{RR}^{-1}G_{R>}a_{>R}\|
\le
\frac12\|a_{\le R}\|.
}
\]

That is exactly coefficient-space tail nonaliasing.

Without this, the projection coefficient can be small even when raw low sine moments are large, or vice versa. In particular, high singular modes can alias into the low projected coefficients.

So there are two valid singular routes:

### Route S-A: raw coefficient route

Use

\[
a_{\le R}=
(D_kS_k)_{3\le k\le R+3}.
\]

Then prove

\[
\|G_{RR}^{-1}G_{R>}a_{>R}\|
\le
\frac12\|a_{\le R}\|.
\]

This is the coefficient-space form of the half-leading tail condition.

### Route S-B: projection coefficient route

Use

\[
\widehat S
=
G_R^{-1}
(\langle F,\Phi_k\rangle)_k.
\]

Then transfer is automatic, but the arithmetic aggregate theorem must be proved for \(\widehat S\), not for the simple raw sine moments.

---

## 4. Which route is better for Stack C2?

For the proof architecture, S-B is cleaner.

The singular aggregate input becomes

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)\,
\|\widehat{\mathcal S}_R(m)\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m).
}
\]

Then good-subset extraction gives

\[
\|\widehat{\mathcal S}_R(m)\|\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

on a polynomial-weight subset, and deterministic projection transfer gives scalar canonical Gate–1.

This avoids all ambiguity about whether \(S_R\) was diagnostic or actual. It is actual by definition.

The price is that \(\widehat S\) may have a less transparent explicit-formula expression. It involves inner products

\[
\langle q''_{\mathrm{can}},\Phi_k\rangle,
\]

which are weighted integrals of the canonical source over the singular window. But those are still canonical and scalar; they can be expanded by explicit formula if needed.

For Stack C2, this is a better trade:

\[
\boxed{
\text{use projection coefficients for transfer, then attack aggregate lower-frame arithmetically.}
}
\]

---

## 5. Arithmetic form of projected singular coefficients

Using the explicit formula,

\[
q''_{\mathrm{can}}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

we get

\[
\widehat S
=
\widehat S^{B_2}
+
\widehat S^{P_2}
+
\widehat S^{D_2}
+
\widehat S^{E_2},
\]

where

\[
\widehat S^{P_2}_j
=
\sum_{n}
c_n(m_0)
\int_I
\lambda^3 e^{i\lambda x\log n}
\Psi_j(x)\,dx,
\]

with \(\{\Psi_j\}\) the dual basis

\[
\Psi_j=\sum_k(G_R^{-1})_{jk}\Phi_k.
\]

Similarly for the folded dual, background, and tail.

Thus the projected singular vector is again a finite vector of explicit-formula weighted packet sums, just with test functions

\[
\widehat\psi_j(\lambda\log n)
=
\int_I e^{i\lambda x\log n}\Psi_j(x)\,dx.
\]

So the singular aggregate lower-frame theorem becomes a lower sampling theorem for these finite test functions, not for raw sine moments.

This is good: it aligns singular, transition, and ordinary branches under one principle:

\[
\boxed{
\text{aggregate lower-frame theorem for actual canonical test-function projections.}
}
\]

---

## 6. Projection route eliminates tail cancellation

Because

\[
\|F\|_{L^2}^2
=
\|P_RF\|_{L^2}^2
+
\|(1-P_R)F\|_{L^2}^2,
\]

there is no cancellation between projected and tail components.

Thus if

\[
\|P_RF\|_{L^2}\ge Q^{-A},
\]

then automatically

\[
\|F\|_{L^2}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is exactly what the raw coefficient expansion lacked. In raw expansion, low block plus high tail can cancel. In orthogonal projection, the tail is orthogonal by construction.

Therefore the singular transfer theorem should be recast as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{large projected canonical singular energy}
\Rightarrow
\text{large scalar canonical source energy}.
}
\]

This is deterministic and unconditional once the finite basis is chosen.

---

## 7. Remaining issue: does projected singular energy have enough dimension?

The projected vector still has dimension

\[
R+1\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Pointwise, this remains dimensionally underpowered. But Stack C2 uses aggregate energy, not pointwise exclusion.

So the aggregate singular theorem should be:

\[
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
\|P_R[\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)]\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho(m).
\]

This is the cleanest singular aggregate input.

Equivalently,

\[
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
\|\widehat{\mathcal S}_R(m)\|_{G_R}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho(m),
\]

where

\[
\|\widehat S\|_{G_R}^2=\widehat S^*G_R\widehat S.
\]

This is even better than Euclidean coefficient norm because it directly equals projected source energy.

---

## 8. Recommended singular formulation

Replace the singular branch observable conceptually as follows:

Old unsafe raw diagnostic:

\[
\mathcal S_R^{\mathrm{raw}}
=
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)
+
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}
\right)_{3\le k\le R+3}.
\]

Safe canonical projected observable:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
=
\left\|
P_R\left[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)
\right]
\right\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
}
\]

Then the singular aggregate input is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)\mathcal E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho(m).
}
\]

And the transfer is trivial:

\[
\mathcal E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)\le
\|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
\]

So on the extracted good subset,

\[
\mathcal E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)\ge Q^{-A}
\]

implies scalar canonical Gate–1.

This is the strongest correction to the singular branch.

---

## Final result of this attack

The singular transfer problem should be solved by **changing the singular observable**:

\[
\boxed{
\text{do not use raw sine moments as the Gate--1 singular energy unless tail nonaliasing is proved.}
}
\]

Use instead:

\[
\boxed{
\text{orthogonal projected canonical source energy onto the finite singular basis.}
}
\]

Then:

1. branch-to-canonical transfer is automatic;
2. tail cancellation is impossible;
3. \(B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\) are included by definition;
4. the arithmetic problem becomes an aggregate lower-frame theorem for actual projected canonical coefficients.

This keeps Stack C2 coherent and removes the deterministic singular remainder as a blocker.

Agent 5 — singular branch correction using projected canonical energy.

The update changes my work in one important way: **the singular branch should no longer be formulated around raw sine moments as Gate–1 energy**. The safe Stack C2 formulation is to use an actual \(L^2\)-projection of the scalar canonical source \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\). This makes branch-to-canonical transfer automatic and removes the half-leading tail problem. 

## 1. Projected singular observable

Fix the singular local window

\[
I=[-c,c],
\]

and define

\[
F_m(x)=\lambda^3 q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x).
\]

Let

\[
V_R=\operatorname{span}\{\Phi_3,\ldots,\Phi_{R+3}\}\subset L^2(I),
\]

where \(\Phi_k\) are the chosen finite singular basis functions. Let

\[
P_R:L^2(I)\to V_R
\]

be the \(L^2(I)\)-orthogonal projection.

The corrected singular Gate–1 energy is

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
=
\|P_RF_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
}
\]

This is the right object because it is defined directly from

\[
q''_{\mathrm{can}}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

No proxy model or diagnostic moment vector is involved.

---

## 2. Deterministic transfer is immediate

Since \(P_R\) is an orthogonal projection,

\[
\|P_RF_m\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)\ge Q^{-A}
\Longrightarrow
\int_I
|\lambda^3 q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)|^2dx
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

So projected singular energy directly implies scalar canonical Gate–1.

This is stronger and cleaner than the raw-coefficient route, where one needed:

\[
\text{coefficient identity}
+
\text{Riesz lower bound}
+
\text{half-leading remainder}.
\]

With projection energy, the tail cannot cancel the low block because

\[
F_m=P_RF_m+(1-P_R)F_m
\]

is an orthogonal decomposition.

---

## 3. Coefficient formulation

If one wants finite coordinates, define the Gram matrix

\[
G_{ij}
=
\langle \Phi_i,\Phi_j\rangle_{L^2(I)},
\qquad
3\le i,j\le R+3.
\]

Let

\[
b_i(m)=\langle F_m,\Phi_i\rangle_{L^2(I)}.
\]

Then the coefficient vector of \(P_RF_m\) in the \(\Phi\)-basis is

\[
\widehat S(m)=G^{-1}b(m),
\]

and

\[
P_RF_m
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}\widehat S_k(m)\Phi_k.
\]

The projected energy is

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
=
\widehat S(m)^*G\widehat S(m)
=
b(m)^*G^{-1}b(m).
\]

If the basis satisfies finite Riesz bounds

\[
\kappa_R\|a\|_2^2
\le
a^*Ga
\le
K_R\|a\|_2^2,
\]

then

\[
\kappa_R\|\widehat S(m)\|_2^2
\le
E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
\le
K_R\|\widehat S(m)\|_2^2.
\]

For trigonometric or Poisson-type singular bases on a nondegenerate window, the expected bound is

\[
\kappa_R\ge e^{-O(R\log R)},
\]

which is polynomially harmless because

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

But the coordinate norm is secondary. The invariant energy is \(E_{\mathrm{sing}}\).

---

## 4. Relation to raw sine moments

Suppose an infinite expansion exists:

\[
F_m(x)=\sum_{k\ge3}a_k(m)\Phi_k(x),
\]

where the raw expected coefficients are

\[
a_k(m)
=
D_k(\mu)
\left(
\sum_j w_j(m)\sin(k\theta_j(m))
+
\mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}}(m)
\right).
\]

Split

\[
a=(a_{\le R},a_{>R}).
\]

Let

\[
G_{RR}=(\langle\Phi_i,\Phi_j\rangle)_{i,j\le R},
\qquad
G_{R>}=(\langle\Phi_i,\Phi_j\rangle)_{i\le R<j}.
\]

Then

\[
\widehat S
=
a_{\le R}
+
G_{RR}^{-1}G_{R>}a_{>R}.
\]

So the raw low sine moments agree with the projected coefficients only if

\[
\boxed{
\|G_{RR}^{-1}G_{R>}a_{>R}\|
\le
Q^{-C}\|a_{\le R}\|
}
\]

or at least

\[
\le \frac12\|a_{\le R}\|.
\]

That is a tail-nonaliasing theorem. Without it, raw sine moments are not safe Gate–1 observables.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{raw }S_R\text{ can remain diagnostic, but projected }E_{\mathrm{sing}}\text{ should be the proof object.}
}
\]

---

## 5. Corrected singular aggregate theorem

The singular aggregate input should be:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho(m).
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
\left\|
P_R\left[
\lambda^3 q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)
\right]
\right\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho(m).
}
\]

This is the singular analogue of actual-coefficient aggregate Gate–1. It is not a statement about arbitrary sine packets; it is a statement about the actual canonical source sampled over routed singular centers.

Good-subset extraction then gives a polynomial-weight subset

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{sing}}
\]

where

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

and therefore scalar canonical Gate–1 holds automatically.

---

## 6. Expansion in canonical pieces

Because

\[
q''_{\mathrm{can}}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

we have

\[
F_m
=
F_m^{B_2}
+
F_m^{P_2}
+
F_m^{D_2}
+
F_m^{E_2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
P_RF_m
=
P_RF_m^{B_2}
+
P_RF_m^{P_2}
+
P_RF_m^{D_2}
+
P_RF_m^{E_2}.
\]

In coefficient form,

\[
b_i(m)
=
\langle F_m,\Phi_i\rangle
=
b_i^{B_2}(m)
+
b_i^{P_2}(m)
+
b_i^{D_2}(m)
+
b_i^{E_2}(m).
\]

For the prime packet piece, schematically,

\[
b_i^{P_2}(m)
=
\sum_n c_n(m)
\int_I
\lambda^3 e^{i\lambda x\log n}
\Phi_i(x)\,dx.
\]

For the dual piece, the same formula holds with folded-dual coefficients and phase. The \(B_2\) and \(E_2\) terms are projected by the same test functions.

So projected singular energy is compatible with the branch-complete actual-coefficient philosophy: it is a finite vector of canonical test-function projections of the actual source.

---

## 7. Compatibility with Agent 1’s branch-complete AggG1

The branch-complete aggregate Gate–1 stack should use:

### Ordinary

\[
E_{\mathrm{ord}}(m)
=
\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X_{\mathrm{can}}(m)\|^2.
\]

### Transition

\[
E_{\mathrm{tr}}(m)
=
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m)\|^2,
\]

where

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m)
=
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^r
[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)
]_{x=0}
\right)_{0\le r\le R}.
\]

### Singular

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
=
\left\|
P_R[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)
]
\right\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
}
\]

Then every branch energy is an actual canonical projection of \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\). This gives a unified principle:

\[
\boxed{
\text{branch Gate--1 energy = canonical projection energy of }q''_{\mathrm{can}}.
}
\]

After extraction, all branch-good packets feed the same scalar downstream theorem.

---

## 8. Final recommendation

The singular branch should be reformulated as follows:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use projected canonical singular energy }E_{\mathrm{sing}},\text{ not raw diagnostic sine moments.}
}
\]

Raw sine moments may be kept only as diagnostics or as an optional stronger route if one proves:

\[
\boxed{
\text{raw coefficient identity + tail nonaliasing/half-leading remainder.}
}
\]

The corrected singular branch theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho
\left\|
P_R[\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}]
\right\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho.
}
\]

This theorem is now fully compatible with corrected Stack C2. It includes \(B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\) by definition and gives scalar canonical Gate–1 without any extra deterministic transfer audit.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 19:56:07)

I’ll push the projected singular route one step further: projection fixes transfer, but it shifts the burden to proving that the actual singular source has aggregate energy in the chosen finite subspace rather than its orthogonal complement.

_Thought for 14s_

Continuing Agent 5: projected singular energy is safe for transfer, but now we must audit whether it is a plausible **aggregate lower-frame object**.

The latest architecture says the singular branch should use

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
=
\left\|
P_R[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)
]
\right\|_{L^2(I)}^2,
\]

rather than raw sine moments. That is correct because it is directly scalar-canonical and avoids tail-cancellation ambiguity. 

The new question is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can aggregate projected singular energy be proved without reintroducing a hidden projection defect?}
}
\]

## 1. Projection transfer is solved, but projection noncapture remains

Since \(P_R\) is an orthogonal projection,

\[
\|P_RF_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\le
\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2,
\qquad
F_m(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x).
\]

Therefore

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)\ge Q^{-A}
\]

implies scalar canonical Gate–1 immediately.

But the converse is false. The scalar source may be large while mostly lying in

\[
V_R^\perp.
\]

So the aggregate singular theorem

\[
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho(m)
\]

is not automatic from scalar source energy. It is a **low-mode capture theorem**:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual singular source has enough average energy in }V_R.
}
\]

This is the replacement arithmetic burden.

---

## 2. Correct branch reference normalization

The singular aggregate theorem should not be compared to a bare count unless the singular packet has already been normalized to unit canonical reference energy.

The safer statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
\|P_RF_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho E_{\mathrm{sing}}
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho N_{\mathrm{sing}},
}
\]

where

\[
N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
=
\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
\]

This mirrors the ordinary branch:

\[
\sum\rho|T_{\mathrm{can}}X|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\sum\rho|X|^2.
\]

So the singular branch should use

\[
d\mu_{\mathrm{sing}}=\rho(m)N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
\]

as the natural measure for extraction.

---

## 3. When can low-mode capture hold?

Let

\[
F_m=\sum_{k\ge3}a_k(m)\Phi_k
\]

in a stable singular basis, and suppose \(P_R\) projects onto

\[
V_R=\operatorname{span}\{\Phi_3,\ldots,\Phi_{R+3}\}.
\]

Then

\[
\|P_RF_m\|^2
\asymp
\sum_{k\le R}|a_k(m)|^2
\]

up to Gram conditioning, while

\[
\|F_m\|^2
\asymp
\sum_{k\ge3}|a_k(m)|^2
\]

if the full basis is Bessel/Riesz on the relevant range.

The aggregate capture theorem becomes

\[
\sum_m\rho(m)\sum_{k\le R}|a_k(m)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_m\rho(m)\sum_{k\ge3}|a_k(m)|^2.
\]

This is plausible only if one of the following is true:

\[
\boxed{
\text{high singular modes are analytically damped;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{the branch definition forces low-mode dominance;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{one uses a multiresolution family of projections rather than one }P_R.
}
\]

Without one of these, \(F_m\) can live mostly in \(V_R^\perp\), and the projected singular aggregate theorem fails.

---

## 4. Damping route

If the singular expansion has coefficients

\[
a_k(m)=D_k(\mu)S_k(m),
\]

with a damping factor such as

\[
D_k=e^{-k\eta}
\quad\text{or}\quad
D_k=\mu^k,
\]

then low-mode capture can be proved if the raw moments \(S_k\) have controlled growth.

For example, if

\[
|S_k(m)|\le Q^C e^{\epsilon k}
\]

and

\[
D_k=e^{-k\eta},
\qquad
\eta>\epsilon+c_0,
\]

then the high tail satisfies

\[
\sum_{k>R}|D_kS_k|^2
\ll
e^{-cR}
\sum_{k\le R}|D_kS_k|^2
\]

provided the low block is not accidentally tiny.

But if the extracted good condition is exactly that the low block is non-tiny, then damping gives capture on that subset.

For aggregate capture, one needs an averaged version:

\[
\sum_m\rho(m)\sum_{k>R}|D_kS_k(m)|^2
\le
Q^C e^{-cR}
\sum_m\rho(m)\sum_{k\le R}|D_kS_k(m)|^2.
\]

This is acceptable because

\[
e^{-cR}=Q^{-o(1)}.
\]

But if \(D_k=\mu^k\) and \(\mu\) is extremely small, then the low block may also be dominated only by the very first few modes. That is fine if those modes are included. If \(\mu\) is not small enough to damp high modes, finite \(R\) projection may miss too much.

So damping gives a route, but it must be encoded in the singular branch definition.

---

## 5. Branch-definition route

A cleaner route is to define “deep singular” precisely as the regime where the source has a valid low-mode singular approximation.

That is, declare a packet singular-good only if

\[
\|(1-P_R)F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\le
Q^C
\|P_RF_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\]

or, more usefully,

\[
\|P_RF_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
\]

But this is circular if it is simply assumed. It becomes meaningful if it follows from the analytic regime parameter:

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}
\]

and kernel damping.

So the singular branch should be defined by an analytic approximation theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\mu=\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}
\Longrightarrow
\|P_RF_m\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\|F_m\|^2
}
\]

for the actual canonical source, except on a small transition-overlap set.

If this theorem is true, singular transfer is fully deterministic and the singular aggregate input can simply lower-bound total singular source energy.

If it is false, one needs multiresolution.

---

## 6. Multiresolution repair

If fixed \(V_R\) may miss the singular source, define a family

\[
V_{R,j},
\qquad
j=0,\ldots,J,
\]

covering dyadic mode blocks:

\[
k\in[2^jR,2^{j+1}R]
\]

or other natural singular scales.

Let

\[
P_{R,j}
\]

be the projection onto \(V_{R,j}\), and define

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
=
\sum_j
\|P_{R,j}F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
\]

If the blocks form a near-orthogonal decomposition of the effective singular source space, then

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
\asymp
\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\]

up to polynomial loss.

This avoids low-mode noncapture.

But it changes downstream extraction: a good packet may be good in a high singular block, not the original low block. That is still scalar-canonical because every \(P_{R,j}F_m\) is a projection of \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\). D4 only needs scalar local energy, so any block works if it implies

\[
\|F_m\|_{L^2}^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Thus multiresolution singular energy is safe for downstream.

The arithmetic aggregate theorem becomes more complex but more robust:

\[
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
\sum_j
\|P_{R,j}F_m\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho(m)N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m).
\]

If the projections cover the effective space, this is nearly tautological. The hard part becomes bounding the number of blocks and ensuring polynomial conditioning.

---

## 7. Recommended singular formulation

The best singular branch formulation is not a single low-mode projection unless damping is proved.

Use one of the two following safe versions.

### Version S1: damped low-mode singular projection

Assume/prove analytic damping:

\[
\|(1-P_R)F_m\|^2
\le
Q^C\|P_RF_m\|^2
\]

on deep singular packets.

Then use

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)=\|P_RF_m\|^2.
\]

### Version S2: multiresolution projected singular energy

Define

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
=
\sum_j\|P_{R,j}F_m\|^2.
\]

Use this as singular Gate–1 energy.

This is safer because it avoids a hidden low-mode capture assumption. It remains scalar-canonical because all \(P_{R,j}\) act on

\[
F_m=\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x).
\]

---

## 8. Consequence for Stack C2

The singular branch in Stack C2 should be updated from

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}=\|P_RF_m\|^2
\]

to either

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{sing}}=\|P_RF_m\|^2
\quad
\text{plus a low-mode capture theorem}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}
=
\sum_j\|P_{R,j}F_m\|^2.
}
\]

The multiresolution version is more robust and probably the better architecture.

Then aggregate singular Gate–1 becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m).
}
\]

If the projection blocks form a polynomially conditioned resolution of the effective singular source space, this theorem is deterministic up to the definition of \(N_{\mathrm{sing}}\).

---

## Final Agent 5 status

Projected singular energy fixed transfer, but fixed low-mode projection may still be too narrow.

The singular branch now has a fork:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove analytic low-mode capture in deep singular packets}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{use multiresolution projected canonical singular energy}.
}
\]

I recommend the multiresolution version for Stack C2, because it keeps the singular branch scalar-canonical while avoiding both raw sine diagnostic errors and low-mode projection noncapture.

_Thought for 15s_

Agent 5 — singular branch: low-mode capture vs. multiresolution.

The update changes my work in a concrete way: the singular branch should no longer be framed around raw sine moments unless a separate coefficient/tail theorem is proved. The proof object should be actual projected canonical source energy, and the remaining decision is whether one projection \(P_R\) is enough or whether the singular branch needs a multiresolution projection family. 

## 1. Single-projection transfer theorem

Let

\[
F_m(x)=\lambda^3 q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x),
\qquad
I=[-c,c],
\]

and let

\[
V_R=\operatorname{span}\{\Phi_3,\ldots,\Phi_{R+3}\}\subset L^2(I).
\]

Let

\[
P_R:L^2(I)\to V_R
\]

be the \(L^2(I)\)-orthogonal projection. Define

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing},R}(m)=\|P_RF_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
\]

Then deterministic transfer is immediate:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{sing},R}(m)\ge Q^{-A}
\Longrightarrow
\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

No coefficient identity, Riesz lower bound, or half-leading remainder is required for transfer, because

\[
\|P_RF_m\|_{L^2}\le \|F_m\|_{L^2}.
\]

So \(P_R\)-energy is a safe singular Gate–1 source.

The limitation is the converse:

\[
\|F_m\|_{L^2}^2\gg Q^{-A}
\centernot\Longrightarrow
\|P_RF_m\|_{L^2}^2\gg Q^{-A'}.
\]

The scalar source can be large but lie mostly in

\[
V_R^\perp.
\]

Thus a single low-mode projection is safe but may be too narrow.

---

## 2. Low-mode capture theorem needed for single \(P_R\)

If we want to keep only the single projection \(P_R\), the needed analytic theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\|P_RF_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\quad
\text{for routed deep singular packets.}
}
\]

An aggregate version is weaker and probably more realistic:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)\|P_RF_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
}
\]

This theorem can follow from a damping principle. For example, suppose in a singular basis

\[
F_m=\sum_{k\ge3}a_k(m)\Phi_k
\]

and

\[
|a_k(m)|\le C_m e^{-ck}
\]

or more generally the high tail satisfies

\[
\sum_{k>R}|a_k(m)|^2
\le Q^A
\sum_{k\le R}|a_k(m)|^2.
\]

Then

\[
\|P_RF_m\|^2
\gtrsim Q^{-A}\|F_m\|^2.
\]

This is plausible if the deep singular regime imposes real analytic damping, e.g.

\[
a_k=D_k(\mu)S_k,\qquad D_k=e^{-k\eta}
\]

with a uniform positive \(\eta\), or

\[
D_k=\mu^k,\qquad \mu\ll1.
\]

But it is **not automatic**. If the canonical singular source has undamped high-mode content, low-mode capture fails.

Therefore the single-\(P_R\) branch requires one extra theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{deep singular low-mode capture for the actual }q''_{\mathrm{can}}.
}
\]

This is deterministic/analytic, not number-theoretic, but it is still a real assumption unless proved from the singular kernel.

---

## 3. Multiresolution projected singular energy

The safer construction is to replace one projection by a finite family.

Let

\[
V_{R,j}
=
\operatorname{span}\{\Phi_k: k\in I_j\},
\]

where \(I_j\) are dyadic or smooth spectral blocks, for example

\[
I_j=[2^jR,2^{j+1}R]
\]

up to an effective cutoff \(K_{\mathrm{eff}}\). Let

\[
P_{R,j}:L^2(I)\to V_{R,j}
\]

be the corresponding orthogonal projection, or an almost-orthogonal smooth spectral projection.

Define

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
=
\sum_{j=0}^{J}
\|P_{R,j}F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
}
\]

If the blocks form a stable frame for the effective singular source space, then

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
\ge
Q^{-A}\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
}
\]

For truly orthogonal blocks covering \(F_m\)’s effective spectral support,

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
=
\|P_{\le K_{\mathrm{eff}}}F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
\]

If the residual high tail satisfies

\[
\|(1-P_{\le K_{\mathrm{eff}}})F_m\|_{L^2}^2
\le Q^{-A}\|F_m\|_{L^2}^2,
\]

then

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
\ge
(1-Q^{-A})\|F_m\|_{L^2}^2.
\]

This makes the singular branch robust.

The number of blocks should be polynomially small:

\[
J\le Q^{o(1)}
\]

or preferably

\[
J=O(\log Q).
\]

Then good-subset extraction loses only polynomial factors.

---

## 4. Corrected singular aggregate theorem

There are now two possible singular aggregate theorems.

### Variant A: single low-mode projection

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)\|P_RF_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
}
\]

This is clean but requires low-mode capture.

### Variant B: multiresolution projection

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
\sum_{j=0}^{J}
\|P_{R,j}F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
}
\]

This is more robust. If the projections cover the effective singular source space, the theorem is nearly deterministic.

For Stack C2, the natural singular reference energy is

\[
\boxed{
N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)=\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
}
\]

Then the singular branch measure for extraction should be

\[
d\mu_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)=\rho(m)N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m).
\]

The normalized singular energy is

\[
E_1^{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
=
\frac{
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
}{
N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
}.
\]

On a dyadic slice where

\[
N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)\asymp N_j,
\]

this interfaces cleanly with the same extraction mechanism used in the ordinary branch.

---

## 5. Compatibility with downstream

Both variants are scalar-canonical because every projection is applied to

\[
F_m(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x).
\]

Thus if extracted good packets satisfy

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)\ge Q^{-A},
\]

then

\[
\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

So singular good packets feed the same downstream chain:

\[
\text{canonical scalar Gate--1}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate--2}
\Rightarrow
\text{forbidden-channel D4}
\Rightarrow
\text{row mobility}.
\]

There is no source-family problem, because we are not introducing arbitrary sources \(u_\nu\). We are only projecting the scalar source \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\) to certify that it is large.

This is the key distinction.

---

## 6. What replaces raw sine moments?

Raw sine moments

\[
S_k^{\mathrm{raw}}
=
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\]

should be treated as diagnostic unless one proves:

\[
\boxed{
\text{raw coefficient identity + tail nonaliasing.}
}
\]

In the corrected singular branch, the proof object is instead:

\[
\boxed{
\langle F_m,\Psi_{j,k}\rangle_{L^2(I)}
}
\]

where \(\Psi_{j,k}\) are the dual/frame functions for the projection blocks.

Expanding by the canonical explicit formula gives

\[
\langle F_m,\Psi_{j,k}\rangle
=
\langle F_m^{B_2},\Psi_{j,k}\rangle
+
\langle F_m^{P_2},\Psi_{j,k}\rangle
+
\langle F_m^{D_2},\Psi_{j,k}\rangle
+
\langle F_m^{E_2},\Psi_{j,k}\rangle.
\]

For the prime piece,

\[
\langle F_m^{P_2},\Psi_{j,k}\rangle
=
\sum_n c_n(m)
\int_I
\lambda^3 e^{i\lambda x\log n}
\overline{\Psi_{j,k}(x)}\,dx.
\]

So the singular aggregate theorem becomes a zero-restricted lower-frame theorem for actual canonical test-function projections, not for sine diagnostics.

This aligns singular with the ordinary and transition branches.

---

## 7. Recommended singular branch stack

I recommend Variant B:

\[
\boxed{
\text{multiresolution projected canonical singular energy.}
}
\]

The singular stack becomes:

### Define

\[
F_m(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x).
\]

### Choose projections

\[
P_{R,j}:L^2(I)\to V_{R,j},
\qquad j=0,\ldots,J,
\]

with

\[
J\le Q^{o(1)}
\]

and frame coverage

\[
\sum_j\|P_{R,j}F_m\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\|F_m\|^2
\]

for the effective singular source class.

### Define energy

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
=
\sum_j\|P_{R,j}F_m\|^2.
\]

### Aggregate theorem

\[
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho N_{\mathrm{sing}}.
\]

### Extraction

On a dyadic \(N_{\mathrm{sing}}\)-slice, extract packets where

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}/N_{\mathrm{sing}}
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

### Transfer

Immediate:

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}\le C_{\mathrm{frame}}\|F_m\|^2
\]

and in particular any nontrivial projection energy gives scalar source energy.

---

## Final recommendation

Use:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
=
\sum_j
\left\|
P_{R,j}
[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)
]
\right\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
}
\]

Do **not** use raw sine moments as the singular Gate–1 proof object.

A single \(P_R\) is acceptable only if the paper proves:

\[
\boxed{
\|P_RF_m\|^2\ge Q^{-A}\|F_m\|^2
}
\]

on the singular branch.

The multiresolution version is the safer Stack C2-compatible singular architecture because it is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual, scalar-canonical, transfer-safe, and robust against low-mode noncapture.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 20:02:02)

I’ll now audit the normalization trap in the multiresolution singular branch: projection coverage alone is not Gate–1 unless the scalar source has nontrivial absolute energy on a polynomial-weight set.

_Thought for 15s_

Continuing Agent 5: multiresolution singular branch, normalization, and extraction.

The previous repair was:

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
=
\sum_j
\left\|
P_{R,j}\left[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)
\right]
\right\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
\]

This is scalar-canonical and transfer-safe. The next issue is more subtle:

\[
\boxed{
\text{projection coverage is not the same as nontrivial Gate--1 energy.}
}
\]

If the total scalar source itself is tiny, then a perfect multiresolution decomposition only proves that the projections accurately capture something tiny.

---

## 1. Define the correct singular quantities

Let

\[
F_m(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x),
\qquad I=[-c,c].
\]

Define total singular source energy

\[
N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
=
\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
\]

Define multiresolution projected energy

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
=
\sum_{j=0}^J\|P_{R,j}F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
\]

There are two different desired facts:

### Coverage

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m).
\]

This says the projections see the scalar source.

### Nontrivial source energy

\[
N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This says the scalar source is actually large enough to be Gate–1.

Only their combination gives singular Gate–1:

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)\ge Q^{-A'}
\Longrightarrow
N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

because

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)\le C_{\mathrm{frame}}N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m).
\]

So the singular aggregate theorem must not only say “the projections cover \(F_m\).” It must produce **absolute projected energy**.

---

## 2. The correct aggregate singular theorem

The cleanest aggregate input is absolute:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m).
}
\]

Then, assuming a polynomial upper bound

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)\le Q^C,
\]

good-subset extraction gives a polynomial-weight subset

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{sing}}
=
\left\{
m:
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)\ge Q^{-A'}
\right\}.
\]

For \(m\in\mathcal G_{\mathrm{sing}}\),

\[
N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
=
\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\ge
C_{\mathrm{frame}}^{-1}E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
\ge Q^{-A''}.
\]

Thus scalar canonical Gate–1 follows.

This is the safest Stack C2 formulation.

---

## 3. Normalized theorem is insufficient by itself

One might instead state

\[
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho N_{\mathrm{sing}}.
\]

This is only a coverage theorem. It does not imply absolute Gate–1.

Extreme counterexample:

\[
N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)=e^{-Q^2}
\quad
\text{for every }m,
\]

and

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)=N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m).
\]

Then the normalized inequality holds perfectly, but no packet has usable Gate–1 energy.

So the singular branch needs either:

\[
\boxed{
\sum\rho E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}\ge Q^{-A}\sum\rho
}
\]

directly, or the pair

\[
\boxed{
\sum\rho N_{\mathrm{sing}}\ge Q^{-A}\sum\rho
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\sum\rho E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}
\ge
Q^{-A}\sum\rho N_{\mathrm{sing}}.
}
\]

The direct absolute theorem is cleaner.

---

## 4. Multiresolution coverage can be deterministic

If the projections form a near-Parseval frame for the effective singular source class, then

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
\asymp
\|P_{\mathrm{eff}}F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2,
\]

where \(P_{\mathrm{eff}}\) projects to the effective spectral range.

If the omitted high tail satisfies

\[
\|(1-P_{\mathrm{eff}})F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\le
Q^{-A}\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2,
\]

then

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
\ge
(1-Q^{-A})N_{\mathrm{sing}}(m).
\]

This part is deterministic analytic bookkeeping.

Thus the singular proof splits into:

\[
\boxed{
\text{deterministic multiresolution coverage}
}
\]

plus

\[
\boxed{
\text{aggregate nontrivial scalar source energy on singular packets}.
}
\]

The second is the real singular Gate–1 arithmetic/explicit-formula content.

---

## 5. What proves aggregate nontrivial singular energy?

The target is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
\|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho(m).
}
\]

This is a branch-specific aggregate canonical source theorem.

It should be attacked like the ordinary/transition aggregate inputs:

\[
q''_{\mathrm{can}}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

Expanding the \(L^2_x\) norm gives a smoothed local quadratic form:

\[
\int_I
\left|
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)
\right|^2dx.
\]

For the prime-side packet, this contains terms

\[
\sum_{n,n'}
a_n(m)\overline{a_{n'}(m)}
e^{im\log(n/n')}
\widehat{\chi_I}\!\left(\lambda\log(n/n')\right),
\]

where \(\widehat{\chi_I}\) is the local-window kernel. Averaging over routed singular centers gives a zero-restricted Gram matrix similar to AggG1, but with the additional local-window factor

\[
\widehat{\chi_I}\!\left(\lambda\log(n/n')\right).
\]

So singular aggregate scalar energy is still a lower zero-Gram theorem, but now for local \(x\)-averaged source energy rather than finite symbolic rows.

This is coherent with Stack C2.

---

## 6. Multiresolution block count

The multiresolution family must not introduce a super-polynomial loss.

A safe setup:

\[
J=O(\log Q)
\]

blocks, each of dimension

\[
O(R),
\qquad
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Then total projected dimension is

\[
O(R\log Q)
=
O\!\left(
\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}
\right),
\]

still much smaller than \(Q/\log Q\), but this is no longer a pointwise dimension-exclusion theorem. We use aggregate energy, so this is acceptable.

For extraction, define

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}
=
\sum_{j\le J}E_j.
\]

If

\[
\sum_m\rho E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}\ge Q^{-A}\sum_m\rho,
\]

then at least one dyadic projection block contributes on average, but we do not need to identify it globally. The sum itself is scalar-canonical.

If downstream wants a single local certificate \(v_m\), one can choose at each \(m\) a dominant block

\[
j(m)
\]

with

\[
E_{j(m)}(m)
\ge
J^{-1}E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m).
\]

Since

\[
J=Q^{o(1)},
\]

this loses only \(Q^{o(1)}\).

---

## 7. Does multiresolution become source-family downstream?

No, provided the output is used only to certify scalar energy.

We are not feeding each projected block as an independent source \(u_j\) into D4. We use

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)\le C\|F_m\|^2
\]

to conclude

\[
\|F_m\|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Then downstream runs on

\[
u=q''_{\mathrm{can}}
\]

exactly as before.

So multiresolution projected singular energy is not a forbidden source-family redesign. It is only a scalar-source detection method.

This distinction is important.

---

## 8. Corrected singular Stack C2 theorem

The singular branch should be stated as follows.

### Deterministic frame coverage

There exist projections

\[
P_{R,j}:L^2(I)\to V_{R,j},
\qquad j=0,\ldots,J,
\]

with

\[
J\le Q^{o(1)}
\]

such that for the effective singular source class,

\[
\sum_{j=0}^{J}
\|P_{R,j}F_m\|^2
\le
C Q^{o(1)}\|F_m\|^2.
\]

Only the upper inequality is needed for transfer from projected energy to scalar energy. A lower coverage inequality is useful if one wants to reduce the aggregate theorem to total source energy.

### Aggregate projected singular energy

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
\sum_{j=0}^{J}
\|P_{R,j}F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m).
}
\]

### Extraction

From the aggregate theorem and upper bounds, extract

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{sing}}
\]

with polynomial weight and

\[
\sum_j\|P_{R,j}F_m\|^2\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

on \(\mathcal G_{\mathrm{sing}}\).

### Transfer

Since

\[
\sum_j\|P_{R,j}F_m\|^2
\le
Q^{o(1)}\|F_m\|^2,
\]

we get

\[
\|F_m\|^2\ge Q^{-A''}.
\]

Thus scalar canonical Gate–1 holds.

---

## 9. Remaining singular arithmetic theorem

The unresolved singular arithmetic theorem is now precise:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
\sum_j
\left\|
P_{R,j}
[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)
]
\right\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m).
}
\]

Expanding projections gives canonical test-function sums:

\[
\left\langle
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x),
\Psi_{j,\ell}(x)
\right\rangle.
\]

For the prime side,

\[
\sum_n c_n(m)e^{im\log n}
\int_I
\lambda^3 e^{i\lambda x\log n}
\overline{\Psi_{j,\ell}(x)}\,dx.
\]

Thus the proof reduces to zero-restricted aggregate lower sampling for these actual canonical test functions.

This is exactly aligned with the current actual-coefficient philosophy.

---

## Final Agent 5 conclusion

The singular branch should use:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
=
\sum_j
\left\|
P_{R,j}
[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)
]
\right\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
}
\]

The singular theorem must be **absolute aggregate projected energy**, not merely normalized capture:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}
\ge
Q^{-A}\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho.
}
\]

This gives scalar canonical Gate–1 after extraction, without raw sine diagnostics, without half-leading tail, and without source-family downstream.

I’ll now simplify the singular branch: if projected multiresolution energy is only used to certify scalar \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\) energy, the cleanest proof object may be the local \(L^2\) energy itself.

_Thought for 14s_

Continuing Agent 5: simplify the singular branch further.

The previous correction was:

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(m)
=
\sum_j
\left\|
P_{R,j}
[
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)
]
\right\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
\]

This is safe because it is scalar-canonical. But if the projections are used only to certify scalar source energy, then the cleanest singular Gate–1 energy is simply the scalar local energy itself:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{L^2}(m)
=
\int_I
\left|
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)
\right|^2dx.
}
\]

This removes the remaining projection-capture issue entirely. The latest Stack C2 update already says the singular branch should use actual canonical projected energy rather than raw sine diagnostics; pushing one step further, the local \(L^2\) energy is the maximal canonical projection and is automatically downstream-compatible. 

## 1. Local \(L^2\) singular Gate–1

Define

\[
F_m(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x),
\qquad I=[-c,c].
\]

Set

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{L^2}(m)=\|F_m\|_{L^2(I)}^2.
}
\]

Then the transfer statement is tautological:

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{L^2}(m)\ge Q^{-A}
\Longrightarrow
\text{scalar canonical Gate--1 at }m.
\]

No coefficient identity, no Riesz bound, no projection coverage, no half-leading remainder, no multiresolution block count.

So the singular branch can be stated with the least possible deterministic overhead:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
\int_I
\left|
\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)
\right|^2dx
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m).
}
\]

This is now purely an **aggregate scalar canonical source theorem**.

---

## 2. Why not keep projections?

Projected energy is useful if one wants finite-dimensional observables compatible with O2/O3-style frames. But for Gate–1 alone, projections only introduce a possible noncapture defect:

\[
P_RF_m\approx0
\quad
\text{while}
\quad
F_m\not\approx0.
\]

Multiresolution fixes this by approximating \(F_m\), but then it is effectively reconstructing the local \(L^2\) energy. Therefore, for the singular Gate–1 branch, the local \(L^2\) energy is cleaner.

The only reason to keep projections would be if the aggregate lower-sampling theorem is easier for finitely many test functions than for the full local \(L^2\) square. But expanding the full \(L^2\) square already gives a canonical positive kernel, so it is not obviously harder.

---

## 3. Fubini reduction of aggregate singular \(L^2\)

The aggregate singular energy is

\[
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
\int_I
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)|^2dx.
\]

Change variables

\[
t=m+\lambda x,
\qquad dt=\lambda dx.
\]

Then

\[
\int_I
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)|^2dx
=
\lambda^{-1}
\int_{m+\lambda I}
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(t)|^2dt.
\]

So

\[
\sum_m\rho(m)E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{L^2}(m)
=
\lambda^{-1}
\int
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(t)|^2
W_{\mathrm{sing}}(t)\,dt,
\]

where

\[
W_{\mathrm{sing}}(t)
=
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)\mathbf 1_{m+\lambda I}(t)
\]

or a smoothed-window analogue.

Thus the singular aggregate theorem reduces to a weighted continuous \(L^2\) lower bound:

\[
\boxed{
\int
|q''_{\mathrm{can}}(t)|^2
W_{\mathrm{sing}}(t)\,dt
\ge
Q^{-A}
\lambda^{-5}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho(m)
}
\]

after accounting for the \(\lambda^3\) normalization.

This is useful because it moves singular Gate–1 away from finite anti-design language and into a continuous weighted source-energy estimate.

---

## 4. Explicit-formula expansion

Expanding

\[
q''_{\mathrm{can}}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

in the weighted \(L^2\) integral gives

\[
\int |q''_{\mathrm{can}}(t)|^2W(t)\,dt
=
\int |P_2(t)+D_2(t)+B_2(t)+E_2(t)|^2W(t)\,dt.
\]

For the prime packet part,

\[
P_2(t)\sim \sum_n a_n n^{-it},
\]

so

\[
\int |P_2(t)|^2W(t)\,dt
=
\sum_{n,n'}a_n\overline{a_{n'}}
\widehat W(\log(n/n')).
\]

Thus singular aggregate \(L^2\) is governed by the Gram kernel

\[
\widehat W_{\mathrm{sing}}(\log(n/n')).
\]

This is structurally similar to the ordinary block-rank-one zero-Gram theorem, except the weight \(W_{\mathrm{sing}}\) is a union of small singular windows rather than a macroscopic smooth window.

The needed theorem is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{weighted lower Gram bound for the actual canonical source under }W_{\mathrm{sing}}.
}
\]

It is not a diagnostic sine-moment theorem.

---

## 5. The real obstacle: support of \(W_{\mathrm{sing}}\)

The difficulty is not transfer. It is whether the singular windows have enough total measure and distribution.

If

\[
W_{\mathrm{sing}}
\]

is too sparse or concentrated, then the weighted \(L^2\) integral might be small even if \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\) has large global energy.

So the singular branch needs one of:

### A. direct branch lower bound

\[
\int
|q''_{\mathrm{can}}|^2W_{\mathrm{sing}}
\ge
Q^{-A}
\int W_{\mathrm{sing}};
\]

### B. density/coverage theorem

\[
W_{\mathrm{sing}}
\]

has enough macroscopic distribution to sample canonical \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\) energy;

### C. branch-complete compensation

if \(W_{\mathrm{sing}}\) misses energy, then ordinary/transition weights cover the missed region.

The branch-complete version is probably safest:

\[
W_{\mathrm{ord}}+W_{\mathrm{tr}}+W_{\mathrm{sing}}
\]

should cover the routed packet region with bounded overlap and no large unsampled gaps.

Then one proves aggregate Gate–1 for the **sum over branches**:

\[
\boxed{
\int
|q''_{\mathrm{can}}(t)|^2
\left(
W_{\mathrm{ord}}(t)+W_{\mathrm{tr}}(t)+W_{\mathrm{sing}}(t)
\right)dt
\ge
Q^{-A}
\int
\left(
W_{\mathrm{ord}}+W_{\mathrm{tr}}+W_{\mathrm{sing}}
\right)dt.
}
\]

The branch-specific energies are then just different local normalizations of the same scalar source.

---

## 6. Comparison of three singular observables

### Raw sine moments

\[
S_R^{\mathrm{raw}}
=
\left(
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right)_{k\le R}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{diagnostic only unless coefficient identity + tail nonaliasing are proved.}
}
\]

### Projected/multiresolution energy

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}
=
\sum_j\|P_{R,j}F_m\|^2.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{safe and scalar-canonical, but may be unnecessary if local }L^2\text{ is allowed.}
}
\]

### Full local \(L^2\) energy

\[
E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{L^2}
=
\|F_m\|^2.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{best transfer object; arithmetic theorem becomes weighted }L^2\text{ lower sampling.}
}
\]

The local \(L^2\) formulation is the cleanest for Stack C2 unless the proof specifically needs finite-dimensional singular coordinates for extraction or O2/O3 coupling.

---

## 7. Does this create a source-family problem?

No.

The source remains

\[
u=q''_{\mathrm{can}}.
\]

We are not feeding separate projected components into D4. We are only certifying

\[
\|q''_{\mathrm{can}}\|_{L^2(\text{local window})}^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Then downstream runs on the same scalar canonical source.

So the local \(L^2\) singular branch is fully compatible with D4/Gate–2.

---

## 8. Updated singular recommendation

I now recommend the singular branch be formulated as:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
=
\int_I
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)|^2dx.
}
\]

Then the singular aggregate theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)E_{\mathrm{sing}}(m)
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}\rho(m).
}
\]

Good-subset extraction gives singular packets with scalar canonical Gate–1 directly.

Projected or raw sine observables can remain auxiliary diagnostics:

\[
\text{raw sine moments}
\to
\text{diagnostic;}
\]

\[
\text{projected energy}
\to
\text{finite-dimensional proxy;}
\]

\[
\text{local }L^2\text{ energy}
\to
\text{actual proof object.}
\]

The singular branch can be simplified:

## 1. Larger simplification: define Gate–1 as local scalar source energy

Let each branch \(b\in\{\mathrm{ord},\mathrm{tr},\mathrm{sing}\}\) have a local scale \(\lambda_b(m)\) and window \(I_b\). Define

\[
F_{b,m}(x)
=
\lambda_b^3 q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda_b x),
\]

and

\[
\boxed{

\int_{I_b}

Then branch Gate–1 becomes simply

\[
\boxed{
E_{1,b}^{L^2}(m)\ge Q^{-A}.
}

This is exactly the scalar source energy needed downstream. No branch-specific projection transfer is required.

by a single scalar object:

}

## 2. Does this lose the existing ordinary AggG1 progress?

Not necessarily. The local \(L^2\) theorem can be proved through finite projections.

For ordinary packets, \(T_{\mathrm{can}}X_{\mathrm{can}}\) remains useful as a **proof device**:

\[
\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X_{\mathrm{can}}(m)\|^2
\le
C Q^{C}
E_{1,\mathrm{ord}}^{L^2}(m)
\]

or conversely, if the finite rows form a stable source frame on the ordinary local class,

\[
E_{1,\mathrm{ord}}^{L^2}(m)
\le
Q^C
\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X_{\mathrm{can}}(m)\|^2
+
\text{controlled tail}.
\]

The current block-rank-one AggG1 theorem is still valuable if it proves

\[
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}
\rho\|T_{\mathrm{can}}X_{\mathrm{can}}\|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{\mathcal C_{\mathrm{ord}}}\rho.
\]

Then finite-row-to-\(L^2\) transfer gives aggregate ordinary scalar source energy.

So the ordinary architecture becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{block-rank-one finite-row AggG1}
\Rightarrow
\text{aggregate local }L^2\text{ source energy}.
}
\]

The final proof object downstream is still \(L^2\) scalar source energy.

---

## 3. Transition branch becomes cleaner

Transition currently uses

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m)
=
\left(
\mu^{-r}\partial_x^r
[\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)]_{x=0}
\right)_{0\le r\le R}.
\]

That is useful to prove local \(L^2\) energy via a jet-to-energy inequality:

\[
\|\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(m)\|\ge Q^{-A}
\Longrightarrow
E_{1,\mathrm{tr}}^{L^2}(m)\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

But the clean branch theorem can be stated directly as

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}
\rho(m)
\int_I
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)|^2dx
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{tr}}}\rho(m).
}
\]

Then \(\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}\) becomes a proof mechanism, not the branch definition.

This avoids the question of whether a finite weighted jet misses energy in directions not seen by the first \(R\) derivatives.

---

## 4. Singular branch becomes fully canonical

For singular packets, the local \(L^2\) formulation is strictly cleaner than raw or projected versions:

\[
\boxed{
E_{1,\mathrm{sing}}^{L^2}(m)
=
\int_I
|\lambda^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda x)|^2dx.
}
\]

Raw sine moments become diagnostic.

Projected energies become optional tools for proving the local \(L^2\) lower bound.

The singular aggregate theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m)
E_{1,\mathrm{sing}}^{L^2}(m)
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_{\mathrm{sing}}}
\rho(m).
}
\]

This removes all singular transfer audits:

\[
\text{coefficient identity},\quad
\text{tail nonaliasing},\quad
\text{low-mode capture},\quad
\text{multiresolution coverage}.
\]

Those only matter if one chooses to prove this theorem via a finite singular expansion.

---

## 5. Fubini turns branch aggregate \(L^2\) into a global weighted \(L^2\) theorem

For each branch,

\[
E_{1,b}^{L^2}(m)
=
\int_{I_b}
|\lambda_b^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda_b x)|^2dx.
\]

Changing variables \(t=m+\lambda_b x\),

\[
E_{1,b}^{L^2}(m)
=
\lambda_b^{-1}
\int_{m+\lambda_b I_b}
|\lambda_b^3q''_{\mathrm{can}}(t)|^2dt.
\]

Summing over \(m\),

\[
\sum_{b,m}
\rho_b(m)E_{1,b}^{L^2}(m)
=
\int
|q''_{\mathrm{can}}(t)|^2
W_{\mathrm{branch}}(t)\,dt,
\]

where

\[
W_{\mathrm{branch}}(t)
=
\sum_{b,m}
\rho_b(m)\lambda_b^5
\mathbf 1_{m+\lambda_b I_b}(t)
\]

up to smoothing conventions.

Thus branch-complete Gate–1 reduces to:

\[
\boxed{
\int
|q''_{\mathrm{can}}(t)|^2
W_{\mathrm{branch}}(t)\,dt
\ge
Q^{-A}
\int W_{\mathrm{branch}}(t)\,dt
}
\]

after normalization.

This is very attractive: it makes Gate–1 a single weighted \(L^2\) lower bound for the scalar canonical source.

---

## 6. Explicit formula form of unified \(L^2\) AggG1

Expanding

\[
q''_{\mathrm{can}}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

the main prime-side quadratic piece is

\[
\int
\left|
\sum_n a_n n^{-it}
\right|^2
W(t)\,dt
=
\sum_{n,n'}
a_n\overline{a_{n'}}
\widehat W(\log(n/n')).
\]

So the unified branch-complete \(L^2\) theorem is a weighted Gram lower bound for the actual canonical packet under

\[
W=W_{\mathrm{branch}}.
\]

This is compatible with Agent 1’s block-rank-one zero-Gram theorem, but it is not identical. Agent 1’s theorem samples zeros and refined cells; this theorem samples branch windows and local scales.

The two can be connected if \(W_{\mathrm{branch}}\) is generated from the routed zero/packet centers. Then the smoothed zero-Gram law controls

\[
\widehat W(\log(n/n')).
\]

The main arithmetic object remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual-coefficient zero-restricted Gram lower bound.}
}
\]

But the proof target is now scalar \(L^2\), not branch-specific coordinates.

---

## 7. How O2/O3 and forbidden wall fit

Corrected Stack C2 still needs local O2/O3 and forbidden wall conditions on the extracted subset. The extraction energy should now use

\[
E_1(m)=E_{1,b}^{L^2}(m)
\]

instead of a branch-specific projection.

The joint aggregate theorem becomes

\[
\boxed{
\int
F_{L^2}
F_{23}
F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}
\,d\mu
\ge
Q^{-A}\mu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

Here

\[
F_{L^2}(m)=
\min\left(
\frac{E_{1,b}^{L^2}(m)}{\eta_1},
1
\right).
\]

This removes branch-transfer factors from the extraction theorem. Once \(F_{L^2}\) is good, scalar Gate–1 is good by definition.

So Agent 5’s branch contribution to Stack C2 becomes simpler:

\[
\boxed{
\text{define }E_1\text{ as local scalar }L^2\text{ source energy in every branch.}
}
\]

---

## 8. Potential downside: finite-dimensional O2/O3 coupling

The only concern is that O2/O3 may be formulated in terms of finite jets or rows. If Gate–1 is local \(L^2\), but O2/O3 uses the augmented finite matrix

\[
\mathcal A_m,
\]

we need both to hold on the extracted subset:

\[
E_{L^2}(m)\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
E_{23}(m)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

That is exactly what the joint aggregate theorem supplies.

There is no need for \(E_{L^2}\) and \(E_{23}\) to be the same kind of object. The extraction layer only needs capped factors.

Thus local \(L^2\) Gate–1 is compatible with finite-dimensional O2/O3.

---

## 9. Revised Agent 5 recommendation

Use the following branch-complete Gate–1 definition:

\[
\boxed{
E_1(m)
=
\int_{I_b}
|\lambda_b^3 q''_{\mathrm{can}}(m+\lambda_b x)|^2dx
\quad
\text{for }m\in\mathcal C_b.
}
\]

Then the branch-complete aggregate Gate–1 theorem is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_b
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_b}
\rho_b(m)E_1(m)
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_b
\sum_{m\in\mathcal C_b}
\rho_b(m).
}
\]

Branch-specific finite observables become proof tools:

\[
T_{\mathrm{can}}X_{\mathrm{can}}
\Rightarrow
E_1
\quad\text{ordinary;}
\]

\[
\mathcal J_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
\Rightarrow
E_1
\quad\text{transition;}
\]

\[
P_R F
\text{ or }E_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{multi}}
\Rightarrow
E_1
\quad\text{singular.}
\]

But the Stack C2 proof object is local \(L^2\) source energy.

---

## Final result of this attack

The singular simplification suggests a broader correction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate--1 should be local scalar }L^2\text{ energy of }q''_{\mathrm{can}}
\text{ in every branch.}
}
\]

This eliminates all branch-to-canonical transfer issues.

The remaining proof burden becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{branch-complete aggregate weighted }L^2\text{ lower bound for }q''_{\mathrm{can}}.
}
\]

This is a single canonical source theorem, compatible with corrected Stack C2 and with the downstream forbidden-channel requirement.

## Assistant (2026-04-28 03:33:51)

I’ll focus on scalar compatibility of the O2/O3 determinant route: whether a phase-aligned pure branch can survive inside the full canonical determinant under the Stack C2 weight, rather than becoming a projected-source certificate.

_Thought for 7s_

Agent 5 — full determinant branch-survival under Stack C2 weight.

The instruction is to test whether a sectorial pure-branch exterior determinant can certify the **full scalar canonical augmented determinant**, not merely a projected branch determinant. This is now one of the key O2/O3 compatibility gates in the corrected Stack C2 architecture. 

## 1. Full determinant decomposition by branch count

Write the full augmented O2/O3 determinant schematically as

\[
D_{\mathrm{full}}(m)=\det A_m^{\mathrm{full}},
\]

where \(A_m^{\mathrm{full}}\) is built from the full canonical source

\[
q''_{\mathrm{can}}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

Each column/row moment in \(A_m^{\mathrm{full}}\) decomposes into canonical pieces:

\[
A_m^{\mathrm{full}}
=
A_m^{P}
+
A_m^{D}
+
A_m^{B}
+
A_m^{E}.
\]

By multilinearity,

\[
D_{\mathrm{full}}
=
\sum_{\beta}D_\beta,
\]

where \(\beta\) records how many exterior factors come from each component:

\[
\beta=(\beta_P,\beta_D,\beta_B,\beta_E),
\qquad
|\beta|=R+2.
\]

The candidate phase-aligned piece is usually

\[
D_{\mathrm{dom}}=D_{(R+2,0,0,0)}
\]

or the analogous folded-dual pure component, depending on which branch has controlled phase and multiplier geometry.

So the scalar-compatibility question is:

\[
\boxed{
\int |D_{\mathrm{full}}|^2\,d\nu
\ge
Q^{-A}
\int |D_{\mathrm{dom}}|^2\,d\nu?
}
\]

Here the Stack C2 measure is

\[
d\nu=F_1F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N\,d\rho
\]

after dyadic normalization and geometric-bad removal.

---

## 2. Why pure-branch positivity is not enough

Suppose Agent 4 proves that \(D_{\mathrm{dom}}\) has sectorial exterior coefficients:

\[
D_{\mathrm{dom}}(m)=\sum_S C_S^{\mathrm{dom}}e^{-im\log N_S}
\]

with \(C_S^{\mathrm{dom}}\) lying in a sector of width \(<\pi/2\), so exact product-collision classes do not cancel internally.

That only proves a lower bound for

\[
\int |D_{\mathrm{dom}}|^2\,d\nu.
\]

It does **not** imply a lower bound for

\[
\int |D_{\mathrm{full}}|^2\,d\nu
\]

because

\[
D_{\mathrm{full}}=D_{\mathrm{dom}}+D_{\mathrm{rest}}
\]

could satisfy

\[
D_{\mathrm{rest}}\approx -D_{\mathrm{dom}}
\]

on the support of \(d\nu\).

Thus the scalar determinant route needs a **branch-survival theorem**. Without it, \(D_{\mathrm{dom}}\) is only a projected/source-family certificate.

---

## 3. Three possible survival mechanisms

### A. Branch-pure dominance

The strongest route is

\[
\boxed{
\int |D_{\mathrm{rest}}|^2\,d\nu
\le
\frac12
\int |D_{\mathrm{dom}}|^2\,d\nu.
}
\]

Then

\[
\int |D_{\mathrm{full}}|^2\,d\nu
\ge
\frac12
\int |D_{\mathrm{dom}}|^2\,d\nu.
\]

This is clean but probably too strong globally, because mixed plus/dual/background/tail exterior terms may have comparable size.

It could hold on a carefully selected sub-branch where one component dominates:

\[
|P_2|\gg |D_2|+|B_2|+|E_2|.
\]

But this is an additional branch-selection theorem. It must preserve the scalar canonical determinant, not replace it with a projected branch determinant.

### B. Branch-count orthogonality

A more plausible route is weighted orthogonality across branch counts:

\[
\int D_\beta\overline{D_{\beta'}}\,d\nu
\approx0
\qquad
(\beta\ne\beta').
\]

Then

\[
\int |D_{\mathrm{full}}|^2\,d\nu
=
\sum_\beta\int |D_\beta|^2\,d\nu
+
\text{small cross terms},
\]

so in particular

\[
\int |D_{\mathrm{full}}|^2\,d\nu
\ge
Q^{-A}\int |D_{\mathrm{dom}}|^2\,d\nu.
\]

This is attractive because plus and folded-dual pieces often have different phase slopes. But the Stack C2 weight

\[
F_1F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N
\]

is itself built from canonical objects and may introduce branch correlations. Orthogonality must be proved **under the weighted measure**, not Lebesgue measure.

The required theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\int
D_\beta\overline{D_{\beta'}}\,F_1F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N\,d\rho
\right|
\le
Q^{-A}
\left(
\int |D_\beta|^2d\nu
\int |D_{\beta'}|^2d\nu
\right)^{1/2}
}
\]

for \(\beta\ne\beta'\), or at least for \(D_{\mathrm{dom}}\) against \(D_{\mathrm{rest}}\).

### C. Sector compatibility across all major branches

If all significant \(D_\beta\) lie in compatible sectors, then they cannot cancel:

\[
D_\beta(m)\in e^{i\theta_0}\{z:|\arg z|\le \pi/4\}
\]

for all major \(\beta\), on the relevant support. Then

\[
|D_{\mathrm{full}}|^2
\gtrsim
\sum_{\beta\in\mathcal B_{\mathrm{major}}}|D_\beta|^2
\]

pointwise or after averaging.

This is elegant but likely hard, because the folded-dual phase and background/tail components need not align with the plus branch. It may be feasible only after a phase normalization or on a restricted branch.

---

## 4. Stack C2 wall weighting may destroy branch orthogonality

The measure

\[
d\nu=F_1F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N\,d\rho
\]

is not neutral.

The forbidden wall factor is

\[
F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}
=
\min\left(
\frac{|H|^2|M_{\mathrm{forb}}\Gamma|^2/\mathcal N_{\mathrm{D4}}}{\eta},
1
\right).
\]

Here

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

is a nonlinear function of the same canonical source. Therefore wall weighting may correlate with plus/dual phases and ruin naive orthogonality.

A safe survival theorem must be wall-weighted:

\[
\boxed{
\int |D_{\mathrm{full}}|^2F_1F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N\,d\rho
\ge
Q^{-A}
\int |D_{\mathrm{dom}}|^2F_1F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N\,d\rho.
}
\]

If this cannot be proved, one could use a modular extraction order:

1. prove determinant branch-survival under \(F_1N\,d\rho\);
2. prove forbidden-wall anti-concentration relative to the determinant-good measure.

But the current Stack C2 formulation prefers the one-shot weighted theorem because it avoids disjoint good sets.

---

## 5. Denominator compatibility: cofactor survival

The determinant numerator is only half of the exterior-pivot ratio. Locally,

\[
F_{23}
\sim
\min\left(
Q^A
\left|
\frac{\det A_m}{\operatorname{Cof}_{ij}(A_m)}
\right|^2,
1
\right)
\]

on a dominant cofactor class.

Even if

\[
D_{\mathrm{dom}}
\]

survives in

\[
D_{\mathrm{full}},
\]

the chosen cofactor denominator might be dominated by an unrelated branch class. Then the pure-branch ratio does not control the full ratio.

We need a matched cofactor theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{(i,j)\in\mathcal M}
|\operatorname{Cof}_{ij}^{\mathrm{matched}}(A_m)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{i,j}
|\operatorname{Cof}_{ij}(A_m)|^2
}
\]

on the same weighted support, where \(\mathcal M\) is the class whose cofactor is analytically matched to the sectorial determinant numerator.

Equivalently, on a polynomial-mass cofactor-pivot subset,

\[
\operatorname{Cof}_{ij}(A_m)
\]

must be controlled by the same branch structure used in \(D_{\mathrm{dom}}\).

Without matched cofactor survival, a phase-aligned determinant lower bound does not prove O2/O3.

---

## 6. Candidate scalar-compatibility theorem

The right theorem should combine numerator and denominator survival.

Let

\[
D_{\mathrm{full}}=\det A_{\mathrm{full}},
\]

and let \(C_{\mathrm{full},ij}\) be a cofactor. Let

\[
D_{\mathrm{dom}},
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{dom},ij}
\]

be the phase-aligned branch components.

A scalar-compatible exterior-pivot theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
\int
\min\left(
Q^A
\left|
\frac{D_{\mathrm{full}}}{C_{\mathrm{full},ij}}
\right|^2,
1
\right)d\nu
\ge
Q^{-B}\nu(C)
}
\]

proved by showing, on a polynomial-mass subset,

\[
|D_{\mathrm{full}}|
\ge
Q^{-A}|D_{\mathrm{dom}}|,
\]

\[
|C_{\mathrm{full},ij}|
\le
Q^{A}|C_{\mathrm{dom},ij}|,
\]

and

\[
\min\left(
Q^{A'}
\left|
\frac{D_{\mathrm{dom}}}{C_{\mathrm{dom},ij}}
\right|^2,
1
\right)
\]

has average \(\ge Q^{-B}\).

So the determinant route must prove three things:

\[
\boxed{
\text{pure branch numerator anti-trough;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{numerator branch survival in the full determinant;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{matched cofactor denominator control.}
}
\]

Agent 4’s phase-aligned divided-difference work addresses only the first part.

---

## 7. Which survival route is most plausible?

I rank them as follows.

### Most plausible: branch-count orthogonality under a neutralized weight

If we can dyadically or angularly freeze the wall factor so that it varies slowly relative to plus/dual phase oscillations, then branch-count orthogonality may work.

A target estimate is:

\[
\int D_{\mathrm{dom}}\overline{D_{\mathrm{rest}}}\,d\nu
\le
\frac12
\int |D_{\mathrm{dom}}|^2d\nu.
\]

This is plausible if \(D_{\mathrm{rest}}\) has different effective frequencies or branch phases.

### Second: phase-compatible full determinant

If plus and folded-dual pieces can both be sector-normalized, then several major branches may add rather than cancel. This is possible but more delicate.

### Least plausible: global branch-pure dominance

The full canonical determinant likely has comparable mixed terms. Pure dominance may hold only on special subpackets.

---

## 8. Source-family risk

If we prove only

\[
\int |D_{\mathrm{dom}}|^2d\nu\ge Q^{-A}\nu(C),
\]

then we have certified a projected plus-branch determinant. That is not enough.

It risks becoming a source-family theorem because \(D_{\mathrm{dom}}\) is not the determinant of the full scalar canonical augmented map.

To remain scalar-compatible, the theorem must mention

\[
D_{\mathrm{full}}
\]

and

\[
C_{\mathrm{full},ij}
\]

explicitly.

Therefore the phase-aligned route must be phrased as a **survival theorem inside the full determinant**, not as a standalone branch determinant theorem.

---

## Final Agent 5 verdict

The phase-aligned determinant route is scalar-compatible only if it proves:

\[
\boxed{
\int |D_{\mathrm{full}}|^2d\nu
\ge
Q^{-A}
\int |D_{\mathrm{dom}}|^2d\nu
}
\]

and, for the pivot denominator,

\[
\boxed{
|C_{\mathrm{full},ij}|
\le
Q^A |C_{\mathrm{dom},ij}|
}
\]

on a polynomial-mass matched cofactor class, or the equivalent harmonic-exterior ratio statement.

The best current attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{branch-count orthogonality under the Stack C2 weight}
}
\]

plus

\[
\boxed{
\text{matched cofactor mass via basis design}.
}
\]

Without these, Agent 4’s sectorial pure-branch determinant is only a projected-source certificate and does not prove the full scalar canonical O2/O3 condition.

## Assistant (2026-04-28 03:35:44)

I’ll push the determinant-survival problem further: reduce branch-count orthogonality to a concrete phase-frequency separation estimate, then identify how wall weighting can be neutralized or where it breaks.

_Thought for 4s_

Continuing Agent 5: full determinant branch-survival, now focusing on **branch-count orthogonality under Stack C2 weights**.

The previous conclusion was that a sectorial pure-branch determinant \(D_{\mathrm{dom}}\) is not enough. O2/O3 needs the full scalar determinant \(D_{\mathrm{full}}\), so we need survival:

\[
\int |D_{\mathrm{full}}|^2\,d\nu
\ge
Q^{-A}
\int |D_{\mathrm{dom}}|^2\,d\nu,
\]

under the Stack C2 measure

\[
d\nu=F_1F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N\,d\rho.
\]

The current attack is to determine whether this can follow from branch-count orthogonality. 

## 1. Branch-count decomposition

Write

\[
D_{\mathrm{full}}(m)=\sum_{\beta}D_\beta(m),
\]

where \(\beta\) records the number of exterior factors drawn from

\[
P_2,\quad D_2,\quad B_2,\quad E_2.
\]

Let the candidate dominant pure branch be

\[
D_0:=D_{\mathrm{dom}}.
\]

Then

\[
D_{\mathrm{full}}=D_0+R,
\qquad
R=\sum_{\beta\ne0}D_\beta.
\]

A sufficient survival condition is

\[
\left|
\int D_0\overline{R}\,d\nu
\right|
\le
\frac14
\int |D_0|^2\,d\nu
\]

and

\[
\int |R|^2\,d\nu
\ge0.
\]

Then

\[
\int |D_{\mathrm{full}}|^2\,d\nu
=
\int |D_0|^2\,d\nu
+
2\Re\int D_0\overline{R}\,d\nu
+
\int |R|^2\,d\nu
\ge
\frac12\int |D_0|^2\,d\nu.
\]

So the core estimate is:

\[
\boxed{
\int D_0\overline{D_\beta}\,d\nu
\text{ is small for all }\beta\ne0.
}
\]

---

## 2. Phase-frequency form of the cross term

Each determinant component has an exterior Dirichlet expansion:

\[
D_\beta(m)
=
\sum_S C_{\beta,S} e^{-im\log N_{\beta,S}}.
\]

Thus

\[
\int D_0\overline{D_\beta}\,d\nu
=
\sum_{S,T}
C_{0,S}\overline{C_{\beta,T}}
\widehat{\nu}
\left(
\log N_{0,S}-\log N_{\beta,T}
\right).
\]

Therefore branch-count orthogonality reduces to a weighted Fourier decay / separation statement:

\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\nu}(\omega)
\text{ is small on cross-branch exterior frequency differences.}
}
\]

More precisely, we need

\[
\sum_{S,T}
|C_{0,S}|\,|C_{\beta,T}|\,
\left|
\widehat{\nu}
\left(
\log N_{0,S}-\log N_{\beta,T}
\right)
\right|
\le
Q^{-A}
\left(
\sum_S|C_{0,S}|^2
\right)^{1/2}
\left(
\sum_T|C_{\beta,T}|^2
\right)^{1/2},
\]

or the corresponding clustered version.

This is the exact analytic object behind “branch-count orthogonality.”

---

## 3. Why unweighted smoothing might work

If

\[
d\nu = w_T(m)\,dm
\]

with a smooth macroscopic window of length \(H\), then

\[
\widehat{\nu}(\omega)
=
H\,\widehat w(H\omega)e^{-iT\omega}.
\]

So cross terms are killed unless

\[
|\omega|\lesssim H^{-1}.
\]

If plus-branch exterior products and mixed plus/dual exterior products have separated phase slopes, then

\[
|\log N_{0,S}-\log N_{\beta,T}|
\gg H^{-1}Q^B,
\]

and orthogonality follows by rapid decay.

This is analogous to Agent 1’s exact-ratio zero-Gram mechanism.

Thus branch-count survival is plausible under two conditions:

\[
\boxed{
\text{macroscopic smooth measure;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{cross-branch exterior frequency separation.}
}
\]

---

## 4. Why Stack C2 weighting is the problem

In Stack C2,

\[
d\nu
=
F_1F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N\,d\rho.
\]

The factors

\[
F_1,\quad F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}},\quad N
\]

are not smooth external weights. They are nonlinear functions of the same canonical source and therefore can contain high-frequency branch phases.

If \(F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}\) has Fourier content at exactly the cross-branch frequency difference, then

\[
\widehat\nu(\log N_{0,S}-\log N_{\beta,T})
\]

need not be small.

So the survival theorem cannot simply cite macroscopic smoothing. It needs one of the following.

---

## 5. Three possible repairs

### Repair A: freeze the Stack C2 weight on coarse atoms

Partition the height interval into atoms \(I_\alpha\) on which

\[
F_1F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N
\]

is nearly constant:

\[
F_1F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N
=
c_\alpha(1+O(Q^{-A}))
\quad
\text{on }I_\alpha.
\]

Then on each atom the cross term reduces to smooth unweighted branch orthogonality:

\[
\int_{I_\alpha}D_0\overline{D_\beta}d\rho
\approx0.
\]

This requires the atom length to remain large enough for Fourier decay:

\[
|I_\alpha|\gg
\left|
\log N_{0,S}-\log N_{\beta,T}
\right|^{-1}Q^B.
\]

But if the weight oscillates at prime-log speed, the atoms may be too short. Then this repair fails.

So Repair A requires a **slow-variation theorem**:

\[
\boxed{
F_1F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N
\text{ has no significant cross-branch Fourier content.}
}
\]

That is unlikely without additional structure.

---

### Repair B: include the weight in the determinant expansion

Instead of trying to neutralize the weight, expand it.

For example,

\[
F_1
\]

is a capped version of Gate–1 energy, and

\[
F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}
\]

is capped forbidden D4 energy. Capping is nonlinear, but approximate it by a polynomial or dyadic indicator.

On a dyadic/capped level set, one can replace

\[
F_1F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N
\]

by structured products of canonical polynomials. Then the survival inequality becomes a higher-order exterior moment inequality.

This is possible in principle but increases exterior degree. It risks pushing product lengths beyond the range where zero-sampling can be controlled.

The needed theorem becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{higher-order branch-count orthogonality for determinant }D_\beta
\text{ times the Stack C2 weight factors.}
}
\]

This is very hard but honest.

---

### Repair C: use joint theorem with full determinant from the start

Avoid proving survival from \(D_{\mathrm{dom}}\) to \(D_{\mathrm{full}}\). Instead formulate the O2/O3 theorem directly for

\[
D_{\mathrm{full}}
\]

under the Stack C2 weight.

That is,

\[
\int
\min\left(
Q^A
\left|
\frac{D_{\mathrm{full}}}{C_{\mathrm{full},ij}}
\right|^2,
1
\right)d\nu
\ge Q^{-B}\nu(C).
\]

Then \(D_{\mathrm{dom}}\) is only a lower-bound device inside the proof, not the theorem statement.

This is logically safest. The proof can still use sectorial branch pieces, but it must prove that they survive after including all other pieces and the weight.

This is the formulation I recommend.

---

## 6. Matched cofactor version of survival

The same issue appears for cofactors.

Let

\[
C_{\mathrm{full},ij}=C_{\mathrm{dom},ij}+C_{\mathrm{rest},ij}.
\]

For the exterior-pivot ratio, we need denominator control:

\[
|C_{\mathrm{full},ij}|
\le
Q^A |C_{\mathrm{dom},ij}|
\]

on a polynomial-mass pivot subset, or at least

\[
|C_{\mathrm{dom},ij}|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{i,j}|C_{\mathrm{full},ij}|^2
\]

on a matched cofactor class.

Again, branch-count orthogonality can help if

\[
\int |C_{\mathrm{full},ij}|^2d\nu
\asymp
\sum_\beta
\int |C_{\beta,ij}|^2d\nu.
\]

But the same weight problem arises.

Thus the clean theorem is a **matched full-pivot theorem**:

There exists a pivot class \((i,j)\) and a polynomial-mass subset such that

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{D_{\mathrm{full}}}{C_{\mathrm{full},ij}}
\right|
\ge
Q^{-A}
\left|
\frac{D_{\mathrm{dom}}}{C_{\mathrm{dom},ij}}
\right|
}
\]

or more directly,

\[
\boxed{
\min\left(
Q^A
\left|
\frac{D_{\mathrm{full}}}{C_{\mathrm{full},ij}}
\right|^2,
1
\right)
}
\]

has nontrivial weighted average.

The branch determinant is only a proof witness.

---

## 7. A concrete survival theorem to target

The most useful scalar-compatibility theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Weighted full-determinant branch survival.}
}
\]

Let \(d\nu=F_1F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N\,d\rho\). Suppose \(D_{\mathrm{dom}}\) is a phase-aligned branch determinant component. Then either

\[
\int |D_{\mathrm{full}}|^2d\nu
\ge
Q^{-A}
\int |D_{\mathrm{dom}}|^2d\nu,
\]

or there is a structured cancellation certificate:

\[
D_{\mathrm{rest}}\approx -D_{\mathrm{dom}}
\]

on a \(d\nu\)-large set.

The second alternative should imply a new algebraic relation among the canonical components \(P_2,D_2,B_2,E_2\). If such a relation is impossible, survival follows.

This suggests a new attack:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove that branch-cancellation }D_{\mathrm{rest}}\approx-D_{\mathrm{dom}}
\text{ forces an impossible AFE/gamma/tail identity.}
}
\]

That may be more tractable than estimating all cross terms.

---

## 8. Current assessment

### What is viable

The determinant route can remain scalar-compatible if the theorem is stated for the full objects:

\[
D_{\mathrm{full}},
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{full},ij},
\]

and uses pure branch pieces only as witnesses.

### What is unsafe

A theorem only for

\[
D_{\mathrm{dom}}
\]

or

\[
D_{\mathrm{dom}}/C_{\mathrm{dom},ij}
\]

is not enough. It becomes a projected branch/source-family statement.

### Most important missing estimate

\[
\boxed{
\int D_{\mathrm{dom}}\overline{D_{\mathrm{rest}}}\,d\nu
\text{ is not too negative.}
}
\]

or equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\text{no weighted branch cancellation of the full determinant.}
}
\]

---

## Final result of this attack

The phase-aligned determinant path now has an exact scalar-compatibility gate:

\[
\boxed{
\text{weighted full-determinant branch survival under }
d\nu=F_1F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N\,d\rho.
}
\]

To prove it, the best current route is either:

\[
\boxed{
\text{branch-count orthogonality after neutralizing the Stack C2 weight}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{show weighted cancellation }D_{\mathrm{rest}}\approx-D_{\mathrm{dom}}
\text{ forces an impossible canonical identity.}
}
\]

Until one of those is proved, Agent 4’s sectorial divided-difference determinant is a promising witness but not yet a proof of the full scalar O2/O3 condition.
