## Assistant (2026-04-28 04:13:42)

I’ll now test the \(\alpha\)-tangent issue against the defining property of the singular coherence constraint. If \(\mathcal K_9\) really vanishes on the actual EF family, then its linearization should automatically kill genuine source-parameter tangents.

_Thought for 22s_

Continuing Agent 5 — \(\alpha\)-tangent versus D4 normality.

The concern was:

\[
\alpha\text{ helps O2/O3 determinant survival}
\]

but might enlarge the actual-source singular manifold enough to absorb the D4 normal direction, especially the promising order-nine \(Y12\) channel. The right way to test this is not by comparing raw vectors. It is by **linearizing the singular coherence constraint**. 

## 1. The key correction: use the covariant coherence residual

Let singular actual-source coefficients be

\[
s=s(p),
\]

where \(p\) denotes actual EF parameters:

\[
p=(m,\lambda,\alpha,\text{cutoff/branch parameters},\ldots).
\]

A singular order-nine coherence relation has schematic form

\[
\mathcal K_9(s;p)
=
s_9-\mathcal R_{7\to9}(p)s_7-\mathcal R_{<7\to9}(p)s_{<7}
=
0
\]

for every actual EF-coherent source.

Now differentiate:

\[
D_s\mathcal K_9\,\delta s
+
D_p\mathcal K_9\,\delta p
=
0.
\]

So if \(\delta s=\partial_\alpha s\) is a genuine actual-source tangent, then

\[
D_s\mathcal K_9\,\partial_\alpha s
+
\partial_\alpha \mathcal K_9
=
0.
\]

Therefore the correct normal test is **not**

\[
D_s\mathcal K_9(\delta s_{\mathrm{D4}})\neq0
\]

alone. It is

\[
\boxed{
D_s\mathcal K_9(\delta s_{\mathrm{D4}})
\notin
\operatorname{span}
\left\{
-\,D_p\mathcal K_9(\partial_{p_j})
\right\}_{p_j\text{ allowed actual parameters}}.
}
\]

Equivalently, D4 is normal iff no allowed actual parameter variation \(\delta p\) satisfies

\[
D_s\mathcal K_9(\delta s_{\mathrm{D4}})
+
D_p\mathcal K_9(\delta p)
=
0.
\]

This is the exact finite audit.

---

## 2. Consequence for \(\alpha\)

If \(\alpha\) is admitted as an actual EF source parameter, then \(\partial_\alpha s\) is tangent by definition.

That does **not** automatically kill D4 normality. It only removes the component of D4 residual lying in the one-dimensional parameter-residual direction

\[
-D_\alpha\mathcal K_9.
\]

Thus the correct test is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{rank}
\left[
D_s\mathcal K_9
\left(
T_{\mathrm{tr}\to\mathrm{sing}}
E_{\mathrm{car}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
L_{\mathrm{clean}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\right)
\right]
\quad
\text{modulo }
\operatorname{span}\{D_\alpha\mathcal K_9,D_m\mathcal K_9,D_\lambda\mathcal K_9,\ldots\}.
}
\]

So \(\alpha\)-admission is dangerous only if

\[
D_\alpha\mathcal K_9
\]

spans the same residual direction as the D4 live carrier.

It does not enlarge the tangent space arbitrarily.

---

## 3. The \(Y12\) channel remains promising

D4 gives, schematically,

\[
\delta s_{\mathrm{D4}}
=
H\left(
c_7[\mathsf C_7]\Gamma_G
+
\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_G
+
\alpha_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_{G,2}
\right).
\]

The order-nine coherence residual gives

\[
D_s\mathcal K_9(\delta s_{\mathrm{D4}})
=
H\left[
\left(
\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
-
\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])
\right)\Gamma_G
+
\alpha_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_{G,2}
\right]
\]

up to lower-order tangent corrections.

The clean rank-one hope is the pure

\[
\boxed{
H\,\alpha_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_{G,2}
}
\]

component.

For \(\alpha\)-admission to kill this channel, one would need

\[
D_\alpha\mathcal K_9
\]

to have a component proportional to

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\]

in the same residual codomain.

That is not automatic. In fact, if \(\alpha\) is mainly an AFE branch-phase tilt, then \(\partial_\alpha s\) changes existing actual EF coefficients by phase/log-frequency weights. It is a tangent deformation of the existing source family. It is not generically a new quadratic mixed-block \(Y12\) carrier.

So the default expectation is:

\[
\boxed{
\partial_\alpha s\text{ should be tangent to actual EF coherence and should not span the formal }Y12\text{ D4 normal.}
}
\]

But this must be checked.

---

## 4. Fixed-operator versus covariant-operator trap

There is a subtle trap.

If one freezes the operator

\[
\mathcal K_9(\cdot;p_0)
\]

and applies it to \(s(p_0+\delta p)\), then even an actual parameter change can produce a nonzero residual:

\[
\mathcal K_9(s(p_0+\delta p);p_0)
\approx
D_s\mathcal K_9\,\partial_p s\,\delta p.
\]

But the true coherence relation at the new parameter is

\[
\mathcal K_9(s(p_0+\delta p);p_0+\delta p)=0.
\]

The missing term is

\[
D_p\mathcal K_9\,\delta p.
\]

Therefore, using a frozen \(\mathcal K_9\) would falsely classify actual parameter tangents as forbidden normal directions.

The downstream \(\Lambda\) must be **covariant**:

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_p(s)=\mathcal K_9(s;p),
}
\]

with \(p\)-dependence included.

Then actual rows satisfy

\[
\Lambda_p(s(p))=0,
\]

and the forbidden residual sees only deviations from the actual-source manifold, not ordinary chart-parameter motion.

This is important for the global upper.

---

## 5. Finite matrix test

Let the residual codomain of \(\mathcal K_9\) be \(Y\). Define the D4 residual matrix

\[
M_{\mathrm{D4}}
=
D_s\mathcal K_9\,
T_{\mathrm{tr}\to\mathrm{sing}}
E_{\mathrm{car}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
L_{\mathrm{clean}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
:
\mathbb C^2\to Y.
\]

Define the parameter residual matrix

\[
M_{\mathrm{par}}
=
\left[
D_{p_1}\mathcal K_9,\ldots,D_{p_d}\mathcal K_9
\right]
:
\mathbb C^d\to Y.
\]

Allowed parameters include at least

\[
m,\lambda,\alpha
\]

if admitted, and possibly cutoff/normalization/chart parameters. They should not include arbitrary EF coefficients.

The D4 forbidden rank is

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{rank}
\left(
\Pi_{(\operatorname{ran}M_{\mathrm{par}})^\perp}
M_{\mathrm{D4}}
\right).
}
\]

Rank cases:

- rank \(0\): D4 is tangent to the actual EF manifold; no forbidden channel.
- rank \(1\): one forbidden linear combination of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\).
- rank \(2\): raw D4 anisotropy survives.

This is the clean finite audit.

---

## 6. How \(\alpha\) affects the rank

Let

\[

\]

be the parameter matrix without \(\alpha\), and

\[
M_{\mathrm{par}}^{(\alpha)}
=
[M_{\mathrm{par}}^{(0)},D_\alpha\mathcal K_9].
\]

Then \(\alpha\) is compatible with D4 if

\[
\operatorname{rank}
\left(
\Pi_{(\operatorname{ran}M_{\mathrm{par}}^{(\alpha)})^\perp}
M_{\mathrm{D4}}
\right)
\ge1.
\]

It is dangerous if this rank drops from \(1\) or \(2\) to \(0\).

Thus the exact yes/no question is:

\[
\boxed{
D_\alpha\mathcal K_9
\text{ spans the same residual direction as }
D_s\mathcal K_9(T[\mathsf C_{Y12}])
\text{ or not?}
}
\]

If no, \(\alpha\)-twisting is compatible with the singular-discard D4 route.

}

Call this:

}

Then the full admissibility package becomes:

\[
\boxed{

=
\mathrm{AlphaAdmissibility}
+
\mathrm{AlphaD4Compatibility}.
}
\]

This is the correct condition for using \(\alpha\)-twist as a proof-critical O2/O3 tool while keeping the downstream D4 contradiction.

## 1. The residual should be filtered by singular order

Let the singular coefficient tower be

\[

and suppose the actual-source coherence relation at order nine is

=

The tangent equation for an actual parameter \(p_a\) is

\[

+

=

So an actual-source tangent is not detected by the covariant residual. This is correct: actual deformations should be tangent.

Now compare a formal D4 displacement. Its clean part has the triangular shape

These variations carry coherent footprints in several orders:

\delta s_{<7},\quad \delta s_7,\quad \delta s_8,\quad \delta s_9.
\]

The coherence relation then adjusts \(\delta s_9\) according to the changes in lower orders and in the parameter dependence of \(\mathcal R_{7\to9}\).

By contrast, the pure D4 \(Y12\) channel is designed to be a formal order-nine carrier not generated by lower-order actual-source transport. In the residual quotient

\[

Here

is the covariant residual class.

## 3. Why \(\partial_\alpha\) probably does not equal \(Y12\)

=

+
\partial_\alpha \mathcal B_k^{\mathrm{can}},
\]

where \(\omega_j\) is some branch/phase/log-frequency weight.

This is still a **linear actual-source deformation**. It should remain inside the linearization of the EF-coherent source family.

The \(Y12\) carrier, however, came from a promoted mixed-block quadratic carrier, structurally tied to

\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}
=

coupled through the same-point whitening slot. That is not the same type of object as a first-order AFE phase tilt.

This means \(\alpha\)-twisting can be admitted for determinant survival without killing the \(Y12\) D4 channel.

## 1. The finite signature strategy

We need to prove

\[
\mathsf C_{Y12}
\notin
\mathcal T_{\mathrm{par}}
+
\mathcal T_7
+
\mathcal T_{<7}.
\]

The efficient way is not to compute every coefficient. It is to find a signature preserved by all allowed tangent and connection operations, but carried nontrivially by \(Y12\).

A useful signature package is:

\[
\Sigma
=
(\text{source degree},\ \text{branch bidegree},\ \text{same-point quadratic carrier},\ \text{whitening-slot count},\ \text{reflection parity}).
\]

The \(Y12\) carrier came from the promoted quadratic mixed-block object

\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2],
\]

coupled to one same-point linear whitening slot. That gives it a very specific signature:

\[
\boxed{
\Sigma(Y12)
=
(\text{quadratic source-Hessian},\ \text{mixed branch},\ \text{same-point},\ \text{one whitening slot},\ \text{fixed reflection parity}).
}
\]

The question is whether any allowed actual-source tangent or lower connection residual can have the same signature.

---

## 2. Parameter tangents are first-order source deformations

Allowed actual parameters include things like

\[
m,\quad \lambda,\quad \alpha,\quad \text{normalization/cutoff/branch parameters}.
\]

Their tangents act on the actual EF source family by differentiating existing linear packets, phases, weights, or background terms.

Schematically:

\[
\partial_m(a_ne^{-im\log n})
=
-i(\log n)a_ne^{-im\log n},
\]

\[
\partial_\alpha(a_n(\alpha)e^{-im\log n})
=
(\partial_\alpha a_n)e^{-im\log n},
\]

\[
\partial_\lambda F(m+\lambda x)
=
xF'(m+\lambda x)+\text{scale term}.
\]

These operations can raise derivative order, insert log weights, alter phase, or rescale coefficients. But they do **not** create a new second Fréchet derivative source carrier

\[
D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2].
\]

So parameter tangents should lie in the first-source-linear sector:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal T_{\mathrm{par}}
\subset
\{\text{linear EF source deformations + deterministic background/tail tangents}\}.
}
\]

Unless \(\alpha\) is secretly defined to vary the nonlinear source map \(N_0\) itself, \(\partial_\alpha\) cannot generate the \(Y12\) signature.

Thus, generically,

\[
\Sigma(\partial_\alpha u)\ne \Sigma(Y12).
\]

This is the key reason \(\alpha\)-admission should not kill the \(Y12\) D4 channel.

---

## 3. Lower-order connection residuals should not create primitive \(Y12\)

The subspaces

\[
\mathcal T_7=\mathcal R_{7\to9}(Y_7),
\qquad
\mathcal T_{<7}
\]

represent residuals induced from lower-order singular data and lower connection transport.

They can carry order-nine consequences of order-seven or lower objects. But they should not create a **primitive order-nine quadratic same-point Hessian carrier** unless the connection itself contains a quadratic source-Hessian promotion.

So the needed finite structural property is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{7\to9}
\text{ preserves source-Hessian signature and does not promote first-source-linear data into }Y12.
}
\]

If this triangularity holds, then

\[
\mathsf C_{Y12}\notin \mathcal T_7+\mathcal T_{<7}.
\]

This is now a precise finite audit: check whether the singular connection table has any coefficient mapping lower-order linear/connection classes into the \(Y12\) signature sector.

If no such map exists, the \(Y12\) class survives.

---

## 4. Reflection/parity gives a likely separating invariant

The earlier source-grade reflection machinery gives a natural candidate invariant. The mixed-block swap identity and source-grade reflection imply signs of the form

\[
(Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle})^T
=
(-1)^{g+e}
Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}.
\]

The \(Y12\) carrier has a fixed pair

\[
(g,e)
\]

coming from the quadratic mixed-block remainder plus one whitening slot. Parameter tangents such as \(m,\lambda,\alpha\) variations generally preserve the source-linear parity sector. Lower connection transport also preserves the reflection class unless the connection table explicitly mixes parities.

So we should project the residual space onto the \(Y12\)-parity eigenspace:

\[
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}\mathcal Y_9.
\]

Then test:

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}
(\mathcal T_{\mathrm{par}}+\mathcal T_7+\mathcal T_{<7})
=0
\quad\text{but}\quad
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}\mathsf C_{Y12}\ne0.
}
\]

If true, this proves

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\ne0
\quad\text{in}\quad
\mathcal Q_9^{\mathrm{forb}}.
\]

This is the cleanest possible finite proof.

---

## 5. Consequence for D4 rank

Modulo lower connection effects, the D4 residual is

\[
D_s\mathcal K_9(\delta s_{\mathrm{D4}})
\equiv
H\left(
\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_G
+
\alpha_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_{G,2}
\right)
\quad
\text{in }\mathcal Q_9^{\mathrm{forb}}.
\]

Since the clean D4 calculation has

\[
\alpha_9\ne0,
\]

we get a rank-one forbidden channel if

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\ne0.
\]

The forbidden wall factor becomes, at minimum,

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}
\sim
|H|^2\,|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\,
\|[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\|_{\mathcal Q_9^{\mathrm{forb}}}^2
}
\]

up to the \(\Gamma_G\)-mixed term and normalization.

So the proof does not need raw two-dimensional \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\)-anisotropy. The pure \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) channel is already enough if \(Y12\) survives.

---

## 6. What could go wrong?

There are three specific failure modes.

### Failure A: \(\alpha\) is not merely a phase/source parameter

If \(\alpha\) changes the nonlinear source map \(N_0\) itself, then

\[
\partial_\alpha u
\]

could contain second-source-Hessian components. Then

\[
D_\alpha\mathcal K_9
\]

might overlap \(Y12\).

This would make \(\alpha\)-admission dangerous.

But if \(\alpha\) is an AFE tilt, phase deformation, or coefficient weighting parameter, it should remain source-linear and not create \(D^2N_0\)-type carriers.

### Failure B: connection transport creates \(Y12\)

If

\[
\mathcal R_{7\to9}(Y_7)
\]

contains a \(Y12\)-signature term, then \(Y12\) may be lower-connection-induced rather than primitive.

This is a finite connection-table audit.

### Failure C: the singular coherence manifold is defined too broadly

If

\[
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\]

allows arbitrary local EF amplitudes or arbitrary second-source variations, then \(Y12\) becomes tangent by definition.

So the actual-source manifold must allow only genuine arithmetic EF parameters:

\[
m,\lambda,\alpha,\text{ cutoff/normalization}
\]

and fixed source formulas. It must **not** allow free local \(D^2N_0\) amplitudes.

---

## 7. The decisive finite theorem

The next useful theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Y12 Signature Separation Theorem.}
}
\]

Statement:

Let

\[
\mathcal Y_9^{Y12}
\]

be the source-grade/reflection/same-point quadratic signature subspace generated by the promoted carrier \(Y_{12}^{(2)}\) coupled to the same-point whitening slot.

Then:

1. \(\mathsf C_{Y12}\) has nonzero image in \(\mathcal Y_9^{Y12}\);

2. allowed actual-source parameter tangents have zero image in \(\mathcal Y_9^{Y12}\);

3. lower-order connection residuals have zero image in \(\mathcal Y_9^{Y12}\).

Therefore

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\ne0
\quad\text{in}\quad
\mathcal Q_9^{\mathrm{forb}}.
\]

This proves rank at least one for the singular-discard D4 channel.

---

## 8. Current conclusion

The \(Y12\) channel remains the strongest finite-D4 opportunity.

Admitting \(\alpha\) is compatible with D4 provided:

\[
\boxed{
\partial_\alpha
\text{ is source-linear and has no }Y12\text{ signature.}
}
\]

The finite audit should now focus on signature separation:

\[
\boxed{
\Sigma(Y12)
\notin
\Sigma(\mathcal T_{\mathrm{par}})
+
\Sigma(\mathcal T_7)
+
\Sigma(\mathcal T_{<7}).
}
\]

If this holds, then the order-nine \(Y12\) residual supplies a robust rank-one forbidden channel, and \(\alpha\)-twisting remains available for O2/O3 determinant survival without collapsing downstream D4 normality.

\mathcal T_{\mathrm{par}}^{(0)}
+
\mathcal T_7
+
\mathcal T_{<7}
\right),
\]

and

\[
\mathcal Q_9^{\mathrm{forb},\alpha}
=
\mathcal Y_9/
\left(
\mathcal T_{\mathrm{par}}^{(0)}
+
\mathbf C\,D_\alpha\mathcal K_9
+
\mathcal T_7
+
\mathcal T_{<7}
\right).
\]

The finite test is:

\[
\boxed{
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\ne0
\quad
\text{in}
\quad
\mathcal Q_9^{\mathrm{forb},\alpha}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\mathsf C_{Y12}
\notin
\mathcal T_{\mathrm{par}}^{(0)}
+
\mathbf C\,D_\alpha\mathcal K_9
+
\mathcal T_7
+
\mathcal T_{<7}.
}
\]

If this holds, \(\alpha\)-twisting is compatible with the \(Y12\) D4 route.

---

## 3. What kind of tangent is \(\partial_\alpha u\)?

The decisive classification is whether \(\partial_\alpha u\) is source-linear or source-nonlinear.

In the intended tilted-zero / AFE setting, \(\alpha\) should change phases, weights, or tilts of the same explicit-formula source. Then it acts schematically as

\[
\partial_\alpha
\left(
a_n(\alpha)e^{-im\log n}
\right)
=
(\partial_\alpha a_n)e^{-im\log n},
\]

or

\[
\partial_\alpha
\left(
e^{i\Theta_\alpha(m)}b_n e^{im\log n}
\right)
=
i(\partial_\alpha\Theta_\alpha)
e^{i\Theta_\alpha(m)}b_n e^{im\log n}
+
e^{i\Theta_\alpha(m)}(\partial_\alpha b_n)e^{im\log n}.
\]

These are **first-order EF source deformations**. They insert log/phase/weight factors into already existing source atoms.

By contrast, the \(Y12\) carrier comes from a promoted quadratic mixed-block Hessian object:

\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}
=
D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2],
\]

with same-point whitening.

That is a second-source-variation carrier, not a first-order phase or scale deformation.

Thus the structural expectation is:

\[
\boxed{
\Sigma(\partial_\alpha u)
\ne
\Sigma(Y12).
}
\]

So \(\partial_\alpha\) should not kill the \(Y12\) normal direction unless \(\alpha\) secretly changes the nonlinear source map \(N_0\) itself.

---

## 4. Signature separation criterion

Let

\[
\Sigma(Y12)
=
(\text{quadratic source-Hessian},
\text{mixed branch},
\text{same-point},
\text{one whitening slot},
\text{reflection parity}).
\]

The key finite statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}
\left(
\mathcal T_{\mathrm{par}}^{(0)}
+
\mathbf C\,D_\alpha\mathcal K_9
+
\mathcal T_7
+
\mathcal T_{<7}
\right)
=
0,
}
\]

while

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}\mathsf C_{Y12}\ne0.
}
\]

This proves

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\ne0
\quad\text{in}\quad
\mathcal Q_9^{\mathrm{forb},\alpha}.
\]

The likely proof is by source-grade/reflection parity:

- parameter tangents \(\partial_m,\partial_\lambda,\partial_\alpha\) are first-order source-linear;
- \(\mathcal T_7\) transports order-seven coherent data and should not create primitive same-point quadratic \(Y12\);
- \(\mathcal T_{<7}\) is lower-order and cannot produce primitive order-nine \(D^2N_0\)-same-point whitening signature;
- \(Y12\) is a primitive quadratic mixed-block carrier.

---

## 5. What would make \(\alpha\) dangerous?

There are only a few ways for \(\alpha\) to kill the \(Y12\) channel.

### Failure A — \(\alpha\) changes the nonlinear source map

If

\[
\partial_\alpha N_0
\]

contains a second Fréchet source-Hessian term, then

\[
\partial_\alpha u
\]

could carry a \(Y12\)-like signature.

Then \(\alpha\)-admission may make \(Y12\) tangent.

But this would mean \(\alpha\) is not merely an AFE tilt or branch phase. It is changing the nonlinear source algebra.

### Failure B — lower connection transport creates \(Y12\)

If

\[
\mathcal R_{7\to9}(\mathcal Y_7)
\]

contains the same signature as \(Y12\), then \(Y12\) is not primitive order-nine data. It is lower-order connection-induced.

Then the D4 \(Y12\) channel may be killed by \(\mathcal T_7\).

### Failure C — singular manifold is over-enlarged

If

\[
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\]

is defined with arbitrary local EF coefficients or arbitrary quadratic source amplitudes, then \(Y12\) becomes tangent by definition.

This is a definition error. The actual-source manifold must allow only genuine arithmetic parameters, not arbitrary local \(D^2N_0\)-directions.

---

## 6. Consequence for D4 rank

D4 has clean image

\[
\delta s_{\mathrm{D4}}
=

+
\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_G
+
\alpha_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_{G,2}
\right).
\]

After applying the order-nine residual and quotienting lower connection effects,

\[
[D_s\mathcal K_9(\delta s_{\mathrm{D4}})]
=
H\left(
[\beta_9\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_G
+
[\alpha_9\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_{G,2}
\right)
\quad
\text{in }
\mathcal Q_9^{\mathrm{forb},\alpha}.
\]

Since

\[
\alpha_9\ne0,
\]

we get a rank-one channel through \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) if

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\ne0.
\]

Thus the forbidden wall can be defined as

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{K9}
\asymp
\frac{
|H|^2
|
a\,\Gamma_G+b\,\Gamma_{G,2}
|^2
}{
\mathcal N_{\mathrm{D4}}
},
\]

with

\[
b\ne0
\]

in the clean \(Y12\)-survival case.

If the \(\Gamma_G\)-component is contaminated by order-seven transport, the pure \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) channel remains the clean target.

---

## 7. Recommendation on \(\alpha\)

The current best judgment:

\[
\boxed{
\alpha\text{-twisting is compatible with D4 if }\alpha\text{ is a source-linear AFE tilt.}
}
\]

It is dangerous only if \(\alpha\) is promoted to a source-nonlinear deformation that can create \(D^2N_0\)-type \(Y12\) carriers.

So the correct \(\alpha\)-policy is:

1. Permit \(\alpha\) for O2/O3 branch-count survival if AlphaAdmissibility holds.
2. Include \(\partial_\alpha u\) in the tangent space for D4 normality only as a source-linear parameter.
3. Prove signature separation:

\[
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}
D_\alpha\mathcal K_9=0.
\]

4. If this fails, do not use \(\alpha\) as an admitted downstream EF parameter; restrict it to auxiliary averaging, or use fixed-\(\alpha\) O2/O3 survival instead.

---

## 8. Final AlphaD4Compatibility theorem

A clean theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{AlphaD4Compatibility.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(\alpha\) acts on the canonical explicit-formula source only by source-linear branch phase/weight deformation;

2. the singular connection maps \(\mathcal R_{7\to9}\) and lower residual maps preserve source-grade/reflection signatures and do not promote first-source-linear classes into the primitive \(Y12\) signature;

3. \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{arith}}\) admits only actual EF parameters, not arbitrary local \(D^2N_0\) amplitudes;

4. \(\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}\mathsf C_{Y12}\ne0\).

Then

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\ne0
\quad\text{in}\quad
\mathcal Q_9^{\mathrm{forb},\alpha}.
\]

Therefore the D4 clean \(Y12\) channel survives \(\alpha\)-admission and gives a rank-one forbidden direction.

## 1. Rank-one forbidden wall factor

Modulo actual-source tangents and lower connection effects,

\[
D_s\mathcal K_9(\delta s_{\mathrm{D4}})

up to the fixed norm of \([\mathsf C_{Y12}]\) in the forbidden quotient.

Rank one is enough, but it demands anti-concentration for the specific moving linear form

## 2. Is this already supplied by old wall escape?

Old wall escape often tries to prove something like

\[
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2\ge Q^{-A}
\]

or a sublevel estimate

\[
\mu\{|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2<\varepsilon\}
\le Q^C\varepsilon^\theta \mu(\mathcal C).
\]

That does **not** automatically imply

\[
|\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Even if \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) is nonzero, it can lie near the moving null line

\[
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

So the rank-one \(Y12\) route needs a sharper wall theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{moving forbidden-linear-form anti-concentration.}
}
\]

---

## 3. When raw anisotropy does imply rank-one wall

Raw anisotropy suffices if the moving direction is controlled in a finite net and the vector \(\Gamma\) is not concentrated near any line.

A sufficient theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\mu\left\{
\frac{|\ell_m(\Gamma(m))|^2}
{|\Gamma_G(m)|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|^2}
<\varepsilon
\right\}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\mu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

Equivalently, the angle between

\[
\Gamma(m)
\]

and the forbidden null line

\[
\{\beta_9(m)u+\alpha_9(m)v=0\}
\]

cannot be too small on most of the extracted set.

If \((\beta_9,\alpha_9)\) varies slowly, one can freeze it into \(Q^C\) angular caps. Then the theorem reduces to fixed-line anti-concentration:

\[
\mu\left\{
|a\Gamma_G+b\Gamma_{G,2}|<\varepsilon |\Gamma|
\right\}
\le Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\mu(\mathcal C)
\]

for finitely many \((a,b)\).

Thus the extraction layer should include either:

\[
F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{K9}
=
\min\left(
\frac{|H|^2|\ell_m(\Gamma)|^2}{\eta\mathcal N_{\mathrm{D4}}},
1
\right),
\]

or a modular sublevel theorem for \(\ell_m(\Gamma)\) under the post-Gate/O2O3 measure.

## 4. Can \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) alone be used?

Since

\[
\alpha_9\neq0,
\]

one might hope to use

\[
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\]

as the wall factor. This is valid only if the \(\Gamma_G\)-term is absent or absorbable.

But the rank-one form is generally

\[
\ell_m(\Gamma)=\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

If

\[
\beta_9=0
\]

in the chosen normalization, then yes:

\[
\ell_m(\Gamma)=\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

If

\[
\beta_9\ne0,
\]

then \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) alone is not enough because cancellation can occur:

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
\approx
-\frac{\beta_9}{\alpha_9}\Gamma_G.
\]

Therefore one should not prematurely simplify the wall factor to \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) unless a finite normalization can make

\[
\beta_9=0
\]

or make \(\beta_9\Gamma_G\) tangent/lower-order in \(\mathcal Q_9^{\mathrm{forb}}\).

This suggests a finite gauge question:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the order-nine residual }\mathcal K_9
\text{ be normalized so that }\beta_9\text{ is removed?}
}
\]

If yes, the wall theorem simplifies to \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-anti-concentration.

---

## 5. Gauge-normalizing away \(\beta_9\)

Recall the order-nine residual has form

\[
\mathcal K_9=s_9-\mathcal R_{7\to9}s_7-\cdots.
\]

Changing

\[
\mathcal R_{7\to9}
\]

changes the coefficient of the \(\Gamma_G\)-dependent order-nine D4 piece.

Specifically, D4 contributes

\[
s_7^{\mathrm{D4}}=Hc_7[\mathsf C_7]\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
s_9^{\mathrm{D4}}=H\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_G
+
H\alpha_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

If one can choose

\[
\mathcal R_{7\to9}([\mathsf C_7])
=
\frac{\beta_9}{c_7}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\]

inside the allowed connection subtraction, then

\[
\mathcal K_9(\delta s_{\mathrm{D4}})
=
H\alpha_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

This would isolate the pure \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) channel.

But this is allowed only if the connection relation for actual EF-coherent singular data genuinely has that coefficient. We cannot choose \(\mathcal R_{7\to9}\) arbitrarily just to simplify D4. It must annihilate actual-source tangents.

So the finite audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the covariant actual-source connection } \mathcal R_{7\to9}
\text{ subtract the }\beta_9\Gamma_G\text{ piece?}
}
\]

If yes:

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{K9}\sim |H|^2|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2.
\]

If no:

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{K9}\sim |H|^2|\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}|^2.
\]

Either is usable, but the latter requires moving-linear-form anti-concentration.

---

## 6. Relation to old wall escape

Old wall escape had two curvature quantities:

\[
\Gamma_G,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

The \(Y12\) residual shows why the second one is structurally important. The order-nine channel naturally sees

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

independently of the order-seven channel.

So the wall theorem should be reformulated as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{forbidden linear curvature nonconcentration}
}

rather than generic anisotropy.

A clean statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\nu\left(
|\ell_m(\Gamma)|^2<Q^{-A}
\right)
\le Q^{-B}\nu(\mathcal C)
}
\]

or, in capped form,

\[
\boxed{

\min\left(

1
\right)
\,d\nu
\ge Q^{-B}\nu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

Here

\[

\]

is the post-Gate/O2O3 smooth measure, before hard extraction.

---

## 7. Potential obstruction: \(\ell_m(\Gamma)\) may vanish identically

If actual canonical geometry imposes

\[
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0
\]

on the extracted set, then the rank-one \(Y12\) channel is invisible despite \(Y12\) surviving in the quotient.

This would mean the D4 normal direction exists, but the scalar curvature vector \(\Gamma\) never excites it.

That is a separate no-go possibility.

It can happen if:

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
-\frac{\beta_9}{\alpha_9}\Gamma_G
\]

is an actual identity or wall constraint.

So the wall anti-concentration theorem must explicitly exclude this.

This is analogous to the earlier “wall escape” problem, but now for a specific forbidden line.

### Finite normality

\quad

### EFCompletion\(_{K9}\)

### Local D4 lower

\[

\ge

Then the positive atomic forbidden sum contradicts the upper.

The \(Y12\) normality theorem gives a **rank-one** D4 channel, not automatically a full two-dimensional wall.

Actual parameter curvature has only parameter-generated source slots:

If those slots are global phase/scale/log-weight deformations of the same EF packet, they may be mixed branch but not arbitrary same-point \(\xi_1,\xi_2\) slots. Therefore \(Y12\) likely remains primitive.

## 6. Completion term \(E_2\)

The completion/tail term \(E_2\) is dangerous because it is part of the **actual canonical source**, not an error if the manifold is defined by full \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\).

There are four cases.

### Case A: absent

Then \(E_2\) is harmless.

### Case B: fixed forcing, not tangent

If \(E_2\) contributes a freely varying \(Y12\)-signature direction under admissible tail/completion parameters, then

may contain \(\mathsf C_{Y12}\), killing the forbidden channel.

### Case D: nuisance quotient

If \(E_2\)'s \(Y12\)-signature is placed into a nuisance quotient that is removed before D4, then D4 visibility may also be lost unless \(\mathsf C_{Y12}\) survives the same quotient.

The safe condition is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathsf C_{Y12}
\notin
\mathcal T_{E_2,Y12}.
}

This must be checked.

Continuing Agent 5 — second-order \(Y12\) audit.

The current quotient is

\mathcal Q_{9,2}^{\mathrm{forb}}

\quad\text{in}\quad

The new issue is that \(Y12\) is quadratic, so it might be absorbed by the second fundamental form

\[
\mathcal{II}_{\mathrm{arith},9}
\]

of the actual EF singular manifold. The key is to distinguish **global parameter Hessians** from **independent local source-slot Hessians**.

---

## 1. Actual EF second curvature has constrained slots

Let the actual finite EF source be parameterized as

\[
F_X^\theta
=
B_2^\theta+P_{2,\le X}^\theta+D_{2,\le X}^\theta,
\]

with parameters

\[
\theta=(m,\lambda,\alpha,\text{normalization},\text{chart},\text{cutoff},\ldots).
\]

At the nonlinear source-map level, schematically,

\[
u(\theta)=N_0(h(\theta)).
\]

Then

\[
\partial_a u
=
DN_0[h_a],
\]

and

\[
\partial_a\partial_b u
=
D^2N_0[h_a,h_b]+DN_0[h_{ab}].
\]

The second derivative does contain a source-Hessian term. So the old argument “actual parameters are first-order” is not sufficient.

But the slots

\[
h_a,\ h_b
\]

are not arbitrary. They are global parameter-induced source variations: phase shifts, scale shifts, log-weight insertions, cutoff changes, and chart/normalization changes.

By contrast, the \(Y12\) carrier comes from

\[
D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2],
\]

where \(\xi_1,\xi_2\) are independent mixed-block local source variations coupled at the same point with one whitening slot.

Thus the correct separating invariant is not merely \(\operatorname{pdeg}=2\). It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Hessian slot type}.
}
\]

---

## 2. Define the slot subspaces

Let

\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}
=
\operatorname{span}\{h_a:\ a\in\text{actual EF parameters}\}
\]

be the source-slot subspace generated by actual parameter variations.

Then

\[
\mathcal{II}_{\mathrm{arith},9}
\]

has Hessian component inside

\[
D^2N_0[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}},
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}
].
\]

The \(Y12\) carrier lies in

\[
D^2N_0[
\mathcal H_1^{\mathrm{loc}},
\mathcal H_2^{\mathrm{loc}}
]_{\mathrm{same\ point},1w},
\]

where \(\mathcal H_1^{\mathrm{loc}}\) and \(\mathcal H_2^{\mathrm{loc}}\) are the two mixed local source blocks.

Therefore \(Y12\) survives the arithmetic second curvature if

\[
\boxed{
D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2]
\notin
D^2N_0[\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}},\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}]
+
DN_0[\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par},2}]
}
\]

after projecting to the order-nine same-point one-whitening mixed signature.

Equivalently, in signature notation,

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}
D^2N_0[\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}},\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}]
=0,
}
\]

while

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}
D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2]\neq0.
}
\]

This is the finite second-order audit.

---

## 3. Why global parameter slots should not span \(Y12\)

The actual parameter slots have restricted forms:

### \(m\)-variation

\[
h_m
\sim
\partial_m h
\]

is a transport/log-frequency derivative of the same source.

It is not a new independent mixed-block source. Its Hessian pair

\[
D^2N_0[h_m,h_m]
\]

has two transport slots, not one branch-1 local source and one branch-2 local source coupled at the same point.

### \(\lambda\)-variation

\[
h_\lambda
\sim
x\,\partial_m h+\text{scale term}.
\]

Again, this is a global scaling/transport slot.

### \(\alpha\)-variation

If \(\alpha\) is an AFE tilt,

\[
h_\alpha
\sim
\text{phase/log-weight deformation of existing EF atoms}.
\]

This is still a global slot, not an independent local mixed block.

### cutoff variation

Cutoff parameters change envelopes, not the nonlinear source map itself.

So the span

\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}
\]

should be low-dimensional and highly structured. It should not contain the independent local variations

\[
\xi_1,\xi_2
\]

needed to build \(Y12\).

Thus generically,

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}
\mathcal{II}_{\mathrm{arith},9}=0.
}
\]

But “generically” is not a proof; the finite audit is to verify that the source-slot signatures differ.

---

## 4. Same-point whitening is likely the decisive separator

The \(Y12\) carrier is not just any Hessian:

\[
D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2].
\]

It is coupled through a **same-point linear whitening slot**.

Actual parameter Hessians such as

\[
D^2N_0[h_m,h_\alpha]
\]

may be mixed branch in a broad sense, but they need not have the same same-point whitening incidence. They arise from differentiating a coherent global packet, not inserting two independent local source variations into the same-point whitened carrier.

So the most useful signature may be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-point whitening incidence}.
}
\]

The finite theorem could be:

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{same\ point},1w}
D^2N_0[\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}},\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}]
=0,
\]

whereas

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{same\ point},1w}
Y12
\ne0.
\]

This is stronger and more specific than source degree alone.

---

## 5. What if actual parameters include local amplitude freedom?

If the actual-source manifold is defined too broadly, for example allowing arbitrary local amplitudes in the two EF branches, then

\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}
\]

could contain

\[
\xi_1,\xi_2.
\]

Then

\[
D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2]
\in
D^2N_0[\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}},\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}],
\]

and \(Y12\) becomes actual-source curvature. Rank zero.

Therefore the definition of

\[
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\]

is critical. It must be the manifold of actual arithmetic EF sources parameterized by genuine global variables, not the universal span of all local packet amplitudes.

This is the same “universal EF atom span” trap in a second-order form.

---

## 6. Completion term \(E_2\) revisited

If

\[
E_2
\]

is a deterministic functional of the same actual EF parameters, then its second curvature belongs in

\[
\mathcal{II}_{\mathrm{arith},9}.
\]

If \(E_2\) includes a free regularized tail parameter with local mixed-block amplitudes, then it can enlarge the tangent/curvature space and kill \(Y12\).

So \(E_2\) must be treated as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{fixed deterministic completion, not a free local parameter.}
}
\]

Then it may shift the base relation \(\mathcal K_9\), but it does not add a free \(Y12\) tangent unless its deterministic dependence on global parameters has the \(Y12\) signature.

The audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}
\partial_a\partial_b E_2=0
\quad
\text{for allowed }a,b.
}
\]

If true, \(E_2\) does not kill the forbidden \(Y12\) direction.

## 7. Refined second-order separation theorem

The finite theorem should be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Second-order \(Y12\) slot separation.}
}
\]

Let

\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}
\]

be the finite-dimensional source-slot space generated by allowed actual EF parameter derivatives, including \(E_2\)'s deterministic parameter dependence. Let

\[
\mathcal H_{Y12}
=
\operatorname{span}\{\xi_1,\xi_2\}
\]

be the local mixed same-point source-slot pair giving \(Y12\).

Assume:

1. \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}\) has no component in the local same-point \(Y12\) slot type:

\[
\Pi_{Y12\text{-slot}}\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}=0;
\]

2. lower connection maps preserve the \(Y12\)-slot filtration:

\[
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}(\mathcal T_7+\mathcal T_{<7})=0;
\]

3. \(E_2\) has no free \(Y12\)-signature curvature:

\[
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}\mathcal T_{E_2,Y12}=0;
\]

4. \(T_{\mathrm{tr}\to\mathrm{sing}}\mathsf C_{Y12}\) has nonzero \(Y12\)-signature projection.

Then

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\ne0
\quad
\text{in}
\quad
\mathcal Q_{9,2}^{\mathrm{forb}}.
\]

---

## 8. Consequence for \(\alpha\)

If \(\alpha\) is source-linear, then

\[
h_\alpha\in\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}.
\]

The second derivative

\[
\partial_\alpha^2u
=

is harmless if

\[

\]

has no \(Y12\)-slot component. Thus \(\alpha\) remains compatible with D4 if

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{Y12\text{-slot}}h_\alpha=0.
}
\]

This is a sharper and simpler condition than checking all of

\[
\partial_\alpha u,\quad \partial_\alpha^2u.
\]

It says: the \(\alpha\)-source slot is not one of the two local same-point mixed-block slots that generate \(Y12\).

For an AFE tilt, this is likely true.

---

## 9. What to compute next

The next finite computation should identify the source-slot types of:

\[
h_m,\quad h_\lambda,\quad h_\alpha,\quad h_{\mathrm{norm}},\quad h_{\mathrm{cutoff}},\quad h_{E_2}.
\]

Then project them onto the \(Y12\)-slot signature.

If all vanish,

\[
\mathcal{II}_{\mathrm{arith},9}
\]

has no \(Y12\) component, and the rank-one D4 route survives.

If any do not vanish, determine whether the induced Hessian actually spans the same carrier as

\[
T_{\mathrm{tr}\to\mathrm{sing}}\mathsf C_{Y12}.
\]

---

## Final result of this attack

The second-order \(Y12\) audit reduces to a source-slot separation theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{allowed global EF parameter slots do not contain the local same-point mixed slots }(\xi_1,\xi_2).
}
\]

If this holds, then even the second fundamental form

\[
\mathcal{II}_{\mathrm{arith},9}
\]

does not absorb \(Y12\). The \(Y12\) carrier remains a true normal direction, and the finite-D4 rank-one forbidden channel survives.

means same-point plus one-whitening projection.

Actual EF parameter curvature occupies

\[
\operatorname{Sym}^2\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}},
\]

where

\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}
=
\operatorname{span}\{h_m,h_\lambda,h_\alpha,h_{\mathrm{norm}},h_{\mathrm{cutoff}},\ldots\}.
\]

So the decisive algebraic test is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathsf y_{12}
\notin
\Pi_{\mathrm{sp},1w}
\operatorname{Sym}^2\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}.
}
\]

This is stronger and cleaner than checking every second derivative separately.

---

## 2. A rank criterion for exclusion

Let

\[
U=\Pi_{\mathrm{sp},1w}\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}
\subset
\Pi_{\mathrm{sp},1w}(\mathcal H_1\oplus\mathcal H_2).
\]

Then the actual second fundamental form can only produce

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{sp},1w}\operatorname{Sym}^2 U.
\]

The \(Y12\) slot is a specific mixed tensor

\[
\xi_1\odot\xi_2.
\]

Thus \(Y12\) is absorbed only if

\[
\xi_1\odot\xi_2\in \operatorname{Sym}^2 U.
\]

A sufficient condition for survival is

\[
\boxed{
\dim \Pi_{\mathcal H_1}U=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\dim \Pi_{\mathcal H_2}U=0.
}
\]

That is, if actual parameters do not generate both local branch slots, they cannot generate the mixed Hessian.

More generally, even if \(U\) has components in both branches, survival holds if

\[
\boxed{
\xi_1\notin \Pi_{\mathcal H_1}U
\quad\text{or}\quad
\xi_2\notin \Pi_{\mathcal H_2}U.
}
\]

So the finite test reduces to whether the actual parameter slot space contains the two specific same-point local source slots.

---

## 3. Why global EF parameters should fail this test

The allowed parameter slots are global:

\[
h_m,\ h_\lambda,\ h_\alpha,\ h_{\mathrm{cutoff}},\ldots
\]

They look like phase/log/scale/envelope derivatives of the existing EF packet. In a local source-slot basis, they are coherent across many points/frequencies:

\[
h_m \sim \sum_n (-i\log n)a_n e^{-im\log n}e_n,
\]

\[
h_\alpha \sim \sum_n \omega_\alpha(n)a_n e^{-im\log n}e_n,
\]

\[
h_\lambda \sim x\partial_m h+\cdots.
\]

They are not localized independent atoms

\[
\xi_1,\quad \xi_2
\]

at a same point. They are global coherent directions.

So unless the actual parameter space is artificially enlarged to allow arbitrary local packet amplitudes, one expects

\[
\xi_1,\xi_2\notin \mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}.
\]

Hence

\[
\xi_1\odot\xi_2\notin \operatorname{Sym}^2\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}.
\]

This is the geometric reason \(Y12\) should survive the second fundamental-form quotient.

---

## 4. The only dangerous actual parameters

There are three dangerous parameter classes.

### A. Local amplitude parameters

If the actual-source manifold includes parameters

\[
a_{1,p},\quad a_{2,p}
\]

that independently vary the two local branch slots at the same point, then

\[
h_{a_{1,p}}=\xi_1,\qquad h_{a_{2,p}}=\xi_2.
\]

Then

\[
D^2N_0[h_{a_{1,p}},h_{a_{2,p}}]
=
D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2],
\]

and \(Y12\) is tangent/curvature of the actual-source manifold.

This would kill the finite-D4 normal direction.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{sing}}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\text{ must not allow arbitrary local branch amplitudes.}
}
\]

It must be the actual arithmetic EF family, not a universal packet manifold.

### B. Local cutoff-shape parameters

If cutoff parameters are allowed to vary freely at local scale, they can approximate local amplitude directions. This can also generate \(\xi_1,\xi_2\).

Therefore cutoff variation must be restricted to a fixed finite/global family, not arbitrary local bump deformations.

### C. Tail/completion free parameters

If \(E_2\) is treated as having freely variable local correction amplitudes, it can span \(Y12\).

So \(E_2\) must be deterministic/coherent, not an arbitrary nuisance.

---

## 5. \(E_2\) classification in the tensor test

Let the completion/tail contribution be

\[
E_2=E_2(p)
\]

as a deterministic function of actual parameters.

Then its second curvature contributes

\[
\partial_a\partial_bE_2.
\]

It is safe if

\[
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}\partial_a\partial_bE_2=0
\]

for all allowed \(a,b\).

Equivalently, the source slots of \(E_2\) lie in

\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}},
\]

not in the independent local \(Y12\)-slot directions.

If \(E_2\) is not parameterized but fixed by the explicit formula, then it shifts the base source and possibly the base coherence relation, but does not add tangent or curvature directions. In that case it cannot kill the normal channel.

Thus the safe rule is:

\[
\boxed{
E_2\text{ may be fixed/coherent, but not free in the }Y12\text{ slot.}
}
\]

---

## 6. Lower connection transport in tensor language

The lower connection subspace

\[
\mathcal T_7+\mathcal T_{<7}
\]

can kill \(Y12\) only if the connection maps lower-order data into

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{sp},1w}(\mathcal H_1\odot\mathcal H_2).
\]

So define the primitive \(Y12\) projection

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{prim}\,Y12}.
\]

The finite table condition is

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\mathrm{prim}\,Y12}
\mathcal R_{7\to9}=0,
\qquad
\Pi_{\mathrm{prim}\,Y12}
\mathcal R_{<7\to9}=0.
}
\]

This says lower connection transport cannot manufacture a primitive same-point mixed Hessian carrier.

If this triangularity fails, then \(Y12\) is not primitive; it may be lower-order connection-induced.

---

## 7. Final finite criterion

The strongest concise criterion is:

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\mathrm{prim}\,Y12}
\left[
\operatorname{Sym}^2\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}
+
\mathcal T_7
+
\mathcal T_{<7}
+
\mathcal T_{E_2}
\right]
=0,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\mathrm{prim}\,Y12}
T_{\mathrm{tr}\to\mathrm{sing}}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\ne0.
}
\]

Then

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\ne0
\quad\text{in}\quad
\mathcal Q_{9,2}^{\mathrm{forb}}.
\]

This proves the rank-one D4 forbidden channel.

---

## 8. Consequence for \(\alpha\)

For \(\alpha\), the condition is simply:

\[
h_\alpha\notin
\operatorname{span}\{\xi_1,\xi_2\}
\quad
\text{in the primitive same-point local source-slot quotient.}
\]

If \(\alpha\) is a global AFE phase/tilt, this should hold.

Then even

\[
D^2N_0[h_\alpha,h_\alpha]
\]

does not generate \(Y12\), and \(\alpha\)-twisting remains compatible with the D4 channel.

So \(\alpha\) is dangerous only if it is secretly a local amplitude/shape parameter at the same-point mixed slot.

---

## 9. Current theorem statement

A proof-ready theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Primitive \(Y12\) Slot Separation.}
}
\]

Let \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}\) be the source-slot space generated by all allowed actual EF parameters, including \(\alpha\) if admitted and deterministic \(E_2\)-parameter dependence. Let \(\Pi_{\mathrm{prim}\,Y12}\) be the projection to the primitive same-point mixed Hessian one-whitening signature.

Assume:

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{prim}\,Y12}\operatorname{Sym}^2\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}=0,
\]

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{prim}\,Y12}(\mathcal T_7+\mathcal T_{<7})=0,
\]

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{prim}\,Y12}\mathcal T_{E_2}=0,
\]

and

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{prim}\,Y12}
T_{\mathrm{tr}\to\mathrm{sing}}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\ne0.
\]

Then

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\ne0
\quad
\text{in}
\quad
\mathcal Q_{9,2}^{\mathrm{forb}}.
\]

---

## Final result of this attack

The \(Y12\) second-order normality question reduces to an explicit source-slot containment test:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Sym}^2\mathcal H_{\mathrm{par}}
\text{ does not contain the primitive same-point mixed Hessian slot } \xi_1\odot\xi_2.
}
\]

This is the cleanest finite formulation so far.

It also clarifies the main no-go:

\[
\boxed{
\text{if the actual-source manifold allows arbitrary local branch amplitudes, }Y12\text{ dies.}
}
\]

Therefore the actual-source manifold must be genuinely arithmetic/coherent, not the universal local packet span.

Agent 5 — moving forbidden wall anti-concentration.

Assume the \(Y12\) class survives in the second-order forbidden quotient, so finite D4 gives the rank-one residual channel

\[
\ell_m(\Gamma)
=
\beta_9(m)\Gamma_G(m)+\alpha_9(m)\Gamma_{G,2}(m),
\qquad
\alpha_9\ne0.
\]

The task is now to decide whether this rank-one channel has enough mass. This is necessary because raw two-dimensional anisotropy in \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) does not automatically imply non-smallness of the particular moving linear form \(\ell_m(\Gamma)\). 

## 1. Required wall theorem

The downstream wall factor should be

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{K9}(m)
=
\frac{
|H(m)|^2
|\ell_m(\Gamma(m))|^2
}{
\mathcal N_{\mathrm{D4}}(m)
}.
\]

Before hard extraction, use a smooth/capped aggregate theorem under the post-Gate/O2/O3 measure \(d\nu\):

\[
\boxed{
\int
\min\!\left(
Q^A
\frac{|H|^2|\ell_m(\Gamma)|^2}{\mathcal N_{\mathrm{D4}}},
1
\right)
d\nu
\ge
Q^{-B}\nu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

Equivalently, after dyadic normalization of \(|H|^2/\mathcal N_{\mathrm{D4}}\), the core theorem is

\[
\boxed{
\nu\{|\ell_m(\Gamma)|<\varepsilon\}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta \nu(\mathcal C)
}
\]

for \(\varepsilon\) down to polynomial scale.

This is the exact rank-one wall anti-concentration input.

---

## 2. Raw anisotropy is insufficient

A theorem of the form

\[
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2\ge Q^{-A}
\]

does not imply

\[
|\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

The vector

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

can be large while lying near the null line

\[
\beta_9 u+\alpha_9 v=0.
\]

So the old wall escape theorem is not enough unless it includes angular nonconcentration relative to moving forbidden lines.

The needed strengthening is:

\[
\boxed{
\nu\left\{
\frac{|\ell_m(\Gamma)|^2}{|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2}
<\varepsilon
\right\}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\nu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

This says \(\Gamma\) cannot concentrate near the moving forbidden null line.

---

## 3. Can \(\beta_9\) be removed?

The cleanest case would be

\[
\ell_m(\Gamma)=\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

This occurs if the covariant order-nine residual subtracts the \(\Gamma_G\)-dependent order-nine piece through the order-seven connection.

D4 gives

\[
s_7^{\mathrm{D4}}=Hc_7[\mathsf C_7]\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
s_9^{\mathrm{D4}}
=
H\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_G
+
H\alpha_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

The residual

\[
K_9=s_9-\mathcal R_{7\to9}s_7-\cdots
\]

removes the \(\Gamma_G\) component if

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])
=
\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\quad
\text{in the }Y12\text{ quotient}.
}
\]

If this identity is true, then

\[
K_9(\delta s_{\mathrm{D4}})
=
H\alpha_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and the wall theorem reduces to \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-anti-concentration.

If false, the moving form

\[
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

is unavoidable.

So there is a finite audit:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the covariant connection absorb the }\beta_9\Gamma_G\text{ component?}
}
\]

This audit should be performed before proving the wall theorem, because it may lower the wall complexity and reduce the O2/O3 branch-charge bandwidth \(d_0\).

---

## 4. Moving-line reduction by angular freezing

If \(\beta_9/\alpha_9\) cannot be removed, handle the moving form by freezing its direction.

Let

\[
r(m)=\frac{\beta_9(m)}{\alpha_9(m)}.
\]

Assume

\[
|r(m)|\le Q^C
\]

and \(r(m)\) has polynomial variation on the relevant smooth pre-extraction atoms. Cover the range of \(r\) by \(Q^C\) angular caps:

\[
r(m)\in \mathcal A_j.
\]

On each cap,

\[
\ell_m(\Gamma)
=
\alpha_9(\Gamma_{G,2}+r(m)\Gamma_G)
\]

is comparable, up to polynomial loss, to a fixed linear form

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+r_j\Gamma_G.
\]

Thus moving-line anti-concentration reduces to finitely many fixed-line estimates:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_j\{|\Gamma_{G,2}+r_j\Gamma_G|<\varepsilon|\Gamma|\}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\nu_j.
}
\]

This is a reasonable scalar wall theorem if \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) has no hidden one-dimensional constraint.

---

## 5. The real no-go: a forbidden-line identity

The rank-one \(Y12\) channel can still fail if the actual geometry imposes

\[
\boxed{
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0
}
\]

on the relevant Stack C2 set.

This would mean D4 is normal in principle but never excited by the curvature vector \(\Gamma\).

This is a distinct no-go from \(Y12\) being tangent. It says:

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\ne0
\quad
\text{but}
\quad
\ell_m(\Gamma)=0.
\]

So the wall theorem must explicitly exclude a curvature-line identity:

\[
\boxed{
\ell_m(\Gamma)\not\equiv0
\quad\text{and does not have polynomially large sublevel sets.}
}
\]

This is likely the downstream analogue of the old wall-escape input.

---

## 6. Interaction with O2/O3 branch-charge bandwidth

The wall factor used in O2/O3 pre-extraction should be smooth and bounded-degree:

\[
W_{\mathrm{bd}}
=
N_{\mathrm{sm}} |H|^2 |\ell_m(\Gamma)|^2.
\]

The branch-charge bandwidth is

\[
d_0=d_N+2d_H+2d_\Gamma.
\]

If \(\ell_m=\Gamma_{G,2}\), then \(d_\Gamma\) may be smaller. If \(\ell_m=\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}\), then \(d_\Gamma\) is the maximum branch charge appearing in either term.

So the \(\beta_9\)-absorption audit affects O2/O3 complexity.

A smaller \(d_0\) reduces the near-pure Schur block:

\[
D_{-n},D_{-n+1},\ldots,D_{-n+d_0}.
\]

Thus the order of work should be:

\[
\boxed{
Y12\text{ survival}
\rightarrow
\beta_9\text{ absorption audit}
\rightarrow
d_0\text{ computation}
\rightarrow
near-pure O2/O3 block}.
}
\]

---

## 7. Recommended wall theorem

The final wall theorem should be stated in rank-one form:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{ForbiddenLinearWallAntiConcentration.}
}
\]

Let

\[
\ell_m(\Gamma)=\beta_9(m)\Gamma_G+\alpha_9(m)\Gamma_{G,2},
\qquad \alpha_9(m)\ne0,
\]

and let \(d\nu\) be the smooth post-Gate/O2O3 measure before hard extraction. Then

\[
\boxed{
\int
\min\left(
Q^A
\frac{|H|^2|\ell_m(\Gamma)|^2}{\mathcal N_{\mathrm{D4}}},
1
\right)
d\nu
\ge
Q^{-B}\nu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

A sufficient route is:

1. dyadically freeze \(|H|^2/\mathcal N_{\mathrm{D4}}\);
2. angularly freeze \(r=\beta_9/\alpha_9\);
3. prove fixed-line anti-concentration for

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+r_j\Gamma_G;
\]

4. sum over \(Q^C\) caps.

---

## 8. Current verdict

The \(Y12\) route gives a rank-one channel, but it replaces raw anisotropy with a sharper wall input:

\[
\boxed{
\ell_m(\Gamma)
=
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\text{ must be anti-concentrated.}
}
\]

This is likely manageable if:

- the covariant connection removes \(\beta_9\), or
- the curvature vector \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) is not locked to the moving forbidden line.

It fails if the actual geometry imposes a forbidden-line identity.

The next finite audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])
\stackrel{?}{=}
\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\quad
\text{in the }Y12\text{ quotient}.
}
\]

If yes, the wall becomes essentially \(\Gamma_{G,2}\). If no, prove moving-linear-form anti-concentration.

_Thought for 8s_

Continuing Agent 5 — \(\beta_9\)-absorption in the order-nine residual.

We currently have the rank-one forbidden wall form

\[
\ell_m(\Gamma)
=
\beta_9(m)\Gamma_G(m)+\alpha_9(m)\Gamma_{G,2}(m),
\qquad
\alpha_9\neq0.
\]

The key question is whether the **covariant** order-nine singular connection residual can remove the \(\beta_9\Gamma_G\) term, leaving the cleaner channel

\[
\ell_m(\Gamma)=\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

This matters because the \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-only wall is simpler and lowers the branch-charge bandwidth in the O2/O3 determinant-survival problem. 

## 1. What \(\beta_9\)-absorption means

The D4 clean output has triangular form:

\[
s_7^{\mathrm{D4}}
=
Hc_7[\mathsf C_7]\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
s_9^{\mathrm{D4}}
=
H\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_G
+
H\alpha_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

A covariant order-nine residual has the schematic form

\[
K_9(s)
=
s_9-\mathcal R_{7\to9}s_7-\mathcal R_{<7\to9}s_{<7}.
\]

Applying this to D4 gives

\[
K_9(s^{\mathrm{D4}})
=
H\left(
\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
-
\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])
\right)\Gamma_G
+
H\alpha_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Therefore \(\beta_9\)-absorption is exactly the finite identity

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])
=
\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\quad
\text{in the }Y12\text{ quotient}.
}
\]

If this holds, then

\[
\boxed{
K_9(s^{\mathrm{D4}})
=
H\alpha_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_{G,2}.
}
\]

If it fails, the moving wall form remains.

---

## 2. Covariance strongly suggests partial absorption, not arbitrary absorption

The residual \(K_9\) is not chosen freely. It must annihilate actual EF-coherent source variations. Therefore \(\mathcal R_{7\to9}\) is determined by the actual singular connection table.

The natural interpretation is:

\[
\mathcal R_{7\to9}
=
\text{actual order-seven to order-nine connection induced by singular coherence}.
\]

So \(\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])\) is the order-nine component forced by the order-seven \(C_7\) displacement **if that displacement is tangent to the actual-source singular manifold**.

But the D4 \(C_7\) displacement is not necessarily an actual-source tangent. It is a formal carrier. So covariance does not automatically imply absorption.

The correct test is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the formal }[\mathsf C_7]\text{ carrier have the same connection lift as an actual coherent order-seven source displacement?}
}
\]

If yes, \(\beta_9\Gamma_G\) is subtractable.

If no, the \(\Gamma_G\) part may also be forbidden.

---

## 3. Relation to \(Y12\) primitivity

There is a tension:

- If

\[
\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])
=
\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}],
\]

then \(Y12\) appears as an order-seven connection consequence in the \(\Gamma_G\) channel.

- But the \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) channel still contains

\[
\alpha_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\]

with no order-seven antecedent.

Thus \(\beta_9\)-absorption does **not** kill \(Y12\)-normality. It only says the \(\Gamma_G\)-dependent \(Y12\) part is connection-induced by \(C_7\). The primitive normal component is still

\[
\boxed{
\alpha_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_{G,2}.
}
\]

This is why the \(Y12\) route is robust: even maximal absorption of the \(\Gamma_G\) part leaves the \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) channel.

---

## 4. Three possible outcomes

### Outcome A: exact absorption

\[
\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])
=
\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}].
\]

Then the wall factor becomes

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{K9}
\asymp
\frac{|H|^2|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2}{\mathcal N_{\mathrm{D4}}}.
}
\]

This is best. The wall anti-concentration theorem reduces to

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

not being too often small.

The O2/O3 branch-charge weight also simplifies.

---

### Outcome B: no absorption, but nonzero \(Y12\)

\[
\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])
\neq
\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}],
\]

while

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\neq0
\quad\text{in}\quad
\mathcal Q_{9,2}^{\mathrm{forb}}.
\]

Then the wall form is genuinely moving:

\[
\boxed{
\ell_m(\Gamma)
=
\left(
\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
-
\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])
\right)\Gamma_G
+
\alpha_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\Gamma_{G,2}.
}
\]

This is still usable but requires moving-linear-form anti-concentration.

---

### Outcome C: over-absorption / \(Y12\) killed

If the quotient declares

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]=0,
\]

then both \(\Gamma_G\) and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) channels die in \(Y12\). This is the downstream failure mode.

This would mean \(Y12\) is part of actual-source tangent/curvature/completion coherence, not a forbidden normal direction.

---

## 5. Finite test in the \(Y12\)-graded quotient

Let

\[
\Pi_{Y12}
\]

denote projection to the primitive \(Y12\)-graded quotient. Then the absorption audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{Y12}
\left(
\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])
-
\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\right)
=0?
}
\]

But first one must know

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{Y12}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\neq0.
}
\]

If

\[
\Pi_{Y12}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\neq0
\]

and the above equality holds, wall simplifies to \(\Gamma_{G,2}\).

If not, use the full moving form.

---

## 6. Effect on branch-charge bandwidth \(d_0\)

The pre-extraction O2/O3 weight includes

\[
|H|^2|\ell_m(\Gamma)|^2.
\]

If

\[
\ell_m=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

then

\[
d_\Gamma=d(\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

If

\[
\ell_m=a(m)\Gamma_G+b(m)\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

then

\[
d_\Gamma
=
\max\{d(a\Gamma_G),d(b\Gamma_{G,2})\}.
\]

Usually this is larger or equal. Therefore exact \(\beta_9\)-absorption can shrink

\[
d_0=d_N+2d_H+2d_\Gamma.
\]

That directly reduces the O2/O3 near-pure Schur block

\[
D_{-n},D_{-n+1},\ldots,D_{-n+d_0}.
\]

So the \(\beta_9\)-audit should be done before finalizing the O2/O3 determinant survival problem.

---

## 7. If \(\beta_9\) is not absorbed: fixed-line anti-concentration

When the moving form remains, write

\[
\ell_m(\Gamma)
=
b(m)\left(\Gamma_{G,2}+r(m)\Gamma_G\right),
\]

where

\[
r(m)=\frac{a(m)}{b(m)}
\]

and \(b(m)\neq0\) on the visible \(Y12\) set.

Assume

\[
|r(m)|\le Q^C
\]

and \(r\) has polynomial complexity. Cover the range of \(r\) by \(Q^C\) angular caps. On each cap, reduce to a fixed form

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+r_j\Gamma_G.
\]

Then prove

\[
\boxed{
\nu_j
\left\{
|\Gamma_{G,2}+r_j\Gamma_G|<\varepsilon
\right\}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta \nu_j.
}
\]

So no absorption does not kill the route. It only moves the wall theorem from \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-sublevel to fixed-line/moving-line sublevel.

---

## 8. Current finite priority list

The order is now:

1. **\(Y12\) survival**
   
   \[
   \Pi_{Y12}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\neq0
   \quad
   \text{mod }
   \mathcal T_{\mathrm{par}}+\mathcal T_7+\mathcal T_{<7}+\mathcal{II}_{\mathrm{arith},9}+\mathcal T_{E_2}.
   \]

2. **\(\beta_9\)-absorption**
   
   \[
   \Pi_{Y12}
   \left(
   \mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])
   -
   \beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
   \right)=0?
   \]

3. **Wall anti-concentration**
   
   Either

   \[
   \Gamma_{G,2}\text{ anti-concentration}
   \]

   or

   \[
   \beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ moving-line anti-concentration}.
   \]

4. **Branch-charge \(d_0\) computation**
   
   Use the final wall factor.

## Final result of this attack

The \(\beta_9\)-absorption audit is now a finite \(Y12\)-graded connection identity:

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{Y12}
\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])
=
\Pi_{Y12}\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]?
}
\]

If yes, the finite-D4 wall is essentially \(\Gamma_{G,2}\), the cleanest possible rank-one channel.

If no, the route remains viable but needs moving-linear-form anti-concentration for

after lower-connection correction.

_Thought for 14s_

Continuing Agent 5 — interaction between \(Y12\)-primitivity and \(\beta_9\)-absorption.

The previous attack asked whether the covariant order-nine residual can remove the \(\beta_9\Gamma_G\) part:

\[
\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])
\stackrel{?}{=}
\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\quad
\text{in the }Y12\text{ quotient}.
\]

There is now a sharper structural point:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If \(Y12\) is truly primitive, then \(\beta_9\)-absorption is unlikely.}
}
\]

More precisely, if the \(Y12\)-signature separation theorem holds, then lower connection transport should have no primitive \(Y12\) component. That means

\[
\Pi_{Y12}\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])=0.
\]

Therefore the absorption identity

\[
\Pi_{Y12}\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])
=
\Pi_{Y12}\beta_9[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\]

can hold only if

\[
\boxed{
\beta_9=0
\quad
\text{in the primitive \(Y12\) quotient.}
}
\]

So the expected generic outcome is not pure \(\Gamma_{G,2}\). It is the moving forbidden wall form

\[
\boxed{
\ell_m(\Gamma)
=
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}.
}
\]

This is not bad. It is the structurally honest rank-one wall.

---

## 1. The dichotomy

There are two coherent possibilities.

### Case A: \(Y12\) primitive

Then

\[
\Pi_{Y12}\mathcal R_{7\to9}(\mathcal Y_7)=0.
\]

Hence

\[
\Pi_{Y12}K_9(s^{\mathrm{D4}})
=
H\Pi_{Y12}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
(\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

The wall is the moving linear form:

\[
\ell_m(\Gamma)=\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

This is compatible with the \(Y12\)-normality theorem.

### Case B: \(\beta_9\)-absorption

If

\[
\Pi_{Y12}\mathcal R_{7\to9}(c_7[\mathsf C_7])
=
\beta_9\Pi_{Y12}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\ne0,
\]

then lower connection transport **does** create the primitive \(Y12\) signature.

But then \(Y12\) is not fully primitive relative to \(\mathcal T_7\). This weakens the \(Y12\)-signature separation theorem.

The \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) term may still survive because it has no order-seven antecedent, but the quotient structure becomes subtler:

\[
\Gamma_G\text{-part connection-induced,}
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\text{-part primitive.}
\]

So Case B is possible, but it means the forbidden quotient must distinguish the \(Y12\) carrier paired with \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) from the same carrier paired with the order-seven-induced \(\Gamma_G\) direction.

That is an extra grading:

\[
\boxed{
\text{curvature-slot label: } \Gamma_G \text{ versus } \Gamma_{G,2}.
}
\]

Without that extra label, absorption of \(Y12\) through \(\mathcal T_7\) risks killing the whole \(Y12\) class.

---

## 2. Recommended interpretation

The cleanest consistent route is:

\[
\boxed{
Y12\text{ is primitive, so }\beta_9\text{ is not absorbed unless }\beta_9=0.
}
\]

Then the downstream wall should be formulated from the beginning as

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{Y12}
=
\frac{
|H|^2
|\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
}{
\mathcal N_{\mathrm{D4}}
}.
}
\]

Do not rely on \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-only unless a separate finite calculation proves

\[
\beta_9=0
\]

in the primitive quotient.

This avoids a hidden inconsistency between:

\[
\boxed{
\text{\(Y12\) primitive}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{\(Y12\) generated by lower order connection}.
}
\]

---

## 3. Moving-line anti-concentration becomes central

Assuming Case A, the next theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\nu\{|\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}|<\varepsilon\}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\nu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

This is now unavoidable.

The clean way to prove it is to freeze the ratio

\[
r(m)=\frac{\beta_9(m)}{\alpha_9(m)}.
\]

Since \(\alpha_9\neq0\), write

\[
\ell_m(\Gamma)
=
\alpha_9(m)\left(\Gamma_{G,2}+r(m)\Gamma_G\right).
\]

Assume

\[
|\alpha_9(m)|\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
|r(m)|\le Q^C,
\]

and \(r(m)\) has polynomial complexity. Decompose into caps where

\[
r(m)\approx r_j.
\]

Then the moving-line theorem reduces to finitely many fixed-line estimates:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_j\{
|\Gamma_{G,2}+r_j\Gamma_G|<\varepsilon
\}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\nu_j.
}
\]

So the wall problem is now a two-dimensional scalar curvature anti-concentration problem.

---

## 4. Can the fixed-line estimate be reduced to a Wronskian?

Let

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

A fixed-line failure says

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx -r\Gamma_G
\]

on a large set.

If \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) are independent curvature functionals of the scalar source \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\), then this is a first-order ODE/recurrence constraint on the local source geometry.

A useful target is:

\[
\boxed{
W_\Gamma
=
\Gamma_G\,\partial_m\Gamma_{G,2}
-
\Gamma_{G,2}\,\partial_m\Gamma_G
}
\]

or a discrete branch analogue.

If

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}/\Gamma_G
\]

is not locally constant, then \(\Gamma\) cannot lie near one fixed line on a large set.

So one possible wall theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\partial_m
\left(
\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}}{\Gamma_G}
\right)
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

outside a small exceptional set, together with a standard sublevel estimate.

This is a scalar curvature nondegeneracy theorem. It may be easier than proving arbitrary moving-line anti-concentration directly.

---

## 5. Interaction with branch-charge bandwidth

The wall factor is now

\[
|\ell_m(\Gamma)|^2.
\]

The branch-charge bandwidth contribution is

\[
d_\Gamma
=
\max\{
d(\beta_9\Gamma_G),
d(\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2})
\}.
\]

If \(\beta_9\) is not absorbed, \(d_\Gamma\) may be larger than the pure \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) case. But it is still finite and likely \(O(1)\).

Thus the O2/O3 near-pure block becomes

\[
D_{-n},D_{-n+1},\ldots,D_{-n+d_0},
\]

with

\[
d_0=d_N+2d_H+2d_\Gamma.
\]

The important point:

\[
\boxed{
d_0\text{ is still }O(1).
}
\]

So even without \(\beta_9\)-absorption, the fixed-\(\alpha\) bounded-charge O2/O3 route remains viable. It just has a slightly larger near-pure Schur block.

---

## 6. If \(\beta_9=0\) by normalization

There is one favorable possibility:

\[
\beta_9=0
\]

not because connection absorbs it, but because the clean D4 matrix can be normalized into a strictly diagonal form in the forbidden quotient:

\[
L_{\mathrm{clean}}^{Y12}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&\alpha_9
\end{pmatrix}
\]

after quotienting the \(\Gamma_G\)-order-nine component as tangent or lower connection.

This is subtly different from saying lower connection creates primitive \(Y12\). It says the \(\Gamma_G\)-dependent order-nine component is not in the forbidden \(Y12\) quotient after choosing the covariant residual, while the \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-component is.

This is allowed if the quotient is refined by **curvature-slot origin**:

\[
(\text{order-nine }Y12,\ \Gamma_G\text{-induced})
\]

versus

\[
(\text{order-nine }Y12,\ \Gamma_{G,2}\text{-induced}).
\]

But unless this refined grading is explicitly defined, the safe wall is the full linear form.

---

## 7. Updated theorem stack for the wall

### Theorem 1: \(Y12\)-survival

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\neq0
\quad
\text{in}
\quad
\mathcal Q_{9,2}^{\mathrm{forb}}.
\]

### Theorem 2: wall coefficient nondegeneracy

\[
|\alpha_9|\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
|\beta_9|+|\alpha_9|\le Q^C.
\]

Optionally:

\[
\beta_9=0
\]

in the refined quotient.

### Theorem 3: forbidden-line anti-concentration

\[
\int
\min\left(
Q^A|\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}|^2,
1
\right)d\nu
\ge Q^{-B}\nu(\mathcal C).
\]

### Theorem 4: branch-charge bound

\[
d_\Gamma=O(1),
\qquad
d_0=d_N+2d_H+2d_\Gamma=O(1).
\]

Then the rank-one wall is compatible with the bounded-charge O2/O3 strategy and the atomic D4 contradiction.

---

## Final conclusion

The likely consistent outcome is:

\[
\boxed{
Y12\text{ primitive } \Rightarrow \beta_9\text{ generally not absorbed.}
}
\]

So the correct downstream wall should be the moving linear form

\[
\boxed{
\ell_m(\Gamma)=\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}.
}
\]

This is not fatal. It only adds a moving-line anti-concentration theorem and may increase the O2/O3 branch-charge bandwidth by an \(O(1)\) amount.

The next useful attack is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove fixed-line anti-concentration for }
\Gamma_{G,2}+r\Gamma_G
\text{ after freezing }r=\beta_9/\alpha_9.
}
\]

Agent 5 — near-pure O2/O3 via Christoffel substitution marginal.

The instruction is to finalize the fixed-\(\alpha\) O2/O3 survival reduction after the \(Y12/K_9\) wall has fixed the Stack weight. The goal is to reduce full determinant survival to an \(O(1)\)-dimensional moment problem for the plus-to-dual substitution ratio. This follows the current coordinator direction: prove O2/O3 using smooth bounded-degree pre-extraction weights, then extract afterward. 

## 1. Branch-charge bandwidth \(d_0\)

Use the smooth pre-extraction weight

\[
W_{\mathrm{bd}}
=
N_{\mathrm{sm}}\,|H|^2\,|\ell(\Gamma)|^2,
\]

with denominator factors such as \(\mathcal N_{\mathrm{D4}}\) dyadically frozen and with no hard caps yet.

Let branch charge be

\[
\operatorname{ch}(+)= -1,\qquad
\operatorname{ch}(-)=+1,\qquad
\operatorname{ch}(\mathrm{bg})=0.
\]

The pure plus determinant has charge

\[
-n,\qquad n=R+2.
\]

The weight has finite branch-charge bandwidth

\[
d_0=d_N+2d_H+2d_\Gamma.
\]

Here:

\[
d_N=\text{branch-charge bandwidth of }N_{\mathrm{sm}},
\]

\[
d_H=\text{branch-charge bandwidth of }H,
\]

\[
d_\Gamma=\text{branch-charge bandwidth of }\ell(\Gamma).
\]

There are two cases.

### Case A: moving \(Y12\) wall

\[
\ell(\Gamma)=\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Then

\[
d_\Gamma
=
\max\{
d(\beta_9\Gamma_G),
d(\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2})
\}.
\]

This is still \(O(1)\), but it may be larger than the pure \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) case.

### Case B: \(\beta_9\) disappears in the refined \(Y12\) quotient

\[
\ell(\Gamma)=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Then

\[
d_\Gamma=d(\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

and

\[
d_0=d_N+2d_H+2d(\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

This is the cleanest case and gives the smallest near-pure block.

Conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
d_0=O(1)
}
\]

in either case. The exact value should be computed after the final \(Y12\) wall form is fixed.

---

## 2. Branch-charge reduction

Write the determinant expansion by branch charge:

\[
D_{\mathrm{full}}
=
\sum_s D_s.
\]

The pure plus sector is

\[
D_{-n}.
\]

When integrating

\[
|D_{\mathrm{full}}|^2 W_{\mathrm{bd}},
\]

a cross term

\[
D_{-n}\overline{D_s}
\]

can survive branch-charge averaging only if the weight supplies charge

\[
s+n.
\]

Since the weight has branch-charge bandwidth \(d_0\), resonance is possible only for

\[
0\le s+n\le d_0.
\]

Thus \(D_{-n}\) can interact only with

\[
D_{-n},D_{-n+1},\ldots,D_{-n+d_0}.
\]

All farther sectors are nonresonant under the smooth bounded-degree weight.

Therefore full determinant survival reduces to the near-pure Schur complement:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(W_{\mathrm{bd}})}
\left(
D_{-n},
\operatorname{span}\{D_{-n+1},\ldots,D_{-n+d_0}\}
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\|D_{-n}\|_{L^2(W_{\mathrm{bd}})}^2.
}
\]

This is the key reduction.

---

## 3. Effective one-slot substitution measure

Each near-pure sector \(D_{-n+k}\) is obtained from the pure plus exterior determinant by replacing \(k\) plus slots by non-plus slots: dual, background, or completion slots.

For a single plus-to-dual substitution, the relevant ratio is

\[
r(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}
\]

up to phase and smooth amplitude factors. More generally,

\[
R_{\pm}(x)
=
e^{i\Theta}
\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}
(1+\varepsilon(x)).
\]

The one-slot substitution measure \(\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}\) is the one-point marginal of the pure plus exterior determinant ensemble.

In a Riesz-normalized polynomial basis, this marginal has the Christoffel form

\[
d\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}(x)
=
\frac{1}{n}K_n(x,x)w(x)\,dx,
\]

where

\[
K_n(x,x)=\sum_{j=0}^{n-1}|p_j(x)|^2
\]

is the Christoffel-Darboux kernel for the orthonormalized plus-branch basis.

Here

\[
n=R+2.
\]

The normalization is chosen so

\[
\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}(\Omega)=1
\]

on the active plus interval \(\Omega\).

---

## 4. Christoffel spread estimate

Assume \(R^C\)-Riesz normalization on the active interval away from pathological endpoints. Then

\[
K_n(x,x)w(x)\le R^C n
\]

on the relevant branch support.

Therefore, for every interval \(J\subset\Omega\),

\[
\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}(J)
=
\frac1n\int_JK_n(x,x)w(x)\,dx
\le
R^C |J|.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}(J)\le R^C |J|.
}
\]

This prevents the substitution slots from concentrating on a tiny interval, including the central fold tube, unless that tube has polynomial width.

This is the spread input needed for near-pure Schur survival.

---

## 5. Reduction to a fixed-degree moment problem

The near-pure sectors are generated by elementary symmetric functions of substitution ratios.

For fixed

\[
d_0=O(1),
\]

the Schur complement reduces to proving that the constant function \(1\) is not approximated too well by low-degree functions of the substitution ratio.

A sufficient scalar theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\mu_{\mathrm{sub}})}
\left(
1,
\operatorname{span}\{R_{\pm},R_{\pm}^2,\ldots,R_{\pm}^{d_0}\}
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}.
}
\]

For the model ratio

\[
r(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2},
\]

this becomes

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\mu_{\mathrm{sub}})}
\left(
1,
\operatorname{span}\{r,r^2,\ldots,r^{d_0}\}
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}.
}
\]

If multiple substitution types appear, dual/background/tail, the span is enlarged by finitely many ratios:

\[
\operatorname{span}
\{
R_1^{a_1}\cdots R_M^{a_M}:
1\le a_1+\cdots+a_M\le d_0
\}.
\]

Since \(d_0=O(1)\), this remains a fixed-dimensional problem.

---

## 6. Proof of the finite moment lower bound

Because

\[
r(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}
\]

is strictly monotone on each side of the central point \(x=1/2\), choose \(d_0+1\) subintervals

\[
J_0,\ldots,J_{d_0}
\]

outside the central tube such that

\[
r(J_i)
\]

are separated by at least \(R^{-C}\).

By Christoffel spread and branch mass distribution, assume each \(J_i\) has

\[
\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}(J_i)\ge R^{-C}.
\]

Then for any polynomial

\[
P(z)=\sum_{k=1}^{d_0}a_k z^k,
\]

if

\[
|1-P(r(x))|
\]

were \(<R^{-C}\) on all \(J_i\), then \(1-P(z)\), a degree-\(d_0\) polynomial with constant term \(1\), would have \(d_0+1\) separated approximate zeros. The Vandermonde lower bound gives a contradiction unless the error is at least

\[
R^{-C(d_0)}.
\]

Since \(d_0=O(1)\),

\[
R^{-C(d_0)}
=
Q^{-o(1)}
\]

and hence certainly

\[
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

after adjusting constants.

Therefore

\[
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\mu_{\mathrm{sub}})}
\left(
1,
\operatorname{span}\{r,\ldots,r^{d_0}\}
\right)^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This proves the fixed-degree moment lower bound, assuming there are \(d_0+1\) separated intervals carrying polynomial \(\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}\)-mass.

---

## 7. Central tube handling

The dangerous region is

\[
|x-\tfrac12|<\delta.
\]

Use

\[
\delta=R^{-C}.
\]

Then

\[
\delta^R=R^{-CR}=Q^{-O(1)}.
\]

This is acceptable for exterior-degree losses.

There are two cases.

### Mass outside the central tube

If

\[
\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}\{|x-\tfrac12|\ge\delta\}\ge Q^{-A},
\]

then the monotonicity and separation of \(r(x)\) outside the tube give the finite moment lower bound above.

### Mass inside the central tube

Rescale

\[
x=\frac12+\delta y.
\]

Then

\[
r(x)
=
\frac{(1/2-\delta y)^2}{(1/2+\delta y)^2}
=
1-8\delta y+O(\delta^2y^2).
\]

The variation is small but not zero. The exterior loss is \(\delta^R\), still polynomial. This is the transition-scale regime. Use the multiscale fold-routing theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{central concentration is routed to the rescaled transition branch, where graph non-polynomiality is proved after scaling.}
}
\]

Thus the central tube is not an exceptional failure set. It is a rescaled branch.

---

## 8. Final bounded-charge O2/O3 theorem

A clean theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{BoundedChargeNearPureO2O3.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(A_m\) is represented in an \(R^C\)-normalized analytic Riesz basis;

2. the pre-extraction Stack weight

\[
W_{\mathrm{bd}}=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2|\ell(\Gamma)|^2
\]

has branch-charge bandwidth \(d_0=O(1)\);

3. the pure plus determinant \(D_{-n}\) has nontrivial \(L^2(W_{\mathrm{bd}})\) mass;

4. the one-slot substitution marginal satisfies Christoffel spread:

\[
\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}(J)\le R^C|J|;
\]

5. multiscale fold routing handles the central tube.

Then

\[
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(W_{\mathrm{bd}})}
\left(
D_{-n},
\operatorname{span}\{D_{-n+1},\ldots,D_{-n+d_0}\}
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\|D_{-n}\|_{L^2(W_{\mathrm{bd}})}^2.
\]

Consequently, full determinant survival holds:

\[
\int |D_{\mathrm{full}}|^2W_{\mathrm{bd}}
\ge
Q^{-A}
\int |D_{-n}|^2W_{\mathrm{bd}},
\]

and, with \(R^C\)-normalization,

\[
\int \mathcal H_{23}(A_m)W_{\mathrm{bd}}
\ge
Q^{-A}\int W_{\mathrm{bd}}.
\]

---

## 9. Remaining exact inputs

The reduction leaves three concrete inputs.

### Input 1: final wall form and \(d_0\)

Need the final \(Y12\) wall:

\[
\ell(\Gamma)=\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

or possibly

\[
\ell(\Gamma)=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Then compute

\[

\]

### Input 2: Christoffel spread

Need \(R^C\)-Riesz normalization of the plus exterior ensemble.

\[
\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}(J)\le R^C|J|.
\]

### Input 3: central routing

Need multiscale fold routing at

\[
\delta=R^{-C}
\]

with only polynomial loss.

## Final Agent 5 conclusion

Fixed-\(\alpha\) O2/O3 survival is plausible without \(\alpha\)-averaging.

The route is:

\[
\boxed{
Y12\text{ wall fixes }d_0=O(1)
}

This is now a concrete finite-dimensional O2/O3 path, not a broad determinant collision problem.

## 1. The finite moment claim

Let

\[
d=d_0=O(1).
\]

We need a lower bound

\[
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\mu)}
\left(

\ge Q^{-A},
\]

where

\[
