for the O2/O3 fold-substitution ratio

\[
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

I will not use \(r\) for any of these.

The pre-amplitude-projection wall is

\[
F_Y
=
H\alpha_9(\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G).
\]

This follows the updated convention in the prompt. 

---

# Agent 5 — wall finite type, forced ODE trap, and trap disposal

The wall layer begins after the \(Y12\)-fiber graph has been subtracted. Set

\[
A:=\Gamma_G,
\qquad
B:=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and define

\[
W_{\mathrm{wall}}
=
B+\rho_\Gamma A.
\]

The effective wall amplitude is

\[
F_Y=H\alpha_9 W_{\mathrm{wall}}.
\]

If a coherent amplitude space \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\) is present, the actual object is not \(F_Y\), but

\[
F_Y^{\mathrm{eff}}
=
(I-P_{\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}})F_Y
\]

with the projection fixed under the smooth pre-extraction measure. The wall theorem must be stated for \(F_Y^{\mathrm{eff}}\).

---

## 1. Large-\(|\Gamma_G|\) branch

On the region

\[
|A|=|\Gamma_G|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

define

\[
R_\Gamma:=\frac{B}{A}
=
\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}}{\Gamma_G}.
\]

Then

\[
W_{\mathrm{wall}}
=
A(R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma).
\]

So the wall is small only if

\[
R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma
\]

is small.

The first derivative witness is

\[
\boxed{
W_\ell
=
A B'-A'B+\rho_\Gamma' A^2.
}
\]

Indeed,

\[
A^2(R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma)'
=
A^2\left(\frac BA+\rho_\Gamma\right)'
=
AB'-A'B+\rho_\Gamma'A^2.
\]

Thus, if

\[
|W_\ell|\ge Q^{-C}|A|^2
\]

on a polynomial fraction of the smooth post-Gate/O2/O3 measure, then

\[
R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma
\]

has polynomial finite type, and standard sublevel estimates give

\[
\nu\{|W_{\mathrm{wall}}|<\varepsilon\}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\nu(\mathcal C).
\]

More generally, it is enough that for some fixed

\[
1\le j\le J=O(1),
\]

we have

\[
\left|
\partial_m^j(R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma)
\right|
\ge Q^{-C}
\]

on most of the measure. Then

\[
\nu\{|R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma|<\varepsilon\}
\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/J}\nu(\mathcal C).
\]

This is the clean finite-type wall theorem.

---

## 2. Small-\(|\Gamma_G|\) branch

On

\[
|\Gamma_G|<Q^{-C},
\]

the ratio \(R_\Gamma\) is not stable. But then

\[
W_{\mathrm{wall}}
=
\Gamma_{G,2}+O(Q^C|\Gamma_G|).
\]

So if

\[
|\Gamma_{G,2}|\ge Q^{-C'}
\]

the wall is automatically non-small.

The only dangerous small-\(|\Gamma_G|\) region is

\[
|\Gamma_G|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|\Gamma_{G,2}|<\varepsilon.
\]

Thus the required auxiliary theorem is

\[
\boxed{
\nu\{
|\Gamma_G|<\varepsilon,\,
|\Gamma_{G,2}|<\varepsilon
\}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\nu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

This is weaker than full two-dimensional wall anisotropy. It is needed only on the small-\(\Gamma_G\) branch.

---

## 3. Coherent amplitude space

If

\[
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\neq 0,
\]

the wall theorem must be a distance theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\nu)}
\left(
H\alpha_9(\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G),
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\left\|
H\alpha_9(\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G)
\right\|_{L^2(\nu)}^2.
}
\]

Equivalently, if

\[
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
=
\operatorname{span}\{\psi_1,\ldots,\psi_M\},
\qquad M\le Q^C,
\]

then the required Schur residual is

\[
\delta_{\mathrm{wall}}^2
=
\|F_Y\|^2
-
b^*G^\dagger b
\ge Q^{-A}\|F_Y\|^2,
\]

where

\[
G_{ij}=\langle\psi_i,\psi_j\rangle_{L^2(\nu)},
\]

\[
b_i=\langle F_Y,\psi_i\rangle_{L^2(\nu)}.
\]

If \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\) contains extraction-scale local amplitudes, this Schur residual may vanish. That is the local-free amplitude failure.

---

## 4. Low-order condition on \(\rho_\Gamma\)

The wall is meaningful only if

\[
\rho_\Gamma
=
\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9}
\]

is genuinely low-order.

The required audit is

\[
\boxed{
\rho_\Gamma\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{low}},
\qquad
\partial_{\Gamma_{G,2}}\rho_\Gamma=0.
}
\]

Here \(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{low}}\) may depend on low Gram/whitening variables and fixed carrier constants, for example

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi},
\qquad
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''_{\mathrm{can}}\right),
\]

but it must not depend on

\[
q^{(4)},\quad
\Gamma_{G,2},\quad
s_9^Y,\quad
\text{or actual order-nine source data}.
\]

If \(\rho_\Gamma\) depends on any of those high-order/wall variables, the equation

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G=0
\]

may become tautological.

---

## 5. Forced wall ODE

If

\[
W_{\mathrm{wall}}
=
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G
\approx0,
\]

then, using the current sign convention from the prompt, the source is trapped near

\[
\boxed{
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q_0^2+\rho_\Gamma)q''
-
36\rho_\Gamma q_0
+
12\rho_\Gamma q_0^3.
}
\]

If a coherent amplitude

\[
\phi\in\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\]

is present, the forced version is

\[
\boxed{
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q_0^2+\rho_\Gamma)q''
-
36\rho_\Gamma q_0
+
12\rho_\Gamma q_0^3
-
6\frac{\phi}{H\alpha_9}.
}
\]

I am retaining the sign convention exactly as specified, but this sign must be checked against the final definitions of \(\Gamma_G\) and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\).

This ODE trap is meaningful only if \(\rho_\Gamma\) is low-order and \(\phi\) belongs to a fixed/finite-dimensional coherent amplitude space. If \(\phi\) is locally free, the trap is vacuous.

---

## 6. Finite-type-or-trap theorem

The correct wall result should be stated as a dichotomy.

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{MovingWallFiniteTypeOrForcedODETrap.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(Y12\) survives the fiber Schur test;

2. the graph-subtracted wall is

\[
W_{\mathrm{wall}}=\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G;
\]

3. \(\rho_\Gamma\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{low}}\) and

\[
\partial_{\Gamma_{G,2}}\rho_\Gamma=0;
\]

4. \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\) is either zero or finite-dimensional/coherent with polynomial conditioning.

Then one of the following holds.

### Wall-good branch

\[
\boxed{
\int
\min\left(
Q^A\,
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
H\alpha_9 W_{\mathrm{wall}},
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)^2,
1
\right)
d\nu
\ge Q^{-B}\nu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

This supplies the rank-one wall mass.

### Trap branch

On a polynomial-weight subset,

\[
q
\]

lies near the finite-dimensional forced ODE model

\[
\boxed{
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q_0^2+\rho_\Gamma)q''
-
36\rho_\Gamma q_0
+
12\rho_\Gamma q_0^3
-
6\frac{\phi}{H\alpha_9},
\qquad
\phi\in\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}.
}
\]

The trap branch must then be excluded or routed.

---

## 7. Trap-disposal options

The rank-one \(Y12\) wall closes only if the trap branch is handled. There are three viable directions.

### Option A: anti-ODE theorem

Prove actual canonical EF sources cannot satisfy the forced ODE model on a polynomial-weight Stack-good set.

This is the cleanest disposal:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\nu)}
\left(
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q),
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)\|.
}
\]

where

\[
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
=
q^{(4)}
-
6(1-q_0^2+\rho_\Gamma)q''
+
36\rho_\Gamma q_0
-
12\rho_\Gamma q_0^3.
\]

### Option B: higher-order derivative residual

If the wall ODE holds, differentiate it and test whether

\[
\partial_m\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
\]

has a new primitive signature not absorbed by the ODE model. This is a targeted higher-order residual route.

### Option C: rank-two rescue

If another D4 normal direction survives, the vector wall may still have mass even when

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G=0.
\]

Then rank-one failure is not fatal.

---

## 8. Current conclusion

The wall layer is now precise:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite type of }R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma
\quad\text{or}\quad
\text{forced low-order ODE trap}.
}
\]

The key prerequisites are:

\[
\boxed{
\rho_\Gamma
\text{ is low-order}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\text{ is finite-dimensional/coherent, not locally free}.
}
\]

If both hold, the wall problem is no longer vague. Persistent wall failure is exactly a forced fourth-order ODE branch, which must be attacked as a new finite model-space condition.

I’ll now attack the trap branch as a model-space problem: if the wall ODE holds, determine whether it is already incompatible with the finite O2/O3 graph model or whether it requires a higher-order residual.

_Thought for 6s_

Continuing Agent 5 — disposal of the forced wall-ODE trap.

I will keep the current nomenclature:

\[
\rho_Y=\text{the }Y12\text{ fiber graph slope},
\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

The effective wall is

\[
W_{\mathrm{wall}}
=
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G.
\]

The previous attack produced the dichotomy:

\[
\boxed{
\text{wall finite type}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\text{forced low-order ODE trap}.
}
\]

The trap is

\[
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q_0^2+\rho_\Gamma)q''
-
36\rho_\Gamma q_0
+
12\rho_\Gamma q_0^3
-
6\frac{\phi}{H\alpha_9},
\qquad
\phi\in\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}.
\]

The question now is whether this trap is contradictory, routable, or a genuine escape. 

---

## 1. Trap as a finite-dimensional jet manifold

Define

\[
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
=
q^{(4)}
-
6(1-q_0^2+\rho_\Gamma)q''
+
36\rho_\Gamma q_0
-
12\rho_\Gamma q_0^3.
\]

The trap is

\[
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)\in \mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}.
\]

If \(\rho_\Gamma\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{low}}\), then \(\mathcal W_\Gamma\) expresses \(q^{(4)}\) in terms of lower-order variables plus a finite-dimensional coherent forcing. Differentiating gives

\[
q^{(5)},q^{(6)},\ldots
\]

as functions of lower jets, derivatives of \(\rho_\Gamma\), and derivatives of \(\phi\). Thus the trap defines a finite-dimensional jet manifold:

\[
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{ODE}}
=
\left\{
J_K(q):
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)\in\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}},
\ 
\partial_m^j\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)\in\partial_m^j\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}},
\ 0\le j\le K-4
\right\}.
\]

So the wall-trapped branch is another structured model-space condition:

\[
\boxed{
J_K(q)
\text{ lies near }
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{ODE}}.
}
\]

This is not automatically impossible. It is a new model branch.

---

## 2. Does O2/O3 already exclude the trap?

O2/O3 currently gives graph non-polynomiality of

\[
1/m_{\can,+}
\]

and finite determinant survival. The wall ODE relates

\[
q^{(4)}
\]

to

\[
q_0,\quad q'',\quad \rho_\Gamma,\quad \phi.
\]

Unless \(m_{\can,+}\) depends directly on \(q^{(4)}\), O2/O3 does not immediately see this relation.

In the current low-order convention, \(\rho_\Gamma\) is not allowed to depend on \(q^{(4)}\), and \(m_{\can,+}\) appears to be built from lower Gram/whitening data such as

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi},
\qquad
h=\frac{1}{\pi}\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''_{\can}\right).
\]

Then O2/O3 and the wall ODE operate on different layers:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{O2/O3}:
\text{non-polynomiality of a lower-order multiplier;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{wall\ trap}:
\text{constraint on fourth-order curvature.}
}
\]

Therefore O2/O3 does **not** automatically exclude the wall trap.

It may help only if the trap forces \(m_{\can,+}\) into a polynomially approximable regime, or if differentiating the ODE feeds back into \(m_{\can,+}\). That relation is not currently established.

So the trap branch is not killed by existing O2/O3.

---

## 3. Does Gate–1 exclude the trap?

Gate–1 is local scalar \(L^2\) energy:

\[
\int_I |\lambda^3q''_{\can}(m+\lambda x)|^2\,dx\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The wall ODE permits nonzero \(q''\). Indeed, it determines \(q^{(4)}\) from lower data; it does not force \(q''=0\).

So Gate–1 is compatible with the trap.

Gate–1 can still help by ensuring that the ODE solution is not trivial, but it does not provide a contradiction.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate--1 does not dispose of the wall ODE trap.}
}
\]

---

## 4. The trap likely requires a higher residual

If the rank-one \(Y12\) wall is trapped, the natural next residual is the derivative of the trapped equation:

\[
\partial_m\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
-
\Pi_{\partial\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}}
\partial_m\mathcal W_\Gamma(q).
\]

This residual lives at order five relative to \(q\), or at the next singular carrier level relative to the original \(Y12\) order-nine package.

The finite-D4 analogue is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{differentiate the }Y12\text{ normal residual and test its primitive signature.}
}
\]

In the paper’s carrier language, this likely corresponds to an order-eleven or next-carrier residual, not a generic high-order search. It is targeted:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Order-nine }Y12\text{ trapped}
\Rightarrow
\text{test derivative/connection of }Y12\text{ residual.}
}
\]

So the trap branch suggests a precise higher-order attack, not a broad escalation.

---

## 5. Rank-two rescue possibility

If another independent D4 normal direction survives in the quotient, the wall vector becomes two-dimensional:

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{forb}}D_{\mathrm{D4}}\Gamma
=
H\left(
v_1\Gamma_G+v_2\Gamma_{G,2}
\right),
\]

with \(v_1,v_2\) independent.

Then wall failure would require both components small, not just

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G\approx0.
\]

This would replace the forced ODE trap by a stronger joint condition:

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0
\]

in a suitable basis.

So rank-two D4 would avoid the moving-line trap.

The finite audit is:

\[
\operatorname{rank}
\left[
c_7y_7+\beta_9y_Y,\ \alpha_9y_Y
\right]
\stackrel{?}{=}2
\]

after quotienting actual-source and nuisance directions.

If rank two holds, the wall theorem is substantially easier. If rank one only, the ODE-trap branch remains.

Thus, even though rank one is enough in principle, rank two may be needed to avoid the trap branch.

---

## 6. Anti-ODE theorem as an arithmetic input

The cleanest disposal is an anti-ODE theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\nu)}
\left(
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q),
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)
\ge
Q^{-A}
\|\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)\|_{L^2(\nu)}.
}
\]

But this is essentially another model-space transversality theorem, now for a fourth-order nonlinear ODE model.

It is analogous to:

- Gate–1 anti-lock, which excludes \(L^2\)-AFE cancellation;
- O2/O3 graph non-polynomiality, which excludes \(1/m_{\can,+}\in\mathbf C_R[x]\);
- Y12 normality, which excludes \(y_Y\in\mathcal A\).

So anti-ODE is structurally plausible, but it is a **new theorem**, not a consequence of previous ones.

The finite proof strategy would be:

1. show \(\rho_\Gamma\) is low-order and finite-type;
2. show \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\) is finite-dimensional/coherent;
3. prove the actual EF source \(q\) cannot lie near the solution manifold of the forced ODE on the Stack-good set.

This is likely an arithmetic/explicit-formula theorem.

---

## 7. Trap branch classification

The wall-trap branch has three possible statuses.

### Green if anti-ODE theorem holds

Then wall finite type is effectively established.

### Yellow if higher residual is available

If the trap branch can be routed to an order-eleven derivative residual with a new primitive signature, the proof survives but requires another finite carrier audit.

### Red if trap is a genuine actual-source model

If actual EF sources can satisfy the forced wall ODE on polynomial mass and no higher residual sees it, the rank-one \(Y12\) route fails.

This would mean the D4 \(Y12\) normal direction exists fiberwise, but the actual curvature vector \(\Gamma\) never excites it away from the coherent model.

---

## 8. Updated theorem statement

The wall module should be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{MovingWallFiniteTypeOrRoutedTrap.}
}
\]

Assume:

\[
Y12\text{ survives},
\quad
\rho_\Gamma\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{low}},
\quad
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\text{ is not locally free}.
\]

Then either:

1. the rank-one wall has polynomial mass:

\[
\int \min(Q^A\operatorname{dist}(F_Y,\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}})^2,1)d\nu
\ge Q^{-B}\nu(\mathcal C);
\]

or

2. the source lies on the forced wall-ODE branch:

\[
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)\in\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\]

to high order on polynomial mass, and this branch must be handled by:

\[
\text{AntiODE}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\text{HigherResidual}_{Y12}.
\]

This is the honest downstream state.

---

## Final result of this attack

The low-order wall ODE trap is not automatically contradictory and is not automatically killed by Gate–1 or O2/O3.

Therefore the \(Y12\) rank-one route still needs one more disposal theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{AntiODE for the forced wall model}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{higher-order residual on the wall-trapped branch.}
}
\]

This is the main remaining downstream bottleneck after \(Y12\) fiber normality and amplitude non-absorption.

I’ll push the trap disposal through the higher-residual route, since Gate–1 and O2/O3 do not automatically exclude the wall ODE. The goal is to define the next residual only on the trapped branch, not globally escalate D4.

Continuing Agent 5 — targeted higher residual for the wall-ODE trap branch.

I’ll keep the current notation:

\[
\rho_Y=\text{the }Y12\text{ fiber graph slope},
\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

The rank-one \(Y12\) wall is

\[
F_Y
=
H\alpha_9(\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G).
\]

If this wall has finite type, the downstream D4 contradiction proceeds. If not, the source is trapped near the forced wall ODE:

\[
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
=
q^{(4)}
-
6(1-q_0^2+\rho_\Gamma)q''
+
36\rho_\Gamma q_0
-
12\rho_\Gamma q_0^3
\in
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}.
\]

The previous attack showed Gate–1 and O2/O3 do not automatically dispose of this trap. So the natural next step is a **targeted higher residual on the trapped branch**.

---

## 1. Define the trap residual

Let

\[
\psi\in \mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\]

be the coherent forcing that best approximates

\[
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q).
\]

Define

\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{trap}}(q)
=
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)-\psi.
\]

On the trap branch,

\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{trap}}(q)\approx0.
\]

The next residual is its derivative modulo the tangent of the coherent forcing space:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{trap}}^{(1)}(q)
=
\partial_m\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
-
\Pi_{\partial\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}}
\partial_m\mathcal W_\Gamma(q).
}
\]

If

\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{trap}}^{(1)}(q)
\]

is nonzero at polynomial scale, then the wall trap is unstable and yields a new forbidden direction.

This is the correct higher residual: not a generic order-eleven search, but the derivative of the wall-ODE normal form.

---

## 2. Expansion of the derivative residual

Write

\[
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
=
q^{(4)}
-
6(1-q_0^2+\rho_\Gamma)q''
+
36\rho_\Gamma q_0
-
12\rho_\Gamma q_0^3.
\]

Then

\[
\partial_m\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
=
q^{(5)}
-
6(1-q_0^2+\rho_\Gamma)q'''
+
12q_0q_0'q''
-
6\rho_\Gamma' q''
\]

\[
\qquad
+
36\rho_\Gamma' q_0
+
36\rho_\Gamma q_0'
-
12\rho_\Gamma' q_0^3
-
36\rho_\Gamma q_0^2q_0'.
\]

Grouping:

\[
\boxed{
\partial_m\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
=
q^{(5)}
-
6(1-q_0^2+\rho_\Gamma)q'''
-
6\rho_\Gamma' q''
+
12q_0q_0'q''
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\qquad
+
36\rho_\Gamma' q_0
+
36\rho_\Gamma q_0'
-
12\rho_\Gamma' q_0^3
-
36\rho_\Gamma q_0^2q_0'.
}
\]

Thus the derivative trap residual has leading term

\[
q^{(5)}
\]

plus lower-order terms controlled by

\[
q_0,\ q_0',\ q'',\ q''',\ \rho_\Gamma,\ \rho_\Gamma'.
\]

If

\[
\rho_\Gamma
\]

is low-order, this is a genuine next-order residual.

---

## 3. Finite-type hierarchy

If

\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{trap}}^{(1)}(q)
\]

also lies in the derivative coherent space, differentiate again. Define recursively

\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{trap}}^{(j)}(q)
=
\partial_m^j\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
-
\Pi_{\partial^j\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}}
\partial_m^j\mathcal W_\Gamma(q).
\]

Then one of two things happens for some bounded

\[
0\le j\le J=O(1).
\]

### Higher residual appears

\[
\|\mathcal R_{\mathrm{trap}}^{(j)}(q)\|
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

on the trapped mass. This gives a new normal direction and a new forbidden channel.

### Infinite finite-order trapping

All

\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{trap}}^{(j)}(q)
\]

are small for

\[
0\le j\le J.
\]

Then the source lies near a finite-dimensional jet solution manifold of the forced ODE to order \(J\). This is a stronger ODE model-space trap.

Thus the wall trap can be handled by a finite hierarchy:

\[
\boxed{
\text{wall finite type}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\text{higher residual}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\text{high-order ODE model trap}.
}
\]

---

## 4. Relation to D4 order

The original \(Y12\) residual was order-nine in the singular carrier package. Differentiating the wall-ODE residual corresponds to one higher singular order, plausibly order eleven depending on the normalization and parity.

But the escalation is targeted:

\[
\boxed{
\text{only the wall-trapped branch needs the higher residual.}
}
\]

This is better than globally replacing the finite-D4 package with a high-order D4 package.

The next carrier to audit should be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the primitive signature of }
\partial_m\left(
\Pi_YD_{\mathrm{D4}}
-
\text{coherent wall graph}
\right).
}
\]

That is the derivative of the \(Y12\)-normal residual, not an arbitrary order-eleven carrier.

---

## 5. Rank-two rescue remains preferable if available

Before committing to the higher-residual hierarchy, one should still check whether the original forbidden quotient has rank two.

If the quotient sees two independent D4 vectors

\[
v_1=c_7y_7+\beta_9y_Y,
\qquad
v_2=\alpha_9y_Y,
\]

then the wall energy is

\[
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)
\]

in a conditioned basis, and the moving-line trap disappears.

So the priority order remains:

1. test \(Y12\) rank-one survival;
2. test whether the same quotient is actually rank two;
3. if rank one, prove moving-wall finite type;
4. if moving-wall finite type fails, use the targeted higher residual.

---

## 6. Anti-ODE theorem vs higher residual

The anti-ODE theorem would say:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q),
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

on the Stack-good mass.

This is exactly

\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{trap}}^{(0)}(q)
\]

being large. If it fails, the derivative residual checks whether the failure is stable.

So the hierarchy unifies the two approaches:

\[
\boxed{
\text{AntiODE}
=
j=0\text{ case of the trap residual hierarchy.}
}
\]

Higher residuals are

\[
j\ge1.
\]

Thus the clean theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\exists j\le J
\text{ such that }
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{trap}}^{(j)}(q)
\text{ has polynomial mass,}
}
\]

or the source is trapped near an order-\(J\) forced ODE jet manifold.

---

## 7. The remaining hard theorem

The hierarchy still needs a final exclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual EF source cannot lie near the forced ODE jet manifold to order }J
\text{ on polynomial mass.}
}
\]

This is the genuine arithmetic/model-space input.

But it is now sharply formulated. The model is finite-dimensional, determined by

\[
\rho_\Gamma,\quad
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}},
\]

and the low-order variables.

This is much more concrete than “wall anti-concentration.”

---

## 8. Updated downstream theorem

The downstream module should be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Y12WallOrTrapHierarchy.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(Y12\) fiber graph is nonvertical;

2. \(\rho_\Gamma\) is low-order;

3. \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\) is finite-dimensional/coherent, not locally free.

Then either:

### Wall-good

\[
F_Y^{\mathrm{eff}}
\]

has polynomial \(L^2\) mass and gives the D4 contradiction;

or

### Trap-residual-good

For some \(1\le j\le J\),

\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{trap}}^{(j)}(q)
\]

gives a higher-order forbidden residual;

or

### ODE-model branch

The source lies near a finite-dimensional forced ODE jet manifold through order \(J\). This branch requires a separate anti-model theorem or indicates failure of rank-one \(Y12\).

---

## Final result of this attack

The wall ODE trap is not a dead end. It creates a targeted hierarchy:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q),\ 
\partial_m\mathcal W_\Gamma(q),\ 
\partial_m^2\mathcal W_\Gamma(q),\ldots
}
\]

modulo coherent amplitude spaces.

The next residual should be the derivative of the \(Y12\) wall residual, not a generic new D4 carrier.

If a bounded derivative residual is nonzero, the trapped branch is eliminated. If all bounded derivatives vanish, the source is trapped in a finite-dimensional forced ODE jet model, which becomes the next explicit model-space obstruction.

## 1. Define the forced-ODE jet model

Fix a local atom or smooth block \(\omega\). Let

\[
\mathcal C_{Y,\omega}^{\mathrm{arith}}
=
\operatorname{span}\{\psi_1,\ldots,\psi_M\}
\]

be the coherent \(Y12\)-amplitude space on \(\omega\), with \(M\le Q^C\).

For \(J=O(1)\), define the forced-ODE jet model

\[
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{ODE},J}(\omega)
\]

as the set of \(q\)-jets satisfying

\[
\partial_m^j\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
\in
\partial_m^j\mathcal C_{Y,\omega}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\qquad
0\le j\le J.
\]

Equivalently, for each \(0\le j\le J\),

\[
\partial_m^j\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
=
\sum_{a=1}^{M} c_a\,\partial_m^j\psi_a
\]

with the same coefficient vector \(c=(c_a)\) across all \(j\).

This “same coefficient vector” point matters. If each derivative level had independent coefficients, the model would be artificially too large.

Thus the trap model is finite-dimensional:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{ODE},J}
=
\left\{
J_{4+J}(q):
\partial_m^j\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
=
\sum_a c_a\partial_m^j\psi_a,\ 
0\le j\le J
\right\}.
}
\]

---

## 2. Trap residual as a block Schur complement

Define the block vector

\[
\mathbf W_J(q)
=
\left(
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q),
\partial_m\mathcal W_\Gamma(q),
\ldots,
\partial_m^J\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
\right).
\]

Define the coherent forcing block matrix

\[
\Psi_J
=
\left[
(\psi_a,\psi_a',\ldots,\psi_a^{(J)})
\right]_{a=1}^M.
\]

Then the trap residual is

\[
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{trap},J}^2
=
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\omega)}
\left(
\mathbf W_J(q),
\operatorname{ran}\Psi_J
\right)^2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\delta_{\mathrm{trap},J}^2
=
\|\mathbf W_J(q)\|^2
-
b^*G_\Psi^\dagger b,
\]

where

\[
G_\Psi=\Psi_J^*\Psi_J,
\qquad
b=\Psi_J^*\mathbf W_J(q).
\]

So the wall-trap branch is another explicit Schur residual.

The desired theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{trap},J}^2
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf W_J(q)\|^2
}
\]

on the trap branch, for some bounded \(J\), unless the source belongs to the ODE model.

---

## 3. Relation to the moving-wall theorem

The wall module can now be stated in a clean three-way form.

### Branch 1: wall finite type

\[
F_Y^{\mathrm{eff}}
\]

has polynomial \(L^2\) mass, and the rank-one \(Y12\) wall supplies the D4 contradiction.

### Branch 2: finite trap residual

For some \(1\le J\le J_0\),

\[
\delta_{\mathrm{trap},J}^2
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf W_J(q)\|^2.
\]

Then the derivative of the wall-ODE residual supplies a higher but targeted forbidden channel.

### Branch 3: true ODE-model concentration

For all \(J\le J_0\),

\[
\delta_{\mathrm{trap},J}^2
\ll Q^{-A}\|\mathbf W_J(q)\|^2.
\]

Then

\[
q
\]

is genuinely concentrated near the forced ODE jet model

\[
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{ODE},J_0}.
\]

This must be handled by an anti-model theorem or by escalating to a different D4 carrier.

This is now precise.

---

## 4. Why the same-coefficient condition is important

Suppose

\[
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\]

has dimension \(M\). The derivative block should be

\[
\operatorname{span}
\left\{
(\psi_a,\psi_a',\ldots,\psi_a^{(J)}):
1\le a\le M
\right\},
\]

not

\[
\bigoplus_{j=0}^{J}\partial_m^j\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}.
\]

The latter has dimension \((J+1)M\) and allows different coefficients at each derivative level. That would overfit the trap.

Actual coherent amplitude functions have one coefficient vector. Their derivatives are linked.

So the correct coherent derivative model is graph-like, not vertically free.

This repeats the core theme:

\[
\boxed{
\text{graph-like coherence is allowed; free vertical amplitudes are fatal.}
}
\]

---

## 5. What would make the ODE model too large?

The trap Schur theorem can fail for two reasons.

### Failure A: locally free coherent amplitude space

If

\[
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\]

contains extraction-scale bump functions, then \(\Psi_J\) can fit arbitrary \(\mathbf W_J(q)\) locally. The Schur residual vanishes.

This is the same NoLocalFreeAmplitude condition.

### Failure B: \(\rho_\Gamma\) is high-order/fitted

If

\[
\rho_\Gamma
\]

depends on

\[
q^{(4)},\quad \Gamma_{G,2},\quad s_9^Y,
\]

then

\[
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
\]

may be designed to vanish. The trap model is tautological.

Thus the trap Schur theorem requires:

\[
\rho_\Gamma\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{low}},
\qquad
\partial_{\Gamma_{G,2}}\rho_\Gamma=0.
\]

---

## 6. Potential link to O2/O3

The ODE jet model constrains higher derivatives of \(q\), but O2/O3 uses lower graph data through

\[
m_{\mathrm{can},+}.
\]

If

\[
m_{\mathrm{can},+}
\]

depends only on lower variables \(q_0,q''\), then O2/O3 does not directly exclude the ODE model.

However, if the forced ODE model persists across a thick set, it may imply that

\[
m_{\mathrm{can},+}
\]

has a special evolution. That could either:

1. force \(1/m_{\mathrm{can},+}\) closer to \(\mathbf C_R[x]\), contradicting the graph theorem; or  
2. force a special branch-ratio identity affecting \(R_{\mathrm{fold}}\), contradicting near-pure moment separation.

This is speculative. It is not yet a theorem.

So for now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{O2/O3 does not automatically dispose of the ODE trap.}
}
\]

The trap needs its own Schur/anti-model theorem.

---

A direct anti-model theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{

}
\]

\]

be defined by

\[
\mathbf W_J(q)\in\operatorname{ran}\Psi_J.

Then on the Stack C2 good measure,

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\mathbf W_J(q),
\operatorname{ran}\Psi_J
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\|\mathbf W_J(q)\|^2
}

unless the source is routed to a higher residual branch.

This theorem is an explicit model-space transversality statement, parallel to:

\[
q''_{\can}\notin\text{branch holes},
\]

\[
1/m_{\can,+}\notin \mathbf C_R[x],
\]

\[
y_Y\notin\mathcal A.
\]

So the architecture remains consistent.

If

The corresponding D4 variation is the derivative of the \(Y12\) wall variation:

\left[

\right],
\qquad
0\le j\le J.

This is not a completely new carrier. It is the derivative tower of the existing \(Y12\) normal channel.

Thus the higher residual is still downstream-compatible and does not reopen the source-family architecture.

The new wall factor would be

E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{trap}}
=
\left\|

\left(
\partial_m^j[

\right)_{j=0}^{J}

This is a higher-order wall factor, but still generated by the same \(Y12\) normal channel.

The final downstream theorem should be formulated as:

\[
\boxed{

}

Assume:

1. \(\mathrm{LiveY12DualPair}\);

has polynomial mass;

\[
q
\]

lies near

\]

on a polynomial-weight set.

The wall ODE trap can be made finite and algebraic:

=

# Agent 5 — Wall finite type, amplitude Schur, and forced ODE trap hierarchy

## 1. Basic wall residual

Set

\[
A:=\Gamma_G,
\qquad
B:=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Then

\[
W_{\mathrm{wall}}=B+\rho_\Gamma A.
\]

On the region

\[
|A|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

define

\[
R_\Gamma:=\frac BA.
\]

Then

\[
W_{\mathrm{wall}}
=
A(R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma).
\]

Thus wall smallness is equivalent to

\[
R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma
\]

being small, up to the nonzero factor \(A\).

---

## 2. First finite-type witness

The first derivative witness is

\[
\boxed{
W_\ell
=
AB'-A'B+\rho_\Gamma'A^2.
}
\]

Indeed,

\[
A^2(R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma)'
=
A^2\left(\frac BA+\rho_\Gamma\right)'
=
AB'-A'B+\rho_\Gamma'A^2.
\]

Therefore, if

\[
|W_\ell|\ge Q^{-C}|A|^2
\]

on a smooth atom, then

\[
|(R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma)'|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and the usual one-dimensional sublevel estimate gives

\[
\nu_\omega\{|R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma|<\varepsilon\}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\,\nu_\omega(\omega).
\]

Consequently,

\[
\nu_\omega\{|W_{\mathrm{wall}}|<\varepsilon\}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\,\nu_\omega(\omega)
\]

after dyadic freezing of \(|A|\).

---

## 3. Higher finite-type version

The first derivative can vanish. The robust finite-type theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\exists\,1\le j\le J=O(1):
\left|
\partial_m^j(R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma)
\right|
\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

on each smooth atom, outside a controlled exceptional set.

Then

\[
\nu_\omega\{|R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma|<\varepsilon\}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/J}\nu_\omega(\omega).
\]

Thus the wall-good branch is:

\[
\boxed{
\int
\min\left(
Q^A |H\alpha_9|^2|W_{\mathrm{wall}}|^2,
1
\right)d\nu
\ge Q^{-B}\nu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

This assumes no coherent \(Y12\)-amplitude space is being subtracted. If such a space exists, use the distance version below.

---

## 4. Small-\(|\Gamma_G|\) branch

The ratio

\[
R_\Gamma=B/A
\]

is not valid when

\[
|A|=|\Gamma_G|
\]

is small.

On

\[
|\Gamma_G|<Q^{-C},
\]

the wall is

\[
W_{\mathrm{wall}}
=
\Gamma_{G,2}+O(Q^C|\Gamma_G|).
\]

So the only dangerous set is

\[
|\Gamma_G|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|\Gamma_{G,2}|<\varepsilon.
\]

The needed joint sublevel estimate is:

\[
\boxed{
\nu\{
|\Gamma_G|<\varepsilon,\,
|\Gamma_{G,2}|<\varepsilon
\}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\nu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

Therefore the wall theorem splits into:

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge Q^{-C}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{finite type of }R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma,
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|<Q^{-C}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{joint sublevel for }(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

---

## 5. Coherent amplitude spaces

If

\[
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\neq0,
\]

then \(F_Y\) itself is not the forbidden wall. The forbidden quantity is its distance from the coherent amplitude model.

Let

\[
F_Y=H\alpha_9(\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G).
\]

The amplitude Schur condition is

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\nu)}
\left(
F_Y,\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\|F_Y\|_{L^2(\nu)}^2.
}
\]

If

\[
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
=
\operatorname{span}\{\psi_1,\ldots,\psi_M\},
\qquad
M\le Q^C,
\]

then

\[
\delta_{\mathrm{amp}}^2
=
\|F_Y\|^2-b^*G^\dagger b,
\]

where

\[
G_{ab}=\langle \psi_a,\psi_b\rangle_{L^2(\nu)},
\]

\[
b_a=\langle F_Y,\psi_a\rangle_{L^2(\nu)}.
\]

The wall-good condition becomes

\[
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{amp}}^2\ge Q^{-A}\|F_Y\|^2.
}
\]

If \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\) contains extraction-scale atom-local amplitudes, this Schur residual can vanish. That is the locally free amplitude no-go.

---

## 6. Forced wall ODE

If the wall is absorbed or lacks finite type, then

\[
W_{\mathrm{wall}}
=
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G
\]

is small modulo coherent amplitude forcing.

Using the current convention, wall failure gives the forced ODE

\[
\boxed{
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q_0^2+\rho_\Gamma)q''
-
36\rho_\Gamma q_0
+
12\rho_\Gamma q_0^3
-
6\frac{\phi}{H\alpha_9},
\qquad
\phi\in\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}.
}
\]

Define

\[
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
=
q^{(4)}
-
6(1-q_0^2+\rho_\Gamma)q''
+
36\rho_\Gamma q_0
-
12\rho_\Gamma q_0^3.
\]

Then the trap is

\[
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
=
-6\frac{\phi}{H\alpha_9}
\]

up to sign convention, or more invariantly,

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)\in \widetilde{\mathcal C}_Y^{\mathrm{arith}},
}
\]

where

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal C}_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
=
\left\{
-6\phi/(H\alpha_9):
\phi\in\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right\}.
\]

The sign should be audited once the final definitions of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) are fixed.

---

## 7. Trap derivative hierarchy

Define the trap jet vector

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf W_J(q)
=
\left(
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q),
\partial_m\mathcal W_\Gamma(q),
\ldots,
\partial_m^J\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
\right).
}
\]

If \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\) has basis \(\psi_a\), define the coherent derivative model

\[
\boxed{
\Psi_J
=
\left[
(\psi_a,\psi_a',\ldots,\psi_a^{(J)})
\right]_a.
}
\]

Crucial correction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the same coefficient vector must be used across all derivative levels.}
}
\]

That is, the model is

\[
\sum_a c_a(\psi_a,\psi_a',\ldots,\psi_a^{(J)}),
\]

not

\[
\bigoplus_{j=0}^J\partial_m^j\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\]

with independent coefficients at each derivative. Allowing independent coefficients would make the model artificially too large and could erase the residual.

The trap Schur residual is

\[
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{trap},J}^2
=
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\mathbf W_J(q),
\operatorname{ran}\Psi_J
\right)^2.
}
\]

If

\[
\delta_{\mathrm{trap},J}^2\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf W_J(q)\|^2,
\]

then a derivative-wall residual supplies a targeted higher-order forbidden channel.

If

\[
\delta_{\mathrm{trap},J}^2\ll Q^{-A}\|\mathbf W_J(q)\|^2
\]

for all \(J\le J_0\), then the source lies near a finite-dimensional forced ODE jet model.

---

## 8. Wall hierarchy theorem

The current theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{WallFiniteTypeOrTrapHierarchy.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(Y12\) survives the fiber Schur test;

2. \(\rho_\Gamma\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{low}}\);

3.

\[
\partial_{\Gamma_{G,2}}\rho_\Gamma=
\partial_{q^{(4)}}\rho_\Gamma=
\partial_{s_9^Y}\rho_\Gamma=0;
\]

4. \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\) is not locally free.

Then one of the following holds.

### Branch 1: wall finite type

\[
F_Y
\]

has polynomial mass modulo \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\), giving the rank-one D4 wall.

### Branch 2: derivative-wall residual

For some

\[
1\le J\le J_0,
\]

\[
\delta_{\mathrm{trap},J}^2
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf W_J(q)\|^2.
\]

Then the derivative-wall residual becomes the forbidden channel.

### Branch 3: forced ODE jet model

For all

\[
J\le J_0,
\]

\[
\mathbf W_J(q)
\]

lies near

\[
\operatorname{ran}\Psi_J.
\]

Then the actual source is trapped near a finite-dimensional forced fourth-order ODE jet model. This is the remaining escape branch.

---

## 9. What remains if the ODE trap persists?

If Branch 3 occurs, neither Gate–1 nor O2/O3 automatically kills it.

The options are:

### Option A: anti-ODE theorem

Prove actual EF sources cannot concentrate near

\[
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)\in\widetilde{\mathcal C}_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\]

to order \(J_0\).

### Option B: higher primitive residual

Find the next primitive carrier in the derivative tower of the \(Y12\) residual.

This is targeted high order, not generic high-order D4.

### Option C: rank-two rescue

If the original quotient has rank two, then the moving-line trap is avoided.

### Option D: no-go

If the actual source genuinely satisfies the forced ODE model and no higher/rank-two residual sees it, the rank-one \(Y12\) route is insufficient.

---

## Final Agent 5 conclusion

The wall theorem is now a nested finite Schur hierarchy:

\[
\boxed{
\text{wall finite type}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{derivative-wall Schur residual}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{forced ODE jet model trap}.
}
\]

The decisive assumptions are:

\[
\boxed{
\rho_\Gamma\text{ is low-order and non-tautological}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\text{ is finite coherent, not locally free.}
}
\]

If both hold, the wall problem is no longer vague: it is a finite-type/sublevel theorem with a precisely defined forced-ODE fallback.

## Assistant (2026-04-28 06:25:06)

I’ll continue by testing whether the forced ODE jet model can be absorbed into the existing finite-type framework, rather than requiring a wholly new theorem.

Continuing Agent 5 — can the forced ODE jet trap be folded back into the finite-type framework?

I will keep the established notation:

\[
\rho_Y=\text{the }Y12\text{ fiber graph slope},
\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

The effective wall is

\[
F_Y=H\alpha_9(\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G),
\]

and the forced wall ODE residual is

\[
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
=
q^{(4)}
-
6(1-q_0^2+\rho_\Gamma)q''
+
36\rho_\Gamma q_0
-
12\rho_\Gamma q_0^3.
\]

The trap branch says

\[
\mathbf W_J(q)
=
(\mathcal W_\Gamma,\partial_m\mathcal W_\Gamma,\ldots,\partial_m^J\mathcal W_\Gamma)
\]

lies near

\[
\operatorname{ran}\Psi_J
=
\operatorname{span}
\{(\psi_a,\psi_a',\ldots,\psi_a^{(J)})\}_a.
\]

---

## 1. The trap is itself a finite-type failure

The wall finite-type theorem fails when

\[
R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma
\]

and its first few derivatives are small. But

\[
R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma
=
\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G}{\Gamma_G}
=
\frac{W_{\mathrm{wall}}}{\Gamma_G}.
\]

On

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

smallness of the wall and its derivatives is equivalent to smallness of

\[
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
\]

and its derivatives, up to low-order nonzero factors.

Thus the forced ODE trap is not a separate phenomenon from finite-type failure. It is the structured form of finite-type failure:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite type fails}
\Longleftrightarrow
\text{the wall ODE residual has a high-order zero modulo coherent forcing.}
}
\]

This means the trap can be integrated into the same finite-type framework if we use the block residual

\[
\mathbf W_J(q)
\]

from the start.

---

## 2. Replace scalar wall sublevel by jet-distance wall

Instead of first proving sublevel estimates for

\[
W_{\mathrm{wall}},
\]

then separately handling the trap, define the wall quantity as a jet distance:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall},J}^{Y12}
=
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\mathbf W_J(q),
\operatorname{ran}\Psi_J
\right)^2.
}
\]

For \(J=0\), this is the ordinary amplitude Schur:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q),
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)^2.
\]

For \(J\ge1\), it also detects finite-type failures.

Then the wall theorem becomes a single statement:

\[
\boxed{
\int
\min\left(
Q^A E_{\mathrm{wall},J}^{Y12},
1
\right)d\nu
\ge
Q^{-B}\nu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

This is stronger than the rank-one scalar wall but avoids the separate trap branch.

The price is that the wall factor now involves derivatives up to order \(J+4\). That may increase branch-charge degree and transition-basis requirements. But \(J=O(1)\), so this may remain manageable.

---

## 3. Advantages of jet-distance wall

Using

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall},J}^{Y12}
\]

has three advantages.

### A. It handles coherent forcing correctly

The same coefficient vector is used across derivatives:

\[
\sum_a c_a(\psi_a,\psi_a',\ldots,\psi_a^{(J)}).
\]

Thus graph-like coherent forcing is allowed, but vertically free derivative-by-derivative forcing is not.

### B. It removes the finite-type/trap split

Finite-type failure becomes exactly the event that

\[
\mathbf W_J(q)
\]

is close to

\[
\operatorname{ran}\Psi_J.
\]

So no separate branch is required unless even the jet distance is small.

### C. It creates a stronger wall for extraction

If

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall},J}^{Y12}
\]

has mass, the D4 contradiction uses a vector wall rather than a scalar wall. This may reduce reliance on delicate one-dimensional sublevel estimates.

---

## 4. Disadvantages

There are also costs.

### A. Higher derivative control

The actual-row upper must now control

\[
\partial_m^j\Pi_YJ_{\mathrm{sing}}(q''_{\can})
\]

for

\[
0\le j\le J.
\]

So \(\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{Y12}\) must be upgraded to a Sobolev/jet estimate:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{Y12,J}.
}
\]

This may be substantially stronger than the \(J=0\) estimate.

### B. Branch-charge degree may increase

The wall factor now includes derivatives of

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},\rho_\Gamma,H,\alpha_9.
\]

The effective branch-charge degree becomes

\[
d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{eff}}(J),
\]

not just

\[
d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{eff}}(0).
\]

Still, if \(J=O(1)\) and all coefficients are low-order, then

\[
d_0(J)=d_N+2d_H+2d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{eff}}(J)
\]

remains \(O(1)\), though larger. The transition basis should use

\[
d_{\max}
\]

large enough to cover this.

### C. Potential overkill

If the scalar wall finite-type theorem is easier, the jet-distance wall may be unnecessarily strong. It should be introduced as a fallback or a packaged theorem with \(J=0\) allowed.

---

## 5. Proposed hierarchy

Use a tiered wall theorem.

### Tier 0: scalar wall

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall},0}
=
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
F_Y,\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)^2.
\]

If Tier 0 has mass, use it.

### Tier 1: first derivative wall

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall},1}
=
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
(\mathcal W_\Gamma,\partial_m\mathcal W_\Gamma),
\operatorname{span}\{(\psi_a,\psi_a')\}_a
\right)^2.
\]

If Tier 0 is trapped but Tier 1 has mass, use it.

### Tier \(J\): bounded derivative wall

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall},J}
=
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
(\partial_m^j\mathcal W_\Gamma)_{j=0}^{J},
\operatorname{span}\{(\partial_m^j\psi_a)_{j=0}^{J}\}_a
\right)^2.
\]

If all tiers up to \(J\) fail, declare the source trapped in the order-\(J\) forced ODE jet model.

This is clean and finite.

---

## 6. How this interacts with O2/O3

O2/O3 uses the wall weight before extraction. If we use Tier \(J\), the smooth weight becomes

\[
W_{\mathrm{bd},J}
=
N_{\mathrm{sm}}E_{\mathrm{wall},J}^{Y12}.
\]

If \(E_{\mathrm{wall},J}\) is a global projection distance, it may be nonlocal and branch-charge complicated. In that case we should not put it directly into O2/O3.

Safer order:

1. Use the raw scalar wall

\[
|F_Y|^2
\]

for O2/O3 where possible.

2. Prove O2/O3.

3. Then apply amplitude/jet Schur after O2/O3 under the smooth measure.

If Tier \(J\) is needed and nonlocal, the contradiction becomes block-level, not pointwise atomic.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{do not feed projected jet-distance walls into O2/O3 unless their branch-charge complexity is controlled.}
}
\]

This matches the prior correction for amplitude Schur.

---

## 7. Final theorem reformulation

The mature downstream wall theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Y12WallJetSchurHierarchy.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(\mathrm{LiveY12DualPair}\);

2. \(Y12\)-fiber graph is nonvertical;

3. \(\rho_\Gamma\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{low}}\);

4. \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\) is not locally free.

Then for some bounded \(J\), either:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall},J}^{Y12}
\text{ has polynomial mass}
}
\]

and the D4 contradiction proceeds, or

\[
\boxed{
q
\text{ lies near a forced ODE jet model of order }J.
}
\]

The remaining anti-model theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual EF sources cannot lie near this forced ODE jet model on Stack-good mass.}
}
\]

---

## 8. Strategic recommendation

Do not immediately replace the scalar wall with the jet wall. Use this escalation order:

1. Try scalar moving-wall finite type for

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G.
\]

2. If finite type fails, use \(J=1\) derivative-wall Schur.

3. If \(J=1\) fails, formulate the forced ODE jet model and decide whether a higher-order residual or anti-model theorem is plausible.

This keeps the proof minimal while making the trap branch precise.

---

## Final result of this attack

The forced ODE trap can be folded into a **jet-distance wall hierarchy**:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall},J}^{Y12}
=
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
(\partial_m^j\mathcal W_\Gamma(q))_{j=0}^{J},
\operatorname{span}\{(\partial_m^j\psi_a)_{j=0}^{J}\}_a
\right)^2.
}
\]

This captures scalar wall anti-concentration and trap disposal in one finite Schur framework.

The cost is stronger \(Y12\)-sector completion estimates and possibly higher branch-charge complexity, so the hierarchy should be used only as needed.

# Agent 5 — finite model non-absorption meta-lemma

The repeated mathematical form is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(V,\mathcal M)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\|V\|^2.
}
\]

It appears in:

1. amplitude Schur:

\[
V=F_Y,\qquad \mathcal M=\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}};
\]

2. trap Schur:

\[
V=\mathbf W_J(q),\qquad \mathcal M=\operatorname{ran}\Psi_J;
\]

3. near-pure O2/O3:

\[
V=1,\qquad
\mathcal M=\operatorname{span}\{R_{\mathrm{fold}},R_{\mathrm{fold}}^2,\ldots,R_{\mathrm{fold}}^{d_0}\}.
\]

So the reusable theorem should be a finite-dimensional non-absorption lemma.

---

## 1. General finite model non-absorption lemma

Let \((X,\nu)\) be a measure space fixed **before hard extraction**. Let

\[
V\in L^2(\nu)
\]

and let

\[
\mathcal M=\operatorname{span}\{\psi_1,\ldots,\psi_M\}\subset L^2(\nu)
\]

with

\[
M\le Q^C.
\]

Define the Gram matrix

\[
G_{ij}=\langle\psi_i,\psi_j\rangle_{L^2(\nu)},
\]

and

\[
b_i=\langle V,\psi_i\rangle_{L^2(\nu)}.
\]

Then

\[
\operatorname{dist}(V,\mathcal M)^2
=
\|V\|^2-b^*G^\dagger b.
\]

The desired lower bound is

\[
\boxed{
\|V\|^2-b^*G^\dagger b
\ge Q^{-A}\|V\|^2.
}
\]

A proof strategy needs three inputs:

### Input 1: model conditioning

The model basis has polynomial Gram conditioning on its nonzero span:

\[
\lambda_{\min}^{+}(G)\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
\lambda_{\max}(G)\le Q^C.
\]

### Input 2: no-local-free leverage

The model space cannot interpolate arbitrary atom-scale values. A usable condition is a leverage bound:

\[
K_{\mathcal M}(x)
=
\sum_{i,j}\psi_i(x)(G^\dagger)_{ij}\overline{\psi_j(x)}
\le Q^C\frac{M}{\nu(X)}
\]

on smooth atoms or blocks.

Equivalently, on every block \(\omega\),

\[
\dim \mathcal M|_\omega \ll \#\{\text{atoms in }\omega\}
\]

and the restricted model has no spike basis at extraction scale.

This is the precise version of “not locally free.”

### Input 3: separating finite-type / moment witness

There is a bounded-order differential, Wronskian, or moment functional \(\mathscr L\) such that

\[
\mathscr L(\mathcal M)=0
\quad\text{or is controlled,}
\]

but

\[
|\mathscr L(V)|\ge Q^{-C}\|V\|.
\]

Equivalently, \(V\) has a finite-type feature not reproducible by \(\mathcal M\).

Then

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(V,\mathcal M)^2\ge Q^{-A}\|V\|^2.
}
\]

This lemma is not one universal theorem with identical proof in all settings; it is a template. The model conditioning and separating witness are verified differently in each module.

---

## 2. Instantiation A: amplitude Schur

Here

\[
V=F_Y
=
H\alpha_9(\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G),
\]

and

\[
\mathcal M=\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}.
\]

The theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\nu_{\mathrm{bd}})}
(F_Y,\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}})^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\|F_Y\|_{L^2(\nu_{\mathrm{bd}})}^2.
}
\]

The measure \(\nu_{\mathrm{bd}}\) must be a smooth pre-extraction/post-Gate/O2/O3 measure. It cannot be chosen after seeing the extracted set.

The separating witness is finite type of

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G
\]

modulo \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\). On

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

use

\[
R_\Gamma=\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}}{\Gamma_G}
\]

and the witness

\[
W_\ell
=
\Gamma_G\Gamma_{G,2}'
-
\Gamma_G'\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\rho_\Gamma'\Gamma_G^2.
\]

If

\[
R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma
\]

has polynomial finite type and \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\) has bounded leverage, amplitude Schur holds.

Failure modes:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\text{ locally free;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
F_Y\in \mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\text{ because of coherent }E_2^Y;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\rho_\Gamma\text{ high-order/tautological;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
F_Y\text{ trapped by the forced wall ODE model.}
}
\]

---

## 3. Instantiation B: trap Schur

Here

\[
V=\mathbf W_J(q)
=
(\mathcal W_\Gamma,\partial_m\mathcal W_\Gamma,\ldots,\partial_m^J\mathcal W_\Gamma),
\]

where

\[
\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
=
q^{(4)}
-
6(1-q_0^2+\rho_\Gamma)q''
+
36\rho_\Gamma q_0
-
12\rho_\Gamma q_0^3.
\]

The model space is

\[
\mathcal M=\operatorname{ran}\Psi_J,
\]

where

\[
\Psi_J
=
\operatorname{span}\{(\psi_a,\psi_a',\ldots,\psi_a^{(J)})\}_a.
\]

The crucial guardrail is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the same coefficient vector is used across derivative levels.}
}
\]

That is, \(\operatorname{ran}\Psi_J\) consists of

\[
\sum_a c_a(\psi_a,\psi_a',\ldots,\psi_a^{(J)}),
\]

not independent sums at each derivative level.

The theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(\mathbf W_J(q),\operatorname{ran}\Psi_J)^2
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf W_J(q)\|^2.
}
\]

A separating witness can be a derivative-level Wronskian: the vector

\[
\mathbf W_J(q)
\]

has a finite jet pattern not reproducible by the coherent forcing basis \(\Psi_J\).

Failure means:

\[
q
\]

lies near a finite-dimensional forced fourth-order ODE jet model through order \(J\).

This is the precise formulation of the wall-trap branch.

---

## 4. Instantiation C: near-pure O2/O3 Schur

Here

\[
V=1,
\]

and

\[
\mathcal M
=
\operatorname{span}\{
R_{\mathrm{fold}},R_{\mathrm{fold}}^2,\ldots,R_{\mathrm{fold}}^{d_0}
\}
\]

in

\[
L^2(\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}),
\]

where

\[
\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}
\]

is the one-slot substitution marginal and

\[
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

The theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\mu_{\mathrm{sub}})}
\left(
1,
\operatorname{span}\{
R_{\mathrm{fold}},\ldots,R_{\mathrm{fold}}^{d_0}
\}
\right)^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Here the model is fixed-dimensional because

\[
d_0=O(1).
\]

The leverage/spread input is Christoffel spread:

\[
\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}(J)\le R^C|J|.
\]

The lower support input is Vandermonde noncollapse from pure-plus determinant mass: \(\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}\) has polynomial mass on polynomially separated \(R_{\mathrm{fold}}\)-values.

The separating witness is finite moment/Vandermonde interpolation:

A degree-\(d_0\) polynomial

\[
Q(z)=1-P(z),
\qquad P\in\operatorname{span}\{z,\ldots,z^{d_0}\},
\]

with constant coefficient \(1\), cannot be small at \(d_0+1\) separated values.

Thus

\[
1
\]

cannot be absorbed by the near-pure model.

---

## 5. General failure taxonomy

The same failure types appear in all three settings.

### Failure A: model dimension too high

\[
\dim\mathcal M
\]

is comparable to the number of atoms. Then the model is locally free.

### Failure B: leverage spike

Even with small dimension, \(\mathcal M\) has basis vectors concentrated at extraction scale.

### Failure C: model fitted to \(V\)

The model contains \(V\) by definition. Examples:

\[
\rho_\Gamma\text{ fitted from }s_9^Y;
\]

\[
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\text{ contains }F_Y;
\]

\[
\Psi_J\text{ allows independent derivative coefficients}.
\]

### Failure D: separating witness vanishes identically

For O2/O3, this would mean an algebraic identity involving \(R_{\mathrm{fold}}\).

For the wall, this means the forced wall ODE is an actual source identity.

For trap Schur, this means actual EF sources genuinely lie in the forced ODE jet model.

---

## 6. Reusable lemma statement

A compact lemma is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{FiniteModelNonAbsorption.}
}
\]

Let \(V\in L^2(\nu)\), and let \(\mathcal M\subset L^2(\nu)\) have dimension \(M\le Q^C\). Suppose:

1. \(\mathcal M\) has polynomial Gram conditioning;

2. \(\mathcal M\) has no local interpolation power, quantified by a leverage bound or block dimension bound;

3. there exists a finite-type / moment / Wronskian witness separating \(V\) from \(\mathcal M\) with polynomial margin.

Then

\[
\operatorname{dist}(V,\mathcal M)^2
\ge Q^{-A}\|V\|^2.
\]

This is a meta-theorem. Each use must specify the witness.

---

## 7. Strategic implication

This lemma unifies the next proof work:

\[
\boxed{
\text{amplitude Schur}
}
\]

is a finite-model nonabsorption problem for \(F_Y\);

\[
\boxed{
\text{trap Schur}
}
\]

is a finite-model nonabsorption problem for \(\mathbf W_J(q)\);

\[
\boxed{
\text{near-pure O2/O3}
}
\]

is a finite-model nonabsorption problem for \(1\) against powers of \(R_{\mathrm{fold}}\).

So the repeated question is not “can we get a lower bound?” but:

\[
\boxed{
\text{what is the separating witness, and does the model have local freedom?}
}
\]

This is a substantial simplification of the architecture.

I’ll push the finite-model lemma from a template into usable criteria: leverage control plus a Wronskian/moment determinant lower bound, then specialize it back to the \(Y12\) amplitude and trap layers.

_Thought for 11s_

Continuing Agent 5 — turn `FiniteModelNonAbsorption` into a proof-usable criterion.

I will keep the current nomenclature:

\[
\rho_Y=\text{the lower }Y12\text{ graph slope},
\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

The wall amplitude is

\[
F_Y
=
H\alpha_9(\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G).
\]

The current structural reduction is that amplitude Schur, trap Schur, and near-pure O2/O3 are all finite model non-absorption problems. 

---

## 1. Determinantal finite-model criterion

Let

\[
\mathcal M=\operatorname{span}\{\psi_1,\ldots,\psi_M\}
\]

with

\[
M\le Q^C.
\]

Let

\[
V
\]

be the target. To prove

\[
\operatorname{dist}(V,\mathcal M)^2
\ge Q^{-A}\|V\|^2,
\]

it is enough to find \(M+1\) bounded test functionals

\[
L_0,\ldots,L_M
\]

such that the square matrix

\[
\mathcal E
=
\begin{pmatrix}
L_0(V) & L_0(\psi_1)&\cdots&L_0(\psi_M)\\
L_1(V) & L_1(\psi_1)&\cdots&L_1(\psi_M)\\
\vdots&\vdots&&\vdots\\
L_M(V) & L_M(\psi_1)&\cdots&L_M(\psi_M)
\end{pmatrix}
\]

has determinant

\[
|\det \mathcal E|\ge Q^{-A}\|V\|\prod_{i=1}^M\|\psi_i\|.
\]

Indeed, if

\[
V
\]

were within \(Q^{-A'}\|V\|\) of \(\mathcal M\), then the first column of \(\mathcal E\) would be within \(Q^{-A'}\) of the span of the other columns, contradicting the determinant lower bound, provided the \(L_i\) have polynomial operator norms.

This is the finite-dimensional core.

The useful choices of \(L_i\) are:

- point evaluations at separated points;
- local averages over separated atoms;
- derivative functionals;
- Wronskian rows;
- moment functionals.

The proof goal in each module is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{construct a polynomially conditioned }(M+1)\times(M+1)\text{ evaluation/Wronskian determinant.}
}
\]

---

## 2. Leverage condition prevents fake local fitting

The determinant criterion is not enough if \(\mathcal M\) has atom-local spikes. So impose leverage control.

For an orthonormal basis \(\varphi_1,\ldots,\varphi_M\) of \(\mathcal M\), define

\[
K_{\mathcal M}(x)
=
\sum_{j=1}^M |\varphi_j(x)|^2.
\]

Require on every smooth block \(\omega\):

\[
\boxed{
K_{\mathcal M}(x)
\le
Q^C\frac{M}{\nu(\omega)}
\quad
\text{for }x\in\omega.
}
\]

Equivalent block form:

\[
\boxed{
\dim(\mathcal M|_\omega)\le Q^C
\quad
\text{and no basis vector is concentrated on one extraction atom.}
}
\]

This is the no-local-free condition.

If it fails, a finite-dimensional-looking model can still interpolate extraction atoms, and the downstream contradiction becomes illusory.

---

## 3. Amplitude Schur criterion

For amplitude Schur,

\[
V=F_Y
=
H\alpha_9(\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G),
\]

and

\[
\mathcal M=\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}.
\]

A proof-usable criterion is:

There exist \(M+1\) smooth atoms or derivative functionals \(L_i\) such that

\[
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
L_i(F_Y)&L_i(\psi_1)&\cdots&L_i(\psi_M)
\end{pmatrix}_{0\le i\le M}
\]

is polynomially nonzero.

A natural differential witness is generated by

\[
W_{\mathrm{wall}}
=
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G.
\]

On \(|\Gamma_G|\ge Q^{-C}\), use

\[
R_\Gamma=\frac{\Gamma_{G,2}}{\Gamma_G}.
\]

If

\[
R_\Gamma+\rho_\Gamma
\]

has finite type \(k\le k_0\) modulo \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\), then the determinant formed by

\[
F_Y,\ F_Y',\ldots,F_Y^{(M)}
\]

against the model basis cannot vanish too often.

The first Wronskian witness remains

\[
W_\ell
=
\Gamma_G\Gamma_{G,2}'
-
\Gamma_G'\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\rho_\Gamma'\Gamma_G^2.
\]

If \(W_\ell\) is nonzero modulo model derivatives, amplitude Schur holds.

So the amplitude theorem can be stated:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{AmplitudeSchur}_{Y12}:
\quad
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\text{ has bounded leverage and }
F_Y\text{ has finite type modulo }\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\operatorname{dist}(F_Y,\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}})^2
\ge Q^{-A}\|F_Y\|^2.
\]

---

## 4. Trap Schur criterion

For trap Schur,

\[
V=\mathbf W_J(q)
=
(\mathcal W_\Gamma,\mathcal W_\Gamma',\ldots,\mathcal W_\Gamma^{(J)}),
\]

and

\[
\mathcal M=\operatorname{ran}\Psi_J,
\]

where

\[
\Psi_J
=
\operatorname{span}
\{(\psi_a,\psi_a',\ldots,\psi_a^{(J)})\}_a.
\]

The crucial same-coefficient condition says that the model vectors are

\[
(\psi_a,\psi_a',\ldots,\psi_a^{(J)}),
\]

not independent derivative-level forcing vectors.

A determinant witness is now a jet-Wronskian:

\[
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal W_\Gamma & \psi_1 & \cdots & \psi_M\\
\mathcal W_\Gamma' & \psi_1' & \cdots & \psi_M'\\
\vdots & \vdots && \vdots\\
\mathcal W_\Gamma^{(M)} & \psi_1^{(M)} & \cdots & \psi_M^{(M)}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

If this determinant is polynomially nonzero on a block, then

\[
\mathbf W_M(q)
\notin \operatorname{ran}\Psi_M
\]

with polynomial distance.

Thus trap Schur becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the forced ODE residual }\mathcal W_\Gamma(q)
\text{ is not in the differential span of the coherent forcing functions.}
}
\]

If all such Wronskians vanish through bounded order, then \(q\) is genuinely trapped in the forced ODE jet model.

---

## 5. O2/O3 near-pure criterion

For near-pure O2/O3,

\[
V=1,
\]

\[
\mathcal M
=
\operatorname{span}\{R_{\mathrm{fold}},R_{\mathrm{fold}}^2,\ldots,R_{\mathrm{fold}}^{d_0}\}
\]

in

\[
L^2(\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}).
\]

Here the determinant witness is purely algebraic.

Pick \(d_0+1\) points or small intervals whose \(R_{\mathrm{fold}}\)-values

\[
z_i=R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x_i)
\]

are polynomially separated. Then the evaluation matrix is

\[
\begin{pmatrix}
1&z_0&z_0^2&\cdots&z_0^{d_0}\\
1&z_1&z_1^2&\cdots&z_1^{d_0}\\
\vdots&\vdots&&&\vdots\\
1&z_{d_0}&z_{d_0}^2&\cdots&z_{d_0}^{d_0}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Its determinant is the Vandermonde

\[
\prod_{i<j}(z_j-z_i).
\]

Polynomial separation gives

\[
|\det|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Christoffel spread and lower support give the needed mass on the intervals.

So O2/O3 near-pure Schur is the cleanest instantiation of the meta-lemma.

---

## 6. General reusable statement

A compact theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{FiniteModelNonAbsorption.}
}
\]

Let \(V\in L^2(\nu)\), and let \(\mathcal M\subset L^2(\nu)\) be finite-dimensional. Suppose:

1. \(\dim\mathcal M\le Q^C\);

2. \(\mathcal M\) has polynomial Gram conditioning;

3. \(\mathcal M\) has no extraction-local interpolation power, quantified by leverage or block-dimension bounds;

4. there exist \(M+1\) polynomially bounded test functionals whose evaluation determinant on \((V,\mathcal M)\) is at least \(Q^{-A}\).

Then

\[
\operatorname{dist}(V,\mathcal M)^2
\ge Q^{-A'}\|V\|^2.
\]

This theorem can be cited for:

\[
\mathrm{AmplitudeSchur}_{Y12},
\]

\[
\mathrm{TrapSchur}_J,
\]

\[
\mathrm{NearPureMomentSeparation}(R_{\mathrm{fold}},d_0).
\]

---

## 7. Missing piece: choosing the test functionals

The meta-lemma reduces proof effort but does not choose the witness. Current best witnesses:

### Amplitude Schur

Wronskian / finite-type rows of

\[
F_Y
\]

against a basis of

\[
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}.
\]

### Trap Schur

Jet-Wronskian rows of

\[
\mathcal W_\Gamma
\]

against coherent forcing basis

\[
\psi_a.
\]

### Near-pure O2/O3

Point evaluations or local averages at separated

\[
R_{\mathrm{fold}}
\]

values.

So the agent work should now be framed as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{identify the separating determinant and prove it has polynomial lower bound.}
}
\]

---

## 8. Current conclusion

The useful simplification is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{amplitude Schur, trap Schur, and O2/O3 Schur all share one finite non-absorption pattern.}
}
\]

The remaining differences are the witnesses:

\[
\boxed{
F_Y\text{ finite type modulo }\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}};
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal W_\Gamma\text{ Wronskian modulo }\Psi_J;
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
R_{\mathrm{fold}}\text{ Vandermonde spread under }\mu_{\mathrm{sub}}.
}
\]

This should prevent duplicating arguments and gives a clean proof skeleton for the nested Schur tower.

## 1. Case analysis by \(B_Y\)

### Case A: \(B_Y=0\)

Then no actual-source coherence appears in the primitive \(Y12\) fiber.

The quotient is the full two-dimensional fiber. Since

\[

\]

D4 remains rank two.

The wall vector is

\[
H
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\Gamma_G\\
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Under polynomial coefficient conditioning,

\[
|c_7|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\alpha_9|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\beta_9|\le Q^A,
\]

this vector norm is polynomially equivalent to

\[
|H|^2\left(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2\right).
\]

So the downstream wall becomes a vector wall, not a moving-line wall.

The required wall theorem is then the joint sublevel/anisotropy estimate

\[
\boxed{
\nu\left(
|\Gamma_G|<\varepsilon,\,
|\Gamma_{G,2}|<\varepsilon
\right)
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\nu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

This is much cleaner than proving finite type of

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G.
\]

Conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
B_Y=0
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-two D4 rescue.}
}
\]

This should be pursued before the rank-one moving-wall hierarchy.

---

Actual-source coherence is graph-like:

\[
s_9^Y=\rho_Ys_7+\eta_{\mathrm{fixed}}.

The quotient is one-dimensional. The graph-killing covector is

\[

=

+
\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\right].
\]

Equivalently,

\[

=

\left(
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G
\right).
\]

So D4 drops to rank one.

This is the moving-wall route. It needs:

\[
\boxed{
\rho_\Gamma\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{low}}
}
\]

and a wall theorem for

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G,
\]

possibly modulo coherent amplitude spaces.

Conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
B_Y=\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y)
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-one moving-wall hierarchy.}
}
\]

This is the expected route if lower \(7\to9\) connection is graph-like.

\[

\[

\]

This is not the \(Y12\) wall. It may or may not be useful as a different downstream channel, but the \(Y12\)-normal route is dead.

Both D4 columns are coherent actual-source directions.

\Rightarrow

This would mean the actual-source model has too much primitive \(Y12\)-fiber freedom.

## 2. Rank-two route versus rank-one route

The rank-two case is strictly preferable if available.

### Rank two requires

\[
B_Y=0
\]

or at least

\[
\operatorname{ran}B_Y
\]

does not remove either independent D4 direction.

Then the wall is vector-valued:

\[
H(c_7\Gamma_G,\ \beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

The determinant of the coefficient matrix is

\[
c_7\alpha_9\ne0,
\]

so this is equivalent to

\[
H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

up to polynomial conditioning.

This avoids:

\[
\rho_Y,
\quad
\rho_\Gamma,
\quad
\text{moving-wall finite type},
\quad
\text{forced ODE trap}.
\]

### Rank one requires

\[
B_Y=\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y)
\]

with \(\rho_Y\) formal and low-order. Then the wall is

\[
H\alpha_9(\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G),
\]

and the moving-wall/trap hierarchy is unavoidable unless a second independent carrier is found elsewhere.

---

It depends entirely on the lower connection and actual-source coherence.

If the lower \(7\to9\) connection has no primitive \(Y12\)-fiber image, then

\[

\]

is plausible.

If actual-source singular coherence forces

\[

\]

\]

and rank one is the natural outcome.

The latest synthesis suggests lower connection is likely graph-like rather than zero, because the actual-source model may impose an order-seven to order-nine relation. But this is still a finite audit:

\boxed{

=
0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y)?
}

This must be decided before investing in wall finite type.

## 4. Finite Gram rank criterion

Let

\[
v_G=
c_7 e_7+\beta_9 e_Y,
\]

\[
v_{G2}=
\alpha_9 e_Y.
\]

After quotienting by \(B_Y\), define

\[
\bar v_G=\Pi_{\mathbf C^2/B_Y}v_G,
\qquad
\bar v_{G2}=\Pi_{\mathbf C^2/B_Y}v_{G2}.
\]

Rank two means

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{\min}
\operatorname{Gram}(\bar v_G,\bar v_{G2})
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Rank one means the Gram has one nonzero singular value, and the surviving covector is \(\ell_Y\).

Rank zero means both are killed.

In the full carrier space, the same test is:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{\min}
\operatorname{Gram}
\left(
\Pi_{\mathcal A^\perp}
(c_7 e_7+\beta_9e_Y),\
\Pi_{\mathcal A^\perp}
(\alpha_9 e_Y)
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

where \(\mathcal A\) is the local actual-source/nuisance subspace.

---

Even if \(B_Y=0\) and local rank two survives, a coherent amplitude space

\[
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\]

may still absorb the wall functions at amplitude level.

So rank two solves the local moving-line problem but not the amplitude-Schur problem.

The rank-two wall becomes

\[
F_{\mathrm{vec}}
=
H
\begin{pmatrix}

\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

If a coherent amplitude model exists, the needed amplitude theorem is

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\nu)}
\left(
F_{\mathrm{vec}},
\mathcal C_{Y,\mathrm{vec}}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)^2
\ge Q^{-A}\|F_{\mathrm{vec}}\|^2.
}
\]

If \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}=0\), rank two gives the clean pointwise vector wall.

---

The correct order is now:

### Step 1: classify \(B_Y\)

\[

\]

try rank-two D4 first.

- If

\[
B_Y=\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y),

use rank-one moving wall.

- If vertical or rank two actual-source model appears, current \(Y12\) route fails locally.

### Step 3: only after Step 1

Handle \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\):

- zero/fixed: pointwise wall;
- finite coherent: amplitude Schur;
- locally free: route dies at amplitude level.

---

## 7. Route recommendation

Do not spend more effort on rank-one wall finite type until \(B_Y\) is classified.

The highest-value finite check is:

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}
(\mathcal T_7+\mathcal T_{<7}+\mathcal T_{E_2}^{\mathrm{local}})
=
0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y)?
}
\]

If zero, rank-two D4 is available and likely simplifies the downstream layer dramatically.

If graph-like, proceed with:

\[
\rho_Y,\quad \rho_\Gamma,\quad
\text{moving-wall hierarchy}.
\]

If vertical/rank-two, abandon or refine the \(Y12\) channel.

---

The rank-two D4 rescue is exactly the \(B_Y=0\) branch.

\Rightarrow

versus vertical/rank-two.

## 6. Classification theorem

The desired theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{OneSlopeFiberSchur.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. live dual pair exists with condition

\[
\lambda_{\min}(G_{\mathrm{live}})\ge Q^{-A};
\]

2. origin-pair faithfulness gives

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}

=0;

\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}(\mathcal T_7+\mathcal T_{<7})
\subseteq \mathbf C(1,\rho_Y);

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}\mathcal T_{E_2}^{\mathrm{local}}
\subseteq \mathbf C(1,\rho_Y).

Then

\[
B_Y=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
B_Y=\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y).
\]

If \(B_Y=0\), rank-two D4 survives.

If \(B_Y=\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y)\), the vertical distance is

\[
\operatorname{dist}((0,1),\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y))^2
=
\frac{1}{1+|\rho_Y|^2}.

So if

\[
|\rho_Y|\le Q^A,
\]

then

\[

\operatorname{dist}((0,1),B_Y)^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This gives local \(Y12\) fiber normality.

Based on the architecture, the most likely outcome is:

\[
B_Y=\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y),

because actual singular coherence probably imposes a lower \(7\to9\) graph relation.

\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y)?
}
\]

and separately:

\subseteq
0\text{ or }\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y)?
}
\]

The \(B_Y\) classification reduces to two finite questions:

This is now the first downstream fork to resolve.

Let

L_{<9}^Y
:=

for all lower-induced directions.

The bad alternatives are:

\[

or

## 2. The determinant test for one-slope

Choose two lower directions

\[
u,v\in\mathcal T_7+\mathcal T_{<7}.
\]

Their fiber coordinates are

\[
(a_u,b_u)=(\ell_7(u),\ell_9^Y(u)),
\]

\[
(a_v,b_v)=(\ell_7(v),\ell_9^Y(v)).
\]

The rank-two obstruction is the determinant

\[
\Delta_Y(u,v)
=
a_ub_v-a_vb_u.
\]

The one-slope theorem is equivalent to

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_Y(u,v)=0
\quad
\text{for all }u,v\in\mathcal T_7+\mathcal T_{<7}.
}
\]

A vertical lower direction exists if some \(u\) satisfies

\[
a_u=0,\qquad b_u\ne0.
\]

So the finite audit becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\ell_9^Y(u)=\rho_Y\ell_7(u)
\quad
\text{for all lower directions }u,
}
\]

with \(\rho_Y\) formal, not fitted from actual \(q''_{\mathrm{can}}\).

---

## 3. Source of one-slope: unique lower live antecedent

The strongest route is to prove that the lower primitive \(Y12\)-fiber image factors through a single class.

Let

\[
\mathcal L_7^Y
\]

be the lower order-seven live source feeding the primitive \(Y12\) order-nine fiber. The desired structural statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\dim \mathcal L_7^Y\le1.
}
\]

If

\[
\mathcal L_7^Y=\mathbf C[\mathsf C_7],
\]

then every lower-induced direction is some scalar multiple of the same antecedent:

\[

\]

and therefore

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}u
=
\lambda(1,\rho_Y).
\]

This gives

\[
L_{<9}^Y=\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y).
\]

If no lower antecedent survives, then

\[
L_{<9}^Y=0.
\]

Thus the lower-rank audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{there is at most one lower live antecedent feeding the primitive }Y12\text{ fiber.}
}
\]

---

## 4. Use first-live primitive \(Y12\)

The “first live Bottleneck-C carrier” logic is directly relevant.

If \(Y12\) is the first primitive \(D^2N_0\)-origin, same-point, one-whitening, mixed-12 carrier at order nine, then no lower independent class should have primitive \(Y12\)-vertical content.

That gives:

\[

+

This is not just heuristic. It is the correct rank statement to extract from the old Bottleneck-C ledger.

## 5. What would create a second slope?

A second slope can only come from one of three sources.

### A. A second independent lower antecedent

There exists

\[
u_2
\]

not proportional to \(C_7\) with

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}u_2=(1,\rho_2),
\qquad
\rho_2\ne\rho_Y.

Then

\[

\]

This would mean the lower theory already has two independent ways to feed the primitive \(Y12\) order-nine coordinate. That contradicts the “first live” expectation.

### B. A pure lower vertical antecedent

There exists

\[
u_v
\]

with

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}u_v=(0,1).
\]

Then the vertical direction is actual-source coherent. The \(Y12\) D4 channel dies locally.

### C. Local \(E_2^Y\) acting as lower data

If local \(E_2^Y\) contributes an independent slope or vertical amplitude at the same extraction scale, then even if lower connection is one-slope, total \(B_Y\) becomes vertical or rank two.

This is not lower-connection failure; it is \(E_2^Y\)-local freedom.

---

## 6. Formal definition of \(\rho_Y\)

If \(L_{<9}^Y\ne0\), choose the formal generator \(e_7\). Define

\[
\rho_Y
=
\ell_9^Y(\mathcal R_{7\to9}^Y e_7),
\]

with normalization

\[
\ell_7(e_7)=1.
\]

Then for every lower-induced direction \(u\),

\[
\ell_9^Y(u)-\rho_Y\ell_7(u)=0.
\]

This gives the graph-killing covector

\[
\ell_Y=\ell_9^Y-\rho_Y\ell_7.
\]

Important guardrail:

\[
\boxed{
\rho_Y\text{ must be computed from the formal lower connection, not from the actual row ratio }s_9^Y/s_7.
}
\]

If \(\rho_Y\) is fitted from the actual row, the wall

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G
\]

may become tautological.

## 7. Low-order consequence

If the one-slope theorem holds, the next audit is coefficient honesty:

\[
\rho_Y\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{low}},
\]

and

\[

\partial_{q^{(4)}}\rho_Y=
\partial_{s_9^Y}\rho_Y=0.

This is plausible if

is a formal connection coefficient depending only on low Gram/whitening variables.

It fails if

\[

\]

is inferred from actual \(s_9^Y\) data.

Thus one-slope and low-order honesty are coupled.

---

## 8. Intermediate theorem

A precise theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{LowerConnectionOneSlope.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. the live dual pair \((\ell_7,\ell_9^Y)\) exists with polynomial conditioning;

2. the lower primitive \(Y12\)-fiber image has at most one live antecedent:

\[
\dim \mathcal L_7^Y\le1;
\]

3. lower order terms cannot create a primitive \(Y12\)-vertical class independently:

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}\mathcal T_{<7}
\subseteq
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}\mathcal T_7;
\]

4. \(\mathcal T_7\) is generated, if nonzero, by the \(C_7\) antecedent.

Then

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}(\mathcal T_7+\mathcal T_{<7})
=
0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y).
\]

Moreover,

\[

\]

is the formal lower connection coefficient.

---

If lower connection image is zero and no other local \(B_Y\) source exists:

\]

so rank-two D4 survives.

If lower connection image is one-slope:

assuming \(E_2^Y\) is safe. Then the D4 normal residual is

So

If lower connection image is vertical/rank two, current \(Y12\) route dies locally.

The lower-connection part of \(B_Y\) should be attacked through the rank determinant

\[

\ell_7(u)\ell_9^Y(v)-\ell_7(v)\ell_9^Y(u).

The expected proof is:

Then either the lower connection is zero, giving rank-two D4, or it is the graph line

giving the rank-one moving wall.

The next calculation is therefore to verify whether the lower live antecedent space \(\mathcal L_7^Y\) is zero or generated solely by \([\mathsf C_7]\).

If this holds, all lower-than-seven data are harmless.
