\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y).
\]

This means a formal order-seven actual-source displacement has an order-nine \(Y12\)-component forced by coherence.

Then rank-one moving wall is the correct route.

The dangerous alternatives are:

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}\mathcal T_7=\mathbf C(0,1)
\]

or

\[
\dim \Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}\mathcal T_7=2.
\]

Those would mean the actual source has local vertical or full two-dimensional freedom in the primitive \(Y12\) fiber.

---

## 4. Finite invariant deciding Case A versus Case B

Let

\[
u_7
\]

be the formal \(C_7\)-antecedent. Define

\[
a_7=\ell_7(u_7),
\qquad
b_7=\ell_9^Y(u_7).
\]

Then:

- if

\[
a_7=0,\quad b_7=0,
\]

then the \(C_7\)-antecedent has no \(Y12\)-fiber image;

- if

\[
a_7\ne0,
\]

then the graph slope is

\[
\rho_Y=\frac{b_7}{a_7};
\]

- if

\[
a_7=0,\quad b_7\ne0,
\]

then \(C_7\) itself gives a vertical direction, which kills the rank-one \(Y12\) route.

Under the normalization

\[
\ell_7(e_7)=1,
\]

the expected value is

\[
a_7=1,
\]

and

\[
\rho_Y=b_7.
\]

So the audit is simply:

\[
\boxed{
\ell_7(u_7)\stackrel{?}{\ne}0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\ell_9^Y(u_7)\text{ formal/low-order?}
}
\]

If yes, Case B.

If \(\ell_9^Y(u_7)=0\), then \(\rho_Y=0\), which is still graph-like:

\[
B_Y=\mathbf C(1,0).
\]

It is rank one, not rank two.

Rank two requires another independent lower direction, not merely \(\rho_Y=0\).

---

## 5. The determinant test for independent lower directions

For any two lower directions \(u,v\), define

\[
\Delta_Y(u,v)
=
\ell_7(u)\ell_9^Y(v)
-
\ell_7(v)\ell_9^Y(u).
\]

The one-slope theorem is

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_Y(u,v)=0
\quad
\forall u,v\in \mathcal T_7+\mathcal T_{<7}.
}
\]

A practical finite proof:

1. choose a spanning list of lower formal classes

\[
u_1,\ldots,u_M;
\]

2. compute the \(2\times M\) fiber matrix

\[
F_Y^{\mathrm{lower}}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\ell_7(u_1)&\cdots&\ell_7(u_M)\\
\ell_9^Y(u_1)&\cdots&\ell_9^Y(u_M)
\end{pmatrix};
\]

3. verify all \(2\times2\) minors vanish;

4. verify no column is vertical unless all nonzero columns are vertical.

Expected result:

\[
\operatorname{rank}F_Y^{\mathrm{lower}}\le1
\]

and, if nonzero, a nonvertical generator.

---

## 6. Source-grade reason for rank \(\le1\)

The structural reason should be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{there is only one lower source-grade path into the primitive }Y12\text{ order-nine sector.}
}
\]

That path is the \(C_7\)-antecedent.

All other lower terms either:

- have source-linear origin and are killed by \(\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}\);
- have wrong whitening origin;
- have transported rather than same-point incidence;
- have wrong reflection/source-grade parity;
- are nuisance/fixed terms rather than tangent directions.

Thus every nonzero lower fiber contribution factors through the same formal \(C_7\) path.

This is the origin-label version of the first-live-carrier argument.

---

## 7. Consequence for \(\rho_Y\) honesty

If

\[
\rho_Y
=
\frac{\ell_9^Y(u_7)}{\ell_7(u_7)}
\]

with \(u_7\) a formal lower connection class, then \(\rho_Y\) is a formal connection coefficient.

The wall-honesty audit then asks whether

\[
\rho_Y\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{low}}
\]

and

\[
\partial_{\Gamma_{G,2}}\rho_Y=
\partial_{q^{(4)}}\rho_Y=
\partial_{s_9^Y}\rho_Y=0.
\]

This should hold if \(u_7\), \(\ell_7\), and \(\ell_9^Y\) are built from fixed carrier/Gram/whitening data, not from the actual order-nine row.

Thus one-slope also supplies the correct non-tautological definition of \(\rho_Y\).

---

## 8. Route consequences

### If lower image is zero

\[
\mathcal L_7^Y=0.
\]

Then if local \(E_2^Y\) and source tangents also vanish, we get

\[
B_Y=0.
\]

Rank-two D4 survives. This is best case.

### If lower image is one nonvertical graph line

\[
\mathcal L_7^Y=\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y).
\]

Then, if local \(E_2^Y\) aligns with the same line or is absent/fixed, we get

\[
B_Y=\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y).
\]

Rank-one moving wall.

### If lower image vertical or rank two

The current \(Y12\) route dies locally unless a refined quotient separates the vertical direction from actual-source coherence.

---

## 9. Precise finite theorem

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{LowerAntecedentRankTheorem.}
}
\]

Let

\[
\mathcal U_{<9}^Y
\]

be the finite list of formal lower classes that can enter the primitive \(Y12\)-fiber. Suppose:

1. every \(u\in\mathcal U_{<9}^Y\) has a refined origin label;

2. all classes except the \(C_7\)-antecedent have zero \((s_7,s_9^Y)\)-projection by origin/whitening/parity;

3. the \(C_7\)-antecedent, if nonzero, has \(\ell_7(u_7)\ne0\);

4. \(\ell_9^Y(u_7)\) is a formal low-order connection coefficient.

Then

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}(\mathcal T_7+\mathcal T_{<7})
=
0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y).
\]

No vertical or rank-two lower image occurs.

The lower-connection rank audit has a concrete finite form:

The expected structural proof is that all columns vanish except possibly the \(C_7\)-antecedent column, so the image is either zero or one nonvertical graph line.

## 1. Normalize the \(C_7\)-antecedent

The live duals are chosen so that

\[

If the lower antecedent \(u_7\) is exactly the live \(e_7\)-class, then

\[

\qquad
\ell_9^Y(u_7)=0
\]

before applying the formal lower-to-nine connection.

But actual-source coherence is not merely \(u_7=e_7\). It is the statement that an order-seven source displacement has an induced order-nine \(Y12\) component:

\[

=

alone has \(s_9^Y=0\), but the coherent actual-source graph lift of \(e_7\) may have

\[

So the lower graph line is generated by the **coherent lift** of \(C_7\), not by raw \(C_7\) alone.

## 2. Three cases for \(\rho_Y\)

### Case A: \(\mathcal R_{7\to9}^Y e_7=0\)

Then

and the lower image is

\not\Rightarrow

It means actual-source coherence allows the \(s_7\)-direction but does not force an \(s_9^Y\)-component.

So D4 is rank one, not rank two.

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}\mathcal T_7=0
\]

entirely.

### Case B: \(\rho_Y\ne0\), finite low-order

\]

rank one survives, and the wall is

\ell_Y(D4)
=

\]

This is the generic graph-like case.

### Case C: \(\ell_7(u_7)=0,\ell_9^Y(u_7)\ne0\)

This would mean the lower antecedent is vertical. But if \(u_7\) is truly the \(C_7\)-antecedent, this should not happen, because the \(C_7\)-coordinate should be visible through \(\ell_7\).

So this case indicates either:

- the live dual normalization is wrong;
- \(C_7\) is killed by nuisance before reaching the fiber;
- the supposed \(C_7\)-antecedent is not actually \(C_7\);
- or the singular quotient overcollapsed the order-seven coordinate.

It is a serious failure/definition bug.

## 3. Rank-two rescue requires no \(s_7\)-coherent actual direction

This is subtle and important.

Earlier we said:

\[

\]

But if the actual-source model includes any \(C_7\) order-seven tangent, then

\[

\]

contains at least

\[

\]

So rank-two requires more than “no \(Y12\)-vertical direction.” It requires that the actual-source model **does not include the live \(s_7\)-direction in the forbidden fiber**.

If \(s_7\) is a legitimate actual-source tangent, then

\[
B_Y\ne0.
\]

This suggests rank-two may be less likely than previously hoped, because actual-source coherence probably includes order-seven variation.

Thus the likely route is rank one with graph slope \(\rho_Y\).

Rank-two remains possible only if the \(s_7\)-direction is not part of the actual-source/nuisance model in this fiber. That would be the case if \(C_7\) is purely D4-formal and not an actual EF source tangent.

So the decisive question is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Is the }C_7\text{ direction an allowed actual-source fiber tangent, or only a D4 carrier?}
}
\]

If allowed: rank one.

If not allowed: rank two may survive.

Rank one.

In that case

\[

\]

is possible, and D4 is rank two.

The earlier “actual-source normality” framing suggests that if \(C_7\) is a formal D4 carrier rather than an actual EF parameter tangent, we should not automatically put it into \(B_Y\).

\[

from

\[

A formal \(7\to9\) relation does not by itself put \(C_7\) into \(B_Y\). It only describes how \(s_9^Y\) would depend on \(s_7\) **if** \(s_7\) is an allowed actual-source variation.

This is a key correction.

The local allowed model \(B_Y\) contains a graph line only if there exists an actual-source tangent with nonzero \(s_7\) component.

and rank-two D4.

assuming no other local contributors.

}

\[

\]

\quad\text{if }\mathcal A_7^Y\ne0.
\]

This theorem resolves the rank-two/rank-one fork.

\]

Fatal route:

\[
\mathfrak C_Y^W
\]

creates local free primitive \(DW_{\mathrm{same}}\circ D^2N_0\) amplitudes.

---

## 6. Unified routing theorem

A clean theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Y12ContaminantRouting.}
}
\]

For every possible primitive \(Y12\) contaminant \(Z\), where

\[
Z\in\{E_2^Y,\mathfrak C_Y^N,\mathfrak C_Y^L,\mathfrak C_Y^W\},
\]

exactly one of the following holds.

### Safe local zero

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}Z=0.
\]

### Safe graph contribution

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}Z\subseteq \mathbf C(1,\rho_Y).
\]

### Safe finite coherent amplitude

\[
Z\in\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
\]

with bounded dimension/leverage and no extraction-local basis.

### Safe residual

\[
Z\in R_X^Y
\]

with

\[
\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{Y12}.
\]

### Fatal vertical/second slope

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}Z
\]

contains

\[
(0,1)
\]

or a second graph slope

\[
(1,\rho_E),\quad \rho_E\ne\rho_Y.
\]

### Fatal locally free amplitude

\[
Z
\]

creates atom-local \(Y12\)-amplitude freedom.

The current \(Y12\) route survives only in the safe cases.

---

## 7. Consequences for \(B_Y\)

The local fiber model becomes

\[
B_Y
=
B_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
+
B_Y^{E_2,\mathrm{local}}
+
B_Y^{\mathrm{lab},\mathrm{local}}.
\]

If all contaminants are zero or graph-compatible,

\[
B_Y=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
B_Y=\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y).
\]

If any contaminant is vertical or second-slope,

\[
B_Y
\]

is vertical or rank two, and the current \(Y12\) channel dies locally.

Thus this contaminant routing is exactly what decides the local rank fork.

---

## 8. Consequences for \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\)

The coherent amplitude model is

\[
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
=
\mathcal C_Y^{E_2}
+
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{lab}}
+
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{param}}
+\cdots.
\]

If this is zero/fixed, the pointwise wall route is available.

If finite coherent, the route is amplitude Schur and block/global contradiction.

If locally free, rank-one \(Y12\) dies at amplitude level.

---

## 9. Current best expectation

Expected safe outcomes:

\[
E_{\mathrm{tail}},E_{\mathrm{reg}},E_{\mathrm{smooth}},E_{\gamma,\mathrm{rem}}
\]

are source-linear/background/residual, so

\[
\Pi_Y=0
\]

or residual-small.

\[
E_{\mathrm{chart}}
\]

should be origin-filtered unless it recomputes \(N_0\).

\[
E_{\mathrm{model}}
\]

is the only \(E_2\) danger.

\[
\mathfrak C_Y^L
\]

should vanish if \(L\) is affine.

\[
\mathfrak C_Y^N
\]

should vanish by naturality if transition only transports formed carriers.

\[
\mathfrak C_Y^W
\]

is the subtle whitening risk, but origin-pair labels should separate it unless whitening recomputes the primitive \(DW_{\mathrm{same}}\circ D^2N_0\) carrier.

---

## Final result

Both \(E_2^Y\) and \(\mathfrak C_Y\) feed the same routing table:

\[
0,\quad
\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y),\quad
\mathbf C(0,1),\quad
\mathbb C^2,\quad
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}},\quad
R_X^Y.
\]

This unifies the contaminant audit.

The current \(Y12\) route survives if all \(E_2^Y\) and labelled-transition defects are either:

- zero/fixed;
- same-slope graph;
- finite coherent nonlocal amplitude;
- residual-controlled.

It fails if any create vertical/second-slope local fiber freedom or atom-local amplitude freedom.

Continuing Agent 5 — convert contaminant routing into explicit finite rank/leverage tests.

I will keep the current notation:

\[
\rho_Y=\text{the }Y12\text{ fiber graph slope},
\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

The current contaminant audit says every \(Y12\)-visible contribution from \(E_2^Y\) or the labelled-transition commutator \(\mathfrak C_Y\) must route into exactly one of:

\[
0,\quad \mathbf C(1,\rho_Y),\quad \mathbf C(0,1),\quad \mathbf C^2,\quad \mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}},\quad R_X^Y.
\]

The goal now is to make “finite coherent” and “locally free” testable. This matters because finite coherent amplitude is survivable via amplitude Schur, while locally free amplitude kills the rank-one \(Y12\) route. 

---

## 1. Local-freedom criterion for \(E_2^Y\)

Let the primitive \(Y12\) coefficient of \(E_2\) be represented on a block \(\omega\) as

\[
E_2^Y(p)=c_E(p)y_Y(p),
\]

where \(p\) indexes local packets/atoms in \(\omega\).

Define the coefficient vector

\[
\mathbf c_E^\omega=(c_E(p))_{p\in\omega}.
\]

The amplitude space generated by \(E_2^Y\) on \(\omega\) is

\[
\mathcal C_{Y,\omega}^{E_2}
=
\operatorname{span}
\{
\mathbf c_{E,1}^\omega,\ldots,\mathbf c_{E,M}^\omega
\}.
\]

Then:

\[
\boxed{
E_2^Y\text{ is finite coherent on }\omega
\iff
M\le Q^C
\text{ and }
\mathcal C_{Y,\omega}^{E_2}
\text{ has bounded leverage.}
}
\]

A concrete leverage condition is:

\[
\boxed{
K_{E_2,\omega}(p)
=
\sum_{a,b}c_{E,a}(p)
(G_\omega^\dagger)_{ab}
\overline{c_{E,b}(p)}
\le
Q^C\frac{M}{|\omega|}
}
\]

where

\[
(G_\omega)_{ab}
=
\sum_{p\in\omega}c_{E,a}(p)\overline{c_{E,b}(p)}.
\]

If instead \(K_{E_2,\omega}(p)\) is of size \(1\) on individual atoms while \(M\sim|\omega|\), then \(E_2^Y\) is locally free.

So the exact test is:

\[
\boxed{
\dim\mathcal C_{Y,\omega}^{E_2}\ll |\omega|
\quad\text{and}\quad
K_{E_2,\omega}(p)\ll Q^C\dim/|\omega|.
}
\]

If this fails, \(E_2^Y\) can absorb arbitrary local wall amplitudes.

---

## 2. Fiber contribution versus amplitude contribution

The same \(E_2^Y\) coefficient map can affect two different levels.

### Fiber level

If varying an actual local parameter changes the local fiber coordinates by

\[
\delta(s_7,s_9^Y)
=
(a,b),
\]

then it enters \(B_Y\).

Classification:

\[
(a,b)=0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{no fiber effect;}
\]

\[
(a,b)=\lambda(1,\rho_Y)
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{same graph, safe;}
\]

\[
(a,b)=\lambda(0,1)
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{vertical, fatal;}
\]

\[
(a,b)=\lambda(1,\rho_E),\quad \rho_E\ne\rho_Y
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{second slope, fatal if graph already present.}
\]

### Amplitude level

If no local tangent is created but the coefficient \(c_E(p)\) varies coherently across \(p\), it enters

\[
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}.
\]

So the two tests are separate:

\[
\boxed{
D_{\mathrm{local}}c_E
\text{ decides }B_Y;
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{span}\{c_E(p)\}
\text{ decides }\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}.
}
\]

A term can be harmless at fiber level but still create a finite coherent amplitude space.

---

## 3. Finite-rank test for the labelled commutator

The labelled commutator contributes a primitive \(Y12\)-coefficient

\[
c_{\mathfrak C}(p)
\]

through

\[
\mathfrak C_Y(p)=c_{\mathfrak C}(p)y_Y(p).
\]

Decompose

\[
c_{\mathfrak C}
=
c_{\mathfrak C^N}
+
c_{\mathfrak C^L}
+
c_{\mathfrak C^W}.
\]

For each part, apply the same two tests:

\[
D_{\mathrm{local}}c_{\mathfrak C^\bullet}
\quad\text{for }B_Y,
\]

\[
\operatorname{span}\{c_{\mathfrak C^\bullet}(p)\}_{p\in\omega}
\quad\text{for }\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}.
\]

The strongest safe theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
c_{\mathfrak C^\bullet}=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
c_{\mathfrak C^\bullet}\in \mathcal C_{Y,\omega}^{\mathrm{coh}}
\text{ with bounded leverage.}
}
\]

The local no-go is:

\[
\boxed{
D_{\mathrm{local}}c_{\mathfrak C^\bullet}
\text{ spans arbitrary local primitive }Y12\text{ amplitudes.}
}
\]

---

## 4. Normal-form commutator as rank test

Recall

\[
\mathfrak C_Y(\xi_1,\xi_2)
=
\Pi_Y
\left(
D^2N_{0,\mathrm{sing}}[L\xi_1,L\xi_2]
-
S D^2N_{0,\mathrm{tr}}[\xi_1,\xi_2]
\right)
+
\Pi_YDN_{0,\mathrm{sing}}[D^2L(\xi_1,\xi_2)]
+
\mathfrak C_Y^W.
\]

Let \(\{\xi_{1,a}\}\) and \(\{\xi_{2,b}\}\) be finite bases of the relevant mixed source slots. Form the matrix

\[
M_{\mathfrak C}(p)_{ab}
=
\Pi_Y\mathfrak C_Y(\xi_{1,a},\xi_{2,b})(p).
\]

Then:

- if

\[
M_{\mathfrak C}(p)=0
\]

identically, labelled transition is \(Y12\)-faithful;

- if \(M_{\mathfrak C}(p)\) lies in a fixed finite-dimensional span as \(p\) varies, it contributes finite coherent amplitude;

- if \(M_{\mathfrak C}(p)\) can realize arbitrary local matrices at extraction scale, labelled transition creates local freedom and the route fails.

So the commutator theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{rank}_{\mathrm{local}}
\{M_{\mathfrak C}(p)\}_{p\in\omega}
\le Q^C
\quad
\text{with bounded leverage.}
}
\]

This is the finite-rank version of “\(\mathfrak C_Y\) is zero or finite coherent.”

---

## 5. Fiber slope compatibility test

Suppose a contaminant \(Z\) has a local fiber derivative

\[
D_{\mathrm{local}}Z
\]

with coordinates

\[
(a_Z,b_Z).
\]

To test graph compatibility, compute

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_Z
=
b_Z-\rho_Ya_Z.
}
\]

Then:

\[
\Delta_Z=0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
Z\text{ is graph-compatible;}
\]

\[
a_Z=0,\ \Delta_Z=b_Z\ne0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
Z\text{ is vertical fatal;}
\]

\[
a_Z\ne0,\ \Delta_Z\ne0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
Z\text{ creates a second slope.}
\]

This gives an executable local test:

\[
\boxed{
\ell_Y(D_{\mathrm{local}}Z)=0?
}
\]

where

\[
\ell_Y=\ell_9^Y-\rho_Y\ell_7.
\]

If not, the contaminant is not compatible with the one-slope fiber model.

---

## 6. Interaction with rank-two case \(B_Y=0\)

If

\[
B_Y=0
\]

is the target, then even graph-compatible contaminants are not allowed as local tangents. They would create

\[
B_Y=\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y)
\]

and reduce rank two to rank one.

Therefore, for the rank-two route, the local condition is stronger:

\[
\boxed{
D_{\mathrm{local}}E_2^Y=0,\qquad
D_{\mathrm{local}}\mathfrak C_Y=0,
\qquad
\Pi_{s_7}T\mathcal M_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}=0.
}
\]

For the rank-one route, graph-compatible local tangents are allowed:

\[
\boxed{
D_{\mathrm{local}}Z\in \mathbf C(1,\rho_Y).
}
\]

This is an important distinction.

A contaminant that is safe for rank one may destroy rank two.

---

## 7. Updated routing table

For each contaminant \(Z\in\{E_2^Y,\mathfrak C_Y\}\), compute:

\[
D_{\mathrm{local}}Z
\]

and the amplitude span

\[
\mathcal C_Z=\operatorname{span}\{Z(p)\}.
\]

Then route:

| Local derivative | Amplitude span | Outcome |
|---|---|---|
| \(0\) | \(0\)/fixed | no effect |
| \(0\) | finite coherent | amplitude Schur |
| \(0\) | locally free | amplitude no-go |
| \(\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y)\) | any safe span | rank-one only |
| \(\mathbf C(0,1)\) | any | local no-go |
| second slope | any | local no-go |
| atom-local | locally free | no-go |

Thus the full local/amplitude routing is algorithmic.

---

## 8. Practical next finite computations

The next concrete computations are:

### For \(E_2^Y\)

\[
c_E,\quad Dc_E,\quad D^2c_E.
\]

Check whether local derivatives vanish or align with \((1,\rho_Y)\). Then check whether \(c_E(p)\) spans a finite coherent nonlocal space.

### For \(\mathfrak C_Y\)

Compute

\[
M_{\mathfrak C}(p)
\]

for the three pieces:

\[
\mathfrak C_Y^L,\quad \mathfrak C_Y^N,\quad \mathfrak C_Y^W.
\]

Check whether each is zero, finite coherent, residual-controlled, graph-compatible, or locally free.

### For rank-two viability

Check the stronger condition:

\[
D_{\mathrm{local}}E_2^Y=
D_{\mathrm{local}}\mathfrak C_Y=
0
\]

and

\[
\Pi_{s_7}T\mathcal M_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}=0.
\]

Only then \(B_Y=0\) and rank-two survives.

---

## Final result

The contaminant routing can be made fully finite:

\[
\boxed{
\text{local derivative decides }B_Y;
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{amplitude span/leverage decides }\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}};
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{residual size decides }\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{Y12}.
}

The key distinction:

\text{rank-two route requires zero local contaminant derivatives;}
}

\[

}

}

and collapse the rank-two vector wall to the rank-one moving wall. This follows the current correction that \(B_Y\) contains only actual-source/nuisance/local freedoms, not formal D4 carriers.

## 1. Rank-two local requirement

The primitive \(Y12\)-fiber has coordinates

\[
(s_7,s_9^Y).
\]

For rank two, we need

\[

\]

Thus every local contaminant \(Z\) must satisfy

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}T_Z^{\mathrm{local}}=0.
}
\]

In particular:

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}T_{E_2^Y}^{\mathrm{local}}=0,
\qquad
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}T_{\mathrm{lab},Y}^{\mathrm{local}}=0.
}
\]

If instead either contaminant contributes

\[
\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y),
\]

then rank two collapses to rank one.

If either contributes

\[
\mathbf C(0,1)
\]

or a second slope

\[
\mathbf C(1,\rho_E),\qquad \rho_E\ne\rho_Y,
\]

then the current \(Y12\) route dies locally.

---

# 2. \(E_2^Y\) coefficient-map audit

Define the primitive \(Y12\)-coefficient map

\[
c_E(\theta;p)
=
\frac{\Pi_Y E_{\mathrm{model}}(\theta;p)}{y_Y(p)}
\]

on a local atom/packet \(p\), whenever \(y_Y(p)\ne0\).

Here \(\Pi_Y\) detects the refined primitive \(Y12\) signature:

\[
(o_N,o_W)
=
(D^2N_0,DW_{\mathrm{same}}),
\]

mixed branch \(12\), same-point, one whitening slot, order nine, carrier \([\mathsf C_{Y12}]\).

The rank-two local test is:

\[
\boxed{
D_{\mathrm{local}}c_E=0
\quad\text{and}\quad
D_{\mathrm{local}}^2c_E=0
}
\]

in the primitive \(Y12\)-fiber directions.

More explicitly:

- If \(c_E\) is fixed in the local source variables, it shifts the basepoint/amplitude but does not enter \(B_Y\).
- If \(D_{\mathrm{local}}c_E\ne0\) with fiber direction \((1,\rho_Y)\), rank two collapses to rank one.
- If \(D_{\mathrm{local}}c_E\ne0\) with fiber direction \((0,1)\), the vertical \(Y12\) direction is actual-source local freedom; the route dies.
- If two independent local derivatives produce two slopes, \(B_Y\) becomes rank two as an actual-source model; the route dies locally.

Therefore the rank-two-safe condition for \(E_2^Y\) is:

\[
\boxed{
E_2^Y\text{ has no local fiber derivative.}
}
\]

---

## 3. Amplitude-level \(E_2^Y\) is separate

A finite coherent \(E_2^Y\) amplitude is not a local \(B_Y\) tangent.

If

\[
c_E(p)
\]

varies across packets only inside a finite-dimensional coherent space

\[
\mathcal C_Y^{E_2},
\]

with no extraction-scale local interpolation power, then

\[
E_2^Y
\]

contributes to the amplitude model

\[
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}},
\]

not to \(B_Y\).

For rank two, this means:

\[
B_Y=0
\]

can still hold, but the vector wall must satisfy amplitude Schur:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\nu)}
\left(
F_{2Y},\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\|F_{2Y}\|^2.
}
\]

Here, in the rank-two case,

\[
F_{2Y}
=
H(c_7\Gamma_G,\ \beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

Thus finite coherent \(E_2^Y\) is survivable; local \(E_2^Y\)-freedom is not.

# 4. Labelled-transition commutator audit

The labelled-transition defect decomposes as

\[
\mathfrak C_Y
=
\mathfrak C_Y^N+\mathfrak C_Y^L+\mathfrak C_Y^W.
\]

The rank-two-safe requirement is

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}T_{\mathfrak C_Y}^{\mathrm{local}}=0.
}
\]

A same-slope graph contribution would still destroy rank two, even though it would be acceptable for rank one.

---

## 4.1 \(\mathfrak C_Y^L\): nonlinear source-coordinate defect

This term is

\[
\mathfrak C_Y^L
=
\Pi_YDN_{0,\mathrm{sing}}[D^2L(\xi_1,\xi_2)].
\]

If \(L\) is affine/linear in the relevant source slots, then

\[
D^2L=0,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak C_Y^L=0.
}
\]

If \(D^2L\ne0\), then the origin is

\[
DN_0\circ D^2L,
\]

not

\[
D^2N_0.
\]

So it should be killed by the origin-pair filter unless the singular quotient forgets origin labels. Therefore the safe condition is

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_YDN_{0,\mathrm{sing}}[D^2L(\xi_1,\xi_2)]=0.
}
\]

If this term produces primitive \(D^2N_0\)-origin \(Y12\) with local freedom, the labelled transition route fails.

---

## 4.2 \(\mathfrak C_Y^N\): tensorial naturality defect

This term is

\[
\mathfrak C_Y^N
=
\Pi_Y
\left(
D^2N_{0,\mathrm{sing}}[L\xi_1,L\xi_2]
-
S D^2N_{0,\mathrm{tr}}[\xi_1,\xi_2]
\right).
\]

For rank two, we need

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}\mathfrak C_Y^N=0.
}
\]

There are three outcomes:

1. **Naturality holds:**

\[
D^2N_{0,\mathrm{sing}}[L\xi_1,L\xi_2]
=
S D^2N_{0,\mathrm{tr}}[\xi_1,\xi_2]
\]

in the \(Y12\)-sector. Then safe for rank two.

2. **Finite coherent mismatch:** \(\mathfrak C_Y^N\) is nonzero but depends only on chart/block data, not local atom freedom. Then it contributes to

\[
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{lab}},
\]

not \(B_Y\). Rank two survives locally, but amplitude Schur is needed.

3. **Local mismatch:** \(\mathfrak C_Y^N\) can vary freely in the primitive \(Y12\)-fiber. Then rank two dies; if graph-compatible, rank one may remain; if vertical/second-slope, the \(Y12\) route dies locally.

---

## 4.3 \(\mathfrak C_Y^W\): same-point whitening defect

This is the subtle term.

Moving-whitening artifacts can look superficially like one-whitening degree-two objects, for example

\[
D(W^{-1/2})[\xi]\,E_2,
\]

or

\[
D^2W[\xi_1,\xi_2]\,N_0.
\]

But these have different origin-pair labels from the primitive carrier

\[
DW_{\mathrm{same}}\left[D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2]\right].
\]

So the safe condition is:

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_Y\mathfrak C_Y^W=0
}
\]

by origin-pair distinction.

If same-point whitening is recomputed in a way that changes the primitive

\[
DW_{\mathrm{same}}\circ D^2N_0
\]

carrier locally, then the defect must be classified:

\[
0,\quad
\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y),\quad
\mathbf C(0,1),\quad
\mathbf C^2,\quad
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{lab}},\quad
R_X^Y.
\]

For rank two, only \(0\), finite coherent amplitude, or residual-small are acceptable. Same-slope graph is not acceptable for rank two.

---

# 5. Rank-two contaminant-zero theorem

A clean theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoContaminantZero.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(E_2^Y\) has no local fiber derivative:

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}T_{E_2^Y}^{\mathrm{local}}=0;
\]

2. the labelled commutator has no local fiber derivative:

\[
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}T_{\mathfrak C_Y}^{\mathrm{local}}=0;
\]

3. any nonzero \(E_2^Y\) or \(\mathfrak C_Y\) contribution is finite coherent or residual-controlled:

\[
E_2^Y+\mathfrak C_Y
\in
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}
+
R_X^Y;
\]

4. \(\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}}\) is not locally free.

Then \(E_2^Y\) and \(\mathfrak C_Y\) do not contribute to \(B_Y\). Therefore, if the actual-source tangent and nuisance parts also have no \(s_7\) or \(s_9^Y\) projection, then

\[
\boxed{
B_Y=0.
}
\]

Rank-two D4 survives locally.

---

# 6. If rank two fails

If a contaminant contributes:

\[
\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y),
\]

then

\[
B_Y=\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y)
\]

provided no other slope appears. Rank two collapses to rank one, but \(Y12\) may survive.

If a contaminant contributes:

\[
\mathbf C(0,1)
\]

or a second graph slope, then

\[
B_Y
\]

is vertical or rank two, and the current \(Y12\) channel dies locally.

If a contaminant contributes an atom-local amplitude model, then \(Y12\) dies at the amplitude layer even if \(B_Y=0\).

---

# 7. Practical finite outputs to request

For \(E_2^Y\), compute:

\[
c_E,\quad Dc_E,\quad D^2c_E.
\]

For \(\mathfrak C_Y\), compute/classify:

\[
\mathfrak C_Y^L,\quad \mathfrak C_Y^N,\quad \mathfrak C_Y^W.
\]

For each, output one of:

\[
0,
\quad
\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y),
\quad
\mathbf C(0,1),
\quad
\mathbf C^2,
\quad
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}},
\quad
R_X^Y.
\]

For rank two, the only acceptable local outputs are:

\[
0,
\quad
\mathcal C_Y^{\mathrm{arith}},
\quad
R_X^Y.
\]

---

## Final conclusion

For rank-two D4, the standard “safe for rank-one” graph contaminant

\[
\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y)
\]

is **not safe**. It collapses rank two to rank one.

Thus the rank-two contaminant criterion is stricter:

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}T_{E_2^Y}^{\mathrm{local}}=0,
\qquad
\Pi_{\mathrm{fib},Y}T_{\mathfrak C_Y}^{\mathrm{local}}=0.
}
\]

Finite coherent amplitude and residual terms are allowed, but they must be handled later by amplitude Schur or \(\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{Y12}\).

Continuing Agent 5 — rank-two wall theorem conditional on \(B_Y=0\).

But in the rank-two branch,

\[
B_Y=0,
\]

so \(\rho_Y\) and \(\rho_\Gamma\) are not needed for the wall itself. The D4 output remains vector-valued.

## 1. Rank-two D4 wall

If \(B_Y=0\), D4 acts in the live fiber by

\[
M_{\mathrm{D4}}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
\beta_9&\alpha_9
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
c_7\alpha_9\ne0.
\]

Thus

\[
D4(\Gamma)
=
H
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\Gamma_G\\
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Let

\[
F_{2Y}
=
H
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\Gamma_G\\
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

If the coefficient matrix is polynomially conditioned:

\[
|c_7|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\alpha_9|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|c_7|+|\alpha_9|+|\beta_9|\le Q^A,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
|F_{2Y}|^2
\asymp_{Q^A}
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
}
\]

Therefore the rank-two wall is not a moving line. It is the vector curvature wall.

---

## 2. Rank-two wall theorem without amplitude model

If there is no coherent amplitude space:

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}=0
\]

or only a fixed basepoint shift, the wall theorem is simply:

\[
\boxed{
\int
\min\left(
Q^A |H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right),
1
\right)d\nu
\ge
Q^{-B}\nu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

Equivalently, after dyadic freezing of \(|H|\),

\[
\boxed{
\nu\left(
|\Gamma_G|<\varepsilon,\,
|\Gamma_{G,2}|<\varepsilon
\right)
\le Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\nu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

This is strictly easier than rank-one moving-wall anti-concentration, which must exclude

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G\approx0.
\]

Here only simultaneous smallness is dangerous.

---

## 3. Rank-two wall with coherent amplitude model

If finite coherent \(Y12\)-amplitude spaces survive, define the vector model

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\subset L^2(\nu;\mathbf C^2).
\]

This may include finite coherent contributions from

\[
E_2^Y,
\qquad
\mathfrak C_Y,
\qquad
\text{parameter/fixed graph effects},
\]

provided they are not local fiber freedoms.

The wall theorem becomes vector amplitude Schur:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\nu)}
\left(
F_{2Y},
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\|F_{2Y}\|_{L^2(\nu)}^2.
}
\]

If

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}
=
\operatorname{span}\{\Psi_1,\ldots,\Psi_M\},
\qquad \Psi_a:X\to\mathbf C^2,
\]

then the Schur residual is

\[
\delta_{2Y}^2
=
\|F_{2Y}\|^2
-
b^*G^\dagger b,
\]

where

\[
G_{ab}=\langle \Psi_a,\Psi_b\rangle_{L^2(\nu;\mathbf C^2)},
\]

\[
b_a=\langle F_{2Y},\Psi_a\rangle_{L^2(\nu;\mathbf C^2)}.
\]

Rank two survives the amplitude layer if

\[
\delta_{2Y}^2\ge Q^{-A}\|F_{2Y}\|^2.
\]

If \(\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}\) is locally free, the wall can be absorbed and rank-two D4 fails at the amplitude layer.

---

## 4. Why the ODE trap disappears in rank two

In the rank-one case, wall failure means

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G\approx0,
\]

which gives a fourth-order ODE trap.

In rank two, wall failure means

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0
\]

modulo coherent amplitude space.

There is no moving-line relation to convert into

\[
q^{(4)}=F(q_0,q'',\rho_\Gamma).
\]

Instead, the failure is a joint smallness condition for two curvature quantities. That is a different and usually stronger exceptional set.

So the rank-two branch bypasses:

\[
\text{WallHonesty}_{Y12},
\quad
\rho_\Gamma\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{low}},
\quad
\text{moving-wall finite type},
\quad
\text{forced ODE trap},
\quad
\text{trap Schur hierarchy}.
\]

This is the main advantage of proving \(B_Y=0\).

---

## 5. What wall input remains?

Rank two still needs a curvature escape theorem:

\[
\boxed{
(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\text{ is not jointly small on the Stack-good mass.}
}
\]

Possible proof routes:

### A. Existing raw anisotropy

If prior wall work already proves

\[
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

on average or after extraction, then rank two can use it directly.

This was useless for rank one but becomes exactly the needed theorem for rank two.

### B. Finite model non-absorption

Treat

\[
F_{2Y}
\]

as target vector and

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\]

as finite coherent model. Use the finite-model Schur lemma:

\[
F_{2Y}\notin \mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}.
\]

### C. Joint finite type

If needed, prove that \(\Gamma_G\) and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) cannot vanish together to high order except on a negligible set.

This is a two-function finite-type theorem and is weaker than excluding a moving scalar line.

---

## 6. O2/O3 branch-charge under rank two

If \(B_Y=0\), use the raw vector wall weight

\[
W_{\mathrm{bd}}^{(2)}
=
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)
\]

or the coefficient-conditioned equivalent

\[
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|F_{2Y}|^2.
\]

Then the branch-charge bandwidth is

\[
d_0^{(2)}
=
d_N+2d_H+2d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{vec}},
\]

where

\[
d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{vec}}
=
\max\{d_{\Gamma_G},d_{\Gamma_{G,2}}\}.
\]

This is likely \(O(1)\). It does not involve \(\rho_\Gamma\).

Thus rank two also simplifies O2/O3 bookkeeping:

\[
\boxed{
d_0^{(2)}
\text{ depends only on the vector curvature components, not a moving wall ratio.}
}
\]

If \(\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}\neq0\), the safe sequence remains:

1. use raw vector wall for O2/O3;
2. prove amplitude Schur afterward;
3. extract blockwise.

Do not put a projected vector wall into O2/O3 unless its branch-charge complexity is controlled.

---

## 7. Rank-two theorem statement

A clean conditional theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoY12D4Wall.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. live dual pair exists:

\[
e_7,e_Y
\]

span the live fiber with polynomial conditioning;

2. local actual-source/nuisance fiber model vanishes:

\[
B_Y=0;
\]

3. D4 coefficients satisfy

\[
|c_7\alpha_9|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|c_7|+|\alpha_9|+|\beta_9|\le Q^A;
\]

4. coherent amplitude model \(\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}\) is zero/fixed or finite coherent and satisfies vector amplitude Schur;

5. joint curvature wall holds:

\[
\int
\min\left(
Q^A |H|^2
(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2),
1
\right)d\nu
\ge Q^{-B}\nu(\mathcal C).
\]

Then downstream D4 supplies forbidden wall mass without the rank-one moving-wall/trap hierarchy.

---

## 8. What remains if joint curvature wall fails?

If rank two holds but

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0
\]

on a large set, this is not the same as the rank-one ODE trap. It means both curvature channels vanish.

This may imply an even stronger geometric degeneracy, perhaps a lower-order flatness/sterility branch. But it should be attacked as joint curvature degeneracy, not as a moving-line ODE.

So the rank-two fallback branch is:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ jointly small}
}
\]

rather than

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G\text{ line-trapped}.
}
\]

This is likely easier.

---

## Final result

If \(B_Y=0\), the downstream route is substantially simpler:

\[
\boxed{
\text{rank-two vector wall}
}
\]

with energy equivalent to

\[
|H|^2(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2).
\]

This bypasses the moving-line wall, \(\rho_\Gamma\), and the forced ODE trap.

The only remaining downstream requirements are:

1. vector amplitude Schur if coherent amplitude spaces exist;
2. joint curvature anti-concentration;
3. bounded-charge O2/O3 with vector wall degree.

Therefore, proving \(B_Y=0\) should remain the top priority.

## 1. Rank-two wall theorem

The rank-two wall theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\int
\min\left(
Q^A |H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right),
1
\right)
d\nu
\ge
Q^{-B}\nu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

After dyadic freezing of \(|H|\), this reduces to joint anti-concentration:

\[
\boxed{
\nu\left(
|\Gamma_G|<\varepsilon,\ 
|\Gamma_{G,2}|<\varepsilon
\right)
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\nu(\mathcal C).
}
\]

This is substantially weaker than the rank-one requirement

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G
\not\approx0,
\]

because we only need to rule out simultaneous smallness, not proximity to a moving line.

---

## 2. First finite-type witness for the vector wall

For a two-component function

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

joint smallness can be ruled out by a finite-type determinant. A natural first witness is the Wronskian

\[
\boxed{
W_{\Gamma}
=
\Gamma_G\Gamma_{G,2}'
-
\Gamma_G'\Gamma_{G,2}.
}
\]

If

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

and

\[
|W_{\Gamma}|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

on a polynomial fraction of the block, then the vector cannot remain close to zero on a large set. More generally, one wants a bounded-order finite-type condition:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le j\le J}
\left|
\partial_m^j \Gamma_G
\right|
+
\max_{0\le j\le J}
\left|
\partial_m^j \Gamma_{G,2}
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

on the active measure, with \(J=O(1)\).

This gives a vector finite-type sublevel bound:

\[
\nu\left(
|\Gamma_G|<\varepsilon,\ 
|\Gamma_{G,2}|<\varepsilon
\right)
\le Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\nu(\mathcal C).
\]

So the rank-two wall failure branch is:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\text{ both vanish to high finite order.}
}
\]

That is a stronger degeneracy than the rank-one line trap.

---

## 3. Rank-two failure is a flatness branch, not an ODE-line branch

Rank-one failure gave

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G\approx0,
\]

which became a fourth-order ODE constraint.

Rank-two failure gives

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0.
\]

This should be interpreted as a curvature-flatness or wall-flatness branch.

If \(\Gamma_G\) is the lower curvature channel and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) its higher/secondary channel, then simultaneous smallness likely means the local geometry is close to a degenerate lower-dimensional model. This is not automatically impossible, but it is more restrictive than a single moving-line relation.

So the rank-two fallback theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{JointCurvatureFlatnessBranch.}
}
\]

Either the vector wall has mass, or the canonical local geometry lies near the joint-flat model

\[
\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0
\]

to bounded finite order.

---

## 4. Relation to earlier raw anisotropy

Any previous theorem or numerical evidence of raw anisotropy becomes directly useful in the rank-two branch:

\[
\boxed{
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\text{ non-small}
}
\]

is exactly the required vector wall.

This was insufficient for the rank-one wall because a large vector can lie near the null line

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G=0.
\]

But for rank two, raw anisotropy is the target. Therefore any existing “wall escape” or “curvature nonflatness” estimates should be reinterpreted as rank-two wall evidence.

This is a significant reuse opportunity.

---

## 5. Amplitude Schur in rank two

If a coherent amplitude model survives,

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\subset L^2(\nu;\mathbf C^2),
\]

then the wall theorem becomes

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\nu)}
\left(
F_{2Y},
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\|F_{2Y}\|^2.
}
\]

This is the vector version of amplitude Schur.

The same finite-model non-absorption lemma applies:

1. \(\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}\) must have polynomial dimension;
2. it must have bounded leverage;
3. it must not be able to interpolate extraction-scale vector amplitudes;
4. a vector finite-type or Wronskian determinant must separate \(F_{2Y}\) from the model.

If

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}=0
\]

or only fixed basepoint terms exist, no amplitude Schur is needed.

---

## 6. O2/O3 weight under rank two

If \(B_Y=0\), use the raw vector wall for O2/O3:

\[
W_{\mathrm{bd}}^{(2)}
=
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
\]

The branch-charge bandwidth is

\[
d_0^{(2)}
=
d_N+2d_H+2d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{vec}},
\]

where

\[
d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{vec}}
=
\max\{d(\Gamma_G),d(\Gamma_{G,2})\}.
\]

No \(\rho_\Gamma\) appears.

So, compared with rank one, the O2/O3 input is cleaner:

\[
\boxed{
d_0^{(2)}
\text{ is controlled by the two curvature components, not a moving wall ratio.}
}
\]

If the exact degree is not known, use the conservative central basis condition

\[
\mathbf C_{d_{\max}}[y]\subset V_{\mathrm{tr}},
\qquad d_{\max}=14
\]

until \(d_0^{(2)}\) is computed.

---

## 7. Rank-two downstream theorem

A compact conditional theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoD4Downstream.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(B_Y=0\);

2. live pair \((e_7,e_Y)\) is polynomially conditioned;

3. D4 coefficients satisfy

\[
|c_7\alpha_9|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|c_7|+|\alpha_9|+|\beta_9|\le Q^A;
\]

4. any coherent vector amplitude space is finite coherent and satisfies vector amplitude Schur;

5. joint curvature anti-concentration holds:

\[
\int
\min\left(
Q^A |H|^2
(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2),
1
\right)d\nu
\ge Q^{-B}\nu(\mathcal C).
\]

Then D4 gives downstream forbidden mass without invoking:

\[
\rho_Y,\quad
\rho_\Gamma,\quad
\text{moving-wall finite type},\quad
\text{forced ODE trap}.
\]

---

## 8. Remaining rank-two obstruction

The only rank-two analogue of the ODE trap is joint curvature flatness:

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0.
\]

If this persists on a Stack-good set, one needs a separate flatness-disposal theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual canonical source cannot be jointly curvature-flat on polynomial mass}
}
\]

or a routing theorem saying joint flatness forces another contradiction.

But this is likely easier than the rank-one forced ODE trap because it is codimension two.

---

## Final result

If \(B_Y=0\), the downstream wall collapses to a vector anisotropy theorem:

\[
\boxed{
|H|^2(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2)
}
\]

modulo finite coherent amplitude spaces.

This recovers the usefulness of raw anisotropy and bypasses the entire rank-one moving-wall/trap hierarchy.

Therefore, the primary target remains:

\[
\boxed{
B_Y=0?
}
\]

If yes, pursue rank-two vector wall immediately.

I’ll push the rank-two branch into a precise “joint flatness” fallback. If vector wall mass fails, the exceptional set should be \(\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0\) to finite order, not a moving-line ODE.

Continuing Agent 5 — rank-two joint-flatness fallback.

I will keep:

\[
\rho_Y=\text{the }Y12\text{ fiber graph slope},
\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

But in the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), the wall does not use \(\rho_Y\) or \(\rho_\Gamma\). The vector wall is

\[
F_{2Y}
=
H
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\Gamma_G\\
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix},

The remaining failure mode is joint smallness of both curvature channels. This is the rank-two replacement for the rank-one forced ODE trap.

---

## 1. Vector wall theorem as finite-type alternative

The desired vector wall theorem is

\[
\int
\min\left(
Q^A|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right),
1
\right)
d\nu
\ge
Q^{-B}\nu(\mathcal C).
\]

Equivalently, after dyadic normalization of \(|H|\), we need

\[
\nu\{
|\Gamma_G|<\varepsilon,\,
|\Gamma_{G,2}|<\varepsilon
\}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta \nu(\mathcal C).
\]

If this fails, then there is a polynomial-mass set where

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0.
\]

But for a finite-type/sublevel theorem, genuine failure is stronger: both functions and a bounded number of their derivatives are small. Thus the rank-two fallback is a **joint flatness branch**.

---

## 2. Define the joint-flatness jet

Let

\[
\Gamma^{(J)}
=
\left(
\partial_m^j\Gamma_G,\,
\partial_m^j\Gamma_{G,2}
\right)_{0\le j\le J}.
\]

Define the joint flatness energy

\[
E_{\mathrm{flat},J}
=
\sum_{j=0}^{J}
\left(
|\partial_m^j\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\partial_m^j\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
\]

Then the vector-wall finite-type alternative is:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{flat},J}\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

on most of the Stack-good measure, or else

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\text{ are jointly flat through order }J.
}
\]

If \(E_{\mathrm{flat},J}\) has mass, the vector wall has finite type and we get anti-concentration.

If not, the source is in the joint-flat branch.

---

## 3. What does joint flatness mean?

The rank-two wall components are curvature channels. In earlier notation, these are functions of the local scalar source geometry. Joint flatness means:

\[
\Gamma_G=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=0,
\]

and derivatives vanish to bounded order.

This is stronger than the rank-one line condition

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G=0.
\]

Rank-one line trapping leaves a one-dimensional family of curvature vectors. Rank-two joint flatness collapses the vector to zero.

Thus the exceptional model has smaller dimension.

Geometrically, it is a flat/degenerate curvature branch.

---

## 4. Possible disposal of joint flatness

There are three plausible routes.

### A. Joint flatness contradicts O2/O3

If

\[
\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0
\]

means the graph curvature/torsion of

\[
1/m_{\mathrm{can},+}
\]

degenerates, it may contradict the graph non-polynomiality theorem used for O2/O3.

A target statement:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ jointly flat}
\Rightarrow
\operatorname{dist}(1/m_{\mathrm{can},+},\mathbf C_R[x])
\text{ is not polynomially large}
}
\]

or conversely, joint flatness may force an alternative graph degeneracy that O2/O3 detects.

This needs a precise relation between \(\Gamma\) and \(m_{\mathrm{can},+}\).

### B. Joint flatness contradicts Gate–1 nonflatness

Gate–1 gives

\[
\int |q''_{\mathrm{can}}|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Joint flatness of curvature channels might not force \(q''=0\), but if the channels encode all nontrivial local curvature of the source, it may imply too much local flatness.

A target theorem:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{flat},J}\ll Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
\|q''_{\mathrm{can}}\|_{L^2(I)}\ll Q^{-A'}
}
\]

on the branch. If true, Gate–1 kills the joint-flat branch.

This is uncertain but worth testing.

### C. Higher rank / derivative residual

If \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) are jointly flat, take the first nonzero derivative jet:

\[
\partial_m^k(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

for some \(k\le J\). If all bounded derivatives vanish, then the source lies near an even smaller flat model.

This is analogous to the rank-one trap hierarchy, but simpler: it is a vector flatness hierarchy rather than a forced ODE hierarchy.

---

## 5. Vector wall with coherent amplitude spaces

If a finite coherent vector amplitude model exists,

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\subset L^2(\nu;\mathbf C^2),
\]

then joint flatness must be formulated modulo this model.

The vector wall residual is

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
F_{2Y},
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right).
\]

If this distance is small, then

\[
F_{2Y}
\]

lies near a finite coherent vector amplitude model.

The corresponding flatness branch is not simply

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0,
\]

but rather

\[
H
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\Gamma_G\\
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}
\in
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}.
\]

If the amplitude model is finite coherent and nonlocal, this becomes another finite-model nonabsorption theorem.

So, even in rank two, the three cases remain:

1. no amplitude space: joint curvature wall;
2. finite coherent amplitude space: vector amplitude Schur;
3. locally free amplitude: route fails at amplitude level.

---

## 6. Rank-two finite theorem

A clean theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoVectorWallOrJointFlatness.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(B_Y=0\);

2. live pair and D4 coefficients are polynomially conditioned;

3. \(\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}\) is zero/fixed or finite coherent, not locally free.

Then either:

### Vector wall good

\[
\int
\min
\left(
Q^A
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
F_{2Y},
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)^2,
1
\right)d\nu
\ge Q^{-B}\nu(\mathcal C);
\]

or:

### Joint-flat branch

\[
(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

is jointly flat to bounded order modulo the coherent vector amplitude model.

The joint-flat branch must then be disposed by:

- an O2/O3 compatibility theorem;
- a Gate–1 nonflatness theorem;
- or a derivative-vector residual.

---

## 7. Comparison with rank-one trap

Rank-one failure:

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G=0
\]

creates a forced fourth-order ODE with moving coefficient \(\rho_\Gamma\). This is delicate and requires wall-honesty.

Rank-two failure:

\[
\Gamma_G=0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=0
\]

creates a joint curvature-flat branch. It does not involve \(\rho_\Gamma\), and it is codimension two.

Therefore, if \(B_Y=0\) is available, rank two is structurally much stronger.

---

## Final conclusion

The rank-two branch reduces the wall problem to:

\[
\boxed{
(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\text{ not jointly flat}
}
\]

modulo finite coherent amplitudes.

If joint flatness occurs, it is a smaller, more rigid exceptional model than the rank-one forced ODE trap.

So rank-two D4 not only simplifies the wall; it gives a better fallback branch:

\[
\boxed{
\text{joint curvature flatness}
}
\]

instead of

\[
\boxed{
\text{moving-line ODE trap}.
}
\]

This further strengthens the case that proving or disproving \(B_Y=0\) is the top downstream priority.

## Assistant (2026-04-28 07:55:31)

_Thought for 32s_

Continuing Agent 5 — rank-two joint flatness may be directly incompatible with Gate–1.

I will keep:

\[
\rho_Y=\text{the }Y12\text{ fiber graph slope},\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), neither \(\rho_Y\) nor \(\rho_\Gamma\) enters the wall. D4 gives the vector wall

\[
F_{2Y}
=
H
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\Gamma_G\\
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}
\asymp
H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

under coefficient conditioning. The latest prompt emphasizes that this rank-two branch bypasses the rank-one moving-line and forced-ODE hierarchy. 

The remaining bad case is joint flatness:

\[
\Gamma_G\approx 0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}\approx 0.
\]

I now think this branch may be much easier than previously stated: in the exact model, joint flatness appears to force \(q\) to be constant, hence \(q''=0\), contradicting Gate–1.

---

## 1. Recover the two wall equations

From the rank-one wall convention used earlier,

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G=0
\]

implied

\[
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q^2+\rho_\Gamma)q''
-
36\rho_\Gamma q
+
12\rho_\Gamma q^3.
\]

Rearranging,

\[
q^{(4)}
-
6(1-q^2)q''
-
\rho_\Gamma(6q''-36q+12q^3)
=
0.
\]

Thus, up to the sign convention already being used, the natural components are

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
q^{(4)}-6(1-q^2)q'',
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G
=
-6q''+36q-12q^3.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\Gamma_G=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
q''=6q-2q^3.
\]

The sign should still be checked against the final definitions of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\), but this is consistent with the current wall-ODE normalization.

---

## 2. Exact joint flatness forces constancy

Assume exact rank-two flatness:

\[
\Gamma_G=0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

From \(\Gamma_G=0\),

\[
q''=6q-2q^3.
\]

Let

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
q''=f(q),
\]

\[
q'''=f'(q)q',
\]

and

\[
q^{(4)}=f''(q)(q')^2+f'(q)f(q).
\]

Now

\[
f'(q)=6-6q^2,
\qquad
f''(q)=-12q.
\]

The equation \(\Gamma_{G,2}=0\) says

\[
q^{(4)}=6(1-q^2)q''=f'(q)f(q).
\]

Comparing with the differentiated \(\Gamma_G=0\) identity gives

\[
f''(q)(q')^2=0,
\]

hence

\[
\boxed{
-12q(q')^2=0.
}
\]

Therefore, on any interval where the equations hold exactly,

\[
q(q')^2=0.
\]

So either \(q=0\) or \(q'=0\) locally. In either case \(q\) is locally constant. If \(q'=0\), then \(q''=0\), and \(\Gamma_G=0\) gives

\[
6q-2q^3=0,
\]

so

\[
q\in\{0,\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\}.
\]

Thus exact joint flatness forces

\[
\boxed{
q\equiv0,\quad q\equiv\sqrt3,\quad\text{or}\quad q\equiv-\sqrt3
}
\]

locally, and hence

\[
\boxed{
q''\equiv0.}
\]

This directly contradicts Gate–1 local \(L^2\) energy.

---

## 3. Rank-two flatness is therefore stronger than the rank-one ODE trap

Rank-one wall failure gave a fourth-order ODE:

\[
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q^2+\rho_\Gamma)q''
-
36\rho_\Gamma q
+
12\rho_\Gamma q^3.
\]

That equation has many possible nonconstant local solutions.

Rank-two wall failure imposes both

\[
q''=6q-2q^3
\]

and

\[
q^{(4)}=6(1-q^2)q''.
\]

Their compatibility forces

\[
q(q')^2=0,
\]

so only constant solutions survive.

Thus the rank-two bad branch is not merely “joint curvature flatness.” It is likely a **Gate–1 contradiction branch**.

This is a major advantage of proving \(B_Y=0\).

---

## 4. Approximate version needed

The proof will need a stability theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{JointFlatnessStability.}
}
\]

A plausible statement:

If on a local interval \(I\),

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{C^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{C^0(I)}\le \varepsilon,
\]

then

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\le Q^C\varepsilon^\theta
\]

unless \(q\) leaves the chart-good region.

Since Gate–1 gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A},
\]

choosing \(\varepsilon\) polynomially small excludes joint flatness.

Why \(C^2\) or finite derivatives of \(\Gamma_G\)? Because the exact contradiction used differentiating

\[
q''=f(q)
\]

twice and comparing to \(\Gamma_{G,2}\). In approximate form, we need enough control to say

\[
q^{(4)}\approx f'(q)f(q)+f''(q)(q')^2
\]

while also

\[
q^{(4)}\approx f'(q)q'',
\]

forcing

\[
q(q')^2\approx0.
\]

Then \(\Gamma_G\approx0\) forces \(q''\approx0\) unless the solution transitions too fast, which finite derivative bounds should exclude.

---

## 5. Possible issue near \(q=0\)

The exact identity gives

\[
q(q')^2=0.
\]

Near \(q=0\), this does not directly force \(q'\) small. But if \(q\approx0\), then

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0
\]

gives

\[
q''\approx 6q-2q^3\approx0.
\]

So even near \(q=0\), \(q''\) is small. Gate–1 still fails.

Near \(q=\pm\sqrt3\), \(\Gamma_G=0\) also gives

\[
q''\approx0.
\]

For intermediate \(q\), \(q(q')^2\approx0\) forces \(q'\approx0\), and then \(q''=f(q)\) cannot remain nonzero over a thick interval without quickly changing \(q'\). Finite-type control should again force \(q''\) small on average.

So the approximate theorem seems plausible across all chart-good regions.

---

## 6. Rank-two wall theorem can be strengthened

Instead of requiring a new joint curvature anti-concentration theorem, we can try proving:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ jointly small}
\Rightarrow
q''\text{ small}.
}
\]

Then Gate–1 excludes the rank-two bad set.

So the rank-two downstream stack becomes:

\[
B_Y=0
\Rightarrow
\text{vector wall }(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

\[
\Rightarrow
\text{if wall fails, }q''\text{ is small}
\]

\[
\Rightarrow
\text{contradicts Gate--1.}
\]

This avoids both:

- moving-line finite type;
- forced ODE anti-model.

---

## 7. Conditional theorem

A strong rank-two theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoWallGate1Closure.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(B_Y=0\);

2. live pair and D4 coefficient matrix are polynomially conditioned;

3. Gate–1 local scalar energy holds:

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}^2\ge Q^{-A};
\]

4. joint-flatness stability holds:

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{C^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{C^0(I)}
\le Q^{-B}
\Rightarrow
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}^2\le Q^{-A'}
\]

with \(B\) large.

Then the rank-two vector wall has polynomial mass:

\[
\int_I
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This supplies the D4 wall without any rank-one trap hierarchy.

---

## Final result

Rank-two wall failure appears to force

\[
q\equiv0,\ \pm\sqrt3
\]

in the exact model, hence

\[
q''=0.
\]

Therefore the rank-two bad branch is likely killed directly by Gate–1.

This makes the \(B_Y=0\) route even more valuable:

\[
\boxed{
B_Y=0
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-two wall}
\Rightarrow
\text{joint flatness}
\Rightarrow
q''\approx0
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate--1 contradiction.}
}
\]

The next precise theorem to prove is the approximate stability version of this exact calculation.

_Thought for 9s_

Continuing Agent 5 — approximate stability of rank-two joint flatness.

I will keep:

\[
\rho_Y=\text{the }Y12\text{ fiber graph slope},\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), the wall is vector-valued and does **not** use \(\rho_Y\) or \(\rho_\Gamma\):

\[
F_{2Y}
=
H
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\Gamma_G\\
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}
\asymp
H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

The exact joint-flatness calculation suggested:

\[
\Gamma_G=0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
q''=0.
\]

So the rank-two wall failure should contradict Gate–1 after a stability estimate. This is the payoff of the current \(B_Y=0\) branch. 

---

## 1. Normalize the two curvature equations

Using the current wall-ODE normalization, take

\[
\Gamma_G
=
-6q''+36q-12q^3,
\]

so

\[
\Gamma_G=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
q''=6q-2q^3.
\]

Let

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
q''=f(q).
\]

Also take

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
q^{(4)}-6(1-q^2)q''
=
q^{(4)}-f'(q)q'',
\]

since

\[
f'(q)=6-6q^2.
\]

Thus joint flatness is

\[
q''=f(q),
\qquad
q^{(4)}=f'(q)q''.
\]

But if \(q''=f(q)\), differentiating twice gives

\[
q^{(4)}
=
f''(q)(q')^2+f'(q)f(q).
\]

Since \(q''=f(q)\), the second flatness equation gives

\[
q^{(4)}=f'(q)f(q).
\]

Subtracting yields

\[
f''(q)(q')^2=0.
\]

Because

\[
f''(q)=-12q,
\]

exact joint flatness implies

\[
q(q')^2=0.
\]

Together with \(q''=f(q)\), this forces \(q\) locally constant and hence

\[
q''=0.
\]

So exact joint flatness is incompatible with Gate–1.

---

## 2. Approximate residual equations

Define the residuals

\[
E_1:=q''-f(q),
\]

\[
E_2:=q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=-6E_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=E_2.
\]

The goal is to show that if \(E_1,E_2\) are small in a finite-jet norm, then \(q''\) is small in \(L^2\).

Differentiate

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1.
\]

Then

\[
q'''=f'(q)q'+E_1',
\]

and

\[
q^{(4)}
=
f''(q)(q')^2+f'(q)q''+E_1''.
\]

Subtracting the definition of \(E_2\),

\[
E_2
=
q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''
=
f''(q)(q')^2+E_1''.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
-12q(q')^2
=
E_2-E_1''.
}
\]

This is the exact stability identity.

Thus if

\[
\|E_2\|_{L^\infty(I)}+\|E_1''\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le \varepsilon,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
|q|\,|q'|^2\le C\varepsilon.
}
\]

Together with

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1,
\]

we want to conclude

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\lesssim \varepsilon^\theta
\]

unless the interval is too short or the chart degenerates.

---

## 3. Stability away from \(q=0\)

On the region

\[
|q|\ge \eta,
\]

the identity gives

\[
|q'|^2\le C\varepsilon/\eta.
\]

So

\[
|q'|\le C\varepsilon^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2}.
\]

If \(q\) varies slowly and \(q''=f(q)+E_1\), then \(f(q)\) cannot stay bounded away from zero over a thick subinterval. Otherwise \(q'\) would change at speed \(\gtrsim |f(q)|\), contradicting small \(q'\).

Thus on a thick interval,

\[
|f(q)|\lesssim \varepsilon^\theta+\|E_1\|_\infty.
\]

Since

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1,
\]

we get

\[
|q''|\lesssim \varepsilon^\theta+\|E_1\|_\infty
\]

away from \(q=0\).

The only possible approximate constants are near the roots of

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3=2q(3-q^2),
\]

namely

\[
q=0,\quad q=\pm\sqrt3.
\]

At all three roots,

\[
q''\approx0.
\]

So this is compatible with Gate–1 failure.

---

## 4. Stability near \(q=0\)

Near

\[
q=0,
\]

the identity

\[
|q||q'|^2\lesssim \varepsilon
\]

does not force \(q'\) small. But

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3
\]

is small when \(q\) is small. Hence

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1
\]

is also small if \(q\) remains near zero.

If \(q\) does not remain near zero, then it enters \(|q|\ge\eta\), where the previous argument controls \(q'\). A transition from \(q\approx0\) to \(|q|\ge\eta\) with \(q''\approx f(q)\) still requires curvature energy, and the residual identity forces that transition to be sparse. Quantitatively, one can cover the interval by:

\[
|q|<\eta
\quad\text{and}\quad
|q|\ge\eta.
\]

On \(|q|<\eta\),

\[
|q''|\le |f(q)|+|E_1|\le C\eta+\|E_1\|_\infty.
\]

On \(|q|\ge\eta\),

\[
|q''|\le C\varepsilon^\theta\eta^{-C}+\|E_1\|_\infty.
\]

Choose

\[
\eta=\varepsilon^\kappa
\]

for small fixed \(\kappa>0\). Then

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
C|I|^{1/2}\varepsilon^{\theta}
}
\]

for some \(\theta>0\), assuming finite derivative bounds on \(q\) and residuals.

This is the desired approximate stability.

---

## 5. A clean theorem statement

A usable theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{JointFlatnessStability.}
}
\]

Let \(I\) be a chart-good interval of polynomial length. Suppose \(q\) and a bounded number of its derivatives obey polynomial \(C^K\) bounds. Define

\[
E_1=q''-(6q-2q^3),
\]

\[
E_2=q^{(4)}-6(1-q^2)q''.
\]

If

\[
\|E_1\|_{C^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{C^0(I)}\le \varepsilon,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta |I|^{1/2}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{C^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{C^0(I)}
\le \varepsilon
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\le Q^C\varepsilon^\theta.
\]

Thus Gate–1, which gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A},
\]

forces

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{C^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{C^0(I)}
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

That is rank-two wall mass.

---

## 6. Consequence for rank-two D4

If \(B_Y=0\), rank-two D4 gives

\[
|F_{2Y}|^2
\asymp
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
\]

If the vector wall is small on a Stack-good atom, then by finite-type smoothing it is small in the \(C^2/C^0\) sense after passing to a subatom or applying Markov-type bounds.

Then JointFlatnessStability gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2}\ll Q^{-A},
\]

contradicting Gate–1.

So rank-two D4 could close the wall layer using only:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate--1 + joint flatness stability}.
}
\]

This is far cleaner than the rank-one route.

---

## 7. What remains technical

The stability identity is exact:

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

The technical work is to convert small wall energy into the needed residual norm:

\[
\|E_1\|_{C^2}+\|E_2\|_{C^0}\le\varepsilon.
\]

Potential routes:

### A. Work with jet wall directly

Define rank-two wall using the finite jet norm:

\[
\sum_{j=0}^{2}|\partial_m^j\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2.
\]

Then stability is immediate.

This increases wall branch degree mildly but remains \(O(1)\).

### B. Use sublevel finite type

If only \(L^2\) wall energy is small, use finite derivative bounds/Markov inequalities to find a subinterval where the residuals are small in \(C^2\). Then apply stability locally.

### C. Add derivative-wall fallback

If \(\Gamma_G\) is small but its derivatives are not, then derivative wall already gives mass. So either the jet wall has mass or joint flatness stability applies.

Thus the rank-two wall theorem should probably use a **jet-enhanced vector wall**:

\[
E_{2Y,\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_G'|^2+|\Gamma_G''|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right),
\]

with appropriate scale normalization.

---

## 8. Updated rank-two theorem

A stronger theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoJetWallGate1Closure.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(B_Y=0\);

2. D4 coefficient matrix is polynomially conditioned;

3. Gate–1 holds:

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A};
\]

4. \(q\) has polynomial chart-good derivative bounds;

5. the rank-two jet wall is used:

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\partial_m\Gamma_G|^2+|\partial_m^2\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
\]

Then

\[
\int_I E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

This supplies wall mass without a moving-line theorem or forced ODE trap.

---

## Final result

The exact identity

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}-\partial_m^2(\text{normalized }\Gamma_G)
=
-12q(q')^2
}
\]

more precisely, with

\[
E_1=q''-(6q-2q^3),\quad
E_2=q^{(4)}-6(1-q^2)q'',
\]

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2,
}
\]

shows that rank-two joint flatness forces \(q''\) small.

Therefore, in the \(B_Y=0\) branch, Gate–1 can likely dispose of the vector-wall failure directly.

This is a major simplification:

\[
\boxed{
B_Y=0
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-two vector wall}
\Rightarrow
\text{joint flatness}
\Rightarrow
q''\approx0
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate--1 contradiction}.
}
\]

The next exact task is proving the approximate JointFlatnessStability theorem with the correct scaled jet norms.

## 1. Normalization and exact identity

Using the current normalization,

\[
\Gamma_G=-6q''+36q-12q^3.
\]

Thus

\[
\Gamma_G=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
q''=6q-2q^3.
\]

Define

\[

\]

Then

\[
f'(q)=6-6q^2,
\qquad
f''(q)=-12q.
\]

The second wall component is normalized as

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=q^{(4)}-6(1-q^2)q''
=
q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Define residuals

\[
E_1=q''-f(q),
\]

\[
E_2=q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=-6E_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=E_2.
\]

Differentiate

\[

=

Therefore

=

=

So the exact stability identity is

E_2-E_1''=f''(q)(q')^2=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

This is the key rank-two identity.

---

## 2. Exact flatness result

If

\[
E_1=0,\qquad E_2=0
\]

on an interval, then

\[
-12q(q')^2=0.
\]

Thus

\[
q(q')^2=0.
\]

On any connected subinterval where \(q\neq0\), this forces

\[
q'=0.
\]

Then

\[
q''=0.
\]

But \(E_1=0\) gives

\[
0=q''=6q-2q^3=2q(3-q^2),
\]

so

\[
q\in\{\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\}.
\]

If \(q=0\), then again

\[
q''=f(0)=0.
\]

Hence exact joint flatness forces

\[
\boxed{
q\equiv0,\quad q\equiv\sqrt3,\quad\text{or}\quad q\equiv-\sqrt3
}
\]

locally, and therefore

\[
\boxed{
q''\equiv0.
}
\]

So exact rank-two wall failure contradicts Gate–1.

---

## 3. Approximate stability theorem

The needed approximate theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{JointFlatnessStability.}
}
\]

Let \(I\) be a chart-good interval. Assume \(q\) has polynomial \(C^K\)-bounds on \(I\). If

\[
\|E_1\|_{C^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{C^0(I)}
\le \varepsilon,
\]

then for some fixed \(\theta>0\),

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta |I|^{1/2}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{C^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{C^0(I)}
\le \varepsilon
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta |I|^{1/2}.
}
\]

The exact identity gives the core estimate:

\[
|q|\,|q'|^2
\le C\varepsilon.
\]

Indeed,

\[
|q|\,|q'|^2
\le
C(|E_2|+|E_1''|)
\le C\varepsilon.
\]

---

## 4. Control away from \(q=0\)

On the region

\[
|q|\ge \eta,
\]

we get

\[
|q'|^2\le C\varepsilon/\eta.
\]

So

\[
|q'|\le C\varepsilon^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2}.
\]

Since

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1,
\]

if \(|f(q)|\) were bounded below on a thick subinterval, then \(q'\) would change at speed \(\gtrsim |f(q)|\), contradicting small \(q'\). Therefore, on thick subintervals of \(|q|\ge\eta\),

\[
|f(q)|\le Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\eta^{-C}.
\]

Hence

\[
|q''|
\le |f(q)|+|E_1|
\le Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\eta^{-C}.
\]

---

## 5. Control near \(q=0\)

On

\[
|q|<\eta,
\]

we have

\[
|f(q)|=|6q-2q^3|\le C\eta.
\]

Therefore

\[
|q''|
\le |f(q)|+|E_1|
\le C\eta+\varepsilon.
\]

Choose

\[
\eta=\varepsilon^\kappa
\]

for a small fixed \(\kappa>0\). Combining the near-zero and away-from-zero regions gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta |I|^{1/2}.
\]

This proves the desired approximate stability modulo standard finite-cover and chart-goodness assumptions.

---

## 6. Rank-two jet wall

The stability theorem requires \(C^2\)-control of \(\Gamma_G\), not just pointwise or \(L^2\)-control of \(\Gamma_G\). Therefore the safest rank-two wall is jet-enhanced:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\partial_m\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\partial_m^2\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
}
\]

With proper scale normalization, smallness of this wall implies

\[
\|E_1\|_{C^2}+\|E_2\|_{C^0}
\]

is small on a subatom or in a Sobolev-controlled sense.

Then JointFlatnessStability gives

\[
q''\text{ small},
\]

contradicting Gate–1.

---

## 7. Rank-two closure theorem

A strong rank-two closure statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoJetWallGate1Closure.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(B_Y=0\), so D4 is rank two;

2. the D4 coefficient matrix is polynomially conditioned;

3. Gate–1 holds:

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A};
\]

4. \(q\) has chart-good polynomial finite-jet bounds;

5. the rank-two jet wall is used:

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\partial_m\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\partial_m^2\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Thus the rank-two D4 wall lower follows from Gate–1.

---

## 8. Remaining technical gaps

The core identity is solid under the stated normalization:

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

The remaining work is technical:

1. verify the final signs and scaling of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\);

2. choose the correct scale-normalized derivatives in the jet wall;

3. convert small \(L^2\) or averaged wall energy into the \(C^2/C^0\)-type residual control needed for stability, probably by subinterval selection plus Markov/Sobolev bounds;

4. ensure the chart-good assumptions exclude singular denominators or degenerate rescalings;

5. integrate coherent amplitude terms, if present, by replacing \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) with its distance to the finite coherent vector model.

---

## Final conclusion

The rank-two branch has a powerful closure mechanism:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ jointly flat}
\Rightarrow
q''\approx0
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate--1 contradiction}.
}
\]

The key exact identity is

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

So if \(B_Y=0\) can be proved, the downstream D4 wall can likely be closed with Gate–1 and JointFlatnessStability, avoiding the entire rank-one moving-wall/forced-ODE hierarchy.

## Assistant (2026-04-28 12:31:06)

I’ll now make the rank-two Gate–1 closure scale-invariant and check whether we really need a jet-enhanced D4 wall, or whether scalar vector-wall mass plus finite-type selection is enough.

_Thought for 43s_

Continuing Agent 5 — scale-correct rank-two Gate–1 closure.

I will keep:

\[
\rho_Y=\text{the }Y12\text{ fiber graph slope},\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), these wall-ratio variables are not used. The relevant wall is vector-valued:

\[
F_{2Y}
=
H
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\Gamma_G\\
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}
\asymp_{Q^A}
H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

The goal is to prove that small rank-two wall forces small \(q''\), contradicting Gate–1. This is the local stability mechanism behind the rank-two route. 

---

# 1. Exact algebraic identity

Use the current normalization:

\[
\Gamma_G=-6q''+36q-12q^3.
\]

Define

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=-6(q''-f(q)).
\]

Set

\[
E_1=q''-f(q).
\]

Also

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=q^{(4)}-6(1-q^2)q''.
\]

Since

\[
f'(q)=6-6q^2,
\]

define

\[
E_2=q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=-6E_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=E_2.
\]

Differentiating

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1
\]

twice gives

\[
q^{(4)}=f''(q)(q')^2+f'(q)q''+E_1''.
\]

Therefore

\[
E_2
=
q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''
=
f''(q)(q')^2+E_1''.
\]

Since

\[
f''(q)=-12q,
\]

we have the exact identity

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

This is the core rank-two stability identity.

---

# 2. Exact joint flatness

If

\[
E_1=0,\qquad E_2=0,
\]

then

\[
q(q')^2=0.
\]

On any connected subinterval where \(q\neq0\), this gives

\[
q'=0.
\]

Then

\[
q''=0.
\]

But \(E_1=0\) gives

\[
q''=f(q)=2q(3-q^2).
\]

Therefore the only constant solutions are

\[
q\equiv0,\qquad q\equiv\sqrt3,\qquad q\equiv-\sqrt3,
\]

and in all cases

\[
q''\equiv0.
\]

So exact rank-two wall flatness contradicts Gate–1.

---

# 3. Approximate stability: the needed form

The useful theorem should be scale-local. In the coordinate where the \(\Gamma\)-formulas are valid, let \(I\) be a chart-good interval. Then a clean version is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{JointFlatnessStability.}
}
\]

If

\[
\|E_1\|_{C^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{C^0(I)}\le \varepsilon
\]

and \(q\) has polynomial chart-good finite-jet bounds, then

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta |I|^{1/2}
}
\]

for some fixed \(\theta>0\).

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{C^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{C^0(I)}
\le\varepsilon
\Longrightarrow
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le Q^C\varepsilon^\theta |I|^{1/2}.
}
\]

This is exactly the stability theorem needed to let Gate–1 kill rank-two wall failure.

---

# 4. Proof skeleton of approximate stability

From

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2
\]

we get

\[
|q|\,|q'|^2\le C\varepsilon.
\]

Let

\[
Z=\{0,\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\}.
\]

Since

\[
f(q)=2q(3-q^2)
\]

has simple roots at \(Z\), we have

\[
|f(q)|\gtrsim \operatorname{dist}(q,Z)
\]

on chart-good bounded regions.

Split \(I\) into:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(q,Z)<\eta
\]

and its complement.

On the near-root region,

\[
|f(q)|\lesssim \eta,
\]

hence

\[
|q''|\le |f(q)|+|E_1|\lesssim \eta+\varepsilon.
\]

On the complement, either \(|q|\gtrsim\eta\), so

\[
|q'|\lesssim \varepsilon^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2},
\]

or \(q\) is away from all roots with \(|f(q)|\gtrsim\eta\). If \(q''=f(q)+E_1\) stayed \(\gtrsim\eta\) on a thick subinterval, then \(q'\) would change by \(\gtrsim \eta\cdot |J|\), contradicting the smallness of \(q'\) unless that subinterval is short. Using the polynomial finite-jet bound to control the number of such transitions, the total \(L^2\)-mass of \(q''\) on the complement is bounded by

\[
Q^C \varepsilon^\theta |I|.
\]

Choosing

\[
\eta=\varepsilon^\kappa
\]

with small fixed \(\kappa>0\) gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta |I|^{1/2}.
\]

The proof is stable as long as the chart-good bounds prevent arbitrarily many oscillatory crossings of the root neighborhoods.

---

# 5. Do we need a jet-enhanced wall?

There is a subtle but important point.

The stability theorem needs control of

\[
E_1'',
\]

equivalently

\[
\partial_m^2\Gamma_G.
\]

The zero-th vector wall only controls

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

So there are two possible paths.

## Path A: Markov/Sobolev upgrade

If \(\Gamma_G\) belongs to a finite-dimensional/band-limited local source class, then a Markov-type inequality may give

\[
\|\partial_m^2\Gamma_G\|_{C^0(I)}
\le Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{C^0(I)}
\]

after scale normalization.

Then zero-th wall smallness implies the \(C^2\) smallness needed for stability.

This would preserve the simplest wall:

\[
|H|^2(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2).
\]

## Path B: use a jet-enhanced vector wall

If no such Markov upgrade is available, define the wall as

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\partial_m\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\partial_m^2\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)
}
\]

with correct scale normalization.

Then small wall directly implies the hypotheses of JointFlatnessStability.

This increases branch-charge degree but only by \(O(1)\). It is likely acceptable under the bounded-charge O2/O3 framework, with a conservative transition basis such as

\[
\mathbf C_{d_{\max}}[y],
\qquad d_{\max}=14
\]

or a slightly larger fixed bound if derivatives increase degree.

---

# 6. Rank-two Gate–1 closure theorem

A precise conditional theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoJetWallGate1Closure.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(B_Y=0\), so D4 is rank two;

2. the live pair and D4 coefficient matrix are polynomially conditioned;

3. Gate–1 holds on the same local block:

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A}|I|^{1/2};
\]

4. either:

   - a Markov/Sobolev upgrade converts zero-th vector wall smallness into \(C^2/C^0\) residual smallness; or
   - the jet-enhanced vector wall is used;

5. JointFlatnessStability holds.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
\ge Q^{-A'}|I|.
}
\]

In other words, the rank-two vector wall has polynomial mass because otherwise Gate–1 would be violated.

---

# 7. What remains technical

The remaining technical points are now specific.

### A. Sign and normalization audit

Verify the final definitions really give

\[
\Gamma_G=-6(q''-f(q)),
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

If signs differ, the exact identity changes. The stability mechanism may still survive, but the polynomial \(f\) must be corrected.

### B. Scaled derivatives

All derivatives in the jet wall must be normalized to the local physical scale. If \(D_I\) is the scale-normalized derivative, the jet wall should use

\[
|D_I^j\Gamma_G|^2
\]

rather than raw derivatives.

### C. Coherent amplitude model

If a vector amplitude model

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\]

exists, replace \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) by distance to that finite model. The stability theorem then applies to the residual only if the coherent model is fixed/finite and not locally free.

### D. O2/O3 bandwidth

If the jet wall is used in O2/O3, compute the new

\[
d_0^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
d_N+2d_H+2d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{jet}}.
\]

This should remain \(O(1)\), but it may exceed the previous conservative \(d_{\max}=14\).

---

# Final result

The rank-two wall can likely be closed by Gate–1 via the identity

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

The proof strategy is:

\[
B_Y=0
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-two vector wall}
\Rightarrow
\text{joint flatness}
\Rightarrow
q''\approx0
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate--1 contradiction}.
\]

The only serious analytic choice is whether to derive the needed \(C^2\)-control from a Markov/Sobolev upgrade or to build it directly into a jet-enhanced vector wall.
