I’ll now audit whether the jet-enhanced rank-two wall can stay within bounded-charge O2/O3. If yes, the Gate–1 closure becomes much more direct.

_Thought for 9s_

Continuing Agent 5 — bounded-charge audit for the jet-enhanced rank-two wall.

I will keep:

\[
\rho_Y=\text{the }Y12\text{ fiber graph slope},\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), the wall does **not** use \(\rho_Y\) or \(\rho_\Gamma\). The local D4 output is the vector wall

\[
F_{2Y}
=
H
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\Gamma_G\\
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}
\asymp_{Q^A}
H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

The last step showed that joint flatness of \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) should force \(q''\approx0\), contradicting Gate–1. The remaining technical question is whether we should use the plain vector wall or the jet-enhanced vector wall inside O2/O3. The latest architecture makes the rank-two route central if \(B_Y=0\). 

---

## 1. Plain wall versus jet wall

The plain rank-two wall is

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2)}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
\]

The jet-enhanced wall is

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D^2\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right),
\]

where \(D\) should be the scale-normalized local derivative.

The reason for adding \(D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G\) is the exact identity

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2,
\]

where

\[
E_1=q''-(6q-2q^3),
\qquad
E_2=q^{(4)}-6(1-q^2)q''.
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_G=-6E_1,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=E_2,
\]

JointFlatnessStability naturally requires

\[
E_1,E_1'',E_2
\]

small. Thus the jet wall is the direct D4/Gate–1 closure wall.

---

## 2. Bounded-charge effect of derivatives

The bounded-charge O2/O3 argument only needs the wall weight to have finite branch-charge bandwidth:

\[
d_0=d_N+2d_H+2d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{eff}}=O(1).
\]

Derivatives of \(\Gamma_G\) should not change branch charge if they act as local coordinate derivatives on the same finite branch expression. They can change polynomial degree or log-weight degree, but not the plus/dual branch count.

So the expected charge degrees are

\[
d(D^j\Gamma_G)=d(\Gamma_G)
\]

for branch charge, or at worst

\[
d(D^j\Gamma_G)\le d(\Gamma_G)+O(j)
\]

with \(j\le2\). In either case,

\[
d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{jet}}
=
\max\{
d(\Gamma_G),d(D\Gamma_G),d(D^2\Gamma_G),d(\Gamma_{G,2})
\}
=
O(1).
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
d_0^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
d_N+2d_H+2d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{jet}}
=
O(1).
}
\]

This means the jet-enhanced wall should remain compatible with bounded-charge O2/O3.

The practical transition basis requirement becomes

\[
\mathbf C_{d_{\max}}[y]\subset V_{\mathrm{tr}},
\]

with \(d_{\max}\) chosen to dominate \(d_0^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}\). The previous conservative value \(d_{\max}=14\) may still be enough, but the exact derivative contribution should be audited.

---

## 3. Avoiding nonlocal projections

If there is a finite coherent vector amplitude space

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}},
\]

do **not** put a globally projected wall

\[
(I-P_{\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}})F_{2Y}
\]

inside O2/O3 unless its branch-charge complexity is controlled.

The safe ordering remains:

1. use the raw rank-two wall, plain or jet,

\[
W_{\mathrm{bd}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
N_{\mathrm{sm}}E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}};
\]

2. prove O2/O3 with that bounded-charge raw wall;

3. prove vector amplitude Schur afterward:

\[
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\nu_{\mathrm{bd}})}
(F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}},\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}})^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\|F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}}\|^2;
\]

4. extract blockwise if needed.

This avoids circularity and preserves finite branch-charge bookkeeping.

---

## 4. Plain wall may suffice with Markov upgrade

The jet wall is the cleanest stability input, but perhaps unnecessary.

If the local source class satisfies a Markov/Sobolev bound

\[
\|D^2\Gamma_G\|_{C^0(I)}
\le Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{C^0(I)}
\]

or an \(L^2\)-to-\(C^2\) finite-dimensional bound after subinterval selection, then small plain wall implies small jet wall.

That would allow O2/O3 to use

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2)}
=
|H|^2(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2),
\]

and then upgrade to the \(C^2/C^0\) norm required by JointFlatnessStability.

This path has lower wall degree. But it needs a finite-dimensional regularity theorem for \(\Gamma_G\).

Thus there are two rank-two variants:

### Variant A: plain vector wall + Markov upgrade

Use

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2)}
\]

in O2/O3. Later use a Markov/Sobolev lemma to obtain the jet control needed for Gate–1 closure.

### Variant B: jet vector wall directly

Use

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
\]

in O2/O3. No Markov upgrade needed, but the O2/O3 bandwidth \(d_0\) may be slightly larger.

Variant B is safer. Variant A is cleaner if the Markov lemma is available.

---

## 5. Rank-two O2/O3 theorem with jet wall

The bounded-charge O2/O3 theorem should be stated in a version that accepts any fixed finite wall family.

Let

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}
=
\{
\Gamma_G,\ D\Gamma_G,\ D^2\Gamma_G,\ \Gamma_{G,2}
\}.
\]

Set

\[
W_{\mathrm{bd}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\sum_{G\in\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}}|G|^2.
\]

If every \(G\in\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}\) has branch-charge degree \(\le d_\Gamma\), then

\[
d_0=d_N+2d_H+2d_\Gamma.
\]

The near-pure O2/O3 reduction still gives

\[
D_{-n}
\notin
\operatorname{span}
\{D_{-n+1},\ldots,D_{-n+d_0}\}.
\]

The same finite moment theorem applies with

\[
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

So adding finitely many wall components changes only \(d_0\), not the structure of the O2/O3 proof.

---

## 6. Gate–1 closure with jet wall

If the jet wall is small on a block, then

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{C^2}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{C^0}
\]

is small after scale normalization. By JointFlatnessStability,

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2}
\le Q^C\varepsilon^\theta.
\]

But Gate–1 gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Therefore the jet wall cannot be too small:

\[
\boxed{
\int E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Thus, in rank two,

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 wall lower follows from Gate--1 plus JointFlatnessStability.}
}
\]

This is the cleanest downstream closure currently visible.

---

## 7. Remaining finite audits

The rank-two jet route now has the following concrete checklist:

### A. Live-fiber avoidance

\[
B_Y=0.
\]

This remains the primary algebraic blocker.

### B. D4 coefficient conditioning

\[
|c_7\alpha_9|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\beta_9|+|c_7|+|\alpha_9|\le Q^A.
\]

### C. Jet wall branch-charge

\[
d(D^j\Gamma_G),\ d(\Gamma_{G,2})=O(1),
\qquad j=0,1,2.
\]

### D. JointFlatnessStability

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{C^2}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{C^0}\ll1
\Rightarrow
\|q''\|_{L^2}\ll1.
\]

### E. O2/O3 with finite wall family

The bounded-charge graph theorem must accept the wall

\[
\sum_{G\in\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}}|G|^2.
\]

### F. Coherent amplitude Schur if needed

If \(\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}\neq0\), prove vector finite-model nonabsorption after O2/O3.

---

## Final result

The jet-enhanced rank-two wall appears compatible with bounded-charge O2/O3 because it adds only finitely many fixed wall components and should preserve \(d_0=O(1)\).

Thus the rank-two downstream closure can be:

\[
\boxed{
B_Y=0
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
\text{rank-two jet wall}
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
\text{bounded-charge O2/O3}
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
\text{small wall } \Rightarrow q''\text{ small}}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
\text{Gate--1 contradiction.}
}
\]

This further strengthens the case for prioritizing \(B_Y=0\) and JointFlatnessStability over the rank-one moving-wall hierarchy.

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), the wall does **not** use \(\rho_Y\) or \(\rho_\Gamma\). The target is the coercivity implication

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\text{ small}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\text{ small}.
\]

This is the analytic bridge from rank-two D4 wall failure to Gate–1 contradiction, as described in the current rank-two prompt. 

---

# 1. Normalization and exact identity

Use the current normalization

\[
\Gamma_G=-6q''+36q-12q^3.
\]

Define

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=-6(q''-f(q)).
\]

Set

\[
E_1=q''-f(q).
\]

Also

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=q^{(4)}-6(1-q^2)q''.
\]

Since

\[
f'(q)=6-6q^2,
\]

define

\[
E_2=q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Thus

\[
\Gamma_G=-6E_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=E_2.
\]

Now differentiate

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1.
\]

First derivative:

\[
q'''=f'(q)q'+E_1'.
\]

Second derivative:

\[
q^{(4)}
=
f''(q)(q')^2+f'(q)q''+E_1''.
\]

Subtracting \(f'(q)q''\), we get

\[
E_2
=
q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''
=
f''(q)(q')^2+E_1''.
\]

Because

\[
f''(q)=-12q,
\]

the exact identity is

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

This identity is the core of the rank-two coercivity mechanism.

---

# 2. Exact flatness

If

\[
E_1=0,
\qquad
E_2=0,
\]

then

\[
q(q')^2=0.
\]

On any connected subinterval where \(q\ne0\), this implies

\[
q'=0.
\]

Therefore

\[
q''=0.
\]

But \(E_1=0\) also gives

\[
q''=f(q)=6q-2q^3=2q(3-q^2).
\]

So the only exact flat solutions are

\[
q\equiv0,
\qquad
q\equiv\sqrt3,
\qquad
q\equiv-\sqrt3.
\]

In every case,

\[
q''\equiv0.
\]

Thus exact joint wall flatness contradicts any Gate–1 lower bound on \(\|q''\|_{L^2}\).

---

# 3. Approximate coercivity target

The theorem we want is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoCoercivity.}
}
\]

Let \(I\) be a chart-good interval with polynomial \(C^K\)-bounds for \(q\). If

\[
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}\le \delta,
\]

then for some fixed \(\theta>0\),

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\delta^\theta.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\le \delta
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\delta^\theta.
}
\]

This is stronger and more deterministic than a generic two-function sublevel theorem.

---

# 4. Distributional version of the key identity

From

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2,
\]

we obtain

\[
\|q(q')^2\|_{H^{-2}(I)}
\le
C\left(
\|E_2\|_{H^{-2}(I)}
+
\|E_1\|_{L^2(I)}
\right).
\]

If we assume the stronger norm

\[
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}\le\delta,
\]

then by Sobolev embedding on a one-dimensional chart-good interval, after scale normalization,

\[
\|E_1\|_{C^1(I)}+\|E_1''\|_{L^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}
\le Q^C\delta.
\]

So the identity gives

\[
\boxed{
\|q(q')^2\|_{L^2(I)}
\le Q^C\delta.
}
\]

This is the usable approximate replacement for

\[
q(q')^2=0.
\]

---

# 5. Region split: near and away from roots

The roots of

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3
\]

are

\[
Z=\{0,\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\}.
\]

Since these roots are simple,

\[
|f(q)|\asymp \operatorname{dist}(q,Z)
\]

on chart-good bounded \(q\)-ranges.

Because

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1,
\]

we can control \(q''\) by controlling \(f(q)\).

Split \(I\) into

\[
I_{\mathrm{near}}=\{x:\operatorname{dist}(q(x),Z)\le\eta\}
\]

and

\[
I_{\mathrm{far}}=\{x:\operatorname{dist}(q(x),Z)>\eta\}.
\]

On \(I_{\mathrm{near}}\),

\[
|f(q)|\le C\eta,
\]

so

\[
|q''|\le C\eta+|E_1|.
\]

Hence

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{near}})}
\le
C\eta |I|^{1/2}+Q^C\delta.
\]

---

# 6. Away from roots: acceleration–velocity control

On \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\),

\[
|f(q)|\ge c\eta.
\]

If \(q''=f(q)+E_1\), then except where \(E_1\) is large,

\[
|q''|\gtrsim \eta.
\]

This means \(q'\) must change at speed \(\gtrsim\eta\).

But from

\[
\|q(q')^2\|_{L^2}\le Q^C\delta,
\]

and away from the root \(q=0\) we have \(|q|\gtrsim \eta\) except near the \(\pm\sqrt3\) roots, we get an averaged smallness estimate for \(q'\):

\[
\|q'\|_{L^4(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
Q^C\delta^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2}.
\]

The remaining real-variable lemma needed is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{AccelerationVelocityLemma.}
}
\]

If on an interval \(J\),

\[
q''=f(q)+e,
\qquad
|f(q)|\ge \eta,
\]

and

\[
\|q'\|_{L^4(J)}
\le M,
\qquad
\|e\|_{L^2(J)}\le \delta,
\]

then

\[
|J|
\le
Q^C\left(
M^2\eta^{-2}
+
\delta^2\eta^{-2}
\right).
\]

In words: a function cannot have acceleration bounded below by \(\eta\) over a thick interval while its velocity remains small.

Applying this to the far region gives

\[
|I_{\mathrm{far}}|
\le
Q^C\delta^\theta\eta^{-C}.
\]

Then

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
Q^C|I_{\mathrm{far}}|^{1/2}
\le
Q^C\delta^\theta\eta^{-C}.
\]

Choose

\[
\eta=\delta^\kappa
\]

with \(\kappa>0\) small enough. Combining near and far regions yields

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le Q^C\delta^{\theta'}
}
\]

for some fixed \(\theta'>0\).

That proves the intended coercivity, modulo the stated acceleration–velocity lemma and chart-good Sobolev controls.

---

# 7. Wall norm needed for D4

The coercivity theorem naturally uses

\[
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}.
\]

Since

\[
E_1=-\frac16\Gamma_G,
\qquad
E_2=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

the required wall norm is

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}.
}
\]

Thus the clean D4 wall is the jet-enhanced vector wall

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D^2\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right),
}
\]

where \(D\) is the scale-normalized derivative.

This wall is directly compatible with RankTwoCoercivity.

---

# 8. Plain wall plus Markov alternative

If a local Markov/Sobolev estimate is available:

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)},
\]

then the plain vector wall

\[
|H|^2(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2)
\]

is enough.

But absent such a Markov upgrade, the jet wall is safer.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Default: use the jet-enhanced vector wall.}
}
\]

The branch-charge increase is finite and should remain \(O(1)\).

---

# 9. Gate–1 closure

Gate–1 supplies

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

RankTwoCoercivity gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta.
\]

Therefore

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

So the rank-two jet wall has polynomial mass.

This proves:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate--1 + RankTwoCoercivity}
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-two D4 wall lower}.
}
\]

---

# 10. Remaining analytic gaps

The exact algebraic identity is solid, subject to final sign normalization. Remaining gaps are real-analysis details:

1. Prove the AccelerationVelocityLemma in the precise scaled \(L^2/L^4\) norms.

2. Establish chart-good Sobolev embeddings and polynomial derivative bounds.

3. Decide whether the wall is measured in \(H^2/L^2\) directly or obtained from a plain wall by Markov.

4. Handle coherent vector amplitude models by replacing \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) with its distance to the model, if needed.

5. Verify scale-normalized derivatives in the local coordinate used by Gate–1.

---

## Final result

The rank-two wall coercivity theorem is now sharply formulated:

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2}
\text{ small}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|q''\|_{L^2}\text{ small}.
}
\]

The key identity is

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

This gives the rank-two downstream closure:

\[
B_Y=0
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-two vector/jet wall}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate--1 contradiction if wall fails}.
\]

So the analytic part of the rank-two route is now plausible, with the main remaining issue being a standard one-dimensional acceleration–velocity stability lemma.

\qquad

\qquad

For the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), these wall-ratio variables are not used. The wall is

\[
F_{2Y}\asymp H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

The goal is to prove the coercivity step:

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2}\text{ small}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|q''\|_{L^2}\text{ small},
\]

so that Gate–1 rules out rank-two wall failure. This is exactly the rank-two coercivity/gate closure direction identified in the latest architecture.

## 1. Exact algebraic core

Use

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Define

\[
E_1=q''-f(q),
\]

\[
E_2=q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=-6E_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=E_2.
\]

The exact identity is

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=f''(q)(q')^2=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

Thus joint smallness of \(\Gamma_G\) and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\), with two derivatives of \(\Gamma_G\), controls

\[
q(q')^2.
\]

This is what makes the rank-two branch fundamentally stronger than the rank-one moving-line branch.

---

## 2. Strong pointwise version of the lemma

First prove the clean pointwise form.

Assume on a chart-good interval \(I\):

\[
\|E_1\|_{C^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{C^0(I)}\le \varepsilon,
\]

and \(q\) has polynomial \(C^3\)-bounds.

Then

\[
|q|\,|q'|^2\le C\varepsilon.
\]

Let

\[
Z=\{0,\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\}.
\]

Since

\[
f(q)=2q(3-q^2),
\]

the roots are simple, so on chart-good bounded \(q\)-ranges,

\[
|f(q)|\asymp \operatorname{dist}(q,Z).
\]

Split \(I\) into

\[
I_{\mathrm{near}}=\{\operatorname{dist}(q,Z)\le \eta\},
\]

\[
I_{\mathrm{far}}=\{\operatorname{dist}(q,Z)>\eta\}.
\]

On \(I_{\mathrm{near}}\),

\[
|q''|
\le |f(q)|+|E_1|
\le C\eta+C\varepsilon.
\]

On \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\), we have \(|f(q)|\gtrsim\eta\). Since

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1,
\]

the acceleration satisfies \(|q''|\gtrsim\eta\) except for a harmless \(\varepsilon\)-error.

Also, away from \(Z\), in particular away from \(q=0\),

\[
|q|\gtrsim \eta,
\]

so

\[
|q'|\le C\varepsilon^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2}.
\]

A function cannot have acceleration \(\gtrsim\eta\) for long while its velocity remains bounded by \(C\varepsilon^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2}\). Quantitatively, each connected far component has length

\[
\lesssim \varepsilon^{1/2}\eta^{-3/2}
\]

up to polynomial chart constants. With polynomial finite-oscillation control, the total far measure is

\[
|I_{\mathrm{far}}|\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}\eta^{-3/2}.
\]

Therefore,

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le Q^C |I_{\mathrm{far}}|^{1/2}
\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/4}\eta^{-3/4}.
\]

On the near set,

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{near}})}
\le Q^C(\eta+\varepsilon)|I|^{1/2}.
\]

Choose

\[
\eta=\varepsilon^{1/7}.
\]

Then both contributions are polynomial powers of \(\varepsilon\), giving

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/7}|I|^{1/2}.
}
\]

The exponent is not important. Any fixed positive exponent is enough.

---

## 3. Acceleration–velocity lemma

The real-variable lemma used above can be stated as follows.

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{AccelerationVelocityLemma.}
}
\]

Let \(J\subset I\). Suppose

\[
q''=F+e
\]

on \(J\), with

\[
|F|\ge \eta,
\qquad
\|e\|_{L^\infty(J)}\le \eta/4,
\]

and

\[
|q'|\le M
\]

on \(J\). Then each connected component of \(J\) has length

\[
\le C M/\eta.
\]

Proof: on a component, \(q''\) has fixed sign after subdividing into \(O(Q^C)\) sign-controlled intervals, or more generally after a polynomial finite-type partition. Then \(q'\) changes by at least \(\eta |J|/2\), but \(|q'|\le M\). Hence

\[
|J|\le C M/\eta.
\]

In our case,

\[
M\sim \varepsilon^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2},
\]

so

\[
|J|\lesssim \varepsilon^{1/2}\eta^{-3/2}.
\]

This is the missing one-dimensional estimate.

---

## 4. Sobolev version

The D4 wall is naturally \(L^2\)-based, not pointwise. So the more useful theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}\le \delta
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\le Q^C\delta^\theta.
}
\]

To reduce this to the pointwise argument, use one of two routes.

### Route A: Sobolev embedding on normalized atoms

On a one-dimensional interval, scale-normalized \(H^2\) control gives \(C^1\) control, and with one extra derivative or a finite-dimensional Markov bound gives \(C^2\)-type control on \(E_1\). Then the pointwise proof applies.

This requires either

\[
\|E_1\|_{H^3}
\]

or finite-band/finite-jet control of \(E_1\).

### Route B: subinterval selection

If only

\[
\|E_1\|_{H^2}+\|E_2\|_{L^2}
\]

is small, then on most subintervals of a polynomial partition the localized \(C^2/C^0\) norms are small after applying Markov/Sobolev estimates. Apply the pointwise argument on those subintervals and absorb the bad subintervals by measure loss.

This is probably sufficient for the proof architecture, since all losses may be polynomial.

---

## 5. Required wall norm

Because the identity uses \(E_1''\), the direct wall norm is

\[
\|E_1\|_{H^2}+\|E_2\|_{L^2}.
\]

Since

\[
E_1=-\frac16\Gamma_G,
\qquad
E_2=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

the direct wall is the jet-enhanced rank-two wall:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D^2\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right),
}
\]

with \(D\) the scale-normalized derivative.

This is the safest version. A plain wall

\[
|H|^2(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2)
\]

is enough only if a local Markov theorem gives

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2}\le Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2}.
\]

---

## 6. RankTwoCoercivity theorem

The theorem to use downstream is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoCoercivity.}
}
\]

On a chart-good interval \(I\), assume polynomial finite-jet bounds. Then

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta.
}
\]

Consequently, Gate–1,

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A},
\]

implies

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Thus the rank-two jet wall has polynomial mass.

---

## 7. Consequence for the rank-two D4 route

If \(B_Y=0\), D4 gives

\[
F_{2Y}\asymp H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

Using the jet-enhanced wall,

\[
F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}}
\asymp
H(\Gamma_G,D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

the wall lower follows from Gate–1 and RankTwoCoercivity.

So the rank-two downstream chain is:

\[
\boxed{
B_Y=0
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
\text{rank-two D4 vector/jet wall}
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
\text{small wall}\Rightarrow q''\text{ small}
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
\text{Gate--1 contradiction}.
}
\]

This bypasses the rank-one moving-line finite-type and forced-ODE trap.

---

## 8. Remaining analytic gaps

The exact identity is settled modulo final sign normalization:

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
\]

The remaining proof details are:

1. establish the acceleration–velocity lemma with the correct scaled norms;

2. decide whether to use pointwise \(C^2/C^0\), \(H^2/L^2\), or a finite-dimensional Markov upgrade;

3. ensure chart-good bounds prevent infinitely many oscillatory far-region components;

4. verify that \(D\) in the jet wall is the correct scale-normalized derivative for the Gate–1 interval;

5. if finite coherent vector amplitude spaces remain, apply the same coercivity to the residual after vector amplitude Schur, not to a locally fitted projection.

---

## Final result

The rank-two coercivity path is robust.

The key identity

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2
}
\]

turns joint flatness of

\[
(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

into smallness of \(q''\).

Therefore, once \(B_Y=0\) is proved, the downstream D4 wall lower can be obtained from Gate–1 through a deterministic one-dimensional coercivity lemma, preferably using the jet-enhanced rank-two wall.

with

---

# 1. Correct norm for the coercivity theorem

The pointwise version used

\[
\|E_1\|_{C^2}+\|E_2\|_{C^0}.
\]

For the D4/O2O3 stack, a more natural norm is

\[
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}.
\]

The theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta
}
\]

on a chart-good interval \(I\), with scale-normalized Sobolev norms and polynomial finite-jet bounds.

Because

\[
E_1=-\frac16\Gamma_G,
\qquad
E_2=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

this becomes

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta.
}
\]

Gate–1 then forces the rank-two jet wall to have polynomial mass.

---

# 2. From \(H^2/L^2\) smallness to control of \(q(q')^2\)

Assume

\[
\delta
=
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}
\ll 1.
\]

The identity gives

\[
q(q')^2
=
-\frac1{12}(E_2-E_1'').
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\|q(q')^2\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
C\delta.
}
\]

This is already strong enough for a measure-based argument; we do not need pointwise smallness.

---

# 3. Near-root region

Let

\[
Z=\{0,\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\},
\]

the zero set of

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

For a parameter \(\eta>0\), define

\[
I_{\mathrm{near}}=\{x\in I:\operatorname{dist}(q(x),Z)\le \eta\}.
\]

Since the roots are simple and \(q\) is chart-good bounded,

\[
|f(q)|\le C\eta
\]

on \(I_{\mathrm{near}}\). Therefore

\[
|q''|
\le |f(q)|+|E_1|
\le C\eta+|E_1|.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{near}})}
\le
C\eta |I|^{1/2}+\|E_1\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
C\eta |I|^{1/2}+\delta.
}
\]

---

# 4. Far-root region

Let

\[
I_{\mathrm{far}}=I\setminus I_{\mathrm{near}}.
\]

On \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\),

\[
|f(q)|\ge c\eta.
\]

Also, away from \(Z\), either \(|q|\gtrsim\eta\) or we are near the zero root; but the zero root region was included in \(I_{\mathrm{near}}\). Hence on \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\),

\[
|q|\ge c\eta.
\]

From

\[
\|q(q')^2\|_{L^2(I)}\le C\delta
\]

we get

\[
\|(q')^2\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
C\delta \eta^{-1},
\]

hence

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^4(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
C\delta^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2}.
}
\]

This is the velocity smallness needed on the far region.

---

# 5. Far region cannot be thick

On \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\), we have

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1,
\]

with \(|f(q)|\ge c\eta\).

The only way \(q''\) fails to be large is if \(E_1\) cancels \(f(q)\). But \(\|E_1\|_{H^2}\le \delta\) implies \(E_1\) is small except on a small set. In one dimension, Sobolev embedding gives

\[
\|E_1\|_{L^\infty(I)}
\le
Q^C\delta
\]

in scale-normalized coordinates. For \(\delta\ll \eta\), this yields

\[
|q''|\ge c\eta/2
\]

on \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\).

Now use the acceleration–velocity argument. On a connected component \(J\subset I_{\mathrm{far}}\), if \(q''\) has fixed sign, then

\[
|q'(b)-q'(a)|\ge c\eta |J|.
\]

But the \(L^4\) bound on \(q'\) implies, by Hölder,

\[
|q'(b)-q'(a)|
\le
2\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J)}
\]

in the pointwise version. If we only have \(L^4\), use the following integrated variant:

Since \(|q''|\ge c\eta\), \(q'\) changes monotonically on sign-controlled subcomponents, and the \(L^4\)-mass of \(q'\) on a component of length \(L\) is at least

\[
c\eta^4 L^5
\]

(up to constants; this is the \(L^4\)-norm of a ramp with slope \(\eta\)). Therefore

\[
\eta^4 L^5
\le
C\|q'\|_{L^4(J)}^4.
\]

Summing over polynomially many sign-controlled components gives

\[
|I_{\mathrm{far}}|
\le
Q^C
\eta^{-4/5}
\|q'\|_{L^4(I_{\mathrm{far}})}^{4/5}.
\]

Using

\[
\|q'\|_{L^4(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
C\delta^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2},
\]

we obtain

\[
\boxed{
|I_{\mathrm{far}}|
\le
Q^C \delta^{2/5}\eta^{-6/5}.
}
\]

The exponents are not important; any positive powers suffice.

Then, using polynomial chart bounds on \(q''\),

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
Q^C |I_{\mathrm{far}}|^{1/2}
\le
Q^C\delta^{1/5}\eta^{-3/5}.
}
\]

---

# 6. Optimize \(\eta\)

Combining near and far estimates:

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
C\eta |I|^{1/2}
+
\delta
+
Q^C\delta^{1/5}\eta^{-3/5}.
\]

Choose

\[
\eta=\delta^\kappa
\]

with \(0<\kappa<1/3\), for example \(\kappa=1/8\). Then every term is bounded by a positive power of \(\delta\):

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\delta^\theta |I|^{1/2}
}
\]

for some fixed \(\theta>0\).

This proves the desired coercivity in scale-normalized form, modulo sign-partition/finite-oscillation control.

---

# 7. Finite-oscillation control

The above proof assumes \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\) can be divided into polynomially many components on which \(q''\) has controlled sign. This follows from either:

1. polynomial \(C^K\) bounds plus finite-type nondegeneracy of \(f(q)+E_1\); or

2. a standard one-dimensional decomposition into monotonicity intervals with polynomial loss; or

3. using the integrated ramp argument locally via a covering lemma rather than explicit sign intervals.

For the proof architecture, it is enough to include this as a chart-good regularity hypothesis:

\[
\boxed{
q\text{ has polynomial finite-oscillation/finite-type bounds on }I.
}
\]

This is already consistent with the controlled finite-jet setup of the local branch analysis.

---

# 8. Rank-two wall energy

The coercivity theorem uses

\[
\delta=
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}
=
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\]

up to constants. Therefore the wall should be the jet wall:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D^2\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
}
\]

Here \(D\) is the scale-normalized local derivative.

Then small rank-two jet wall implies small \(\delta\), hence small \(q''\), contradicting Gate–1.

---

# 9. Consequence

The final rank-two analytic module is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoCoercivity.}
}
\]

If

\[
\delta=
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)},
\]

then

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\delta^\theta.
\]

Thus Gate–1,

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A},
\]

forces

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

Therefore rank-two D4 has wall mass.

---

## Final result

The acceleration–velocity gap can be closed with the identity

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2
\]

and a one-dimensional far/near root decomposition.

This justifies the rank-two chain:

\[
B_Y=0
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-two jet wall}
\Rightarrow
\text{small wall forces }q''\text{ small}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate--1 contradiction}.
\]

The remaining analytic burden is now standard: scale-normalized Sobolev/finite-oscillation control on chart-good intervals.

Continuing Agent 5 — compactness proof of RankTwoCoercivity.

\qquad

\qquad

\]

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), these do not enter the wall. The wall is controlled by

\[
(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

The current goal is to prove the coercivity statement

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta,
\]

so that Gate–1 forces rank-two wall mass. This is the analytic closure identified in the current rank-two architecture. 

---

## 1. Normalize the problem

Work on a normalized chart interval

\[
I=[-1,1].
\]

Use the current formulas

\[
\Gamma_G=-6q''+36q-12q^3,
\]

and define

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Set

\[
E_1=q''-f(q),
\]

\[
E_2=q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=-6E_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=E_2.
\]

The exact identity is

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

---

## 2. Compactness coercivity lemma

A clean formulation is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{NormalizedRankTwoCoercivity.}
}
\]

Fix a chart-good bound

\[
\|q\|_{H^4(I)}\le M.
\]

Then there exists a modulus

\[
\omega_M(\delta)\to0
\quad\text{as}\quad
\delta\to0
\]

such that if

\[
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}\le\delta,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\le \omega_M(\delta).
}
\]

For proof architecture, it is enough that

\[
\omega_M(\delta)\le Q^C\delta^\theta
\]

after quantitative refinement or finite-type/Markov control. But the compactness lemma already proves the key structural fact:

\[
(E_1,E_2)\to0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
q''\to0.
\]

---

## 3. Compactness proof

Assume the theorem is false. Then there exists a sequence \(q_n\) with

\[
\|q_n\|_{H^4}\le M,
\]

\[
\|E_{1,n}\|_{H^2}+\|E_{2,n}\|_{L^2}\to0,
\]

but

\[
\|q_n''\|_{L^2}\ge c_0>0.
\]

By compactness,

\[
q_n\to q_\infty
\]

strongly in \(H^3\) and weakly in \(H^4\), after passing to a subsequence.

Since

\[
E_{1,n}=q_n''-f(q_n)\to0
\quad\text{in }H^2,
\]

we get

\[
q_\infty''=f(q_\infty)
\]

in \(H^2\).

Since

\[
E_{2,n}=q_n^{(4)}-f'(q_n)q_n''\to0
\quad\text{in }L^2,
\]

we get

\[
q_\infty^{(4)}=f'(q_\infty)q_\infty''
\]

in distributions.

But from

\[
q_\infty''=f(q_\infty),
\]

differentiate twice:

\[
q_\infty^{(4)}
=
f''(q_\infty)(q_\infty')^2
+
f'(q_\infty)f(q_\infty).
\]

Since

\[
q_\infty''=f(q_\infty),
\]

the second equation says

\[
q_\infty^{(4)}
=
f'(q_\infty)f(q_\infty).
\]

Subtract:

\[
f''(q_\infty)(q_\infty')^2=0.
\]

Because

\[
f''(q)=-12q,
\]

we have

\[
q_\infty(q_\infty')^2=0.
\]

Thus \(q_\infty\) is locally constant on \(\{q_\infty\ne0\}\), and on \(\{q_\infty=0\}\) we also have \(q_\infty''=f(0)=0\). Therefore

\[
q_\infty''=0
\]

almost everywhere.

But \(q_n''\to q_\infty''\) strongly in \(L^2\), so

\[
\|q_n''\|_{L^2}\to0,
\]

contradicting

\[
\|q_n''\|_{L^2}\ge c_0.
\]

Therefore the compactness coercivity lemma holds.

---

## 4. Quantitative version

For the proof stack, compactness should be upgraded to a polynomial modulus. The likely theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta.
}
\]

A route to a polynomial modulus:

1. use the exact identity

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2;
\]

2. derive

\[
\|q(q')^2\|_{L^2}\le C\delta;
\]

3. split \(I\) into neighborhoods of

\[
Z=\{0,\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\}
\]

and its complement;

4. on the near-root set, use

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1
\]

and \(|f(q)|\lesssim\operatorname{dist}(q,Z)\);

5. on the far set, use the acceleration–velocity lemma to show the far set has small measure, because \(q''=f(q)+E_1\) has acceleration bounded below while \(q'\) is controlled by \(q(q')^2\);

6. optimize the root-neighborhood radius.

This gives a fixed exponent \(\theta>0\) under polynomial chart-good bounds.

---

## 5. Scale-normalized form

On a physical interval

\[
I_m=m+\lambda[-1,1],
\]

let

\[
D_I=\lambda\,\partial_t
\]

be the scale-normalized derivative. The wall norm should use

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2_I}
=
\sum_{j=0}^2 \|D_I^j\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I_m)}.
\]

The rank-two coercivity statement becomes

\[
\boxed{
\|D_I^2 q\|_{L^2(I_m)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2_I}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I_m)}
\right)^\theta.
}
\]

This is the scale-correct form needed to align with Gate–1’s local \(L^2\)-energy.

---

## 6. Wall energy required

The natural rank-two D4 wall is therefore the jet wall:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D_I\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D_I^2\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
}
\]

If

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
\]

were too small on a Gate–1-good interval, then RankTwoCoercivity gives

\[
\|D_I^2q\|_{L^2}
\]

small, contradicting Gate–1.

Thus rank-two wall lower follows deterministically from Gate–1.

---

## 7. Plain wall alternative

A plain vector wall

\[
|H|^2(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2)
\]

is sufficient only if we also prove a local Markov/Sobolev upgrade:

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2_I}
\le
Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}.
\]

This may hold if \(\Gamma_G\) belongs to a finite-dimensional local source class or a controlled bandlimited class. But until that is proved, the jet wall is the safer default.

---

## 8. Interaction with O2/O3

The jet wall adds finitely many components:

\[
\Gamma_G,\quad D_I\Gamma_G,\quad D_I^2\Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

This should preserve bounded branch-charge:

\[
d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{jet}}
=
\max\{
d(\Gamma_G),d(D_I\Gamma_G),d(D_I^2\Gamma_G),d(\Gamma_{G,2})
\}
=
O(1).
\]

So O2/O3 can use

\[
W_{\mathrm{bd}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
N_{\mathrm{sm}}E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}},
\]

with

\[
d_0^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
d_N+2d_H+2d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{jet}}.
\]

The near-pure moment theorem then runs with \(d_0^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}\), still fixed.

---

## 9. If coherent vector amplitudes remain

If

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}\ne0,
\]

then the jet wall should be interpreted modulo a finite coherent vector/jet model:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}},
\mathcal C_{2Y,\mathrm{jet}}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)^2.
\]

The same compactness/coercivity applies to the residual only if the coherent model is fixed/finite and not locally free. If the coherent model is locally free, rank-two fails at the amplitude layer.

---

## Final conclusion

The compactness proof confirms the analytic heart of the rank-two branch:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G\to0\text{ in }H^2,\quad
\Gamma_{G,2}\to0\text{ in }L^2
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
q''\to0\text{ in }L^2.
}
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
B_Y=0
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-two jet wall}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate--1 wall lower}.
}
\]

The main remaining rank-two tasks are now algebraic/local:

1. prove \(B_Y=0\);
2. verify the D4 coefficient conditioning;
3. confirm jet wall bounded branch-charge;
4. handle any finite coherent vector amplitude space by vector/jet amplitude Schur.

\]

and the target is the quantitative coercivity theorem

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le

\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+

This is the analytic half of the current rank-two route: typed exactness gives \(B_Y=0\), rank-two D4 gives the vector wall, and this coercivity theorem lets Gate–1 force wall mass.

# Agent 5 — RankTwoCoercivity

## 1. Normalization and identity

Using the current normalization,

\[
\Gamma_G=-6q''+36q-12q^3.
\]

Define

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=-6(q''-f(q)).
\]

Set

\[
E_1=q''-f(q).
\]

Also,

\[
f'(q)=6-6q^2,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=q^{(4)}-6(1-q^2)q''
=
q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Set

\[
E_2=q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Thus

\[
\Gamma_G=-6E_1,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=E_2.
\]

Differentiate

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1.
\]

Then

\[
q'''=f'(q)q'+E_1',
\]

and

\[
q^{(4)}
=
f''(q)(q')^2+f'(q)q''+E_1''.
\]

Subtracting \(f'(q)q''\),

\[
E_2=f''(q)(q')^2+E_1''.
\]

Since

\[
f''(q)=-12q,
\]

the exact identity is

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

This identity is the core of the rank-two coercivity mechanism.

---

## 2. Exact flatness

If

\[
E_1=0,\qquad E_2=0
\]

on an interval, then

\[
q(q')^2=0.
\]

On any connected component where \(q\neq 0\), this gives

\[
q'=0.
\]

Then

\[
q''=0.
\]

But \(E_1=0\) also gives

\[
q''=f(q)=2q(3-q^2).
\]

So the constant possibilities are

\[
q\equiv0,\qquad q\equiv \sqrt 3,\qquad q\equiv-\sqrt3,
\]

and in all cases

\[
q''\equiv0.
\]

Therefore exact joint wall flatness implies no Gate–1 energy.

---

## 3. Compactness coercivity

A robust qualitative theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{CompactRankTwoCoercivity.}
}
\]

Let \(I\) be a normalized chart-good interval. Suppose

\[
\|q_n\|_{H^4(I)}\le M,
\]

\[
E_{1,n}\to0\quad\text{in }H^2(I),
\]

\[
E_{2,n}\to0\quad\text{in }L^2(I).
\]

Then

\[
q_n''\to0\quad\text{in }L^2(I).
\]

Proof: by compactness, pass to a subsequence

\[
q_n\to q_\infty
\]

strongly in \(H^3\) and weakly in \(H^4\). The limits satisfy

\[
q_\infty''=f(q_\infty)
\]

and

\[
q_\infty^{(4)}=f'(q_\infty)q_\infty''.
\]

Differentiating \(q_\infty''=f(q_\infty)\) twice gives

\[
q_\infty^{(4)}
=
f''(q_\infty)(q_\infty')^2+f'(q_\infty)f(q_\infty).
\]

Since \(q_\infty''=f(q_\infty)\), comparison with the second equation gives

\[
f''(q_\infty)(q_\infty')^2=0.
\]

Thus

\[
q_\infty(q_\infty')^2=0,
\]

so by the exact-flatness argument

\[
q_\infty''=0.
\]

Strong convergence in \(H^3\) gives

\[
q_n''\to0
\]

in \(L^2\). Contradiction if \(\|q_n''\|_{L^2}\ge c_0\).

This proves structural coercivity and rules out a hidden rank-two analogue of the rank-one ODE trap.

---

## 4. Quantitative theorem

The proof stack needs a polynomial version:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoCoercivity.}
}
\]

On a chart-good interval \(I\), assume scale-normalized finite-jet bounds

\[
\|q\|_{H^K(I)}\le Q^C
\]

for some fixed \(K\) large enough. Let

\[
\delta=
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}.
\]

Then for some fixed \(\theta>0\),

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\delta^\theta.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta.
}
\]

---

## 5. Quantitative proof skeleton

From the identity,

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2,
\]

we get

\[
\|q(q')^2\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
C\delta.
\]

Let

\[
Z=\{0,\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\}.
\]

These are simple roots of

\[
f(q)=2q(3-q^2).
\]

On chart-good bounded \(q\)-ranges,

\[
|f(q)|\asymp \operatorname{dist}(q,Z).
\]

Fix \(\eta>0\) and split

\[
I_{\mathrm{near}}
=
\{x:\operatorname{dist}(q(x),Z)\le\eta\},
\]

\[
I_{\mathrm{far}}
=
I\setminus I_{\mathrm{near}}.
\]

On \(I_{\mathrm{near}}\),

\[
|f(q)|\le C\eta,
\]

and since

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1,
\]

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{near}})}
\le
C\eta |I|^{1/2}+\|E_1\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
C\eta |I|^{1/2}+\delta.
\]

On \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\),

\[
|f(q)|\ge c\eta.
\]

Also \(q\) is away from the zero root, so

\[
|q|\ge c\eta.
\]

The bound on \(q(q')^2\) gives

\[
\|q'\|_{L^4(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
C\delta^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2}.
\]

Since

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1,
\]

and \(E_1\) is small in \(H^2\), Sobolev/Markov control gives \(E_1\) small pointwise outside a polynomially negligible set. Hence on most of \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\),

\[
|q''|\gtrsim \eta.
\]

Now use the one-dimensional acceleration–velocity lemma:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If } |q''|\gtrsim\eta
\text{ on an interval while }
\|q'\|_{L^4}\le M,
\text{ then the interval has length }
\lesssim Q^C M^{4/5}\eta^{-4/5}.
}
\]

The exponent is not important; what matters is a positive power. Applying this with

\[
M\le C\delta^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2}
\]

yields

\[
|I_{\mathrm{far}}|
\le
Q^C\delta^{2/5}\eta^{-6/5}.
\]

Using chart-good bounds for \(q''\),

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
Q^C |I_{\mathrm{far}}|^{1/2}
\le
Q^C\delta^{1/5}\eta^{-3/5}.
\]

Combining,

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
C\eta
+
\delta
+
Q^C\delta^{1/5}\eta^{-3/5}.
\]

Choose

\[
\eta=\delta^\kappa
\]

with a small fixed \(\kappa>0\). Then

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\delta^\theta
\]

for some fixed \(\theta>0\).

This is the desired quantitative coercivity, modulo the standard acceleration–velocity and finite-oscillation lemmas.

---

## 6. Auxiliary lemmas needed

The proof needs three auxiliary facts.

### Lemma A: Sobolev/Markov control of \(E_1\)

From

\[
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}\le\delta,
\]

obtain enough pointwise or localized control to prevent \(E_1\) from canceling \(f(q)\) on a thick subset of \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\). This follows from one-dimensional Sobolev embedding on normalized atoms, or from a local Markov/Remez inequality for the finite source class.

### Lemma B: AccelerationVelocityLemma

If \(q'\) is small in \(L^4\) and \(q''\) is bounded below on a sign-controlled or finite-type component, then that component has small measure.

A convenient version:

If

\[
|q''|\ge \eta
\]

on a component \(J\) and \(q''\) has controlled sign/finite oscillation, then

\[
|J|\le Q^C\eta^{-4/5}\|q'\|_{L^4(J)}^{4/5}.
\]

### Lemma C: finite-oscillation decomposition

The far region can be partitioned into polynomially many components on which the acceleration argument applies. This is a chart-good finite-type/Markov condition.

These are standard one-dimensional real-variable inputs, not new zeta arithmetic.

---

## 7. Wall energy required

The coercivity theorem naturally requires

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}.
\]

Therefore the default rank-two D4 wall should be jet-enhanced:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D^2\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right),
}
\]

where \(D\) is the scale-normalized local derivative.

A plain wall

\[
|H|^2(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2)
\]

is enough only if a LocalMarkov theorem supplies

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}.
\]

Until that is proved, the jet wall is the safer default.

---

## 8. Gate–1 closure

Gate–1 gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

RankTwoCoercivity gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta.
\]

Therefore

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

So the rank-two jet wall has polynomial mass.

Thus the rank-two D4 downstream wall lower follows from:

\[
\boxed{
B_Y=0
+
\text{D4 coefficient conditioning}
+
\text{RankTwoCoercivity}
+
\text{Gate--1}.
}
\]

---

## Final result

The analytic rank-two closure is now proof-quality modulo standard one-dimensional auxiliary lemmas:

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2
}
\]

gives

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2}
\text{ small}
\Rightarrow
\|q''\|_{L^2}\text{ small}.
}
\]

Therefore, if \(B_Y=0\), rank-two D4 wall failure contradicts Gate–1. The moving-line and forced-ODE trap machinery is unnecessary in the rank-two branch.

## Assistant (2026-04-28 13:08:46)

I’ll continue by stress-testing the coercivity proof rather than assuming the acceleration–velocity step for free. The main issue is whether many small oscillatory acceleration intervals can evade the \(L^4\)-velocity bound.

_Thought for 28s_

Continuing Agent 5 — stress test and repair of the RankTwoCoercivity proof.

The rank-two route depends on the implication

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\text{ small}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\text{ small}.
\]

Using

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

\[
E_1=q''-f(q),
\qquad
E_2=q^{(4)}-f'(q)q'',
\]

we have

\[
\Gamma_G=-6E_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=E_2,
\]

and the exact identity

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

The compactness version is solid. The quantitative version needs one extra guardrail: finite oscillation, or an equivalent Remez/Markov control. Without that, many tiny alternating acceleration intervals could in principle evade a naive pointwise acceleration–velocity estimate.

---

## 1. The gap in the naive acceleration–velocity proof

From

\[
\|E_1\|_{H^2}+\|E_2\|_{L^2}\le \delta,
\]

we get

\[
\|q(q')^2\|_{L^2}\le C\delta.
\]

Away from the roots

\[
Z=\{0,\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\},
\]

this gives an \(L^4\)-bound on \(q'\). Also,

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1
\]

and \(|f(q)|\gtrsim \eta\) away from \(Z\). The tempting argument is: if acceleration is large and velocity is small, the region must be short.

That argument is correct on sign-controlled intervals. But if the far region decomposes into many tiny intervals with alternating acceleration, a purely local pointwise proof needs a bound on the number or complexity of those intervals.

So the quantitative theorem needs one of these hypotheses:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite oscillation / finite type / Remez control for }q\text{ on chart-good intervals.}
}
\]

This is not a new arithmetic input; it is a local regularity assumption already implicit in the finite-jet framework.

---

## 2. Correct quantitative coercivity theorem

A proof-usable statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoCoercivity}_{\mathrm{ft}}.
}
\]

Let \(I\) be a scale-normalized chart-good interval. Assume:

1. polynomial finite-jet bounds:

\[
\|q\|_{C^K(I)}\le Q^C
\]

for fixed \(K\);

2. finite oscillation / Remez control: for every \(\eta\ge Q^{-C}\), the set

\[
\{x:\operatorname{dist}(q(x),\{0,\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\})>\eta\}
\]

has at most \(Q^C\eta^{-C}\) sign/monotonicity components, or equivalently admits a polynomial-complexity decomposition on which \(f(q)\) has controlled sign;

3.

\[
\delta
=
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}
\]

is sufficiently small.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\delta^\theta
}
\]

for some fixed \(\theta>0\).

This is the right quantitative form.

---

## 3. Proof under finite oscillation

Let

\[
Z=\{0,\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\}.
\]

Choose

\[
\eta=\delta^\kappa
\]

with small fixed \(\kappa>0\), later optimized.

Split

\[
I_{\mathrm{near}}=\{x:\operatorname{dist}(q(x),Z)\le\eta\},
\]

\[
I_{\mathrm{far}}=I\setminus I_{\mathrm{near}}.
\]

### Near region

Since \(f\) has simple roots at \(Z\),

\[
|f(q)|\le C\eta
\]

on \(I_{\mathrm{near}}\). Therefore

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1
\]

gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{near}})}
\le
C\eta |I|^{1/2}+\|E_1\|_{L^2}
\le
C\eta |I|^{1/2}+\delta.
\]

### Far region

On \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\),

\[
|f(q)|\ge c\eta.
\]

Also, because \(q\) is away from all three roots, in particular away from \(0\),

\[
|q|\ge c\eta.
\]

The identity gives

\[
\|q(q')^2\|_{L^2}\le C\delta,
\]

so

\[
\|q'\|_{L^4(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
C\delta^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2}.
\]

Sobolev control gives \(E_1\) small outside a polynomially small exceptional set; after absorbing that set,

\[
|q''|=|f(q)+E_1|\ge c\eta
\]

on the main far set.

On each sign/monotonicity component \(J\), an acceleration–velocity estimate gives

\[
|J|
\le
Q^C
\eta^{-4/5}
\|q'\|_{L^4(J)}^{4/5}.
\]

Summing over at most \(Q^C\eta^{-C}\) such components gives

\[
|I_{\mathrm{far}}|
\le
Q^C
\delta^{\theta_1}
\eta^{-C}.
\]

Since \(\|q''\|_{L^\infty}\le Q^C\),

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
Q^C |I_{\mathrm{far}}|^{1/2}
\le
Q^C\delta^{\theta_2}\eta^{-C}.
\]

Choosing \(\eta=\delta^\kappa\) with \(\kappa\) small enough gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\delta^\theta.
\]

That proves the quantitative theorem.

---

## 4. A cleaner compactness-plus-Remez route

There is another way to package the proof.

The compactness argument shows:

\[
\delta\to0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|q''\|_{L^2}\to0
\]

on every compact class

\[
\|q\|_{H^K}\le M.
\]

To make this polynomial, use a Remez-type quantitative compactness lemma for the finite local source class:

\[
\boxed{
\text{if a controlled finite-type expression is }o(Q^{-A})
\text{ on polynomial mass, then it is }o(Q^{-A'})
\text{ in the required Sobolev norm.}
}
\]

This converts qualitative compactness into a polynomial modulus. In the current proof architecture, that is likely acceptable because all local source expressions are finite-jet/finite-complexity objects.

So the coercivity theorem can be proved either by:

- direct near/far acceleration estimates; or
- compactness plus quantitative Remez/Markov control.

The second route is cleaner for the paper.

---

## 5. Jet wall remains the safest default

Because the identity uses \(E_1''\), the wall norm must control

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2}.
\]

Therefore, unless we prove a Markov upgrade

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)},
\]

the correct wall is the jet-enhanced vector wall:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D^2\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
}
\]

Here \(D\) is the local scale-normalized derivative.

This is compatible with bounded-charge O2/O3 if the finite wall family

\[
\{\Gamma_G,D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}
\]

has branch-charge degree \(O(1)\).

---

## 6. Final rank-two analytic module

The analytic closure should be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoJetWallGate1Closure.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(B_Y=0\);

2. D4 coefficients are polynomially conditioned;

3. Gate–1 holds:

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A};
\]

4. chart-good finite oscillation / Remez / Markov control holds;

5. the rank-two jet wall is used.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

So rank-two D4 supplies wall mass without moving-line finite type or forced ODE trap.

---

## 7. Current status

The identity

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2
\]

is enough to prove qualitative coercivity. The only remaining issue is quantitative modulus.

The needed extra assumption is not RH-specific. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{chart-good finite oscillation / Remez / Markov control for local source expressions.}
}
\]

Once that is available, the rank-two analytic branch is closed:

\[
B_Y=0
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-two jet wall}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate--1 contradiction if wall is small}.
\]

Thus the main unresolved rank-two problem remains the local typed exactness theorem \(B_Y=0\), not the wall analysis.

Continuing Agent 5 — local Markov/Remez interface for rank-two coercivity.

with

\qquad

The previous step reduced the remaining analytic burden to finite-oscillation/Remez/Markov control. I’ll now state the cleanest interface.

---

# 1. The needed local regularity theorem

The rank-two coercivity proof becomes quantitative if we have the following.

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{LocalRemezMarkov}_{q,\Gamma}.
}
\]

On every chart-good normalized interval \(I\), every local scalar expression appearing in

\[
q,\quad q',\quad q'',\quad \Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}
\]

belongs to a finite-complexity class \(\mathscr A_I\) satisfying:

### M1. Markov derivative control

For \(F\in\mathscr A_I\),

\[
\|D^jF\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\|F\|_{L^2(I^*)},
\qquad 0\le j\le j_0,
\]

where \(I^*\) is a fixed enlargement of \(I\), \(D\) is the scale-normalized derivative, and \(j_0\) is fixed.

### M2. Remez/sublevel control

If \(F\in\mathscr A_I\) is not identically small, then for every \(\varepsilon>0\),

\[
\nu_I\{|F|<\varepsilon \|F\|_{L^\infty(I)}\}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta\nu_I(I).
\]

Equivalently, \(F\) cannot have arbitrarily many tiny oscillatory zero intervals.

### M3. Finite component bound

For every polynomial-scale threshold \(\eta\), the set

\[
\{x: |F(x)|>\eta\}
\]

has at most \(Q^C\eta^{-C}\) connected/sign-controlled components.

This is enough to justify the acceleration–velocity step used in RankTwoCoercivity.

---

# 2. What this buys

Assume

\[
\delta
=
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}
\]

is small.

The exact identity gives

\[
\|q(q')^2\|_{L^2(I)}\le C\delta.
\]

Split by distance to

\[
Z=\{0,\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\}.
\]

On

\[
I_{\rm near}=\{\operatorname{dist}(q,Z)\le \eta\},
\]

we have

\[
|f(q)|\le C\eta,
\qquad f(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

so

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\rm near})}
\le C\eta |I|^{1/2}+\delta.
\]

On

\[
I_{\rm far}=I\setminus I_{\rm near},
\]

we have

\[
|f(q)|\ge c\eta,
\qquad |q|\ge c\eta.
\]

Hence

\[
\|q'\|_{L^4(I_{\rm far})}
\le C\delta^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2}.
\]

Also,

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1.
\]

By M1/M2, \(E_1\) cannot cancel \(f(q)\) on a thick portion of \(I_{\rm far}\) unless \(E_1\) has comparable \(L^2\)-mass, which is excluded by small \(\delta\). Therefore, after removing a set of measure \(Q^C\delta^c\eta^{-C}\), one has

\[
|q''|\gtrsim \eta.
\]

Then the acceleration–velocity lemma plus M3 gives

\[
|I_{\rm far}|\le Q^C\delta^c\eta^{-C}.
\]

With chart-good \(C^K\)-bounds,

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\rm far})}
\le Q^C\delta^c\eta^{-C}.
\]

Choosing

\[
\eta=\delta^\kappa
\]

for small fixed \(\kappa>0\), we obtain

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le Q^C\delta^\theta.
}
\]

So LocalRemezMarkov gives the desired quantitative RankTwoCoercivity.

---

# 3. Why this is likely available

The relevant objects are not arbitrary smooth functions. They are local finite expressions built from:

\[
q,\quad q',\quad q'',\quad q^{(3)},\quad q^{(4)}
\]

and low algebraic operations inside chart-good regions.

In the paper architecture, these already live inside finite-dimensional local jet/exterior spaces with \(R^C\)-conditioning. Such spaces usually satisfy:

\[
\|D^jF\|\le R^C\|F\|
\]

or \(Q^C\)-loss analogues.

Thus LocalRemezMarkov is not a new arithmetic theorem. It is a local finite-complexity lemma for the same chart/Riesz classes already needed by O2/O3.

This is important: the rank-two analytic closure reuses O2/O3 regularity infrastructure.

---

# 4. Plain wall versus jet wall revisited

If LocalRemezMarkov gives

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)},
\]

then the plain wall

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2)}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)
\]

suffices.

If not, use the jet wall

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D^2\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
}
\]

The jet wall avoids depending on a Markov upgrade at the wall stage. It pushes the needed derivatives into the weight.

Since only finitely many fixed derivative components are added, the branch-charge bandwidth remains \(O(1)\), assuming the finite wall-family O2/O3 theorem.

Thus the robust default remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use finite-wall-family O2/O3, with the jet wall allowed.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Coherent amplitude model

If a finite coherent vector amplitude model remains,

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}\subset L^2(\nu;\mathbf C^2),
\]

then rank-two coercivity applies to the residual only if amplitude Schur gives

\[
\operatorname{dist}
(F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}},\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}})
\ge Q^{-A}\|F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}}\|.
\]

If this Schur estimate fails, then the coherent model is absorbing the vector wall. But since \(F_{2Y}\) has two components, absorption is much stricter than in rank one.

The correct fallback is a vector version of finite-model nonabsorption:

\[
\boxed{
F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}}\notin \mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}.
}
\]

If the coherent space is nonlocal and finite-dimensional, this should be a standard Schur/Remez problem. If it is locally free, rank two fails at the amplitude layer.

---

# 6. Final rank-two analytic package

The analytic module can now be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoWallClosure.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. Gate–1:

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A};
\]

2. LocalRemezMarkov for the chart-good local expression class;

3. either plain wall plus Markov upgrade, or jet-enhanced wall;

4. finite coherent amplitude spaces, if present, satisfy vector amplitude Schur.

Then

\[
\int_I E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

This supplies the D4 wall lower.

---

# 7. Current status

The exact coercivity identity is no longer the bottleneck:

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
\]

The remaining proof work is now sharply divided:

### Algebraic/local side

Prove

\[
B_Y=0.
\]

### Analytic side

Prove LocalRemezMarkov and choose plain or jet wall.

The analytic side appears standard relative to the rest of the proof. The local typed exactness \(B_Y=0\) remains the main mathematical bottleneck.

_Thought for 9s_

Continuing Agent 5 — make `LocalRemezMarkov` less black-box by deriving it from the finite wall-family/O2O3 setup.

I will keep the current notation:

\[
\rho_Y=\text{the lower }Y12\text{ fiber graph slope},
\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), the wall does not use \(\rho_Y\) or \(\rho_\Gamma\). The analytic target remains

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta.
\]

The latest rank-two plan reduces the analytic side to `LocalRemezMarkov` plus the exact identity

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
\]

The remaining issue is to justify `LocalRemezMarkov` from the finite local function classes already needed by O2/O3, not to introduce a new ungrounded analytic axiom. 

---

## 1. Replace generic smoothness by finite atlas complexity

The right hypothesis is not merely

\[
\|q\|_{C^K}\le Q^C.
\]

That controls derivatives but not zero complexity. The rank-two coercivity proof needs a finite-oscillation statement. A better assumption is:

\[
\boxed{
q,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\text{ lie in a finite }R^C\text{-conditioned local algebra } \mathscr A_I.
}
\]

Here \(\mathscr A_I\) should be the same local algebra already used by the bounded-charge O2/O3 proof:

- finite branch-charge;
- bounded local degree or Riesz dimension;
- \(R^C\)-conditioned basis;
- chart-good denominators;
- stable under \(D,D^2\) for the finite derivatives used in the jet wall.

Then Markov/Remez are consequences of finite dimensionality and conditioning.

So the analytic interface becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\mathscr A_I\text{ is }R^C\text{-Riesz and derivative-stable through order }K.
}
\]

This is cleaner than postulating arbitrary finite oscillation.

---

## 2. Derivative stability

Let

\[
F\in \mathscr A_I.
\]

In an \(R^C\)-conditioned basis \(\{p_j\}_{j=1}^N\), with

\[
N\le R^C,
\]

we have

\[
F=\sum_{j=1}^N a_jp_j.
\]

Derivative stability means that for \(0\le k\le K\),

\[
D^kF
\]

lies in an enlarged finite space

\[
\mathscr A_I^{(K)}
\]

with dimension \(N_K\le R^C\) and conditioning \(R^C\). Then standard finite-dimensional norm equivalence gives

\[
\boxed{
\|D^kF\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
R^C\|F\|_{L^2(I^*)}.
}
\]

This is the `LocalMarkov` part.

Applied to \(\Gamma_G\),

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le
R^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}
\]

if \(\Gamma_G\) belongs to a derivative-stable finite local space.

If this is proved, the **plain rank-two wall** is enough. If not, use the jet wall.

---

## 3. Remez from finite conditioning

The required Remez statement is:

If \(F\in\mathscr A_I\) and \(\|F\|_{L^2(I)}=1\), then \(F\) cannot be tiny on almost all of \(I\). More quantitatively, for \(\varepsilon>0\),

\[
\boxed{
|\{x\in I: |F(x)|\le \varepsilon\}|
\le
1-cR^{-C}
}
\]

for \(\varepsilon\le R^{-C}\), after normalization.

A more useful sublevel form is:

\[
\boxed{
|\{|F|<\varepsilon\|F\|_{L^\infty(I)}\}|
\le
R^C\varepsilon^\theta |I|.
}
\]

This follows from a finite-dimensional Remez inequality if \(\mathscr A_I\) is an algebraic/analytic Chebyshev-type class. If not globally Chebyshev, it is enough to partition \(I\) into \(R^C\) subintervals where such a Remez inequality holds.

Thus the actual required theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{LocalFiniteRemez: }
\mathscr A_I
\text{ admits an }R^C\text{-piecewise Remez inequality.}
}
\]

This is plausible for the same analytic basis used in O2/O3.

---

## 4. Finite component bound

The acceleration–velocity step needs the far set

\[
I_{\mathrm{far}}=\{\operatorname{dist}(q,Z)>\eta\}
\]

to have controlled component complexity.

But

\[
\operatorname{dist}(q,Z)>\eta
\]

is determined by sublevel sets of

\[
P_Z(q):=q(q^2-3).
\]

Since

\[
P_Z(q)\in\mathscr A_I
\]

if \(\mathscr A_I\) is closed under fixed polynomial operations, LocalFiniteRemez gives component/oscillation control for \(P_Z(q)\). Therefore

\[
I_{\mathrm{far}}=\{|P_Z(q)|\gtrsim \eta\}
\]

has at most \(R^C\eta^{-C}\) controlled components after a standard sign/monotonicity partition.

So the component bound needed in RankTwoCoercivity follows from:

\[
\boxed{
q\in\mathscr A_I,\quad \mathscr A_I\text{ polynomially closed, and LocalFiniteRemez.}
}
\]

---

## 5. RankTwoCoercivity with finite algebra assumption

We can now state the quantitative theorem cleanly.

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoCoercivityFromFiniteAlgebra.}
}
\]

Assume on a normalized chart interval \(I\):

1. \(q,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\in\mathscr A_I^{(K)}\), with \(R^C\)-conditioning;

2. \(\mathscr A_I^{(K)}\) is stable under \(D,D^2\) and fixed polynomial operations needed for \(f(q)\);

3. \(\mathscr A_I^{(K)}\) satisfies LocalFiniteRemez;

4. chart denominators are \(Q^{-C}\)-bounded away from zero.

Then

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta.
\]

This is now a local finite-algebra theorem, not a new zeta arithmetic input.

---

## 6. Why this fits O2/O3

O2/O3 already needs a finite basis with:

\[
R^C\text{-Riesz conditioning},
\]

Christoffel spread, and finite-degree moment separation for

\[
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

Those hypotheses are stronger than or parallel to what is needed here. The same finite atlas should give:

\[
\text{LocalMarkov}+\text{LocalFiniteRemez}.
\]

Thus the rank-two analytic closure reuses the O2/O3 analytic infrastructure.

This is a significant consolidation:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{BoundedChargeGraph/O2O3}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}
\]

share the same local finite-algebra regularity assumptions.

---

## 7. Plain versus jet wall decision

We can now make the wall choice conditional on LocalMarkov.

### If LocalMarkov is proved

Use the plain wall:

\[
W_{\mathrm{bd}}^{(2)}
=
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
\]

Then

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2}
\le
Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2}
\]

upgrades the plain wall to the coercivity norm.

This is cleaner for O2/O3.

### If LocalMarkov is not yet proved

Use the jet wall:

\[
W_{\mathrm{bd}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+
|D\Gamma_G|^2+
|D^2\Gamma_G|^2+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
\]

This bakes the coercivity norm into the wall. Since this is a finite wall family, bounded-charge O2/O3 should still apply with a larger but fixed \(d_0\).

---

## 8. Remaining technical dependency

The next analytic task is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{LocalFiniteAlgebraRegularity.}
}
\]

Prove for the local chart algebra \(\mathscr A_I\):

1. derivative stability through order \(K\);

2. Riesz conditioning;

3. Remez/sublevel control;

4. finite component/sign partition control;

5. closure under the fixed polynomial operations

\[
q\mapsto q(q^2-3),\qquad q\mapsto f(q),\qquad q\mapsto f'(q).
\]

Once this theorem is available, RankTwoCoercivity is essentially complete.

---

## Final result

The analytic rank-two branch can be reduced to a single finite-algebra regularity theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{LocalFiniteAlgebraRegularity}
\Rightarrow
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}.
}
\]

Together with Gate–1:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}+\mathrm{Gate1}
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-two wall lower}.
}
\]

This means the rank-two route now has two main blockers:

1. local typed exactness \(B_Y=0\);
2. finite-algebra regularity for the local chart/O2O3 basis.

The second blocker is likely shared with O2/O3, so the unique new burden is mostly \(B_Y=0\).

## Assistant (2026-04-28 13:15:35)

_Thought for 18s_

Continuing Agent 5 — make `LocalFiniteAlgebraRegularity` proof-ready.

I will keep:

\[
\rho_Y=\text{the }Y12\text{ fiber graph slope},\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), these do not enter the wall. The rank-two analytic closure now needs:

\[
\mathrm{LocalFiniteAlgebraRegularity}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}
\Longrightarrow
\text{Gate--1 wall lower}.
\]

The latest architecture makes this an auxiliary analytic regularity theorem shared with O2/O3, not a new zeta-specific obstruction. 

---

# 1. Finite-dimensionality alone is not enough

A finite-dimensional space can still have basis vectors that spike at extraction scale if it is badly conditioned. So the correct local regularity package is not merely:

\[
\dim \mathscr A_I\le Q^C.
\]

We need a **controlled finite algebra**:

\[
\boxed{
\mathscr A_I
\text{ has bounded dimension, bounded conditioning, derivative stability, and Remez/nonspiking control.}
}
\]

The minimal useful hypotheses are:

1. \(R^C\)-Riesz conditioning in \(L^2(I)\);
2. \(L^\infty\)-leverage bound;
3. derivative closure through the needed order;
4. Remez/sublevel control;
5. closure under the fixed polynomial operations used by \(f(q)=6q-2q^3\).

Without these, RankTwoCoercivity can fail quantitatively even though the compactness argument remains qualitatively true.

---

# 2. A sufficient local algebra model

A clean sufficient model is:

\[
\mathscr A_I
=
\left\{
\frac{P_0(x)+\sum_{\nu=1}^{M}P_\nu(x)u_\nu(x)}
{D(x)}
:
\deg P_\nu\le R^C
\right\},
\]

where:

- \(u_\nu\) are fixed chart-good analytic atoms on \(I^*\);
- \(D\) is a chart denominator with

\[
|D(x)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

on \(I^*\);

- all \(u_\nu\) and \(D^{-1}\) have analytic extension to a complex neighborhood of \(I\) of polynomial relative width;
- the resulting basis is \(R^C\)-conditioned.

This is broad enough to cover polynomial/rational local chart functions, finite branch combinations, and fixed bounded-charge wall components.

Under these conditions, the following are available.

---

# 3. Markov derivative control

For \(F\in\mathscr A_I\) and scale-normalized derivative \(D_I\),

\[
\boxed{
\|D_I^jF\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\|F\|_{L^2(I^*)},
\qquad
0\le j\le j_0.
}
\]

Proof sketch:

Use analytic extension plus Cauchy estimates on \(I^*\), or, in a polynomial/Riesz basis, use finite-dimensional norm equivalence for the derivative operator

\[
D_I^j:\mathscr A_I\to \mathscr A_I^{(j)}.
\]

Since \(j_0\) is fixed and the basis conditioning is \(R^C\), the operator norm is polynomial.

This gives the desired LocalMarkov estimate:

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}
\]

if \(\Gamma_G\in\mathscr A_I\) and derivative stability holds.

If this Markov estimate is proved, the **plain** rank-two wall is enough.

---

# 4. Remez/sublevel control

We also need:

\[
\boxed{
|\{x\in I: |F(x)|<\varepsilon\|F\|_{L^\infty(I)}\}|
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^\theta |I|
}
\]

for nonzero \(F\in\mathscr A_I\).

A sufficient route:

1. partition \(I\) into \(Q^C\) subintervals on which \(\mathscr A_I\) is a Chebyshev-type or bounded-degree analytic class;
2. apply a one-dimensional Remez inequality on each subinterval;
3. sum over \(Q^C\) pieces.

For rational/analytic finite-degree functions with denominators bounded below, this follows because excessive sublevel concentration would force many approximate zeros, contradicting the bounded degree/finite analytic complexity unless \(F\) is globally small.

This gives both sublevel control and finite component control.

---

# 5. Finite component control

RankTwoCoercivity uses the far set

\[
I_{\mathrm{far}}
=
\{x:\operatorname{dist}(q(x),Z)>\eta\},
\qquad
Z=\{0,\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\}.
\]

This is equivalent to

\[
|P_Z(q(x))|>\eta'
\]

where

\[
P_Z(q)=q(q^2-3).
\]

If \(\mathscr A_I\) is closed under fixed polynomial operations, then

\[
P_Z(q)\in\mathscr A_I^{\mathrm{poly}}
\]

with controlled complexity.

Remez control for \(P_Z(q)\) gives a polynomial bound on the number and complexity of near/far components. Therefore the acceleration–velocity proof does not suffer from infinitely many tiny oscillatory intervals.

This is the exact role of Remez in the rank-two proof.

---

# 6. Closure under nonlinear operations

The coercivity proof uses

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3,
\qquad
f'(q)=6-6q^2,
\qquad
P_Z(q)=q(q^2-3).
\]

So the local algebra must satisfy:

\[
q\in\mathscr A_I
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
q^2,q^3,f(q),f'(q),P_Z(q)\in \mathscr A_I^{+}
\]

with complexity still \(Q^C\).

Because these are fixed-degree polynomial operations, this is automatic for a finite algebra closed under products up to fixed degree. The dimension may increase, but only by a fixed polynomial factor.

This is why the local regularity theorem should be stated for a small algebra closure

\[
\mathscr A_I^{+}
\]

rather than only the original linear span.

---

# 7. RankTwoCoercivity from LocalFiniteAlgebraRegularity

Assume:

\[
\delta=
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}.
\]

From

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2,
\]

we get

\[
\|q(q')^2\|_{L^2(I)}\le C\delta.
\]

Choose

\[
\eta=\delta^\kappa.
\]

On

\[
I_{\mathrm{near}}=\{\operatorname{dist}(q,Z)\le \eta\},
\]

\[
|q''|\le |f(q)|+|E_1|
\le C\eta+|E_1|,
\]

so

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{near}})}
\le C\eta+\delta.
\]

On

\[
I_{\mathrm{far}},
\]

\[
|q|\ge c\eta,
\qquad |f(q)|\ge c\eta.
\]

The identity gives

\[
\|q'\|_{L^4(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le C\delta^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2}.
\]

LocalMarkov/Remez prevents \(E_1\) from canceling \(f(q)\) on a thick set. Therefore on most of \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\),

\[
|q''|\gtrsim \eta.
\]

Finite component control plus the acceleration–velocity lemma imply

\[
|I_{\mathrm{far}}|\le Q^C\delta^{c}\eta^{-C}.
\]

Hence

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le Q^C\delta^{c}\eta^{-C}.
\]

With \(\eta=\delta^\kappa\), choose \(\kappa\) small enough to get

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\delta^\theta.
}
\]

This proves:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{LocalFiniteAlgebraRegularity}
\Rightarrow
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}.
}
\]

---

# 8. Plain wall versus jet wall

The distinction is now clear.

## Plain wall route

Use

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2)}
=
|H|^2(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2).
\]

Requires LocalMarkov:

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}.
\]

If true, plain wall controls the coercivity norm.

## Jet wall route

Use

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+
|D_I\Gamma_G|^2+
|D_I^2\Gamma_G|^2+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
\]

This directly controls

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2}.
\]

It avoids relying on LocalMarkov for \(\Gamma_G\), at the cost of slightly larger but still \(O(1)\) branch bandwidth.

So the safest theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{FiniteWallFamilyO2/O3}
}
\]

with wall family

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}
=
\{\Gamma_G,D_I\Gamma_G,D_I^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}.
\]

---

# 9. O2/O3 compatibility

The bounded-charge O2/O3 proof only needs:

\[
d_0=d_N+2d_H+2d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{wall}}=O(1).
\]

If

\[
D_I^j\Gamma_G
\]

does not alter branch charge, then

\[
d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{wall}}
=
\max\{d(\Gamma_G),d(\Gamma_{G,2})\}.
\]

If derivatives add a fixed amount, still

\[
d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{wall}}=O(1).
\]

Thus the jet wall is compatible with O2/O3 provided the transition basis includes

\[
\mathbf C_{d_{\max}}[y]
\]

for a conservative fixed \(d_{\max}\).

This keeps the analytic rank-two closure aligned with the O2/O3 architecture.

---

# 10. Final interface theorem

The clean theorem statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{LocalFiniteAlgebraRegularity.}
}
\]

For every chart-good interval \(I\), the finite local algebra \(\mathscr A_I\) containing \(q,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) and the required finite derivatives satisfies:

1. \(R^C\)-Riesz conditioning;
2. derivative stability through order \(K\);
3. Remez/sublevel control;
4. finite component control;
5. closure under fixed polynomial operations;
6. denominator lower bounds.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}
}
\]

holds:

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta.
\]

Then Gate–1 gives rank-two wall lower.

---

## Final result

The analytic rank-two branch now has a clean dependency:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{LocalFiniteAlgebraRegularity}
+
\mathrm{Gate1}
\Rightarrow
\mathrm{RankTwoWallLower}.
}
\]

This is likely shared with O2/O3’s finite atlas/Riesz infrastructure.

Therefore, after this reduction, the unique rank-two burden remains local typed exactness:

\[
\boxed{
B_Y=0.
}
\]

The wall analysis itself is no longer exploratory.

Continuing Agent 5 — remove possible circularity between `LocalFiniteAlgebraRegularity`, O2/O3, and the rank-two jet wall.

\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},\qquad
