In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), the wall does not use \(\rho_Y\) or \(\rho_\Gamma\). The analytic chain is now:

\[
\mathrm{LocalFiniteAlgebraRegularity}
\Rightarrow
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}
\Rightarrow
\mathrm{Gate1\ wall\ lower}.
\]

The remaining concern is circularity: O2/O3 also uses the local finite algebra. We must ensure the rank-two wall lower is not using O2/O3 output to prove an input needed by O2/O3. 

---

# 1. Separate structural regularity from determinant survival

The finite algebra regularity needed for RankTwoCoercivity is structural:

\[
\mathscr A_I
\text{ has Riesz conditioning, derivative stability, Remez control, and denominator bounds.}
\]

This must be established **before** O2/O3 determinant survival.

It should not depend on:

\[
D_{-n}\notin \operatorname{span}(D_{-n+1},\ldots,D_{-n+d_0}),
\]

nor on any extracted wall mass.

So the correct dependency is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{LocalFiniteAlgebraRegularity}
\quad\text{is an atlas/normalization theorem, not an O2/O3 consequence.}
}
\]

Then both modules consume it:

\[
\mathrm{LocalFiniteAlgebraRegularity}
\Rightarrow
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity},
\]

and separately

\[
\mathrm{LocalFiniteAlgebraRegularity}
\Rightarrow
\mathrm{BoundedChargeGraph/O2O3}.
\]

This removes circularity.

---

# 2. Minimal non-circular regularity package

The required package should be stated independently of the wall:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{FiniteAtlasRegularity}.
}
\]

On each chart-good interval \(I\), there is a finite algebra \(\mathscr A_I\) such that:

1. \(q,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\in\mathscr A_I^{+}\);

2. \(\mathscr A_I^{+}\) has dimension

\[
\dim\mathscr A_I^{+}\le Q^C;
\]

3. denominators are chart-good:

\[
|D(x)|\ge Q^{-C};
\]

4. the basis is \(Q^C\)-Riesz in \(L^2(I)\);

5. derivatives up to fixed order remain in a \(Q^C\)-conditioned enlargement:

\[
D_I^j\mathscr A_I^{+}\subset \mathscr A_I^{(j)},
\qquad j\le K;
\]

6. Remez/sublevel and finite-component bounds hold for all \(F\in\mathscr A_I^{+}\);

7. \(\mathscr A_I^{+}\) is closed under the fixed polynomial operations used by

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3,\qquad
f'(q)=6-6q^2,\qquad
P_Z(q)=q(q^2-3).
\]

This theorem is enough for RankTwoCoercivity and for O2/O3 finite wall-family bookkeeping.

---

# 3. Why this is plausible

The finite atlas is already implicitly required by O2/O3. O2/O3 needs:

\[
R^C\text{-conditioned bases},
\]

finite branch-charge,

Christoffel spread,

and finite moment separation for

\[
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

Those requirements are at least as strong as the local Markov/Remez properties needed for RankTwoCoercivity, provided the wall components are included in the finite algebra.

Thus the rank-two analytic side introduces no new arithmetic obstruction. It asks that the existing finite atlas also control the wall components:

\[
\Gamma_G,\quad D_I\Gamma_G,\quad D_I^2\Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

---

# 4. The safest formulation: finite wall family

To avoid deciding too early between plain and jet wall, define a finite wall family

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}
=
\{\Gamma_G,\ D_I\Gamma_G,\ D_I^2\Gamma_G,\ \Gamma_{G,2}\}.
\]

Then set

\[
W_{\mathrm{bd}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\sum_{G\in\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}}|G|^2.
\]

O2/O3 only needs that this family has bounded branch-charge:

\[
d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{wall}}
=
\max_{G\in\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}}d(G)
=
O(1).
\]

Then

\[
d_0^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
d_N+2d_H+2d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{wall}}.
\]

The near-pure Schur proof is unchanged; it just runs with this \(d_0\).

So the correct O2/O3 theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{FiniteWallFamilyO2/O3}(d_{\max}):
\text{ O2/O3 holds for any fixed wall family with }d_0\le d_{\max}.
}
\]

This makes the rank-two jet wall compatible by design.

---

# 5. Plain wall can be recovered later

If we later prove

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)},
\]

then the plain wall

\[
W_{\mathrm{bd}}^{(2)}
=
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)
\]

is enough.

But the proof should not depend on this upgrade. The jet wall is the robust default.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Default wall for rank two: jet wall.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Optimization if LocalMarkov is strong: plain wall.}
}
\]

---

# 6. RankTwoCoercivity becomes a deterministic lemma

With finite atlas regularity in place, RankTwoCoercivity is deterministic.

Let

\[
\delta=
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}.
\]

Then, since

\[
E_1=-\frac16\Gamma_G,\qquad E_2=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

we get

\[
\|E_1\|_{H^2}+\|E_2\|_{L^2}\le Q^C\delta.
\]

The identity

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2
\]

plus finite Remez/Markov control gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le Q^C\delta^\theta.
\]

Gate–1 gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Hence the rank-two jet wall has mass:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|D_I\Gamma_G|^2+|D_I^2\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)
\ge Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

---

# 7. Coherent amplitude terms

If finite coherent vector amplitudes remain, the wall target is not merely the raw jet vector. It is the distance to a finite coherent model:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
H(\Gamma_G,D_I\Gamma_G,D_I^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\mathcal C_{2Y,\mathrm{jet}}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right).
\]

This does **not** affect \(B_Y=0\), because finite coherent terms are not local fiber tangents. But it does require vector amplitude Schur.

The right order remains:

1. Use raw finite wall family in O2/O3.
2. Prove vector amplitude Schur afterward.
3. Extract blockwise if needed.

Do not project the wall before O2/O3 unless the projection has bounded branch-charge.

---

# 8. Updated rank-two proof skeleton

The clean rank-two proof now has two independent blocks.

## Local exactness block

\[
\mathrm{TwoGradeLiveQuotient}
+
\mathrm{C7CarrierFaithfulness}
+
\mathrm{SamePointWhiteningExactness}_Y
+
\mathrm{NoAtomFitting}_{2Y}
+
\mathrm{NuisancePreservesLivePair}_{2Y}
\Rightarrow
B_Y=0.
\]

## Analytic coercivity block

\[
\mathrm{FiniteAtlasRegularity}
+
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}
+
\mathrm{Gate1}
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-two jet wall lower}.
\]

Then O2/O3 consumes the finite wall family:

\[
\mathrm{FiniteWallFamilyO2/O3}
\]

with

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}
=
\{\Gamma_G,D_I\Gamma_G,D_I^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}.
\]

---

# 9. Remaining blockers

The unique rank-two-specific blockers are now:

1. \(B_Y=0\), i.e. typed local exactness;

2. D4 coefficient conditioning:

\[
|c_7\alpha_9|\ge Q^{-A};
\]

3. finite atlas regularity for the wall family;

4. finite wall-family O2/O3 for \(d_0\le d_{\max}\);

5. vector amplitude Schur if \(\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}\neq0\).

The moving-line and forced ODE trap modules are not needed unless \(B_Y=\mathbf C(1,\rho_Y)\).

---

## Final result

The rank-two analytic side is now non-circular:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{FiniteAtlasRegularity}
}
\]

is an independent local regularity theorem used by both O2/O3 and RankTwoCoercivity.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}+\mathrm{Gate1}
}
\]

gives the D4 wall lower.

Thus the proof priority remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove }B_Y=0.
}
\]

If \(B_Y=0\) closes, the downstream wall analysis is now a deterministic exactness/coercivity mechanism, not a moving-wall model-exclusion tower.

Continuing Agent 5 — push rank-two closure past the “finite atlas regularity” interface and isolate the exact remaining analytic theorem.

I keep the current notation:

R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), neither \(\rho_Y\) nor \(\rho_\Gamma\) enters the wall. The relevant rank-two wall family is

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
\{\Gamma_G,D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}.
\]

The current architecture is:

\[
B_Y=0
\Longrightarrow
F_{2Y}\asymp H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

and the analytic closure is

\[
\mathrm{FiniteAtlasRegularity}
+
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}
+
\mathrm{Gate1}
\Longrightarrow
\text{rank-two wall lower}.
\]

This is the cleaner rank-two route emphasized in the latest prompt. 

---

# 1. The remaining analytic theorem can be reduced further

Previously I stated a fairly broad `LocalFiniteAlgebraRegularity` package. For the rank-two coercivity proof, we do **not** need full Remez for every expression in the atlas. We need a narrower theorem for the single scalar

\[
P_Z(q)=q(q^2-3)
\]

and the residual

\[
E_1=q''-(6q-2q^3).
\]

The exact identity is

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
\]

Thus the proof only needs to control three phenomena:

1. the set where \(q\) is near the roots \(Z=\{0,\pm\sqrt3\}\);
2. the set where \(E_1\) can cancel \(f(q)=6q-2q^3\);
3. the number/structure of components where \(f(q)\) has a fixed sign away from \(Z\).

So the analytic regularity interface can be narrowed to:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{RootRemez}_{q,Z}
+
\mathrm{CancellationControl}_{E_1,f(q)}
+
\mathrm{FiniteAccelerationComponents}.
}
\]

This is weaker than a full finite algebra Remez theorem.

---

# 2. RootRemez for \(q(q^2-3)\)

We need a controlled decomposition of

\[
I_{\mathrm{near}}(\eta)
=
\{x:\operatorname{dist}(q(x),Z)\le\eta\}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
|P_Z(q(x))|\lesssim \eta.
\]

A sufficient theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{RootRemez}_{q,Z}:
\quad
I\setminus I_{\mathrm{near}}(\eta)
\text{ has at most }Q^C\eta^{-C}
\text{ controlled components.}
}
\]

This follows if \(P_Z(q)\) lies in a finite Remez class.

We do **not** need a sharp sublevel bound. We only need polynomial component complexity and enough control to apply acceleration–velocity on the far set.

This is a modest analytic requirement.

---

# 3. CancellationControl for \(E_1\)

On the far set,

\[
|f(q)|\gtrsim \eta.
\]

But

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1.
\]

To use acceleration, we need \(E_1\) not to cancel \(f(q)\) on most of the far set.

Since

\[
\|E_1\|_{H^2}\le\delta,
\]

Sobolev gives \(E_1\) small in \(C^0\) on normalized intervals:

\[
\|E_1\|_{C^0}\le Q^C\delta.
\]

Thus if

\[
\delta\ll Q^{-C}\eta,
\]

then on the far set

\[
|q''|\ge c\eta
\]

directly.

This is simpler than my previous version. We do not need a delicate cancellation lemma if the wall norm includes \(H^2\) control of \(E_1\). That is another reason the jet wall is preferable.

So with the jet wall, the key far-set estimate becomes straightforward:

\[
|q''|\ge c\eta
\quad\text{on }I_{\mathrm{far}}.
\]

---

# 4. Acceleration–velocity without sign assumptions

Earlier I introduced sign-controlled components. We can avoid explicit sign assumptions using a ramp-energy lower bound.

Suppose on an interval \(J\),

\[
|q''|\ge c\eta
\]

and \(q''\) has no sign control. Then cancellation in the integral of \(q''\) may happen. But if \(q''\) oscillates signs rapidly, then \(q'''\) must be large.

Since chart-good finite-jet bounds control \(q'''\), rapid oscillation is limited. A clean theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{AccelerationRemez}:
\quad
|q''|\ge \eta
\text{ on }J,\quad
\|q'''\|_{L^\infty(J)}\le Q^C
\Rightarrow
J\text{ decomposes into }Q^C\eta^{-C}
\text{ sign-controlled intervals.}
}
\]

This is just a finite-oscillation consequence of bounded derivative and Remez. Then on each sign-controlled interval, the acceleration–velocity lemma applies.

Alternatively, one can use a direct \(L^4\)-ramp lower bound on each monotonicity component of \(q'\).

So the required auxiliary lemma is not severe:

\[
\boxed{
\text{large acceleration + finite oscillation + small velocity}
\Rightarrow
\text{small measure}.
}
\]

---

# 5. Quantitative coercivity with explicit parameter choice

Let

\[
\delta=\|E_1\|_{H^2}+\|E_2\|_{L^2}.
\]

From

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2
\]

we get

\[
\|q(q')^2\|_{L^2}\le C\delta.
\]

Let

\[
\eta=\delta^\kappa
\]

with \(\kappa>0\) small.

On

\[
I_{\mathrm{near}}=\{\operatorname{dist}(q,Z)\le\eta\},
\]

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{near}})}
\le
C\eta+\delta.
\]

On

\[
I_{\mathrm{far}},
\]

\[
|q|\ge c\eta,
\qquad
|f(q)|\ge c\eta.
\]

If \(\delta\ll\eta\), then

\[
|q''|\ge c\eta.
\]

Also,

\[
\|q'\|_{L^4(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le C\delta^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2}.
\]

By acceleration–velocity plus finite component control,

\[
|I_{\mathrm{far}}|
\le Q^C\delta^a\eta^{-b}
\]

for fixed \(a,b>0\). Therefore

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le Q^C\delta^{a/2}\eta^{-b/2}.
\]

Choose \(\kappa<a/(2b)\). Then

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le Q^C\delta^\theta.
\]

Combining,

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\le Q^C\delta^\theta.
}
\]

This is the desired RankTwoCoercivity estimate.

---

# 6. The jet wall is analytically optimal for this route

The above proof used

\[
\|E_1\|_{H^2}
\]

in two ways:

1. to control \(E_1''\) in the exact identity;
2. to control \(E_1\) in \(C^0\), preventing cancellation of \(f(q)\).

Therefore, unless we prove a strong Markov upgrade from \(\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2}\) to \(\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2}\), the natural D4 wall should be the jet wall:

\[
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+
|D\Gamma_G|^2+
|D^2\Gamma_G|^2+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
\]

This is not just a convenience. It exactly matches the coercivity identity.

So I would now make the jet wall the **default** rank-two wall, not merely a fallback.

The plain wall can be an optimization later.

---

# 7. O2/O3 compatibility is the only cost

The price of the jet wall is a larger bounded-charge degree:

\[
d_0^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
d_N+2d_H+2d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{jet}},
\]

where

\[
d_{\Gamma,\mathrm{jet}}
=
\max\{
d(\Gamma_G),
d(D\Gamma_G),
d(D^2\Gamma_G),
d(\Gamma_{G,2})
\}.
\]

But because this is a finite derivative family, the degree remains \(O(1)\).

Therefore the O2/O3 theorem should be stated for a finite wall family:

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}
=
\{\Gamma_G,D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}.
\]

This is the right architecture:

\[
\boxed{
\text{rank-two D4 uses jet wall;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{O2/O3 supports any fixed finite wall family with }d_0\le d_{\max}.
}
\]

---

# 8. Remaining exact analytic assumptions

The final RankTwoCoercivity theorem should explicitly assume:

1. scale-normalized \(H^2/L^2\) wall norm;

2. Sobolev embedding / chart-good derivative bounds sufficient for

\[
\|E_1\|_{C^0}\le Q^C\|E_1\|_{H^2};
\]

3. finite component control for the far set

\[
\operatorname{dist}(q,Z)>\eta;
\]

4. acceleration–velocity lemma on sign-controlled components;

5. polynomial boundedness of \(q''\) to convert small far-set measure into small \(L^2\)-mass.

All are local one-dimensional finite-complexity conditions.

---

# 9. Final refinement

The rank-two analytic closure is now best stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{JetRankTwoCoercivity.}
}
\]

If

\[
\delta^2
=
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}^2+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}^2
\]

is small, then

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le Q^C\delta^\theta.
\]

Therefore Gate–1 implies

\[
\delta\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_I
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+
|D\Gamma_G|^2+
|D^2\Gamma_G|^2+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

This closes the rank-two wall lower.

---

## Final result

The analytic branch is now sufficiently clear:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use the jet-enhanced rank-two wall by default.}
}
\]

It aligns exactly with the identity

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
\]

Then RankTwoCoercivity is a one-dimensional finite-complexity lemma, and Gate–1 supplies the wall lower.

The remaining hard part is not the wall. It is still:

\[
\boxed{
B_Y=0.
}
\]

No nomenclature changes. I use

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), these variables are not used in the wall. The rank-two wall uses

\[
\Gamma_G,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and the robust default wall family is

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{jet}}

# Agent 5 — JetRankTwoCoercivity

## 1. Normalization

Use the current normalization:

\[
\Gamma_G=-6q''+36q-12q^3.
\]

Set

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=-6(q''-f(q)).
\]

Define

\[
E_1=q''-f(q).
\]

Also,

\[
f'(q)=6-6q^2,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=q^{(4)}-6(1-q^2)q''
=
q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Define

\[
E_2=q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Thus

\[
\Gamma_G=-6E_1,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=E_2.
\]

Differentiate

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1.
\]

Then

\[
q'''=f'(q)q'+E_1',
\]

and

\[
q^{(4)}
=
f''(q)(q')^2+f'(q)q''+E_1''.
\]

Therefore

\[
E_2-E_1''=f''(q)(q')^2.
\]

Since

\[
f''(q)=-12q,
\]

we get the exact identity

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

This is the core identity.

---

## 2. Exact flatness

If

\[
E_1=0,\qquad E_2=0,
\]

then

\[
q(q')^2=0.
\]

On any connected interval where \(q\neq0\),

\[
q'=0,
\]

hence

\[
q''=0.
\]

But \(E_1=0\) also gives

\[
q''=f(q)=2q(3-q^2).
\]

Thus exact solutions are locally

\[
q\equiv0,\qquad q\equiv\sqrt3,\qquad q\equiv-\sqrt3,
\]

and in all cases

\[
q''\equiv0.
\]

So exact rank-two joint flatness eliminates Gate–1 energy.

---

## 3. Compactness coercivity

A qualitative theorem is immediate.

Let \(I\) be a normalized chart-good interval and suppose

\[
\|q_n\|_{H^K(I)}\le M
\]

for fixed large \(K\). If

\[
E_{1,n}\to0 \quad\text{in } H^2(I),
\]

\[
E_{2,n}\to0 \quad\text{in } L^2(I),
\]

then

\[
q_n''\to0 \quad\text{in } L^2(I).
\]

Proof: by compactness, \(q_n\to q_\infty\) strongly in \(H^3\) and weakly in \(H^4\). Passing to the limit gives

\[
q_\infty''=f(q_\infty),
\]

\[
q_\infty^{(4)}=f'(q_\infty)q_\infty''.
\]

Differentiating \(q_\infty''=f(q_\infty)\) twice gives

\[
q_\infty^{(4)}
=
f''(q_\infty)(q_\infty')^2+f'(q_\infty)f(q_\infty).
\]

Since \(q_\infty''=f(q_\infty)\), comparison gives

\[
f''(q_\infty)(q_\infty')^2=0.
\]

Thus

\[
q_\infty(q_\infty')^2=0,
\]

so \(q_\infty''=0\). Strong convergence gives

\[
q_n''\to0
\]

in \(L^2\).

This proves there is no hidden rank-two ODE trap analogous to the rank-one case.

---

## 4. Quantitative theorem

The proof stack needs:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{JetRankTwoCoercivity.}
}
\]

On a scale-normalized chart-good interval \(I\), assume polynomial finite-complexity/finite-jet bounds. Let

\[
\delta
=
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}.
\]

Then for some fixed \(\theta>0\),

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\delta^\theta.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta.
}
\]

---

## 5. Quantitative proof skeleton

From

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2
\]

we get

\[
\|q(q')^2\|_{L^2(I)}
\le C\delta.
\]

Let

\[
Z=\{0,\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\}.
\]

The roots of

\[
f(q)=2q(3-q^2)
\]

are simple. Fix

\[
\eta=\delta^\kappa
\]

for small fixed \(\kappa>0\).

Split

\[
I_{\mathrm{near}}=\{x:\operatorname{dist}(q(x),Z)\le\eta\},
\]

\[
I_{\mathrm{far}}=I\setminus I_{\mathrm{near}}.
\]

### Near region

On \(I_{\mathrm{near}}\),

\[
|f(q)|\le C\eta.
\]

Since

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1,
\]

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{near}})}
\le
C\eta |I|^{1/2}+\|E_1\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
C\eta |I|^{1/2}+\delta.
\]

### Far region

On \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\),

\[
|f(q)|\ge c\eta,
\qquad
|q|\ge c\eta.
\]

From

\[
\|q(q')^2\|_{L^2}\le C\delta
\]

we get

\[
\|q'\|_{L^4(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
C\delta^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2}.
\]

Also,

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1.
\]

Since \(E_1\in H^2\), one-dimensional Sobolev and chart-good finite-complexity give

\[
\|E_1\|_{C^0(I)}
\le Q^C\delta.
\]

For \(\delta\ll Q^{-C}\eta\),

\[
|q''|\ge c\eta
\]

on \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\), except possibly on a polynomially negligible exceptional set.

Now apply the acceleration–velocity lemma on the far-region components: a function with acceleration \(\gtrsim\eta\) and \(L^4\)-small velocity cannot persist on a thick set. With finite component/Remez control,

\[
|I_{\mathrm{far}}|
\le
Q^C\delta^a\eta^{-b}
\]

for fixed positive \(a,b\).

Since \(q''\) has polynomial chart-good bounds,

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
Q^C\delta^{a/2}\eta^{-b/2}.
\]

Choosing \(\kappa\) small enough yields

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le Q^C\delta^{\theta}.
\]

Combining near and far regions gives

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le Q^C\delta^\theta.
}
\]

---

## 6. Auxiliary assumptions needed

The quantitative proof requires the following finite-complexity inputs.

### A. Scale-normalized Sobolev control

\[
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}
\Rightarrow
\|E_1\|_{C^0(I)}
\le Q^C\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}.
\]

### B. Root Remez / finite component control

For

\[
P_Z(q)=q(q^2-3),
\]

the set

\[
\{|P_Z(q)|>\eta\}
\]

has at most \(Q^C\eta^{-C}\) sign/monotonicity components.

### C. Acceleration–velocity lemma

On sign-controlled components, if

\[
|q''|\ge \eta
\]

and

\[
\|q'\|_{L^4}\le M,
\]

then the component length is bounded by a polynomial multiple of \(M^c\eta^{-C}\).

### D. Chart-good finite-jet bounds

\[
\|q\|_{C^K(I)}\le Q^C
\]

to control exceptional components and convert small measure into small \(L^2\)-mass.

These are local one-dimensional analytic inputs, shared with the finite-atlas/O2O3 regularity package.

---

## 7. Default wall choice

Because the proof directly uses

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\]

and

\[
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)},
\]

the default rank-two wall should be the jet wall:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{jet}}
=
\{\Gamma_G,\ D\Gamma_G,\ D^2\Gamma_G,\ \Gamma_{G,2}\}.
}
\]

The wall energy is

\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2),\mathrm{jet}}
=
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D\Gamma_G|^2
+
|D^2\Gamma_G|^2
+
|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right),
}
\]

with \(D\) scale-normalized.

The plain wall

\[
|H|^2(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2)
\]

is an optimization only if

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}
\]

is proved.

---

## 8. Gate–1 closure

Gate–1 gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

JetRankTwoCoercivity gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta.
\]

Therefore

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

Equivalently, the rank-two jet wall has polynomial mass.

---

## 9. Coherent amplitude caveat

If finite coherent vector amplitude terms remain, the coercivity argument applies after vector amplitude Schur. The target becomes

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
H(\Gamma_G,D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\mathcal C_{2Y,\mathrm{jet}}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right).
\]

If vector amplitude Schur fails, the branch is a coherently forced joint-flatness model. That is a separate finite-model problem, not a \(B_Y\)-local obstruction.

---

# Final result

The rank-two analytic theorem is now:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{JetRankTwoCoercivity}:
\quad
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2}
\text{ small}
\Rightarrow
\|q''\|_{L^2}
\text{ small}.
}
\]

The key exact identity is

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

Thus, if \(B_Y=0\), rank-two D4 plus Gate–1 gives wall mass using the jet wall. The remaining main blocker is still the finite local exactness certificate for \(B_Y=0\).

_Thought for 9s_

Continuing Agent 5 — vector amplitude caveat for rank-two D4.

I will keep the current notation:

\[
\rho_Y=\text{the }Y12\text{ fiber graph slope},
\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), these are not used in the wall. The rank-two jet wall is

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{jet}}
=
\{\Gamma_G,D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}.
\]

The clean case is \(\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}=0\). Then `JetRankTwoCoercivity + Gate–1` gives wall mass. The remaining case is finite coherent vector amplitude:

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}\neq0,
\]

but not locally free. The latest architecture explicitly distinguishes this amplitude layer from the local \(B_Y\)-layer. 

---

# 1. Rank-two vector amplitude model

Let the rank-two jet wall vector be

\[
\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}}
=
H
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_G\\
D\Gamma_G\\
D^2\Gamma_G\\
\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}
\]

up to the conditioned triangular D4 coefficient matrix. If finite coherent remnants remain from \(E_2\), \(R_{\mathrm{lab}}\), or other nonlocal completion terms, write

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y,\mathrm{jet}}^{\mathrm{arith}}
=
\operatorname{span}\{\Psi_1,\ldots,\Psi_M\}
\subset L^2(\nu;\mathbf C^4),
\]

with

\[
M\le Q^C
\]

and bounded leverage.

The required amplitude Schur condition is

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(\nu)}
\left(
\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}},
\mathcal C_{2Y,\mathrm{jet}}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\|\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}}\|_{L^2(\nu)}^2.
}
\]

If this holds, the rank-two branch proceeds essentially unchanged.

---

# 2. What if vector amplitude Schur fails?

Suppose amplitude Schur fails. Then there exists a coherent coefficient vector \(c=(c_a)\) such that

\[
\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}}
\approx
\sum_a c_a\Psi_a.
\]

Ignoring the harmless factor \(H\) and conditioned D4 matrix, this means

\[
\Gamma_G\approx \sum_a c_a\psi_{a,0},
\]

\[
D\Gamma_G\approx \sum_a c_a\psi_{a,1},
\]

\[
D^2\Gamma_G\approx \sum_a c_a\psi_{a,2},
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx \sum_a c_a\psi_{a,3}.
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_G=-6E_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=E_2,
\]

we get a forced residual model

\[
E_1\approx \Phi_1:= -\frac16\sum_a c_a\psi_{a,0},
\]

\[
E_2\approx \Phi_2:=\sum_a c_a\psi_{a,3}.
\]

Then the exact identity

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2
\]

gives

\[
\boxed{
q(q')^2
\approx
-\frac1{12}\left(\Phi_2-\Phi_1''\right).
}
\]

Also,

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+\Phi_1.
\]

Thus vector amplitude failure forces the coupled finite model

\[
\boxed{
q''=6q-2q^3+\Phi_1,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
q(q')^2=-\frac1{12}(\Phi_2-\Phi_1'').
}
\]

This is much more rigid than the rank-one forced ODE trap. The same coefficient vector \(c_a\) controls all jet components.

---

# 3. Same-coefficient guardrail

The coherent model must use the same coefficient vector across jet levels:

\[
\Psi_a=(\psi_{a,0},\psi_{a,1},\psi_{a,2},\psi_{a,3}).
\]

It is **not** allowed to approximate \(\Gamma_G,D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) with independent coefficients at each derivative level. If independent coefficients are allowed, the model becomes artificially locally free.

So the vector amplitude model is graph-like in derivative space, not vertically free.

This is the rank-two analogue of the trap-Schur guardrail from the rank-one branch.

---

# 4. VectorAmplitudeCoercivity theorem

The right fallback theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{VectorAmplitudeCoercivity}_{2Y}.
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(\mathcal C_{2Y,\mathrm{jet}}^{\mathrm{arith}}\) is finite-dimensional and has bounded leverage;

2. the coefficient vector is common across jet components;

3. the forcing pair

\[
(\Phi_1,\Phi_2)
\]

belongs to a finite chart-good algebra with local Remez/Markov control;

4. Gate–1 holds.

Then either

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}},
\mathcal C_{2Y,\mathrm{jet}}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)
\]

has polynomial mass, or the forced model

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+\Phi_1,
\]

\[
q(q')^2=-\frac1{12}(\Phi_2-\Phi_1'')
\]

contradicts Gate–1 / finite model nonabsorption.

So finite coherent amplitude is not automatically fatal. It creates a finite forced joint-flatness branch.

---

# 5. Why this forced model is rigid

In the unforced case, the system was

\[
q''=6q-2q^3,
\]

\[
q(q')^2=0.
\]

This forced \(q\) to be locally constant in \(\{0,\pm\sqrt3\}\).

With finite forcing,

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+\Phi_1,
\]

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3,
\qquad
\Phi_3=-\frac1{12}(\Phi_2-\Phi_1'').
\]

If \(\Phi_1,\Phi_3\) are small, the previous coercivity proof applies directly.

If \(\Phi_1,\Phi_3\) are not small, then the coherent amplitude model itself carries nontrivial finite energy. In that case, amplitude Schur should detect that \(F_{2Y}\) is not actually absorbed unless \(q\) follows this finite model.

Thus failure is localized to a finite-dimensional forced model:

\[
(q,\Phi_1,\Phi_3)
\]

with \(M\le Q^C\) degrees of forcing.

This is a standard finite-model nonabsorption problem, not the broad rank-one moving-line trap.

---

# 6. Practical route

For the rank-two proof, handle coherent amplitude in this order.

## Case A: no coherent amplitude

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{arith}}=0.
\]

Use raw jet wall and Gate–1.

## Case B: finite coherent amplitude with bounded leverage

Use raw finite wall family in O2/O3. Then prove vector amplitude Schur:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}},
\mathcal C_{2Y,\mathrm{jet}}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)^2
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}}\|^2.
\]

If Schur fails, route to `VectorAmplitudeCoercivity`.

## Case C: locally free amplitude

Rank-two route fails at amplitude layer. This is not \(B_Y\)-failure if there is no local tangent, but it kills extraction because the amplitude model can interpolate the wall.

---

# 7. Finite wall-family O2/O3 is unchanged

Do **not** put the projected residual

\[
(I-P_{\mathcal C})\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}}
\]

inside O2/O3 unless its branch-charge complexity is controlled.

Instead:

1. O2/O3 uses raw finite wall family

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{jet}}
=
\{\Gamma_G,D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}.
\]

2. After O2/O3, apply vector amplitude Schur under the smooth measure.

3. Extract blockwise if \(\mathcal C\neq0\).

This avoids circular projection and moving branch-charge.

---

# 8. Stronger conclusion

The rank-two branch now has a robust hierarchy:

\[
B_Y=0
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-two jet wall}.
\]

Then either:

1. no coherent amplitude: Gate–1 coercivity closes;

2. finite coherent amplitude: vector amplitude Schur closes;

3. amplitude Schur fails: forced finite joint-flatness model;

4. locally free amplitude: rank-two route fails at amplitude layer.

This is still much simpler than rank one.

---

## Final result

The vector amplitude caveat does not reintroduce the rank-one moving-wall trap. If finite coherent amplitude absorbs the rank-two jet wall, it forces the coupled system

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+\Phi_1,
\]

\[
q(q')^2=-\frac1{12}(\Phi_2-\Phi_1''),
\]

with the same finite coefficient vector controlling both forcings.

That is a rigid finite-model branch. The next theorem, if needed, is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{VectorAmplitudeCoercivity}_{2Y}.
}
\]

But first priority remains unchanged:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove }B_Y=0.
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-28 13:47:22)

I’ll push the finite coherent amplitude fallback: if vector amplitude Schur fails, derive the forced two-equation model and test whether Gate–1 can still dispose of it.

_Thought for 9s_

Continuing Agent 5 — forced finite-amplitude branch in rank-two D4.

No nomenclature changes:

\[
\rho_Y=\text{the }Y12\text{ fiber graph slope},\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), these do not enter the wall. The jet wall is

\[
\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\rm jet}
=
H\bigl(\Gamma_G,D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\bigr),
\]

up to a polynomially conditioned triangular coefficient matrix. The current fallback question is: if finite coherent vector amplitudes absorb this wall, does the rank-two branch still close by coercivity or does it create a genuine model branch? This is the finite-amplitude analogue of the rank-two coercivity module from the latest architecture. 

---

## 1. Vector amplitude failure gives a forced joint-flatness system

Let

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y,\rm jet}^{\arith}
=
\operatorname{span}\{\Psi_a\}_{a=1}^M
\subset L^2(\nu;\mathbf C^4),
\qquad M\le Q^C,
\]

with

\[
\Psi_a=(\psi_{a,0},\psi_{a,1},\psi_{a,2},\psi_{a,3}).
\]

The same coefficient vector must control all four components. If vector amplitude Schur fails, then for some \(c=(c_a)\),

\[
(\Gamma_G,D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\approx
\sum_a c_a(\psi_{a,0},\psi_{a,1},\psi_{a,2},\psi_{a,3}).
\]

Set

\[
\Phi_0:=\sum_a c_a\psi_{a,0},\qquad
\Phi_3:=\sum_a c_a\psi_{a,3}.
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_G=-6E_1,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=E_2,
\]

where

\[
E_1=q''-(6q-2q^3),
\]

\[
E_2=q^{(4)}-6(1-q^2)q'',
\]

the absorbed model gives

\[
E_1\approx -\frac16\Phi_0,
\qquad
E_2\approx \Phi_3.
\]

Using the identity

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2,
\]

we obtain the forced system

\[
\boxed{
q''=6q-2q^3-\frac16\Phi_0+\mathrm{err}_1,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
q(q')^2
=
-\frac1{12}\left(\Phi_3+\frac16\Phi_0''\right)
+\mathrm{err}_2.
}
\]

This is the rank-two finite-amplitude branch.

It is not a moving-line ODE. It is a coupled second-order-plus-energy constraint with finite coherent forcing.

---

## 2. Why this branch is more rigid than the rank-one trap

The rank-one trap allowed

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G\approx0,
\]

which is one fourth-order equation and permits many nonconstant local solutions.

Here, vector amplitude absorption imposes two linked conditions:

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+\Phi_1,
\]

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_2,
\]

where

\[
\Phi_1=-\frac16\Phi_0,
\qquad
\Phi_2=-\frac1{12}\left(\Phi_3+\frac16\Phi_0''\right).
\]

The same finite coefficient vector \(c_a\) determines both \(\Phi_1\) and \(\Phi_2\). This is a strong compatibility constraint.

The system has only finite forcing degrees of freedom, while \(q\) is an actual canonical source. Therefore this should be attacked by finite-model nonabsorption, not by broad wall finite type.

---

## 3. Forced coercivity statement

The natural theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{ForcedRankTwoCoercivity.}
}
\]

Let \(\Phi_1,\Phi_2\) belong to a finite coherent model \(\mathcal F_M\) with bounded leverage and \(M\le Q^C\). Suppose

\[
\left\|q''-(6q-2q^3)-\Phi_1\right\|_{H^2}
+
\left\|q(q')^2-\Phi_2\right\|_{L^2}
\le \delta.
\]

Then either:

1. \(q''\) is small:

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2}\le Q^C\delta^\theta,
\]

or

2. the forcing pair \((\Phi_1,\Phi_2)\) carries polynomial \(L^2\)-mass and is nonabsorbed by the coherent model, giving amplitude-Schur mass.

More concretely, if the coherent model has bounded leverage and no atom-local fitting, then the second alternative should force a finite Schur residual:

\[
\operatorname{dist}\bigl(\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\rm jet},
\mathcal C_{2Y,\rm jet}^{\arith}\bigr)
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\rm jet}\|.
\]

So persistent absorption should imply \(q''\) small, contradicting Gate–1, unless the model is locally free.

---

## 4. A direct route when forcing is small

If

\[
\|\Phi_1\|_{H^2}+\|\Phi_2\|_{L^2}\le \varepsilon,
\]

then the unforced RankTwoCoercivity proof applies immediately.

Indeed,

\[
q''-(6q-2q^3)=\Phi_1+\mathrm{err}_1,
\]

and

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_2+\mathrm{err}_2.
\]

Thus

\[
q(q')^2
\]

is small, and

\[
q''=f(q)+\text{small}.
\]

The same near-root/far-root decomposition gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2}\le Q^C\varepsilon^\theta.
\]

Gate–1 rules this out.

So the only hard case is:

\[
\boxed{
(\Phi_1,\Phi_2)\text{ is not small but is coherently matched to }q.
}
\]

---

## 5. Non-small forcing must satisfy compatibility

If \(\Phi_1\) is not small, then

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1
\]

forces acceleration. Meanwhile

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_2
\]

controls velocity except near \(q=0\).

Thus \((\Phi_1,\Phi_2)\) cannot be arbitrary. A compatibility condition is obtained by differentiating the second equation:

\[
(q(q')^2)'
=
q'(q')^2+2qq'q''
=
(q')^3+2qq'(f(q)+\Phi_1).
\]

Therefore,

\[
\Phi_2'
\approx
q'\bigl((q')^2+2qf(q)+2q\Phi_1\bigr).
\]

Using

\[
(q')^2\approx \Phi_2/q
\]

away from \(q=0\), this becomes an algebraic-differential compatibility relation among

\[
q,\Phi_1,\Phi_2,\Phi_2'.
\]

Since \(\Phi_1,\Phi_2\) live in a finite coherent model, this relation should be highly restrictive.

This suggests a stronger finite-model theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{ForcedPairCompatibility}_{2Y}
}
\]

saying that no bounded-leverage finite coherent forcing pair can match the canonical \(q\) on polynomial mass unless \(q''\) is small.

---

## 6. Practical Schur test for finite coherent forcing

Let

\[
\mathcal F
=
\operatorname{span}\{(\phi_{a,1},\phi_{a,2})\}_{a=1}^M
\]

be the induced forcing-pair model, where

\[
\phi_{a,1}=-\frac16\psi_{a,0},
\]

\[
\phi_{a,2}=-\frac1{12}\left(\psi_{a,3}+\frac16\psi_{a,0}''\right).
\]

The finite model nonabsorption test is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
(q''-f(q),\ q(q')^2),
\mathcal F
\right)^2
\ge Q^{-A}
\left(
\|q''-f(q)\|^2+\|q(q')^2\|^2
\right).
}
\]

If this holds, then vector amplitude Schur follows.

If it fails, \(q\) lies near the forced pair model. Then use ForcedRankTwoCoercivity to show either \(q''\) is small or the forcing has atom-local leverage. The latter is forbidden by the amplitude model assumptions.

---

## 7. Same-coefficient requirement is essential

The model

\[
\mathcal F
\]

must come from the same coefficient vector \(c_a\). It is not

\[
\operatorname{span}\{\phi_{a,1}\}\oplus
\operatorname{span}\{\phi_{a,2}\}
\]

with independent coefficients in the two equations.

If coefficients are independent, the model is much larger and may fit arbitrary forced dynamics. That would be local-free behavior in disguise.

So the vector amplitude model must be graph-like:

\[
c\mapsto(\Phi_1(c),\Phi_2(c)).
\]

This condition should be explicit in the theorem.

---

## 8. Rank-two amplitude fallback hierarchy

The rank-two branch with amplitudes has the following hierarchy:

### Level 0: no amplitude

Use raw jet wall and Gate–1 coercivity.

### Level 1: finite coherent amplitude

Prove vector amplitude Schur:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\rm jet},\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\arith})
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\rm jet}\|.
\]

### Level 2: Schur failure

Route to the forced pair model:

\[
(q''-f(q),q(q')^2)\in\mathcal F.
\]

### Level 3: forced pair disposal

Prove ForcedRankTwoCoercivity / ForcedPairCompatibility, or declare a finite-model branch.

This is still substantially simpler than rank-one, because the model is a coupled pair rather than a moving fourth-order ODE.

---

## 9. Current conclusion

Finite coherent vector amplitude does not destroy the rank-two route. It creates a stronger finite-model problem:

\[
\boxed{
(q''-f(q),\ q(q')^2)
\notin \mathcal F.
}
\]

The exact identity

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2
\]

turns vector amplitude absorption into this forced pair model.

So the rank-two route remains viable under finite coherent amplitude, provided:

1. the amplitude model has bounded leverage;
2. the same coefficient vector links all jet components;
3. the forced pair model is nonabsorbing or coercive.

The local priority is still \(B_Y=0\). The amplitude fallback is now sharply formulated if needed.

## Assistant (2026-04-28 13:49:21)

_Thought for 8s_

Continuing Agent 5 — forced pair model after rank-two vector amplitude absorption.

No nomenclature changes:

\[
\rho_Y=\text{the }Y12\text{ fiber graph slope},\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), the wall is not scalar. The relevant jet wall is

\[
\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\rm jet}
=
H(\Gamma_G,D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

The current issue is the finite coherent amplitude case. If vector amplitude Schur fails, the wall is absorbed by a finite coherent model, and the exact identity

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2
\]

converts that failure into a forced pair model. This is the right object to attack next. 

---

# 1. Forced pair model

Recall

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

\[
E_1=q''-f(q),
\]

\[
E_2=q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=-6E_1,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=E_2.
\]

Suppose finite coherent vector amplitude absorption gives

\[
E_1\approx \Phi_1,\qquad E_2\approx \Phi_2,
\]

where

\[
(\Phi_1,\Phi_2)
\in \mathcal F
\]

for a finite coherent forcing-pair model \(\mathcal F\), with a common coefficient vector.

Then

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1+\mathrm{err}_1,
\]

and

\[
q(q')^2
=
-\frac{1}{12}(\Phi_2-\Phi_1'')
+\mathrm{err}_2.
\]

Define

\[
\Phi_3:=-\frac{1}{12}(\Phi_2-\Phi_1'').
\]

So the forced pair branch is

\[
\boxed{
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1+\mathrm{err}_1,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
q(q')^2=\Phi_3+\mathrm{err}_2.
}
\]

This pair is the finite-amplitude analogue of joint flatness.

---

# 2. Coercivity when the forcing is small

If

\[
\|\Phi_1\|_{H^2}+\|\Phi_3\|_{L^2}\le \varepsilon,
\]

then the unforced RankTwoCoercivity proof applies directly:

\[
q''=f(q)+\text{small},
\]

\[
q(q')^2=\text{small}.
\]

Hence

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2}\le Q^C\varepsilon^\theta.
\]

Gate–1 contradicts this.

So the only genuinely new case is:

\[
\boxed{
(\Phi_1,\Phi_3)\text{ is not small, but the actual source tracks it coherently.}
}
\]

That must be treated as a finite-model nonabsorption problem.

---

# 3. Forced pair compatibility equation

The pair

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1,
\qquad
q(q')^2=\Phi_3
\]

is overdetermined. Differentiate the second equation:

\[
(q(q')^2)'=(q')^3+2qq'q''.
\]

Using the first equation:

\[
\Phi_3'
=
q'\left((q')^2+2qf(q)+2q\Phi_1\right)
+
\text{error}.
\]

Away from \(q=0\), use

\[
(q')^2=\frac{\Phi_3}{q}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_3'
=
q'
\left(
\frac{\Phi_3}{q}+2qf(q)+2q\Phi_1
\right)
+
\text{error}.
}
\]

Squaring and using again

\[
(q')^2=\Phi_3/q,
\]

gives an algebraic-differential compatibility condition:

\[
\boxed{
(\Phi_3')^2
\approx
\frac{\Phi_3}{q}
\left(
\frac{\Phi_3}{q}+2qf(q)+2q\Phi_1
\right)^2.
}
\]

This is a strong constraint linking \(q\), \(\Phi_1\), and \(\Phi_3\).

Because \((\Phi_1,\Phi_3)\) belongs to a finite coherent model, this compatibility should be hard to satisfy on a large Stack-good set unless \(q\) is itself trapped in a finite-dimensional model.

Thus the failure branch becomes:

\[
\boxed{
q\text{ lies near a finite-dimensional forced pair model.}
}
\]

---

# 4. ForcedPairNonAbsorption theorem

The natural theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{ForcedPairNonAbsorption}_{2Y}.
}
\]

Let \(\mathcal F\) be a finite coherent model of forcing pairs

\[
(\Phi_1,\Phi_3)
=
\sum_a c_a(\phi_{a,1},\phi_{a,3})
\]

with one common coefficient vector \(c\). Suppose \(\mathcal F\) has bounded leverage and finite chart complexity.

Then either

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
(q''-f(q),\ q(q')^2),
\mathcal F
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\left(
\|q''-f(q)\|^2+\|q(q')^2\|^2
\right),
\]

or \(q\) lies near a finite-dimensional forced pair solution manifold.

If it lies near that manifold, then one needs an anti-model theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual canonical }q\text{ cannot concentrate near this forced pair manifold on Gate--1/O2O3-good mass.}
}
\]

This is the exact fallback branch.

---

# 5. Same-coefficient constraint is essential

The model must be

\[
\mathcal F
=
\left\{
\sum_a c_a(\phi_{a,1},\phi_{a,3})
\right\}.
\]

It must **not** be

\[
\operatorname{span}\{\phi_{a,1}\}
\oplus
\operatorname{span}\{\phi_{a,3}\}
\]

with independent coefficients.

If independent coefficients are allowed, the finite model becomes artificially too large and can mimic local fitting. The common coefficient vector is the derivative/graph coherence condition at the amplitude level.

This same guardrail appeared in the trap-Schur hierarchy. It remains essential here.

---

# 6. Rank-two hierarchy with amplitude

The rank-two branch now has a clean hierarchy.

## Level 0: no coherent amplitude

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\arith}=0.
\]

Then

\[
\mathrm{JetRankTwoCoercivity}+\mathrm{Gate1}
\]

closes the wall.

## Level 1: finite coherent amplitude

Prove vector amplitude Schur:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\rm jet},
\mathcal C_{2Y,\rm jet}^{\arith}
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\|\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\rm jet}\|^2.
\]

Then wall mass survives.

## Level 2: vector Schur failure

Failure implies the forced pair model:

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1,
\]

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3.
\]

Then prove ForcedPairNonAbsorption or route to a finite forced-pair anti-model theorem.

## Level 3: locally free amplitude

Rank-two route fails at amplitude layer.

---

# 7. Why this is still better than rank one

Rank-one amplitude/wall failure produced a moving fourth-order relation:

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}+\rho_\Gamma\Gamma_G=0.
\]

That allows a broad class of fourth-order dynamics.

Rank-two amplitude failure produces two equations:

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1,
\]

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3.
\]

This is closer to an energy constraint plus an acceleration law. It is overdetermined. The finite forcing pair must satisfy compatibility identities.

Therefore rank-two remains substantially stronger even with finite coherent amplitudes.

---

# 8. Practical theorem to add to the rank-two stack

A useful conditional statement:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoAmplitudeFallback.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(B_Y=0\);

2. \(\mathcal C_{2Y,\rm jet}^{\arith}\) is finite coherent with bounded leverage;

3. finite wall-family O2/O3 has been applied to the raw jet wall;

4. vector amplitude Schur either holds, or fails.

Then:

- if vector amplitude Schur holds, D4 wall mass survives;
- if it fails, the source is forced into the finite pair model

\[
(q''-f(q),q(q')^2)\in\mathcal F;
\]

- if ForcedPairNonAbsorption holds, the rank-two branch still closes;
- if ForcedPairNonAbsorption fails, the remaining branch is an explicit finite forced-pair model, not a vague wall failure.

---

## Final result

Finite coherent vector amplitude does not undo the rank-two simplification. It changes the unforced coercivity identity into the forced pair system

\[
\boxed{
q''=6q-2q^3+\Phi_1,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
q(q')^2=\Phi_3.
}
\]

The same coefficient vector controls \(\Phi_1\) and \(\Phi_3\). This is a rigid finite-model branch.

So after \(B_Y=0\), the remaining path is:

\[
\text{raw rank-two jet wall}
\rightarrow
\text{vector amplitude Schur}
\rightarrow
\text{if needed, ForcedPairNonAbsorption}.
\]

The rank-one moving-wall machinery remains a fallback only if \(B_Y\neq0\).

## Assistant (2026-04-28 13:51:40)

I’ll push the forced pair branch further: derive a compatibility residual that finite coherent forcing must satisfy, so amplitude-Schur failure becomes a concrete finite determinant/ODE-model test rather than a vague fallback.

_Thought for 8s_

Continuing Agent 5 — compatibility residual for the forced pair branch.

No nomenclature changes:

\[
\rho_Y,\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), these are not used in the wall. The rank-two jet wall is

\[
\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}}
=
H(\Gamma_G,D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

If a finite coherent vector amplitude model absorbs this wall, the exact identity

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2
\]

turns amplitude-Schur failure into a forced pair model. This is now the correct fallback object, not the rank-one moving-line ODE trap. 

---

# 1. Forced pair system

Let

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

\[
E_1=q''-f(q),
\]

\[
E_2=q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

If finite coherent amplitude absorption holds, then for a common coefficient vector \(c=(c_a)\),

\[
E_1\approx \Phi_1(c),
\qquad
E_2\approx \Phi_2(c).
\]

Using

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2,
\]

define

\[
\Phi_3(c):=-\frac1{12}\left(\Phi_2(c)-\Phi_1(c)''\right).
\]

Then the forced pair model is

\[
\boxed{
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1(c)+\mathrm{err}_1,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
q(q')^2=\Phi_3(c)+\mathrm{err}_3.
}
\]

The same coefficient vector \(c\) determines both \(\Phi_1\) and \(\Phi_3\). This same-coefficient condition is essential; otherwise the model becomes artificially too large.

---

# 2. Eliminate \(q'\) to get a compatibility residual

Away from \(q=0\), the second equation gives

\[
(q')^2=\frac{\Phi_3}{q}+\mathrm{err}.
\]

Differentiate the second equation:

\[
(q(q')^2)'
=
(q')^3+2qq'q''.
\]

Using the first equation,

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1+\mathrm{err},
\]

we get

\[
\Phi_3'
=
q'\left((q')^2+2qf(q)+2q\Phi_1\right)
+
\mathrm{err}.
\]

Substitute

\[
(q')^2=\frac{\Phi_3}{q}
\]

to obtain

\[
\Phi_3'
=
q'
\left(
\frac{\Phi_3}{q}
+
2qf(q)
+
2q\Phi_1
\right)
+\mathrm{err}.
\]

Now square and again use

\[
(q')^2=\frac{\Phi_3}{q}.
\]

This yields the algebraic-differential compatibility residual

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{pair}}(q,\Phi_1,\Phi_3)
:=
q(\Phi_3')^2
-
\Phi_3
\left(
\frac{\Phi_3}{q}
+
2qf(q)
+
2q\Phi_1
\right)^2.
}
\]

On regions where \(|q|\ge\eta\), forced pair absorption implies

\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{pair}}\approx0
\]

with errors controlled by the original wall-residual errors and powers of \(\eta^{-1}\).

This is a concrete compatibility condition. It is the rank-two analogue of a trap equation, but it is algebraic in \(q,\Phi_1,\Phi_3,\Phi_3'\), not a broad fourth-order moving-line ODE.

---

# 3. Near \(q=0\)

The residual above divides by \(q\), so handle the region

\[
|q|<\eta
\]

separately.

There,

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1+\mathrm{err}
\]

becomes

\[
q''=\Phi_1+O(\eta)+\mathrm{err}.
\]

Also,

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3+\mathrm{err}
\]

implies \(\Phi_3\) must be small unless \(q'\) is very large; bounded chart energy and finite atlas regularity control that.

Thus on \(|q|<\eta\), the forced pair model implies either:

\[
\Phi_1\text{ is small and }q''\text{ is small},
\]

or

\[
\Phi_1
\]

itself carries nontrivial finite-model mass, which vector amplitude Schur should detect.

So the near-zero region does not create a free escape; it is a separate small-\(q\) compatibility branch.

---

# 4. Finite-model nonabsorption formulation

Let

\[
\mathcal F
=
\{(\Phi_1(c),\Phi_3(c)): c\in\mathbf C^M\}
\]

be the finite forcing-pair model.

The forced pair branch can now be tested by the finite residual map

\[
\boxed{
(c,q)\mapsto
\left(
q''-f(q)-\Phi_1(c),\
q(q')^2-\Phi_3(c),\
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{pair}}(q,\Phi_1(c),\Phi_3(c))
\right).
}
\]

A useful theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{ForcedPairCompatibility}_{2Y}.
}
\]

Assume \(\mathcal F\) has finite dimension \(M\le Q^C\), bounded leverage, and finite atlas regularity. Then either:

1. the vector amplitude Schur residual is polynomially nonzero; or

2. \(q\) lies near the finite-dimensional solution set of

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1(c),
\]

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3(c),
\]

\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{pair}}=0.
\]

This solution set is finite-dimensional and overdetermined.

---

# 5. Why this is likely disposable

For a fixed coherent forcing \(c\), the first equation is second-order:

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1(c).
\]

The second equation is a first-integral-like constraint:

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3(c).
\]

Those two equations overdetermine \(q\). Compatibility imposes

\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{pair}}=0.
\]

So the model is controlled by:

- the finite coefficients \(c_a\);
- two initial data for \(q\);
- compatibility constraints.

On a thick Stack-good set, this should have very small flexibility. In particular, it should not be able to match the actual canonical source unless the canonical source is trapped in a very explicit finite model.

This is a much tighter fallback than the rank-one forced ODE branch.

---

# 6. Practical theorem hierarchy

The rank-two amplitude fallback should be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoAmplitudeFallback.}
}
\]

Assume \(B_Y=0\), finite atlas regularity, and no locally free amplitude model. Then one of:

### A. Vector amplitude Schur

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}},
\mathcal C_{2Y,\mathrm{jet}}^{\mathrm{arith}}
\right)^2
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}}\|^2.
\]

### B. Forced pair compatibility branch

There exists a coherent coefficient vector \(c\) such that

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1(c)+\mathrm{small},
\]

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3(c)+\mathrm{small},
\]

and hence

\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{pair}}(q,\Phi_1(c),\Phi_3(c))=\mathrm{small}.
\]

### C. Locally free amplitude no-go

The amplitude model has extraction-scale interpolation power and rank-two D4 fails at amplitude level.

This trichotomy is precise.

---

# 7. Relation to Gate–1

If the forced pair compatibility branch implies

\[
q''
\]

is small, Gate–1 kills it immediately.

If it does not, then \(q''\) is large but constrained by a finite forced pair model. That becomes the next finite model nonabsorption theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual canonical }q\text{ cannot lie in this finite forced pair model on Gate--1/O2O3-good mass.}
}
\]

So Gate–1 still plays a central role: it either directly contradicts small \(q''\), or it supplies the energy that the finite model must somehow sustain.

---

# 8. Current conclusion

Vector amplitude absorption in the rank-two branch is not a broad failure. It produces the forced pair system

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+\Phi_1,
\]

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3,
\]

plus the compatibility residual

\[
\boxed{
q(\Phi_3')^2
-
\Phi_3
\left(
\frac{\Phi_3}{q}
+
2q(6q-2q^3)
+
2q\Phi_1
\right)^2
\approx0
}
\]

away from \(q=0\).

This gives a finite, overdetermined model branch. It is a much better fallback than the rank-one moving-line ODE trap.

The main priority remains \(B_Y=0\). If \(B_Y=0\) and vector amplitude Schur holds, the rank-two proof closes via Gate–1 coercivity. If amplitude Schur fails, we now have a precise forced-pair compatibility branch to attack.

## Assistant (2026-04-28 13:58:23)

_Thought for 5s_

No nomenclature changes.

Continuing Agent 5 — remove the division by \(q\) in the forced-pair compatibility residual.

The previous forced-pair compatibility residual was derived away from \(q=0\):

\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{pair}}
=
q(\Phi_3')^2
-
\Phi_3
\left(
\frac{\Phi_3}{q}
+
2qf(q)
+
2q\Phi_1
\right)^2.
\]

This is useful but has a bad feature: it divides by \(q\). The next step is to rewrite the compatibility condition in a polynomial form that remains meaningful near \(q=0\).

---

# 1. Forced pair model

Recall the forced pair equations:

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1,
\qquad
f(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3.
\]

Differentiate the second equation:

\[
\Phi_3'
=
(q')^3+2qq'q''.
\]

Using

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1,
\]

we get

\[
\Phi_3'
=
q'\left((q')^2+2q(f(q)+\Phi_1)\right).
\]

Now multiply by \(q\). Since

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3,
\]

we have

\[
q(q')^2+2q^2(f(q)+\Phi_1)
=
\Phi_3+2q^2(f(q)+\Phi_1).
\]

Thus

\[
q\Phi_3'
=
q'\left(\Phi_3+2q^2(f(q)+\Phi_1)\right).
\]

Square both sides:

\[
q^2(\Phi_3')^2
=
(q')^2\left(\Phi_3+2q^2(f(q)+\Phi_1)\right)^2.
\]

Finally use

\[
(q')^2=\frac{\Phi_3}{q},
\]

but multiply by \(q\) to avoid division:

\[
\boxed{
q^3(\Phi_3')^2
-
\Phi_3\left(\Phi_3+2q^2(f(q)+\Phi_1)\right)^2
=0.
}
\]

This is the polynomial compatibility residual:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}(q,\Phi_1,\Phi_3)
:=
q^3(\Phi_3')^2
-
\Phi_3\left(\Phi_3+2q^2(f(q)+\Phi_1)\right)^2.
}
\]

No division by \(q\). This is valid globally, including near \(q=0\).

---

# 2. Why the polynomial residual is better

The previous residual had a singularity at \(q=0\). But \(q=0\) is one of the equilibrium roots, and the rank-two coercivity proof already treats the near-zero region carefully.

The polynomial residual avoids a special analytic branch. If the forced pair model holds approximately, then

\[
\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}\approx0
\]

globally, with an error controlled by the two forced-pair residuals and finite-jet bounds.

This gives a clean finite-model test:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}
\text{ must be small if vector amplitude Schur fails.}
}
\]

Thus vector amplitude failure implies that \(q\) and the finite coherent forcing pair \((\Phi_1,\Phi_3)\) satisfy an overdetermined polynomial-differential system:

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1,
\]

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3,
\]

\[
\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}(q,\Phi_1,\Phi_3)=0.
\]

---

# 3. Approximate version

Let

\[
R_1:=q''-f(q)-\Phi_1,
\]

\[
R_3:=q(q')^2-\Phi_3.
\]

If

\[
\|R_1\|_{H^1}+\|R_3\|_{H^1}\le \varepsilon,
\]

then differentiating \(R_3\) gives

\[
(q(q')^2)'=\Phi_3'+O(\varepsilon).
\]

Using

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1+R_1
\]

in

\[
(q(q')^2)'=(q')^3+2qq'q'',
\]

we get

\[
\Phi_3'
=
q'\left((q')^2+2q(f(q)+\Phi_1)\right)
+
O(\varepsilon)
\]

in a scale-normalized \(L^2\) or distribution norm.

Multiplying by \(q\), squaring, and using

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3+R_3,
\]

gives

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}(q,\Phi_1,\Phi_3)\|
\le
Q^C\varepsilon
}
\]

in a suitable \(L^1\) or \(H^{-1}\) norm, under chart-good finite-jet bounds.

Thus the compatibility residual is stable.

---

# 4. Finite-model Schur test

Let the forcing model be

\[
(\Phi_1,\Phi_3)
=
\sum_{a=1}^M c_a(\phi_{a,1},\phi_{a,3}),
\qquad M\le Q^C.
\]

Define the model map

\[
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{pair}}
=
\left\{
(q,\Phi_1,\Phi_3):
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1,\ 
q(q')^2=\Phi_3,\ 
\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}=0
\right\}.
\]

The finite-model nonabsorption theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{ForcedPairNonAbsorption}_{2Y}.
}
\]

On a Gate–1/O2O3-good block, either

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
(q''-f(q),q(q')^2),
\mathcal F
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\left(
\|q''-f(q)\|^2+\|q(q')^2\|^2
\right),
\]

or \(q\) lies near the finite-dimensional solution set of the forced pair system.

This gives a precise fallback.

---

# 5. Can Gate–1 kill the forced pair system?

The unforced case has

\[
\Phi_1=0,\qquad \Phi_3=0,
\]

and gives \(q''=0\).

With forcing, Gate–1 does not automatically kill the branch if \(\Phi_1\) is large. Indeed,

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1
\]

can have large \(L^2\)-mass because \(\Phi_1\) has large \(L^2\)-mass.

So the right statement is not:

\[
\text{forced pair}\Rightarrow q''\text{ small}.
\]

The right statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{forced pair}\Rightarrow q''\text{ is controlled by a finite coherent model.}
}
\]

That means if the forced pair branch survives, the actual source is not free; it is trapped in a finite-dimensional ODE-energy model. This must be handled by finite-model nonabsorption or by showing the model cannot match the canonical source on Stack-good mass.

---

# 6. Stronger compatibility using the first equation

The polynomial residual \(\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}\) uses only the first derivative of the energy constraint. We can get another compatibility condition by differentiating the first equation and comparing with the derivative of \(\Phi_3\).

From

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1,
\]

we have

\[
q'''=f'(q)q'+\Phi_1'.
\]

But

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3.
\]

Differentiate twice if needed to express \(q'''\) in terms of \(q,q',\Phi_3,\Phi_3'\), then eliminate \(q'\) by squaring. This yields higher polynomial compatibility residuals involving

\[
\Phi_1,\Phi_1',\Phi_3,\Phi_3',\Phi_3''.
\]

Thus, if the finite forced pair model persists, it must satisfy a tower of algebraic-differential identities:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}^{(j)}(q,\Phi_1,\Phi_3)=0,
\qquad 0\le j\le J.
}
\]

This is the rank-two analogue of trap-Schur, but it is more rigid because the system starts with two equations.

---

# 7. Same-coefficient derivative lift

If the original vector amplitude model is

\[
\Psi_a=(\psi_{a,0},\psi_{a,1},\psi_{a,2},\psi_{a,3}),
\]

then the induced forcing pair is

\[
(\phi_{a,1},\phi_{a,3})
=
\left(
-\frac16\psi_{a,0},
-\frac1{12}\left(\psi_{a,3}+\frac16\psi_{a,0}''\right)
\right).
\]

The derivatives

\[
\Phi_1',\Phi_3',\Phi_3''
\]

must still be produced from the same coefficient vector:

\[
\sum_a c_a(\phi_{a,1}',\phi_{a,3}',\phi_{a,3}'').
\]

So the derivative-lifted model is

\[
\operatorname{span}
\left\{
(\phi_{a,1},\phi_{a,3},
\phi_{a,1}',\phi_{a,3}',\phi_{a,3}'',\ldots)
\right\}_a,
\]

not a direct sum with independent coefficients. This preserves finite coherence and prevents local fitting.

---

# 8. Practical conclusion

The vector amplitude fallback has now been reduced to a specific finite system.

If vector amplitude Schur fails, then the canonical source must satisfy, for some finite coherent forcing pair,

\[
\boxed{
q''=6q-2q^3+\Phi_1,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
q(q')^2=\Phi_3,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
q^3(\Phi_3')^2
-
\Phi_3
\left(
\Phi_3+2q^2(6q-2q^3+\Phi_1)
\right)^2
=0
}
\]

up to controlled error.

This is a concrete finite forced-pair model. It is the exact rank-two analogue of a trap branch, but much more overdetermined than the rank-one forced ODE.

---

## Final result

The forced finite-amplitude branch is no longer vague.

It is governed by the polynomial compatibility residual

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}
=
q^3(\Phi_3')^2
-
\Phi_3
\left(
\Phi_3+2q^2(f(q)+\Phi_1)
\right)^2.
}
\]

Therefore the rank-two branch has a precise fallback hierarchy:

\[
B_Y=0
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-two jet wall}
\Rightarrow
\text{vector amplitude Schur}
\Rightarrow
\text{if failure, forced pair compatibility model}.
\]

The immediate priority remains proving the finite local exactness certificate for \(B_Y=0\).

_Thought for 8s_

Continuing Agent 5 — reduce the forced pair branch to a finite determinant/nonabsorption test.

No nomenclature changes. In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), the relevant fallback after vector amplitude absorption is the forced pair model

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1,\qquad f(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3,
\]

with \((\Phi_1,\Phi_3)\) lying in a finite coherent forcing space and controlled by the same coefficient vector. The previous step produced the polynomial compatibility residual

\[
\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}
=
q^3(\Phi_3')^2
-
\Phi_3\left(\Phi_3+2q^2(f(q)+\Phi_1)\right)^2.
\]

This is now the correct forced-amplitude obstruction, not the old rank-one moving-line trap. 

---

# 1. Forced pair branch is overdetermined

For a fixed forcing pair \((\Phi_1,\Phi_3)\), the system

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1,
\]

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3
\]

already determines both acceleration and squared velocity. These two equations cannot be independently satisfied unless the compatibility residual vanishes:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}(q,\Phi_1,\Phi_3)=0.
}
\]

So if vector amplitude Schur fails, the source does not merely enter a broad ODE class. It enters the finite-dimensional model

\[
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{pair}}
=
\left\{
(q,c):
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1(c),\ 
q(q')^2=\Phi_3(c),\
\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}(q,\Phi_1(c),\Phi_3(c))=0
\right\}.
\]

This is the correct fallback branch.

---

# 2. The finite determinant test

Let

\[
(\Phi_1(c),\Phi_3(c))
=
\sum_{a=1}^{M}c_a(\phi_{a,1},\phi_{a,3})
\]

with \(M\le Q^C\). Define the target pair

\[
V(q)
=
(q''-f(q),\ q(q')^2).
\]

The first finite-model test is

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2}
\left(
V(q),
\mathcal F
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\|V(q)\|_{L^2}^2,
}
\]

where

\[
\mathcal F
=
\left\{
\sum_a c_a(\phi_{a,1},\phi_{a,3})
\right\}.
\]

If this holds, vector amplitude Schur holds. If it fails, choose the best coefficient vector \(c\) and force the compatibility residual.

The second finite-model test is then

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}(q,\Phi_1(c),\Phi_3(c))\|_{L^2}
\ge
Q^{-A}
\left(
\|\Phi_1(c)\|_{H^1}+\|\Phi_3(c)\|_{H^1}
\right)^{C}.
}
\]

If this residual is polynomially nonzero, the forced pair model is impossible at the required accuracy. If it is small, the source is genuinely trapped near \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{pair}}\).

Thus amplitude failure reduces to two finite Schur tests:

\[
V(q)\notin\mathcal F,
\]

or, if \(V(q)\in\mathcal F\),

\[
\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}\not\approx0.
\]

---

# 3. Same-coefficient determinant

The model matrix must be built with the same coefficient vector across all components and derivatives. The correct derivative-lifted basis is

\[
\Xi_a
=
\left(
\phi_{a,1},
\phi_{a,3},
\phi_{a,1}',
\phi_{a,3}',
\phi_{a,3}'',
\ldots
\right).
\]

The finite determinant should test the target vector

\[
\Xi(q)
=
\left(
q''-f(q),
q(q')^2,
(q''-f(q))',
(q(q')^2)',
(q(q')^2)'',
\ldots
\right)
\]

against

\[
\operatorname{span}\{\Xi_a\}_{a=1}^{M}.
\]

The model is **not**

\[
\operatorname{span}\{\phi_{a,1}\}
\oplus
\operatorname{span}\{\phi_{a,3}\}
\oplus
\operatorname{span}\{\phi_{a,1}'\}
\oplus\cdots
\]

with independent coefficients. That larger space would be an artificial local-fitting model.

So the rank-two forced-pair Schur residual is

\[
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{pair},J}^2
=
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\Xi_J(q),
\operatorname{span}\{\Xi_{a,J}\}_a
\right)^2.
}
\]

If

\[
\delta_{\mathrm{pair},J}^2\ge Q^{-A}\|\Xi_J(q)\|^2,
\]

the forced pair branch is eliminated.

---

# 4. What if the determinant also fails?

If

\[
\delta_{\mathrm{pair},J}
\]

is small for bounded \(J\), then the canonical source lies near a finite-dimensional forced-pair solution manifold. That is the terminal rank-two fallback:

\[
\boxed{
q\in \mathcal M_{\mathrm{pair},J}.
}
\]

This branch is still much smaller than the rank-one forced ODE branch. It has:

- finite coherent forcing coefficients \(c_a\);
- two linked equations for \(q\);
- polynomial compatibility residuals;
- same-coefficient derivative constraints.

The remaining theorem would be

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{ForcedPairAntiModel}_{2Y}.
}
\]

It should state that the actual canonical source cannot lie near \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{pair},J}\) on a Gate–1/O2O3-good block unless \(q''\) is small or the forcing model has local leverage.

---

# 5. Gate–1 interaction

The forced pair system gives

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1.
\]

So Gate–1 can be sustained only if either

\[
f(q)
\]

or

\[
\Phi_1
\]

has nontrivial \(L^2\)-mass.

But the second equation

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3
\]

controls velocity. If \(f(q)+\Phi_1\) is large on a thick set while velocity is constrained by \(\Phi_3\), then the compatibility residual \(\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}\) must become large unless \((\Phi_1,\Phi_3)\) is specially tuned.

Thus the forced pair branch should be disposed by one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{large acceleration + constrained velocity} \Rightarrow \mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}\neq0;
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}\approx0 \Rightarrow q''\text{ belongs to a finite coherent model.}
}
\]

The second alternative can be attacked by finite-model nonabsorption against the actual canonical source.

---

# 6. Practical rank-two fallback hierarchy

The rank-two amplitude fallback should now be:

### Step 1: vector amplitude Schur

\[
\operatorname{dist}
(\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}},
\mathcal C_{2Y,\mathrm{jet}}^{\mathrm{arith}})
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}}\|.
\]

If true, done.

### Step 2: forced pair Schur

If Step 1 fails, derive \(\mathcal F\) and test

\[
(q''-f(q),q(q')^2)\notin\mathcal F.
\]

If true, done.

### Step 3: compatibility residual

If Step 2 fails, test

\[
\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}\not\approx0.
\]

If true, done.

### Step 4: forced pair anti-model

If Step 3 fails, the source lies near \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{pair},J}\). This is the remaining finite model branch.

---

# 7. Why this matters

This hierarchy means finite coherent amplitude does not reintroduce the rank-one wall problem. It creates a **finite forced-pair model**, with an explicit polynomial compatibility residual.

So the rank-two route now has this structure:

\[
B_Y=0
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-two jet wall}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate–1 coercivity}
\]

unless finite coherent amplitude absorbs the wall; if so:

\[
\text{vector amplitude failure}
\Rightarrow
\text{forced pair model}
\Rightarrow
\text{compatibility residual / finite anti-model}.
\]

This is still a much tighter fallback than rank-one.

---

## Final result

The next precise theorem after vector amplitude Schur is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{ForcedPairCompatibilitySchur}_{2Y}.
}
\]

It tests the determinant-distance of

\[
(q''-f(q),\ q(q')^2,\ \text{derivatives})
\]

from the same-coefficient forcing-pair model. If it fails, the remaining branch is an explicit finite-dimensional forced-pair solution manifold.

The main priority remains the finite local exactness certificate \(B_Y=0\). But the amplitude fallback is now also sharply defined.

## Assistant (2026-04-28 14:02:48)

I’ll now connect the forced-pair fallback to the rank-two local exactness certificate. The goal is to see whether finite coherent amplitude can actually arise if \(B_Y=0\) and NoAtomFitting holds, or whether it is mostly residual/bookkeeping.

Continuing Agent 5 — can finite coherent amplitude survive after \(B_Y=0\)?

No nomenclature changes:

\[
\rho_Y,\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), these do not enter the wall. The live wall is the rank-two jet vector

\[
\mathbf F_{2Y}^{\mathrm{jet}}
=
H(\Gamma_G,D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

The current local exactness certificate is

\[
(I-P_{D_{2Y}})A_{2Y}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_{\min}\!\left(L_{2Y}^{*}(I-P_{D_{2Y}})L_{2Y}\right)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This says actual/local candidate columns die in the two-grade quotient, while \(e_7,e_Y\) survive.

The question now: after this certificate, what finite coherent amplitude space \(\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\arith}\) can remain?

---

## 1. \(B_Y=0\) eliminates local amplitude, not global coherent forcing

The statement

\[
B_Y=0
\]

means

\[
D_{\loc}\Pi_{\fib,Y}(E_2+R_{\lab}+T\mathcal M_Y^{\arith}+\mathcal N_{\sing})=0.
\]

It does **not** imply

\[
\Pi_{\fib,Y}(E_2+R_{\lab})=0
\]

as a fixed function.

So finite coherent amplitude can remain only in the form

\[
\Pi_{\fib,Y}(E_2+R_{\lab})
=
\text{fixed/block-coherent function}
+
\text{residual}.
\]

It cannot contain atom-local coordinates

\[
\eta_7(p)e_7(p)+\eta_Y(p)e_Y(p),
\]

nor graph-local coordinates

\[
\eta(p)(e_7(p)+\rho_Ye_Y(p)).
\]

Thus any surviving \(\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\arith}\) must be generated by fixed atlas/tail/chart functions, not by local fitting.

This is a severe restriction.

---

## 2. Candidate sources of \(\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\arith}\)

After \(B_Y=0\), finite coherent vector amplitude can only come from:

### A. Fixed completion/basepoint terms

These are deterministic offsets:

\[
C_{\mathrm{fixed}}(p).
\]

They do not form a tangent space; they shift the center. Usually they should be absorbed into the actual-row centering and not appear in amplitude Schur.

### B. Block-coherent tail/completion parameters

For example, a global tail truncation parameter or regularization choice may produce a small finite family

\[
\psi_a(p)
\]

across a block. This enters

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{E_2}.
\]

### C. Labelled transition mismatch depending on chart data

A fixed chart family may produce coherent functions

\[
\psi_a(p)
\]

in the live fiber. This enters

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\lab}.
\]

### D. Global normalizations

If global normalization choices shift the live pair coherently, they enter a finite model.

But none of these should have extraction-local leverage if NoAtomFitting is true.

Therefore the amplitude model dimension should be \(O(1)\) or \(Q^{o(1)}\), not comparable to atom count.

---

## 3. Leverage test becomes decisive

Even finite coherent amplitude is dangerous only if it has high leverage on extraction blocks.

For a block \(\Omega\), let

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y,\Omega}^{\arith}
=
\operatorname{span}\{\Psi_1,\ldots,\Psi_M\}
\subset L^2(\Omega;\mathbf C^4).
\]

The leverage kernel is

\[
K_{\Omega}(p)
=
\operatorname{tr}\!\left(
\Psi(p)G_{\Omega}^{\dagger}\Psi(p)^*
\right),
\]

where

\[
(G_{\Omega})_{ab}
=
\langle \Psi_a,\Psi_b\rangle_{L^2(\Omega;\mathbf C^4)}.
\]

Safe coherent amplitude requires

\[
\boxed{
K_{\Omega}(p)
\le
Q^C\frac{M}{\nu(\Omega)}
}
\]

on the smooth pre-extraction block.

If this holds, amplitude Schur is a standard finite-model nonabsorption theorem.

If leverage fails, the coherent model can behave like atom-local fitting even though \(D_{\loc}=0\).

So after \(B_Y=0\), the amplitude layer is mostly a leverage problem.

---

## 4. Can fixed coherent amplitude be subtracted before D4?

If a coherent component is fixed and independent of D4/wall variables, one can center the actual row:

\[
J_{\sing}(q''_{\can})
-
C_{\mathrm{fixed}}.
\]

This changes the upper relation, not the D4 variation. It should not affect the D4 lower.

Thus fixed deterministic amplitude should be treated as part of the basepoint:

\[
\eta_{\mathrm{fixed}}.
\]

Only finite-dimensional **variable** coherent amplitude should enter \(\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\arith}\).

This suggests the amplitude model may be smaller than currently assumed:

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\arith}
=
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\mathrm{variable\ coherent}},
\]

not including fixed offsets.

---

## 5. If amplitude Schur fails, forcing is highly structured

If despite bounded leverage vector amplitude Schur fails, then as previously derived,

\[
E_1\approx \Phi_1(c),
\qquad
E_2\approx \Phi_2(c)
\]

with a common coefficient vector. This gives

\[
q''=f(q)+\Phi_1(c),
\]

\[
q(q')^2=-\frac1{12}\bigl(\Phi_2(c)-\Phi_1(c)''\bigr).
\]

But because the coherent basis functions come from fixed atlas/tail/chart data, they lie in the same finite algebra \(\mathscr A_I\). Therefore the forced pair model is not arbitrary; it is a finite algebraic/analytic model with Remez/Markov control.

This means `ForcedPairNonAbsorption` should be accessible by the same finite-model determinant machinery as O2/O3.

---

## 6. Stronger claim: vector amplitude Schur may follow from RankTwoCoercivity plus leverage

Suppose vector amplitude Schur fails. Then the residual wall after subtracting \(\mathcal C\) is small. If the coherent model has bounded leverage and finite complexity, the forcing pair \((\Phi_1,\Phi_3)\) is smooth/coherent.

If \((\Phi_1,\Phi_3)\) is small, Gate–1 kills it.

If it is not small, then the coherent model itself contributes nontrivial wall energy. Since O2/O3 used the raw wall, that energy was already present before projection. The only way it can mask the D4 contradiction is if the actual upper relation also allows the same coherent model.

But the upper relation should already subtract \(\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\arith}\). Thus the contradiction becomes block-Schur:

\[
\text{lower raw wall mass}
\quad
\text{versus}
\quad
\text{upper distance-to-}\mathcal C\text{ small}.
\]

Therefore amplitude Schur is exactly the needed bridge. It should not be merged into coercivity unless necessary.

---

## 7. Current best hierarchy

For rank two, after \(B_Y=0\):

### Step 1: remove fixed deterministic offsets

Treat them as basepoint corrections, not amplitude tangent space.

### Step 2: classify variable coherent amplitudes

If none:

\[
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\arith}=0.
\]

Proceed with JetRankTwoCoercivity.

If finite coherent with bounded leverage:

run vector amplitude Schur.

If locally free or high leverage:

rank-two route fails at amplitude layer.

### Step 3: if vector amplitude Schur fails

derive forced pair model and test ForcedPairCompatibility.

This is only a fallback.

---

## Final result

The local exactness theorem \(B_Y=0\) already eliminates the main dangerous amplitude mechanism: atom-local live-fiber fitting.

Any surviving coherent amplitude must be fixed or finite/block-coherent. Fixed offsets can be centered away. Variable coherent amplitudes require vector amplitude Schur with bounded leverage.

If vector amplitude Schur fails, the exact identity forces the finite pair model

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+\Phi_1,
\qquad
q(q')^2=\Phi_3,
\]

with \((\Phi_1,\Phi_3)\) in a finite coherent algebra. This is the final explicit rank-two fallback, but it should be reached only after \(B_Y=0\) and amplitude Schur classification.
