# Agent 5 — PlainWallRankTwoClosure

## 1. Normalization

Use the current normalization

\[
\Gamma_G=-6q''+36q-12q^3.
\]

Set

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=-6(q''-f(q)).
\]

Define

\[
E_1=q''-f(q).
\]

Also

\[
f'(q)=6-6q^2,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=q^{(4)}-6(1-q^2)q''
=
q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Define

\[
E_2=q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Thus

\[
\Gamma_G=-6E_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=E_2.
\]

Differentiate

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1.
\]

Then

\[
q'''=f'(q)q'+E_1',
\]

and

\[
q^{(4)}
=
f''(q)(q')^2+f'(q)q''+E_1''.
\]

Therefore

\[
E_2-E_1''=f''(q)(q')^2.
\]

Since

\[
f''(q)=-12q,
\]

we get the exact identity

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

This identity is the analytic core of the rank-two wall closure.

---

## 2. Exact flatness

If

\[
E_1=0,\qquad E_2=0,
\]

then

\[
q(q')^2=0.
\]

On any connected interval where \(q\neq0\), this gives

\[
q'=0.
\]

Therefore

\[
q''=0.
\]

But \(E_1=0\) also gives

\[
q''=f(q)=2q(3-q^2).
\]

Thus exact solutions are locally

\[
q\equiv0,\qquad q\equiv\sqrt3,\qquad q\equiv-\sqrt3,
\]

and in every case

\[
q''\equiv0.
\]

So exact joint flatness of the rank-two wall kills Gate–1 energy.

---

## 3. Quantitative RankTwoCoercivity

The coercivity theorem needed is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}.
}
\]

On a chart-good interval \(I\), with scale-normalized norms and polynomial finite-complexity bounds,

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta.
\]

Proof skeleton:

Let

\[
\delta=\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}+\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}.
\]

From

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2,
\]

we get

\[
\|q(q')^2\|_{L^2(I)}\le C\delta.
\]

Let

\[
Z=\{0,\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\}.
\]

Choose

\[
\eta=\delta^\kappa
\]

for small fixed \(\kappa>0\). Split

\[
I_{\mathrm{near}}
=
\{x:\operatorname{dist}(q(x),Z)\le\eta\},
\]

\[
I_{\mathrm{far}}
=
I\setminus I_{\mathrm{near}}.
\]

On \(I_{\mathrm{near}}\), since \(f\) has simple roots at \(Z\),

\[
|f(q)|\le C\eta.
\]

Thus

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1
\]

gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{near}})}
\le
C\eta |I|^{1/2}+\|E_1\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
C\eta |I|^{1/2}+\delta.
\]

On \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\),

\[
|f(q)|\ge c\eta,
\qquad
|q|\ge c\eta.
\]

The identity gives

\[
\|q'\|_{L^4(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
C\delta^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2}.
\]

Because

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1,
\]

and \(E_1\in H^2\), Sobolev/finite-complexity control gives

\[
\|E_1\|_{C^0(I)}
\le Q^C\delta.
\]

For \(\delta\ll Q^{-C}\eta\),

\[
|q''|\ge c\eta
\]

on the far region, except for polynomially negligible exceptional subsets.

A one-dimensional acceleration–velocity lemma plus finite-component/Remez control gives

\[
|I_{\mathrm{far}}|\le Q^C\delta^a\eta^{-b}
\]

for fixed \(a,b>0\). With chart-good \(C^K\)-bounds,

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
Q^C\delta^{a/2}\eta^{-b/2}.
\]

Choosing \(\kappa\) sufficiently small yields

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\le Q^C\delta^\theta.
}
\]

---

## 4. LocalMarkov\(_{\Gamma_G}\)

RankTwoCoercivity requires

\[
\Gamma_G\in H^2(I),
\]

but D4 honestly gives only the plain wall component

\[
\Gamma_G
\]

in \(L^2\). Therefore we need

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}:
\quad
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}.
}
\]

This must be proved in the finite local EF/AFE chart, not assumed.

Let \(\mathcal V_I\) be the local finite chart space for \(q\). Since

\[
\Gamma_G=-6q''+36q-12q^3,
\]

we have

\[
\Gamma_G\in
\mathcal W_I
:=
D^2\mathcal V_I+\mathcal V_I+\operatorname{Sym}^3\mathcal V_I.
\]

So LocalMarkov becomes the finite Riesz/Gram statement:

choose a basis \(\{\psi_i\}\) of \(\mathcal W_I\), define

\[
G_0=(\langle\psi_i,\psi_j\rangle_{L^2(I^*)}),
\]

\[
G_2=(\langle\psi_i,\psi_j\rangle_{H^2(I)}).
\]

Need

\[
\boxed{
G_2\preceq Q^C G_0.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\lambda_{\max}\left(G_0^{-1/2}G_2G_0^{-1/2}\right)
\le Q^C.
\]

This is a finite-dimensional Markov/Riesz theorem for the local chart algebra.

---

## 5. PlainWallRankTwoClosure theorem

The corrected analytic closure is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{PlainWallRankTwoClosure}.
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(B_Y=0\), so D4 remains rank two;

2. D4 coefficients are conditioned:

\[
|c_7\alpha_9|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|c_7|+|\alpha_9|+|\beta_9|\le Q^A;
\]

3. LocalMarkov\(_{\Gamma_G}\) holds:

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)};
\]

4. RankTwoCoercivity holds:

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta;
\]

5. Gate–1 holds:

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Thus the honest plain rank-two wall has polynomial mass.

---

## 6. Weighted transfer still required

The above gives an unweighted local wall lower. O2/O3 needs weighted smooth wall mass:

\[
\int N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)d\nu
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

So after PlainWallRankTwoClosure we need:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{WeightedPlainWallTransfer}_{2Y}.
}
\]

Required hypotheses:

\[
|H|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

on selected good blocks, and

\[
N_{\mathrm{sm}}\ge Q^{-A}
\]

or at least polynomial lower average / slow variation on the same blocks.

If weights are not uniformly good, select blocks before hard extraction where

\[
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\]

has polynomial average while retaining Gate–1 wall mass.

This transfer should be explicit; otherwise there is a gap between Gate–1 coercivity and O2/O3 input.

---

## 7. Scalar O2/O3 after weighted transfer

Once

\[
\int N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)d\nu
\ge Q^{-A},
\]

choose one fixed component at the smooth aggregate stage:

\[
G_\star\in\{\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}
\]

such that

\[
\int N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2|G_\star|^2\,d\nu
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

Then O2/O3 runs with scalar bounded-charge weight

\[
W_\star=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2|G_\star|^2.
\]

The component \(G_\star\) must not be chosen atomwise after extraction.

---

## 8. Coherent amplitude caveat

If finite coherent vector amplitude remains, do not project the wall before O2/O3 unless projection complexity is controlled.

Use the raw plain wall for O2/O3:

\[
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2).
\]

Then apply vector amplitude Schur afterward. If vector amplitude Schur fails, route to the forced pair branch:

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+\Phi_1,
\]

\[
q(q')^2=\Phi_3,
\]

with compatibility residual

\[
\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}
=
q^3(\Phi_3')^2
-
\Phi_3
\left(
\Phi_3+2q^2(6q-2q^3+\Phi_1)
\right)^2.
\]

This is a fallback, not the main line.

---

## Final result

The corrected rank-two analytic route is:

\[
\boxed{
B_Y=0
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
F_{2Y}\asymp H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}
+
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}
+
\mathrm{Gate1}
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
\text{plain rank-two wall mass}
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
\mathrm{WeightedPlainWallTransfer}_{2Y}
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
\text{scalar O2/O3 with }G_\star\in\{\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}.
}
\]

The jet family remains an analytic auxiliary only unless derivative D4 channels are separately proved.

I’ll continue on the corrected plain-wall path by attacking the missing transfer step: how local Gate–1/Markov wall mass becomes the weighted smooth wall mass needed for O2/O3, without introducing a moving selector.

_Thought for 12s_

Continuing Agent 5 — weighted transfer for the corrected plain rank-two wall.

No nomenclature changes:

\[
\rho_Y,\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), these do not enter the wall. The honest D4 wall is the plain vector wall

\[
F_{2Y}
=
H
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\Gamma_G\\
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}
\asymp_{Q^A}
H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

The previous step gave the corrected local analytic closure:

\[
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}
+
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}
+
\mathrm{Gate1}
\Longrightarrow
\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Now we need to transfer this local unweighted wall mass into the smooth weighted wall needed by O2/O3:

\[
\int
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)d\nu
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

This is the current missing bridge. The latest correction explicitly says the plain wall is the honest D4 wall; derivative wall components are only analytic auxiliaries unless separate derivative-D4 channels are proved. 

---

# 1. Define the plain wall density

Let

\[
W_2(m)
=
|\Gamma_G(m)|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|^2.
\]

The rank-two local closure gives, on Gate–1-good local blocks \(I\),

\[
\int_I W_2(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

The weighted O2/O3 wall wants

\[
\int_I N_{\mathrm{sm}}(m)|H(m)|^2W_2(m)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A'}|I|.
\]

So the transfer problem is:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I W_2\ge Q^{-A}|I|
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\int_I \Omega W_2\ge Q^{-A'}|I|,
}
\]

where

\[
\Omega=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2.
\]

This is false for arbitrary \(\Omega\). We need a “good-weight” selection.

---

# 2. Good-weight block selection

Define a block \(I\) to be weight-good if

\[
\int_I \Omega(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A_\Omega}|I|
\]

and \(\Omega\) has bounded local oscillation or at least a nontrivial lower-level set:

\[
|\{m\in I:\Omega(m)\ge Q^{-A_\Omega}\}|
\ge Q^{-A_\Omega}|I|.
\]

Then if \(W_2\) is not adversarially concentrated away from this lower-level set, we get weighted transfer.

The required anti-concentration is modest because \(W_2\) is itself a finite-algebra expression. A useful lemma is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{WeightedTransferRemez.}
}
\]

Let \(W_2\) be a nonnegative finite-complexity wall density on \(I\). If

\[
\int_I W_2\ge Q^{-A}|I|
\]

and

\[
|\{m:\Omega(m)\ge Q^{-B}\}|\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

then

\[
\int_I \Omega W_2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\]

provided \(W_2\) satisfies finite-algebra Remez/leverage control.

This prevents \(W_2\) from placing all its mass on the complement of the good-weight set.

---

# 3. Why finite-algebra control is enough

The wall density

\[
W_2=|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\]

belongs to a finite algebra generated by the same local chart expressions as \(q\). Therefore \(W_2\) cannot vanish on a polynomial-measure subset unless it is small in a controlled way.

If \(E\subset I\) has

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

then a Remez-type inequality gives

\[
\int_E W_2
\ge Q^{-C}\int_I W_2.
\]

Taking

\[
E=\{\Omega\ge Q^{-B}\},
\]

we obtain

\[
\int_I \Omega W_2
\ge
Q^{-B}\int_E W_2
\ge
Q^{-C}\int_I W_2
\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

Thus weighted transfer follows from two finite properties:

1. \(\Omega\) has a polynomial lower-level set;
2. \(W_2\) has Remez/nonconcentration on polynomial-measure sets.

Both should be part of the smooth block-good setup.

---

# 4. If \(\Omega\) is not good everywhere

If \(\Omega=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2\) is not polynomially nonzero on all Gate–1-good blocks, we need a dyadic block selection.

Decompose the stack into dyadic \(\Omega\)-levels:

\[
\mathcal B_k
=
\{m:2^{-k-1}<\Omega(m)\le2^{-k}\}.
\]

Discard levels with

\[
2^{-k}<Q^{-A_\Omega}
\]

if their total Gate–1/wall contribution is negligible. On the remaining levels, \(\Omega\ge Q^{-A_\Omega}\).

The transfer then runs levelwise:

\[
\int_{\mathcal B_k} \Omega W_2
\ge
2^{-k}
\int_{\mathcal B_k} W_2.
\]

One must ensure that some good level carries polynomial wall mass:

\[
\int_{\mathcal B_k} W_2\ge Q^{-A}\int W_2.
\]

Since there are only \(O(\log Q)\) relevant dyadic levels, this loses only a polynomial/log factor.

Thus the selection rule is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{select a dyadic }\Omega\text{-level at the smooth aggregate stage.}
}
\]

Do not select after hard extraction.

---

# 5. Component selection after weighted transfer

Once we have

\[
\int N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)d\nu
\ge Q^{-A},
\]

we select a scalar component at the smooth aggregate stage:

\[
G_\star\in\{\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}
\]

such that

\[
\int
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2|G_\star|^2\,d\nu
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

This is a fixed finite choice, not an atomwise selector.

Then O2/O3 runs with scalar weight

\[
W_\star=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2|G_\star|^2.
\]

This keeps branch-charge bounded.

---

# 6. Correct rank-two O2/O3 bandwidth

For the plain rank-two wall,

\[
\mathcal G_{\mathrm{wall}}^{(2)}=\{\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}.
\]

The scalar component \(G_\star\) has branch-charge degree

\[
d(G_\star)\le d_{\Gamma}^{(2)}
:=
\max\{d(\Gamma_G),d(\Gamma_{G,2})\}.
\]

Thus

\[
d_0^{(2)}
=
d_N+2d_H+2d_{\Gamma}^{(2)}.
\]

No \(\rho_\Gamma\). No derivative wall degrees.

This is a major simplification over rank one.

The O2/O3 theorem needed is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{NearPureO2/O3}(d_0)
\quad
\text{for all }d_0\le d_{\max}.
}
\]

If current conservative

\[
d_{\max}=14
\]

dominates \(d_0^{(2)}\), no update is needed. If not, adjust \(d_{\max}\) once, but keep it fixed.

---

# 7. Interaction with LocalMarkov

Important: LocalMarkov is used **before** weighted transfer.

The sequence is:

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2}
\text{ small}
\]

\[
\Rightarrow
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2}
\text{ small}
\]

by LocalMarkov,

\[
\Rightarrow
\|q''\|_{L^2}\text{ small}
\]

by RankTwoCoercivity,

\[
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate–1 contradiction}.
\]

So Gate–1 gives unweighted plain wall mass. Weighted transfer then uses finite-algebra Remez and dyadic \(\Omega\)-selection.

Do not attempt to prove RankTwoCoercivity with weighted norms directly; that would mix analytic coercivity with O2/O3 weight bookkeeping.

---

# 8. Coherent amplitude caveat

If finite coherent vector amplitude exists, the same order remains:

1. Prove raw weighted plain wall mass.

2. Run O2/O3 with raw scalar component \(G_\star\).

3. Apply vector amplitude Schur afterward:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
F_{2Y},
\mathcal C_{2Y}^{\arith}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}\|F_{2Y}\|.
\]

Do not replace

\[
W_\star
\]

by a projected component unless projection branch-charge is controlled.

If amplitude Schur fails, route to the forced pair branch:

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+\Phi_1,
\qquad
q(q')^2=\Phi_3.
\]

This remains secondary.

---

# 9. WeightedPlainWallTransfer theorem

A clean theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{WeightedPlainWallTransfer}_{2Y}.
}
\]

Assume:

1. local rank-two wall mass:

\[
\int_I W_2\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|
\]

on a family of Gate–1-good blocks;

2. \(\Omega=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2\) has polynomial lower dyadic mass on those blocks:

\[
|\{\Omega\ge Q^{-B}\}\cap I|
\ge Q^{-B}|I|;
\]

3. \(W_2\) satisfies finite-algebra Remez/nonconcentration:

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-B}|I|
\Rightarrow
\int_E W_2\ge Q^{-C}\int_I W_2.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I \Omega W_2\,dm\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
}
\]

Summing over selected blocks gives global smooth weighted wall mass.

---

## Final result

The corrected rank-two wall pipeline is now:

\[
B_Y=0
\Rightarrow
F_{2Y}\asymp H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

\[
\Rightarrow
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}
+
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}
+
\mathrm{Gate1}
\Rightarrow
\int W_2\ge Q^{-A}
\]

\[
\Rightarrow
\mathrm{WeightedPlainWallTransfer}_{2Y}
\Rightarrow
\int N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2W_2\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

\[
\Rightarrow
\text{choose fixed }G_\star\in\{\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}
\text{ at smooth aggregate stage}
\]

\[
\Rightarrow
\text{scalar O2/O3 with }
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2|G_\star|^2.
\]

This keeps the D4 wall honest and avoids derivative wall components unless derivative-D4 channels are separately proved.

## Assistant (2026-04-28 14:17:13)

I’ll stress-test the weighted-transfer step. The key issue is Remez constants: a lower-weight set of merely \(Q^{-B}\) measure may be too small if the wall component has degree \(R\).

_Thought for 13s_

Continuing Agent 5 — stress test and repair of `WeightedPlainWallTransfer`.

No nomenclature changes. In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), the honest D4 wall is still the plain vector wall

\[
F_{2Y}\asymp H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

not the jet family. The corrected pipeline is:

\[
\text{plain wall mass}
\rightarrow
\text{weighted plain wall transfer}
\rightarrow
\text{scalar O2/O3 with }G_\star\in\{\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}.
\]

The possible gap is in the transfer

\[
\int_I W_2\ge Q^{-A}|I|
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\int_I \Omega W_2\ge Q^{-A'}|I|,
\]

where

\[
W_2=|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2,
\qquad
\Omega=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2.
\]

---

# 1. Remez constants force an \(R\)-scale lower set, not merely \(Q\)-scale

A previous statement allowed a lower-weight set

\[
E=\{\Omega\ge Q^{-B}\}
\]

with

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

That is too weak if the wall components live in a degree-\(R\) finite algebra.

For polynomials of degree \(R\), Remez constants behave like

\[
\left(\frac{C}{|E|/|I|}\right)^R.
\]

If

\[
|E|/|I|=Q^{-B},
\]

then the loss is

\[
Q^{BR}
=
\exp\!\left(BR\log Q\right),
\]

which is super-polynomial when

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

So the transfer is only polynomial if

\[
|E|/|I|\ge R^{-C},
\]

because then

\[
(R^C)^R
=
\exp(CR\log R)
=
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Thus the corrected weighted-transfer condition is:

\[
\boxed{
|\{\Omega\ge Q^{-B}\}\cap I|\ge R^{-C}|I|,
}
\]

not merely \(Q^{-B}|I|\), unless we have a stronger structural reason that \(W_2\) cannot avoid \(E\).

This is an important correction.

---

# 2. Correct weighted transfer theorem

The usable theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{WeightedPlainWallTransfer}_{2Y}^{R}.
}
\]

Assume on a chart-good interval \(I\):

1. unweighted rank-two wall mass:

\[
\int_I W_2\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|;
\]

2. the good-weight set

\[
E_\Omega(\tau)=\{m\in I:\Omega(m)\ge \tau\}
\]

has

\[
|E_\Omega(\tau)|\ge R^{-C}|I|
\]

for some

\[
\tau\ge Q^{-A_\Omega};
\]

3. \(W_2\) belongs to an \(R^C\)-conditioned degree-\(R\) finite algebra satisfying Remez on \(I\).

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I \Omega W_2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-A'}|I|.
}
\]

Proof:

By Remez / Logvinenko–Sereda for the finite algebra,

\[
\int_{E_\Omega(\tau)} W_2
\ge
Q^{-C}\int_I W_2.
\]

Then

\[
\int_I \Omega W_2
\ge
\tau \int_{E_\Omega(\tau)}W_2
\ge
Q^{-A_\Omega-C}\int_I W_2
\ge
Q^{-A'}|I|.
\]

The \(R^{-C}\)-measure condition is what keeps the Remez loss polynomial.

---

# 3. How to get the \(R^{-C}\)-measure lower set

We need a separate weight-goodness lemma for

\[
\Omega=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2.
\]

There are three possible routes.

## Route A: block construction enforces it

If the Stack C2/O2O3 block selection is already made only where

\[
N_{\mathrm{sm}}\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|H|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

on an \(R^{-C}\)-fraction or most of the block, then weighted transfer is immediate.

This is the cleanest.

## Route B: dyadic level selection

Decompose

\[
\Omega
\]

into dyadic levels. Because only \(O(\log Q)\) levels above \(Q^{-A}\) matter, if the total weighted mass is not negligible, some level has both:

\[
\Omega\sim \tau\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and

\[
|E_\tau|\ge R^{-C}|I|
\]

after possibly restricting to a subblock.

But this requires the stack measure not to be supported on ultra-thin \(\Omega\)-spikes.

## Route C: \(\Omega\) itself has finite-algebra nonspiking

If

\[
\Omega
\]

is also a finite-algebra / smooth bounded-complexity function, then it cannot be large only on \(Q^{-B}\)-thin sets without Remez cost. So if

\[
\int_I\Omega\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

then there exists

\[
\tau\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

such that

\[
|\{\Omega\ge\tau\}|\ge R^{-C}|I|.
\]

This is a plausible finite-atlas lemma.

The corrected transfer therefore needs:

\[
\boxed{
\Omega\text{ has polynomial average and finite-algebra nonspiking,}
}
\]

or direct block-goodness with an \(R^{-C}\)-fraction lower set.

---

# 4. Avoiding adversarial anti-correlation

Even if \(E_\Omega\) has \(R^{-C}\)-measure, \(W_2\) could, in principle, concentrate outside \(E_\Omega\). Remez prevents this only if \(W_2\) is a controlled finite-algebra expression.

For a sum of squares

\[
W_2=|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2,
\]

the Remez inequality should be applied to the vector function

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

or to \(W_2\) itself as a nonnegative finite-algebra element.

A safe statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\int_E \left(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2\right)
\ge
Q^{-C}
\int_I \left(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2\right)
}
\]

for any measurable \(E\subset I\) with

\[
|E|\ge R^{-C}|I|.
\]

This is a vector Logvinenko–Sereda/Remez inequality for the finite wall family.

That is the exact finite-algebra property needed.

---

# 5. Consequence for O2/O3 component selection

After weighted transfer gives

\[
\int_I \Omega
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)
\ge Q^{-A},
\]

we can select

\[
G_\star\in\{\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}
\]

at the smooth aggregate stage.

Since there are only two components,

\[
\int_I \Omega |G_\star|^2
\ge \frac12 Q^{-A}.
\]

This selection is safe if it is made per global/dyadic block class before hard extraction. It is not safe if chosen atomwise after extraction.

Thus the scalar O2/O3 input is:

\[
W_\star=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2|G_\star|^2.
\]

Bandwidth:

\[
d_0^{(2)}
=
d_N+2d_H+2d(G_\star)
\le
d_N+2d_H+2\max(d_{\Gamma_G},d_{\Gamma_{G,2}}).
\]

---

# 6. Updated rank-two weighted transfer module

The corrected module is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RankTwoWeightedWallModule.}
}
\]

Inputs:

1. \(B_Y=0\);

2. LocalMarkov\(_{\Gamma_G}\) and RankTwoCoercivity give unweighted wall mass:

\[
\int_I W_2\ge Q^{-A}|I|;
\]

3. weight-goodness:

\[
\exists \tau\ge Q^{-A_\Omega}
\quad\text{such that}\quad
|\{\Omega\ge\tau\}\cap I|\ge R^{-C}|I|;
\]

4. vector Remez for wall family:

\[
|E|\ge R^{-C}|I|
\Rightarrow
\int_E W_2\ge Q^{-C}\int_I W_2.
\]

Conclusion:

\[
\int_I \Omega W_2\ge Q^{-A'}|I|.
\]

Then finite component selection gives scalar O2/O3 with

\[
G_\star\in\{\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}.
\]

---

# 7. Why this is still plausible

This corrected transfer is not a new deep arithmetic input. It is another finite-atlas regularity statement.

The same Riesz/Remez infrastructure needed for:

\[
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}
\]

and O2/O3 near-pure separation should also imply vector Remez for the wall family and nonspiking for \(\Omega\).

But the \(R^{-C}\)-measure condition must be explicit. Otherwise the Remez constants are too expensive.

---

## Final result

The weighted transfer step is valid only with an \(R\)-scale good-weight lower set:

\[
\boxed{
|\{N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2\ge Q^{-A}\}|\ge R^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

Then finite-algebra Remez gives

\[
\int \Omega W_2\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

This repairs the bridge:

\[
\mathrm{Gate1}
+
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}
+
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}
\Rightarrow
\text{unweighted wall mass}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{WeightedPlainWallTransfer}_{2Y}^{R}
\Rightarrow
\text{weighted scalar O2/O3 input}.
\]

The main rank-two architecture remains intact, with the corrected \(R^{-C}\) lower-set requirement.

## Assistant (2026-04-28 14:18:50)

I’ll push the remaining weighted-transfer condition: prove that \(\Omega=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2\) has an \(R^{-C}\)-measure polynomial lower-level set on Gate–1-good blocks, rather than assuming it.

_Thought for 9s_

Continuing Agent 5 — weight-goodness for \(\Omega=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2\).

No nomenclature changes:

\[
\rho_Y,\qquad
\rho_\Gamma=\frac{\beta_9-\rho_Yc_7}{\alpha_9},
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{fold}}(x)=\frac{(1-x)^2}{x^2}.
\]

In the rank-two branch \(B_Y=0\), the honest D4 wall is the plain vector wall

\[
F_{2Y}\asymp H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

and the corrected weighted-transfer condition requires an \(R^{-C}\)-large set where

\[
\Omega=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\]

is polynomially non-small. The earlier \(Q^{-C}\)-measure lower set is not enough because Remez losses scale like \((1/|E|)^R\). This was the key correction in the previous step. 

---

# 1. The exact target

We need the following theorem.

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{WeightGoodSet}_{2Y}.
}
\]

On every selected Gate–1-good / Stack-good block \(I\), either:

\[
\int_I \Omega \,dm
\]

is negligible and the block is discarded before O2/O3, or there exists a threshold

\[
\tau\ge Q^{-A}
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
|\{m\in I:\Omega(m)\ge \tau\}|\ge R^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

This is the missing input for

\[
\mathrm{WeightedPlainWallTransfer}_{2Y}^{R}.
\]

---

# 2. Derive \(R^{-C}\)-good set from \(L^1/L^\infty\)

A simple sufficient condition is:

\[
\int_I\Omega\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

and

\[
\|\Omega\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^A.
\]

Then by dyadic decomposition, there exists a level

\[
\tau\in[Q^{-A'},Q^A]
\]

such that

\[
|\{\tau\le \Omega<2\tau\}|
\ge
\frac{Q^{-A}}{O(\log Q)}\,\tau^{-1}|I|.
\]

But this only gives \(Q^{-A}\)-scale measure in the worst case, not \(R^{-C}\)-scale. Since \(Q^{-A}\ll R^{-C}\), this is not enough.

So \(L^1/L^\infty\) alone is insufficient.

We need either:

1. lower boundedness/slow variation of \(\Omega\) on selected blocks; or  
2. finite-algebra nonspiking for \(\Omega\).

---

# 3. Finite-algebra nonspiking for \(\Omega\)

If

\[
\Omega\in\mathscr A_I
\]

where \(\mathscr A_I\) is an \(R^C\)-conditioned finite analytic algebra with Remez control, then \(\Omega\) cannot be concentrated on a \(Q^{-A}\)-thin set without paying an exponential-in-\(R\) cost.

A useful theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{WeightRemezNonspiking.}
}
\]

If

\[
0\le \Omega\in\mathscr A_I,
\]

\[
\int_I\Omega\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

and

\[
\|\Omega\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^A,
\]

then there exists

\[
\tau\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

such that

\[
|\{\Omega\ge \tau\}|\ge R^{-C}|I|.
\]

Why? If every level set above \(Q^{-A'}\) had measure \(<R^{-C}|I|\), then \(\Omega\) would be concentrated in an \(R^{-C}\)-thin union of high-level sets. Remez/Cartan bounds for \(\mathscr A_I\) force a controlled finite-complexity function with polynomial \(L^1\)-mass to occupy an \(R^{-C}\)-scale portion of the interval.

This is precisely the same finite-atlas regularity needed for LocalMarkov and O2/O3.

So the weight-goodness theorem should be folded into the same finite atlas package:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{FiniteAtlasRegularity}
\Rightarrow
\mathrm{WeightGoodSet}_{2Y}.
}
\]

---

# 4. But \(\Omega=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2\) may contain cutoffs

There is a caveat. \(N_{\mathrm{sm}}\) is a smooth/capped weight. It may include cutoffs, dyadic caps, or smooth partitions that are not analytic finite-degree functions.

That is still acceptable if the cutoffs are selected from a fixed finite family and have controlled transition width:

\[
\text{transition width}\ge R^{-C}|I|.
\]

Then each cutoff has an \(R^{-C}\)-scale support structure, and the good-level set condition is built in.

So we need one of two formulations.

### Analytic weight version

\[
\Omega\in\mathscr A_I
\]

with Remez nonspiking.

### Smooth cutoff version

\[
\Omega
\]

is a finite sum/product of chart-good finite-algebra terms and smooth cutoffs whose supports have \(R^{-C}\)-scale thickness and whose nonzero plateau is polynomially large.

Then

\[
\Omega
\]

has an \(R^{-C}\)-measure lower-level set by construction.

Thus the theorem should not require \(\Omega\) to be analytic. It should require:

\[
\boxed{
\Omega\text{ is }R\text{-admissible: no support thinner than }R^{-C}.
}
\]

---

# 5. Define \(R\)-admissible weights

A clean definition:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{\(R\)-admissible smooth weight.}
}
\]

A nonnegative smooth weight \(\Omega\) on \(I\) is \(R\)-admissible if:

1. \(0\le \Omega\le Q^C\);

2. \(\Omega\) is built from \(O(1)\) finite-atlas expressions and smooth cutoffs;

3. every cutoff support or transition interval has length at least \(R^{-C}|I|\);

4. if

\[
\int_I\Omega\ge Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

then some level set

\[
\{\Omega\ge Q^{-A'}\}
\]

has measure at least

\[
R^{-C}|I|.
\]

This fourth property can be taken as a lemma derived from 1–3, or included in the definition.

Then weighted transfer is safe.

---

# 6. Revised weighted transfer statement

The corrected theorem becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{WeightedPlainWallTransfer}_{2Y}^{R}.
}
\]

Assume:

1. local unweighted wall lower:

\[
\int_I W_2\ge Q^{-A}|I|,
\qquad
W_2=|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2;
\]

2. \(\Omega=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2\) is \(R\)-admissible and has polynomial average on \(I\):

\[
\int_I \Omega\ge Q^{-A_\Omega}|I|;
\]

3. vector wall Remez:

\[
|E|\ge R^{-C}|I|
\Longrightarrow
\int_E W_2\ge Q^{-C}\int_I W_2.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I \Omega W_2\ge Q^{-A'}|I|.
}
\]

Proof:

From \(R\)-admissibility, choose

\[
E=\{\Omega\ge Q^{-A_\Omega'}\}
\]

with

\[
|E|\ge R^{-C}|I|.
\]

Then vector Remez gives

\[
\int_E W_2\ge Q^{-C}\int_I W_2.
\]

So

\[
\int_I\Omega W_2
\ge
Q^{-A_\Omega'}\int_EW_2
\ge
Q^{-A'}|I|.
\]

---

# 7. What if \(\Omega\) has no polynomial average?

If

\[
\int_I \Omega\ll Q^{-A}|I|
\]

on a Gate–1-good block, that block cannot feed O2/O3 through this wall weight.

Then the stack must either:

1. discard it and prove enough Gate–1 mass remains on \(\Omega\)-good blocks; or  
2. redefine \(N_{\mathrm{sm}}\) / \(H\)-normalization so that the relevant D4 wall is not suppressed there; or  
3. route to a different branch.

Thus we need a separate mass-retention theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{WeightGoodGateMass.}
}
\]

Gate–1 mass must not be concentrated entirely where

\[
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\]

is super-polynomially small.

A sufficient statement:

\[
\int_{\{\Omega\ge Q^{-A}\}} |q''|^2
\ge Q^{-A'}\int |q''|^2.
\]

This is another finite-atlas/weight-design condition.

---

# 8. Interaction with \(H\)

Since

\[
\Omega=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2,
\]

smallness of \(H\) could kill the weighted wall. If \(H\) is a D4 coefficient factor, we need:

\[
\boxed{
|H|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

on a polynomial part of the Stack-good mass.

If \(H\) has zeros, then either:

1. zeros are finite-type and occupy only \(R^{-C}\)-small neighborhoods; or  
2. those neighborhoods are routed to another chart; or  
3. D4 channel degenerates.

So a needed sublemma is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{HNonvanishing}_{2Y}:
\quad
|\{|H|\ge Q^{-A}\}|\ge R^{-C}|I|
}
\]

on selected blocks.

Again, \(R^{-C}\), not \(Q^{-C}\), is the correct measure scale.

---

# 9. Final corrected rank-two transfer stack

The full corrected pipeline is now:

1. Gate–1 + LocalMarkov + RankTwoCoercivity gives

\[
\int_I W_2\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

2. Weight-goodness gives

\[
E_\Omega=\{\Omega\ge Q^{-A}\}
\]

with

\[
|E_\Omega|\ge R^{-C}|I|.
\]

3. Vector wall Remez gives

\[
\int_{E_\Omega}W_2\ge Q^{-A'}\int_IW_2.
\]

4. Therefore

\[
\int_I\Omega W_2\ge Q^{-A''}|I|.
\]

5. Select fixed component

\[
G_\star\in\{\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}
\]

at smooth aggregate stage.

6. Run scalar O2/O3 with

\[
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2|G_\star|^2.
\]

---

## Final result

The weighted transfer is valid if and only if the weight-good set is \(R^{-C}\)-large, not merely \(Q^{-C}\)-large.

The exact needed condition is:

\[
\boxed{
|\{N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2\ge Q^{-A}\}\cap I|
\ge R^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

Together with vector Remez for

\[
W_2=|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2,
\]

this transfers Gate–1 rank-two wall mass into the weighted O2/O3 wall.

So the remaining analytic inputs are now:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G},
\quad
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity},
\quad
\mathrm{WeightGoodSet}_{2Y},
\quad
\mathrm{VectorWallRemez}.
}
\]

All are finite-atlas/Riesz/weight-design theorems, not rank-one wall/trap phenomena.

## Assistant (2026-04-28 14:27:29)

_Thought for 7s_

No nomenclature changes.

Critical correction retained: in the rank-two branch, D4 honestly supplies only the plain wall

\[
\{\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}.
\]

The derivatives

\[
D\Gamma_G,\quad D^2\Gamma_G
\]

are analytic auxiliaries only unless a separate derivative-D4-channel theorem is proved. 

---

# Agent 5 — PlainWallRankTwoClosure

Assume the rank-two local algebra has already given

\[
B_Y=0.
\]

Then D4 gives

\[
F_{2Y}
=
H
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\Gamma_G\\
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Under coefficient conditioning,

\[
|F_{2Y}|^2
\asymp_{Q^A}
|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right).
\]

The corrected analytic closure must therefore start from the **plain** wall mass

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}.
\]

The purpose of this attack is to show:

\[
\boxed{
\text{plain wall small}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
q''\text{ small},
}
\]

using LocalMarkov\(_{\Gamma_G}\), RankTwoCoercivity, and Gate–1.

---

## 1. Normalization

Use

\[
\Gamma_G=-6q''+36q-12q^3.
\]

Define

\[
f(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=-6(q''-f(q)).
\]

Set

\[
E_1=q''-f(q).
\]

Also,

\[
f'(q)=6-6q^2.
\]

The second component is

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=q^{(4)}-6(1-q^2)q''
=
q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Set

\[
E_2=q^{(4)}-f'(q)q''.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=-6E_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=E_2.
}
\]

---

## 2. Exact identity

Differentiate

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1.
\]

Then

\[
q'''=f'(q)q'+E_1',
\]

and

\[
q^{(4)}
=
f''(q)(q')^2+f'(q)q''+E_1''.
\]

Therefore

\[
E_2-E_1''
=
f''(q)(q')^2.
\]

Since

\[
f''(q)=-12q,
\]

we obtain

\[
\boxed{
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
}
\]

This identity is the analytic core of the rank-two closure.

---

## 3. Exact flatness

If

\[
E_1=0,
\qquad
E_2=0,
\]

then

\[
q(q')^2=0.
\]

On any connected interval where \(q\ne0\), this forces

\[
q'=0.
\]

Then

\[
q''=0.
\]

But \(E_1=0\) also gives

\[
q''=f(q)=2q(3-q^2).
\]

So the only local exact-flat states are

\[
q\equiv0,\qquad q\equiv\sqrt3,\qquad q\equiv-\sqrt3.
\]

In all cases,

\[
\boxed{q''=0.}
\]

So exact joint flatness contradicts Gate–1 energy.

---

## 4. Quantitative RankTwoCoercivity

The useful analytic theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}.
}
\]

On a chart-good interval \(I\), with scale-normalized norms and finite-complexity bounds,

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta.
\]

The proof uses the identity

\[
E_2-E_1''=-12q(q')^2.
\]

Let

\[
\delta=
\|E_1\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|E_2\|_{L^2(I)}.
\]

Then

\[
\|q(q')^2\|_{L^2(I)}
\le C\delta.
\]

Split around the roots

\[
Z=\{0,\sqrt3,-\sqrt3\}
\]

of

\[
f(q)=2q(3-q^2).
\]

On

\[
I_{\mathrm{near}}
=
\{x:\operatorname{dist}(q(x),Z)\le \eta\},
\]

we have

\[
|f(q)|\le C\eta,
\]

hence

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{near}})}
\le
C\eta |I|^{1/2}+\|E_1\|_{L^2(I)}.
\]

On the complement \(I_{\mathrm{far}}\),

\[
|f(q)|\ge c\eta,
\qquad
|q|\ge c\eta.
\]

The identity gives

\[
\|q'\|_{L^4(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
C\delta^{1/2}\eta^{-1/2}.
\]

Also,

\[
q''=f(q)+E_1.
\]

Finite-complexity/Sobolev control gives

\[
\|E_1\|_{C^0(I)}\le Q^C\delta.
\]

For \(\delta\ll Q^{-C}\eta\), this implies

\[
|q''|\ge c\eta
\]

on the far set, up to polynomially negligible exceptional subsets.

Then a one-dimensional acceleration–velocity lemma plus finite-component/Remez control gives

\[
|I_{\mathrm{far}}|\le Q^C\delta^a\eta^{-b}.
\]

With chart-good bounds on \(q''\),

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I_{\mathrm{far}})}
\le
Q^C\delta^{a/2}\eta^{-b/2}.
\]

Choosing

\[
\eta=\delta^\kappa
\]

with \(\kappa>0\) small enough yields

\[
\boxed{
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\delta^\theta.
}
\]

This proves the coercivity theorem, modulo the standard finite-complexity inputs: Sobolev control, finite-component/Remez control, and the acceleration–velocity lemma.

---

## 5. LocalMarkov\(_{\Gamma_G}\)

RankTwoCoercivity requires

\[
\Gamma_G\in H^2(I).
\]

But the honest D4 wall gives only \(\Gamma_G\) in \(L^2\). Therefore we need:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}:
\quad
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}.
}
\]

This must be proved as a finite Riesz/Markov theorem for the local function space containing \(\Gamma_G\).

Let \(\mathcal V_I\) be the local finite EF/AFE chart for \(q\). Since

\[
\Gamma_G=-6q''+36q-12q^3,
\]

we have

\[
\Gamma_G\in
\mathcal W_I
:=
D^2\mathcal V_I+\mathcal V_I+\operatorname{Sym}^3\mathcal V_I.
\]

Thus LocalMarkov\(_{\Gamma_G}\) reduces to:

\[
\boxed{
\|w\|_{H^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\|w\|_{L^2(I^*)}
\qquad
(w\in\mathcal W_I).
}
\]

With basis \(\{\psi_i\}\) of \(\mathcal W_I\), define

\[
G_0=(\langle\psi_i,\psi_j\rangle_{L^2(I^*)}),
\]

\[
G_2=(\langle\psi_i,\psi_j\rangle_{H^2(I)}).
\]

The needed finite Gram condition is

\[
\boxed{
G_2\preceq Q^C G_0.
}
\]

This is the analytic finite-model/Riesz obligation.

---

## 6. Corrected PlainWallRankTwoClosure theorem

The corrected theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{PlainWallRankTwoClosure}.
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(B_Y=0\);

2. D4 coefficients are conditioned:

\[
|c_7|,\ |c_7^{-1}|,\ |\alpha_9|,\ |\alpha_9^{-1}|,\ |\beta_9|\le Q^A;
\]

3. LocalMarkov\(_{\Gamma_G}\) holds:

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)};
\]

4. RankTwoCoercivity holds:

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta;
\]

5. Gate–1 holds:

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Thus the **plain** rank-two wall has local mass.

---

## 7. Residual-compatible version

If the canonical source is decomposed as

\[
q=q_X+r,
\]

and \(\Gamma_G(q)\) is approximated by a finite chart element

\[
w\in\mathcal W_I,
\]

we need

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{H^2(I)}(\Gamma_G(q),\mathcal W_I)
\le Q^{-B}.
}
\]

Then LocalMarkov applies to \(w\), and the residual is absorbed into the RankTwoCoercivity error.

This prevents the Markov theorem from being applied to an object outside the finite chart algebra.

---

## 8. Weighted transfer remains separate

PlainWallRankTwoClosure only gives unweighted local wall mass.

To feed O2/O3, we still need:

\[
\mathrm{WeightedPlainWallTransfer}_{2Y}^{R}.
\]

That theorem must account for

\[
\Omega=N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\]

and requires an \(R^{-C}\)-large good-weight set:

\[
|\{\Omega\ge Q^{-A}\}\cap I|
\ge R^{-C}|I|.
\]

Then vector Remez transfers

\[
\int_I
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)
\]

to the weighted integral.

---

## 9. Final corrected pipeline

The corrected analytic pipeline is:

\[
B_Y=0
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
F_{2Y}\asymp H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}
+
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}
+
\mathrm{Gate1}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2}
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{WeightedPlainWallTransfer}_{2Y}^{R}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\int N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)
\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\text{select fixed }G_\star\in\{\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}
\text{ at smooth aggregate stage}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\text{scalar O2/O3 with }
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2|G_\star|^2.
\]

---

## Final result

The rank-two analytic closure is now corrected and honest:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 supplies the plain wall only.}
}
\]

The derivatives needed by coercivity enter through

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G},
}
\]

not through D4.

Thus the analytic burden is exactly:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}
+
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}
+
\mathrm{WeightedPlainWallTransfer}_{2Y}^{R}.
}
\]

The local algebraic burden remains:

\[
\boxed{
B_Y=0.
}
\]

---

# 1. What \(\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}\) really says

Using

\[
\Gamma_G=-6q''+36q-12q^3,
\]

if \(q\) lies in a local finite chart space

\[
\mathcal V_I,
\]

then

\[
\Gamma_G\in
\mathcal W_I
:=
D^2\mathcal V_I+\mathcal V_I+\operatorname{Sym}^3\mathcal V_I.
\]

So \(\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}\) is not a differential equation theorem. It is a finite-model/Riesz theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\|w\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\|w\|_{L^2(I^*)}
\quad
\forall w\in\mathcal W_I.
}
\]

This is the exact finite-dimensional analytic statement needed.

---

# 2. Finite Gram formulation

Choose a basis

\[
\psi_1,\ldots,\psi_M
\]

of \(\mathcal W_I\), with

\[
M\le R^C.
\]

Define

\[
G_0=(\langle \psi_i,\psi_j\rangle_{L^2(I^*)}),
\]

\[
G_2=(\langle \psi_i,\psi_j\rangle_{H^2(I)}).
\]

Then \(\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}\) is equivalent to

\[
\boxed{
G_2\preceq Q^C G_0.
}
\]

Or equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{\max}
\left(
G_0^{-1/2}G_2G_0^{-1/2}
\right)
\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is structurally the same kind of finite Schur/Riesz certificate as the bounded dual-row certificate for \(B_Y=0\).

---

# 3. Why the enlarged interval \(I^*\) matters

The estimate should use

\[
L^2(I^*)
\]

on the right, not just

\[
L^2(I).
\]

Reason: a finite-degree analytic expression can have large derivatives near the boundary of \(I\) relative to its \(L^2(I)\)-mass. The enlarged interval \(I^*\) prevents boundary layer pathologies.

A safe statement is:

\[
I\Subset I^*,
\qquad
\operatorname{dist}(I,\partial I^*)\ge R^{-C}|I|.
\]

Then standard Markov/Cauchy estimates give only

\[
R^C
\]

loss, hence polynomial in \(Q\):

\[
R^{CR}=Q^{O(1)}
\]

under the usual choice

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

So the enlargement \(I^*\) is not cosmetic; it keeps Markov losses polynomial.

---

# 4. Sufficient analytic hypotheses

A clean sufficient theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{FiniteAtlasMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}.
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(\mathcal V_I\) is an \(R^C\)-conditioned finite local EF/AFE chart space;

2. \(\mathcal V_I\) is derivative-stable through order \(4\):

\[
D^j\mathcal V_I\subseteq \mathcal V_I^{(j)},
\qquad j\le4,
\]

with polynomial Riesz constants;

3. \(\mathcal V_I\) is product-stable through cubic order:

\[
\operatorname{Sym}^3\mathcal V_I
\]

has dimension and conditioning at most \(R^C\);

4. all chart denominators are bounded below:

\[
|D_{\mathrm{chart}}|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

on \(I^*\);

5. basis functions extend analytically, or satisfy finite Remez/Markov bounds, on \(I^*\).

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|w\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\|w\|_{L^2(I^*)}
\qquad
(w\in \mathcal W_I).
}
\]

This proves \(\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}\).

---

# 5. Potential failure modes

The Markov theorem can fail in exactly four meaningful ways.

## Failure A: \(\Gamma_G\) not in the finite chart algebra

If

\[
\Gamma_G(q)
\notin
\mathcal W_I
+
\text{small residual},
\]

then the Markov theorem cannot be applied to \(\Gamma_G\). This is a chart-completion failure.

Needed repair:

\[
\operatorname{dist}_{H^2(I)}
(\Gamma_G(q),\mathcal W_I)\le Q^{-B}.
\]

## Failure B: denominator singularity

If chart denominators become too small on \(I^*\), Markov constants can blow up. This must be handled by chart routing:

\[
|D_{\mathrm{chart}}|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

or move to another chart.

## Failure C: product-space ill-conditioning

Even if \(\mathcal V_I\) is well conditioned, the cubic space

\[
\operatorname{Sym}^3\mathcal V_I
\]

may have high leverage or near-linear dependencies. Need a product-Riesz theorem:

\[
\operatorname{Sym}^{\le3}\mathcal V_I
\]

has polynomial conditioning.

## Failure D: boundary concentration

If \(I^*\) is too close to \(I\), derivative norms can exceed polynomial control. Need \(R^{-C}\)-scale buffer.

---

# 6. Relation to O2/O3

This theorem should be reusable.

O2/O3 already needs:

- finite local chart space;
- Riesz conditioning;
- Christoffel spread;
- finite wall-family bounded charge;
- near-pure finite moment separation.

\(\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}\) uses the same finite atlas infrastructure.

So the proof should not introduce a new analytic universe. It should state:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{FiniteModelRieszControl}
\Rightarrow
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}.
}
\]

This aligns the rank-two analytic closure with the O2/O3 stack.

---

# 7. Corrected analytic theorem

The corrected theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{PlainWallRankTwoClosure.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. \(B_Y=0\);

2. D4 coefficients and \(H\) are polynomially good on the routed chart;

3. \(\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}\):

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)};
\]

4. \(\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}\):

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le Q^C
\left(
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\right)^\theta;
\]

5. Gate–1:

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This gives honest plain-wall mass.

---

# 8. Then weighted transfer and scalar O2/O3

Once unweighted mass is known, we still need

\[
\mathrm{WeightedPlainWallTransfer}_{2Y}^{R}.
\]

This requires:

\[
E_\Omega=\{N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2\ge Q^{-A}\}
\]

with

\[
|E_\Omega\cap I|\ge R^{-C}|I|,
\]

and vector wall Remez:

\[
|E|\ge R^{-C}|I|
\Rightarrow

(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2)
\ge Q^{-C}

(|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2).
\]

Then select

\[
G_\star\in\{\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}
\]

at the smooth aggregate stage and run scalar O2/O3 with

\[
N_{\mathrm{sm}}|H|^2|G_\star|^2.
\]

---

The next analytic proof target is not the jet wall. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}
}
\]

for

\[
\mathcal W_I
=
D^2\mathcal V_I+\mathcal V_I+\operatorname{Sym}^3\mathcal V_I.

If we prove the finite Gram condition

\[
\boxed{

}
\]

then plain rank-two D4 wall mass follows from

\[
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}
+
\mathrm{Gate1}.
\]

This keeps the rank-two path honest: D4 supplies \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\), while derivative control comes from finite-model Markov, not from additional D4 channels.

Continuing Agent 5 — proof route for \(\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}\).

No nomenclature changes.

Critical correction retained:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 supplies only the plain wall } \{\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}.
}
\]

The derivatives \(D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G\) are not D4 wall components. They enter only through the analytic Markov step. The corrected route is

\[
B_Y=0
\Rightarrow
F_{2Y}\asymp H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\Rightarrow
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}
+
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}
+
\mathrm{Gate1}.
\]

The target is

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}.
}
\]

This is the finite-model bridge from the honest plain D4 wall to the \(H^2\)-norm required by RankTwoCoercivity. 

---

# 1. Reduce \(\Gamma_G\) to a finite algebra

We have

\[
\Gamma_G=-6q''+36q-12q^3.
\]

Let \(\mathcal V_I\) be the local finite EF/AFE chart space containing \(q\) on the chart-good interval \(I\). Then

\[
\Gamma_G\in
\mathcal W_I
:=
D^2\mathcal V_I+\mathcal V_I+\operatorname{Sym}^3\mathcal V_I.
\]

Thus \(\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}\) follows from

\[
\boxed{
\|w\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\|w\|_{L^2(I^*)}
\qquad
(w\in \mathcal W_I).
}
\]

This is not a special property of \(\Gamma_G\). It is a finite-dimensional Markov/Riesz estimate for the space \(\mathcal W_I\).

---

# 2. Concrete sufficient model for \(\mathcal W_I\)

A proof-ready sufficient model is:

\[
\mathcal V_I
\subset
\left\{
\frac{\sum_{\nu=0}^{M} P_\nu(x)u_\nu(x)}{D(x)}
:
\deg P_\nu\le R,\ M\le R^C
\right\},
\]

where:

1. \(u_\nu\) and \(D\) are fixed chart-good analytic functions on \(I^*\);

2. the denominator obeys

\[
|D(x)|\ge Q^{-C}
\qquad (x\in I^*);
\]

3. the \(u_\nu\), \(D^{-1}\), and their derivatives up to fixed order have polynomial bounds;

4. \(I\Subset I^*\) with buffer

\[
\operatorname{dist}(I,\partial I^*)\ge R^{-C}|I|.
\]

Then \(\mathcal W_I\) is contained in a similar finite rational/analytic space with degree and dimension still \(R^C\). The cubic term increases degree and dimension only polynomially in \(R\), because the cubic power is fixed.

Therefore \(\mathcal W_I\) has finite analytic complexity \(R^C\).

---

# 3. Markov estimate by Cauchy / Bernstein

If \(w\in\mathcal W_I\) extends analytically to a complex neighborhood of \(I\) of relative width \(R^{-C}\), then Cauchy estimates give

\[
\|D^j w\|_{L^\infty(I)}
\le
R^{Cj}\|w\|_{L^\infty(I^*)},
\qquad j\le2.
\]

Finite-dimensional \(L^\infty/L^2\) equivalence on the same class gives

\[
\|w\|_{L^\infty(I^*)}
\le Q^C\|w\|_{L^2(I^*)}.
\]

Hence

\[
\|w\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\|w\|_{L^2(I^*)}.
\]

The important scale is \(R^{-C}\). Since

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

losses of the form

\[
R^{CR}
\]

remain

\[
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

So the Markov loss is polynomial.

---

# 4. Equivalent Gram condition

For implementation, use the finite Gram test.

Choose a basis

\[
\psi_1,\ldots,\psi_M
\]

of \(\mathcal W_I\). Define

\[
G_0=(\langle \psi_i,\psi_j\rangle_{L^2(I^*)}),
\]

\[
G_2=(\langle \psi_i,\psi_j\rangle_{H^2(I)}).
\]

Then

\[
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}
\]

is exactly

\[
\boxed{
G_2\preceq Q^C G_0.
}
\]

This is the form to audit computationally or symbolically. It is also aligned with the rest of the proof stack: bounded dual rows, vector amplitude leverage, O2/O3 moment separation, and wall Remez are all finite Gram/Riesz statements.

---

# 5. Product-space ill-conditioning is the main risk

The dangerous part is not \(D^2\mathcal V_I\) or \(\mathcal V_I\). It is

\[
\operatorname{Sym}^3\mathcal V_I.
\]

Even if \(\mathcal V_I\) is well conditioned, cubic products can become ill-conditioned or high leverage.

So the needed auxiliary theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{ProductRiesz}_{\le3}.
}
\]

It should assert that

\[
\mathcal V_I+\operatorname{Sym}^2\mathcal V_I+\operatorname{Sym}^3\mathcal V_I
\]

has polynomial dimension and polynomial Riesz conditioning on \(I^*\).

If ProductRiesz fails, \(\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}\) may fail even though the linear chart space is controlled.

This is the main analytic sub-blocker.

---

# 6. Residual-compatible version

The actual \(q\) may not lie exactly in \(\mathcal V_I\). Suppose

\[
q=q_{\mathrm{fin}}+r,
\qquad q_{\mathrm{fin}}\in\mathcal V_I.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G(q)
=
\Gamma_G(q_{\mathrm{fin}})
+
\mathcal E_{\Gamma}.
\]

We need

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathcal E_{\Gamma}\|_{H^2(I)}\le Q^{-B}.
}
\]

A sufficient condition is

\[
\|r\|_{H^4(I)}\le Q^{-B}
\]

plus polynomial \(C^K\) bounds for \(q_{\mathrm{fin}}\). Because

\[
q^3-q_{\mathrm{fin}}^3
=
3q_{\mathrm{fin}}^2r+3q_{\mathrm{fin}}r^2+r^3,
\]

the cubic residual is controlled by \(r\) if the chart is bounded.

Then LocalMarkov applies to \(\Gamma_G(q_{\mathrm{fin}})\), and \(\mathcal E_\Gamma\) is absorbed into the RankTwoCoercivity error.

So the residual-compatible theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{H^2(I)}(\Gamma_G(q),\mathcal W_I)\le Q^{-B}.
}
\]

---

# 7. Plain-wall closure using LocalMarkov

Assume the honest plain wall is small:

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\le \varepsilon.
\]

LocalMarkov gives

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\varepsilon.
\]

RankTwoCoercivity gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C
\left(
Q^C\varepsilon+\varepsilon
\right)^\theta.
\]

For

\[
\varepsilon\le Q^{-A}
\]

with \(A\) large enough, this contradicts Gate–1:

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}\ge Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This is the corrected local plain-wall lower.

---

# 8. No derivative wall was used

Important guardrail:

The proof used

\[
D\Gamma_G,D^2\Gamma_G
\]

only internally to estimate \(\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2}\) through LocalMarkov.

It did **not** claim D4 supplies derivative wall components. Therefore the honest D4 wall remains

\[
H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

This preserves the correction.

---

# 9. Remaining analytic checklist

To close \(\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}\), the exact remaining items are:

1. define \(\mathcal V_I\) precisely;

2. prove derivative stability:

\[
D^j\mathcal V_I\subseteq\mathcal V_I^{(j)},\qquad j\le4;
\]

3. prove ProductRiesz for

\[
\operatorname{Sym}^{\le3}\mathcal V_I;
\]

4. prove denominator lower bounds on \(I^*\);

5. prove \(I\Subset I^*\) with \(R^{-C}\)-buffer;

6. prove residual compatibility:

\[
\operatorname{dist}_{H^2(I)}(\Gamma_G(q),\mathcal W_I)\le Q^{-B}.
\]

These are finite-atlas analytic tasks, not rank-one wall tasks.

---

## Final result

\(\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}\) reduces to the finite Gram/Riesz estimate

\[
\boxed{
G_2\preceq Q^C G_0
}
\]

for

\[
\mathcal W_I
=
D^2\mathcal V_I+\mathcal V_I+\operatorname{Sym}^3\mathcal V_I.
\]

With this, the corrected rank-two closure is:

\[
\text{plain wall small}
\Rightarrow
\Gamma_G\text{ small in }H^2
\Rightarrow
q''\text{ small}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate--1 contradiction}.
\]

No derivative D4 wall components are invoked.

# 1. The exact analytic bottleneck

}
\]

The hard subspace is not \(D^2\mathcal V_I\). It is

\[
\operatorname{Sym}^3\mathcal V_I.
\]

Therefore the real remaining analytic theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{ProductRiesz}_{\le3}(\mathcal V_I).
}
\]

---

# 2. Why ProductRiesz is nontrivial

Even if \(\mathcal V_I\) has a well-conditioned basis, products can become ill-conditioned.

Suppose

\[
q(x)=\sum_{i=1}^{M}a_i\phi_i(x).
\]

Then

\[
q^3
=
\sum_{i,j,k}a_ia_ja_k\phi_i\phi_j\phi_k.
\]

The product span

\[
\operatorname{Sym}^3\mathcal V_I
=
\operatorname{span}\{\phi_i\phi_j\phi_k\}
\]

can have many near-linear relations and large leverage even if \(\mathcal V_I\) itself is controlled.

The needed statement is not that all product monomials are independent. The needed statement is that their span has a polynomially conditioned quotient basis.

That is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{after removing near-relations, }
\operatorname{Sym}^{\le3}\mathcal V_I
\text{ has an }R^C\text{-conditioned basis.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Finite Gram formulation

Let

\[
\mathcal U_I
=
D^2\mathcal V_I+\mathcal V_I+\operatorname{Sym}^3\mathcal V_I.
\]

Pick a spanning list

\[
u_1,\ldots,u_N
\]

consisting of:

\[
D^2\phi_i,
\qquad
\phi_i,
\qquad
\phi_i\phi_j\phi_k.
\]

Define

\[
G_0=(\langle u_i,u_j\rangle_{L^2(I^*)}).
\]

ProductRiesz says:

\[
\boxed{
G_0
\text{ has a polynomially conditioned nonzero spectral subspace.}
}
\]

Equivalently, after discarding singular values

\[
< Q^{-C},
\]

the resulting quotient basis \(\psi_1,\ldots,\psi_M\) satisfies

\[
Q^{-C}\|b\|_{\ell^2}^2
\le
\left\|\sum b_m\psi_m\right\|_{L^2(I^*)}^2
\le
Q^C\|b\|_{\ell^2}^2.
\]

Then define

\[
G_2=(\langle \psi_i,\psi_j\rangle_{H^2(I)}).
\]

The Markov theorem is

\[
\boxed{
G_2\preceq Q^C G_0.
}
\]

In a quotient-normalized basis where \(G_0\sim I\), this becomes

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{\max}(G_2)\le Q^C.
}
\]

---

# 4. Analytic sufficient condition

A strong sufficient condition is that every \(\phi_i\) is the restriction of a bounded-degree analytic/rational function on a complex neighborhood \(U(I^*)\) of relative width

\[
R^{-C}.
\]

Assume:

\[
\|\phi_i\|_{H^\infty(U(I^*))}\le Q^C,
\]

and all chart denominators obey

\[
|D_{\mathrm{chart}}|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

on \(U(I^*)\).

Then every product

\[
\phi_i\phi_j\phi_k
\]

also has analytic norm \(\le Q^C\), and Cauchy estimates give

\[
\|D^r(\phi_i\phi_j\phi_k)\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C\|\phi_i\phi_j\phi_k\|_{L^2(I^*)}
\]

after quotienting out near-zero directions.

This proves

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{ProductRiesz}_{\le3}
+
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}
}
\]

in one step, provided the analytic extension and denominator lower bounds hold.

---

# 5. If analytic extension is unavailable

If we do not have complex extension, a real-variable finite-degree route is possible.

Assume \(\mathcal V_I\) is represented by polynomial/rational coordinates in a real chart:

\[
\phi_i(x)=\frac{P_i(x)}{D_i(x)},
\qquad
\deg P_i,\deg D_i\le R^C,
\qquad
|D_i|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Then products are rational functions with degree still \(R^C\). Classical Markov-type inequalities give

\[
\|D^r w\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
R^{C}\|w\|_{L^2(I^*)}
\]

for \(r\le2\), after accounting for denominator lower bounds.

Since \(R^{C R}=Q^{O(1)}\) in the active scaling, this is polynomially acceptable.

So the real-variable theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{RationalMarkov}_{\le3}
\Rightarrow
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}.
}
\]

---

# 6. ProductRiesz failure modes

There are three meaningful failures.

## Failure A: product leverage spike

The cubic span contains functions concentrated at extraction scale. Then

\[
\|w\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\|w\|_{L^2(I^*)}
\]

may fail.

Interpretation: the local chart basis is too flexible and can simulate atom-local fitting. This would also threaten O2/O3 Christoffel spread.

## Failure B: denominator singularity

If chart denominators nearly vanish in \(I^*\), derivatives blow up. This is a chart routing failure, not a rank-two wall failure.

Repair: move to a chart where denominators are \(Q^{-C}\)-bounded.

## Failure C: residual \(q-q_{\mathrm{fin}}\) not controlled

If

\[
q\notin\mathcal V_I+\text{small residual}
\]

in \(H^4\), then \(\Gamma_G(q)\) may not be close to \(\mathcal W_I\). Markov cannot be applied.

Repair: strengthen finite EF/AFE approximation or put this into the residual completion ledger.

---

# 7. Connection to weighted transfer

The same ProductRiesz/Remez package is needed for weighted transfer.

Weighted transfer requires vector Remez for

\[
W_2=|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2.
\]

If \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) lie in finite Riesz spaces with bounded product structure, then \(W_2\) belongs to a finite positive quadratic algebra with controlled Remez constants.

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{ProductRiesz}_{\le3}
}
\]

helps both:

\[
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}
\]

and

\[
\mathrm{WeightedPlainWallTransfer}_{2Y}^{R}.
\]

This is a useful consolidation: the same finite algebra regularity closes both analytic gaps.

---

# 8. Minimal theorem for the rank-two proof

A compact theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{FiniteProductRieszMarkov}.}
\]

On every chart-good interval pair

\[
I\Subset I^*
\]

with \(R^{-C}\)-buffer, the local chart algebra \(\mathcal V_I\) satisfies:

1. \(q\in\mathcal V_I+\mathrm{Res}\), with residual small in \(H^4\);

2. \(\mathcal V_I\) is \(R^C\)-Riesz in \(L^2(I^*)\);

3. \(\operatorname{Sym}^{\le3}\mathcal V_I\) has an \(R^C\)-Riesz quotient basis;

4. derivatives through order \(4\) obey Markov on the quotient basis;

5. denominators are \(Q^{-C}\)-bounded below.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}+Q^{-B}.
}
\]

This is exactly what PlainWallRankTwoClosure needs.

---

# 9. Corrected plain-wall closure after ProductRiesz

Assume:

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\le \varepsilon.
\]

FiniteProductRieszMarkov gives

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\varepsilon+Q^{-B}.
\]

RankTwoCoercivity gives

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^C(\varepsilon+Q^{-B})^\theta.
\]

For \(\varepsilon,Q^{-B}\) small enough, this contradicts Gate–1. Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is honest plain-wall mass, with no derivative D4 channels used.

---

## Final result

The analytic bottleneck \(\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}\) is reducible to:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{ProductRiesz}_{\le3}
}
\]

for the local EF/AFE chart space \(\mathcal V_I\).

The exact required theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\|\Gamma_G\|_{H^2(I)}
\le Q^C\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I^*)}+Q^{-B},
}
\]

where

\[
\Gamma_G\in D^2\mathcal V_I+\mathcal V_I+\operatorname{Sym}^3\mathcal V_I.
\]

This preserves the corrected route:

\[
\text{plain D4 wall}
+
\mathrm{LocalMarkov}_{\Gamma_G}
+
\mathrm{RankTwoCoercivity}
+
\mathrm{Gate1}.
\]

No jet wall is claimed.
